Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Minor's Transactions Between Benefit and Harm
Ruling on minor's sale and similar transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule that a minor's transaction of mixed benefit/harm requires guardian approval, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding gross mispricing.

Core Idea
A minor's sale needs guardian permission; but once given, Abu Hanifa treats the minor as an adult, the Sahibayn do not.

This lesson explores the sixth category of a minor's actions: transactions that can be either beneficial or harmful, such as sale. The Hanafi school establishes that such transactions require the guardian's assessment to tilt the balance toward benefit. However, a key disagreement arises when a minor sells at a grossly unfair price: does the contract stand or fall?

Guided Path
1
Identify the category and its definition
The passage defines the sixth category as transactions 'between benefit and harm' (dāʾir bayn al-nafʿ wa al-ḍarar), like sale. Recognize that such actions are not purely beneficial (like accepting gifts) nor purely harmful (like divorce).
This is the middle ground where guardian oversight is needed.
2
State the general rule: guardian's opinion required
The text says the minor 'owns it with the guardian's opinion' (yamlikuhu bi-raʾy al-walī). The guardian must assess the transaction so that benefit prevails, linking the minor to the adult ruling.
3
Identify the ikhtilaf regarding ghabn fāḥish with strangers
When a minor with guardian permission sells to a stranger at a grossly unfair price (ghabn fāḥish), Abu Hanifa holds the sale is valid (nāfidh); the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is not effective.
This is the main dispute presented.
4
Explain the ta'lil (legal reasoning) of each side
Abu Hanifa: the guardian's permission grants the minor capacity akin to an adult; mispricing does not void the contract. The Sahibayn: the minor lacks full discretion; gross mispricing signals lack of sound judgment, so the contract should be void to protect the minor.
The difference turns on how much authority the guardian's permission confers.
5
Note the additional dispute when the transaction is with the guardian
If the minor sells to the guardian himself with gross mispricing, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one that it is effective, another that it is not. This shows further nuance within the imam's own views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الْقِسمُ السَّادِسُ وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُ وَفِي الدَّائِرِ بَيْنَهُمَا أَى بَيْنَ النَّفْعِ وَالضَّرَرِ كَالْبَيْعِ وَنَحْوِهِ يَمْلِكُهُ بَرَأَي الْوَلِي فَإِنَّ الْبَيْعَ ونَحْوَهُ مِنَ الْمُعَامَلاَتِ إِنْ كَانَ رَابحًا كَانَ نَفْعًا وَإِنْ كَانَ خَاسِرًا كَانَ ضَرَرًا وَأَيْضًا سَالِبٌ وَجَالِبٌ فَلا بُدْ أَنْ يَنْضَمْ إِلَيْهِ رَالَّى الْوَلِي حَتَّى تَتَرَجَحَ جَهَةُ النَّفْعِ فَيُلْحَقِّ بِالْبَالِغ فَيَنْفُذُ تَصَرُّفَة بِالْغَيْنِ الْفَاحِشِ مَعَ الْأَجَانِبِ كَمَا يُفْقَدُ مِنَ الْبَائِعِ عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ خِلَافًا لَهُمَا فَإِنَّهُ لا يَكُونُ كَالبَالِعْ عِنْدَهُمَا فَلا يَنْقُدُ بِالْغَيْنِ الْفَاحِشِ وَإِنْ بَاشِرَ الْبَيْعَ بِالغَيْنِ الْفَاحِشِ مَعَ الْوَلِي فَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ رِوَايَتَانِ فِي رِوَايَةٍ يَنْقُدُ وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ لَا يَنْفُذُ
Then the sixth category, and it is his statement: 'And in what is between them, i.e., between benefit and harm, like sale and the like, he owns it with the guardian's opinion.' For sale and similar transactions, if profitable, it is benefit; if loss-making, it is harm. Also it is both removing and bringing (property). Therefore the guardian's opinion must be joined so that the benefit side prevails. Thus he is attached to the adult, so his transaction with gross mispricing with strangers is effective according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). For according to them, he is not like an adult, so it does not take effect with gross mispricing. And if he conducts the sale with gross mispricing with the guardian, then from Abu Hanifa there are two narrations: in one it takes effect, in the other it does not.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage covers the sixth and final category: transactions that are between benefit and harm (dāʾir bayn al-nafʿ wa al-ḍarar), such as sale (bayʿ) and similar contracts. According to the Ḥanafī school, a rational minor may engage in such transactions only with the guardian's approval (bi-raʾy al-walī). The guardian's role is to assess whether the transaction is beneficial for the minor. If the minor sells at a grossly unfair price (ghabn fāḥish) to a stranger, Abū Ḥanīfah holds that the transaction is still valid because the minor is treated like an adult once the guardian has granted general permission, but Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad disagree; they say the minor is not like an adult and such a transaction is void. If the transaction is with the guardian himself, there are two narrations from Abū Ḥanīfah: one that it takes effect (even with unfair price) and one that it does not. The differences stem from how much authority the guardian has and how to weigh the minor's interest. The authority weight is from Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah for the majority views, with later narrations (riwāyāt) recorded.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghabn fāḥish): Grossly unfair pricing where the minor sells far below market value or buys far above.
رأي الولي (raʾy al-walī): The guardian's considered opinion or permission required for minor's transactions of mixed benefit/harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abū Ḥanīfah, if a minor with guardian permission sells an item to a stranger at a grossly unfair price, the sale is:
A) Void (bāṭil)
B) Valid (nāfidh)
C) Suspended until guardian ratification
D) Conditional on the minor's age

Key Takeaway
In transactions between benefit and harm, guardian permission allows the minor to contract, but gross mispricing triggers a dispute on validity between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Minority as an Accidental Cause: Its Effects on Legal Capacity
Explaining the legal rule that minority drops obligations except faith, with application to inheritance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule regarding the effects of minority (sighar) on legal capacity, identify which obligations are dropped and which remain, and apply this rule to the case of a discerning minor's inheritance.

Core Idea
Minority drops all obligations and punishments except faith; a discerning minor has deficient capacity — his acts are valid but not obligatory.

This lesson examines the legal principle that minority (sighar) is an accidental cause ('arid) that suspends a person's obligation to perform acts of worship and receive punishments. However, the obligation of faith (iman) remains, and a minor who reaches discernment (tamyiz) acquires deficient capacity, meaning his voluntary acts are valid but he is not compelled. Understanding this rule is essential for distinguishing between a minor's legal responsibility and the gradual acquisition of full capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Status of Minority
Recognize that minority is classified as an accidental cause ('arid) that affects ahliyyat al-ada. Observe how the text places it alongside insanity in its initial state, indicating that both suspend full legal responsibility.
The author reminds us that minority is not intrinsic to human nature (Adam was created adult), so it is an accidental condition.
2
Extract the General Rule: What is Dropped and What Remains
From the text, isolate the key statement: 'All that can be forgiven is dropped from him, meaning all acts of worship and punishments except apostasy.' Then note the exception: 'The obligation of faith is not dropped from him.'
The text specifies that acts of worship ('ibadat), hudud punishments, and expiations (kaffarat) are dropped. Apostasy (riddah) is specifically excluded from forgiveness.
3
Define Deficient Capacity (al-Ahliyyat al-Qasira)
Understand that when a minor becomes discerning (mumayyiz), he acquires deficient capacity. The text says 'he has acquired a type of capacity of performance, i.e., the deficient capacity, not the complete one'. This means his acts are valid if performed, but he is not obligated to perform them.
Deficient capacity applies to the mumayyiz child. The non-discerning minor (sabiy ghayr mumayyiz) has no capacity of performance.
4
Apply to a Furu': Inheritance After Killing
The text presents a practical furu': if a minor kills his testator, he is not deprived of inheritance because deprivation would be a punishment, and punishment is dropped from the minor. This contrasts with an adult killer who would be deprived.
The Hanafi position is that deprivation of inheritance for killing is a penalty; penalties are lifted from minors. Disbelief and slavery are different because they negate the capacity to inherit entirely, not as a punishment.

Source Text

أَصَابَ ضَرْبًا مِنْ أَهْلِيَّةِ الأَدَاءِ يَعْنِى الْقَاصِرَة لا الكَامِلَةِ لِيَقَاءِ صغرِهِ وَهُوَ مُدْرٌ لَيَسْقُطُ بِهِ مَمَا يَحْتَمِلُ السَّقُوطُ عَنِ الْبَالِغِ مِنْ حُلُولِ اللهِ تَعَالَى البُلُوغ لَمْ يُجْعَلْ مُرْتَدًا وَجَعَلَةُ الأَمْرَانِ أَنْ تُوْضَعُ عَنْهُ الْعَهْدَةُ أى خلص الأمْرُ الْكُلِّى فِى بَابِ الصَّغَرِ وَحاضِلُ أَحْكامِهِ أَنْ تَسْقُطَ عَنْهُ عُمْدَةُ ما يَحْتَمِلُ جائے تو اس کے تابع اس مجنون کو کر دیا جائے گا اور اگر والدین کا فر اسلام قبول کرنے سے انکار کر دیں تو بیوی اور مجنون کے درمیان تفریق کر دی جائے گی اور فرض اسلام میں تاخیر کرنے سے کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے احتمال رکھتے ہیں یعنی حقوق اللہ میں سے جیسے مہارات حدود اور کھارات کیونکہ عذر پیش آجانے کے وقت یہ ساقط ہو جاتے ہیں اور یہ حقوق فی نفسہ شیخ و تبدیل کا بھی احتمال رکھتے ہیں ولا يسقط عنه فريضة الایمان اور اس سے ایمان کی فرضیت ساقط نہیں ہوتی یہاں تک کہ جب وہ عاقل ہونے کے بعد ایمان لائے گا تو وہ بطور فرض ہی شمار ہو گا اور وہ تمام احکام اس پر ثابت ہو لیا گے جو ایمان کی وجہ سے دوسرے منین پر ثابت ہوتے ہیں مثلا اس کے اور مشترکہ بیوی کے درمیان جدائی ہو جاتا اور مشرکہ بیوی کی میراست سے محروم ہو جاتا اور اس کے مسلمان عزیز و اقارب کے درمیان و راحت کا جاری ہونا۔ ووضع عنه الزام الأداء اور الہتہ میں عاقل سے اداہ ایمان کا نروم ساقط ہے یعنی میں سے ایمان لانے کا لازم ہونا ساقط ہے لہذا اگر زمانہ طفولیت میں بھی اقرار لسانی نہ کرے یا کلمہ شہادت مسلمانوں کے سامنے دوبارہ بالغ ہونے کے بعد نہ پڑھے تو اس کو سرمہ قرار نہ دیا جائے گا۔ وجملة الأأن تُوضعُ عَنْهُ العَبْدَة حاصل کلام یہ ہے کہ مہمی سے مریم کے بارذمہ داری ساقط ہیں خلاصہ کلام صفر کے معاملے میں یہ ہے کہ یعنی احکام شرعی کا حاصل صفر کے بارے میں یہ ہے کہ معافی کا احتمال رکھنے والے احکام یعنی مرتد ہونے کے علاوہ تمام مہارتیں اور سزائیں اور ان کے ذمہ داری کا بوجھ عیسی عاقل سے ساقط ہیں ويصبح منہ اور صحیح ہے اس سے یعنی مطالبہ احکام نہ ہونے اور اس پر ذمہ داری پابندی احکام کی نہ ہونے کے باجود اگر میں خود اپنی خوشی سے انجام دے تو صحیح ہے۔ وَلَهُ مَالَا عُهْدَةَ فِيهِ أَى جَازَ لِلمنني مَالاً ضَرَ فِيهِ مِنْ قَبُول الهبة وَالصَّدَقَةِ وَنَحْوِهِ مِمَّا فِيْهِ نَفْعٌ مَحِضْ وَقَدْ مَرَّ هَذَا فِي بَيَانِ الأهْلِيَةِ ثُمَّ قَوْلُهُ فَلَا يُحْرَمُ عَن المِيْرَاتِ بِالْقَتْلِ عِنْدَنَا تَفْرَيعٌ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ أَنْ تُوْضَعَ عَنْهُ الْعُهْدَةُ يَعْنِي لَوْقَتَلْ الصنى مُؤرِثَهُ عَمَدًا أَوْ خَطَاءً لأَيُحْرَمُ عَنْ مِيَرَانِهِ لأنَّه عَقُوبَةٌ وَعُهْدَةً بالكفر وَالرِّقَ فَاجَابَ عَنْهُ بَقَوْلِهِ بِخِلَافِ الكُفْرِ وَالرّقِ لأنَّ حِرْمَانَ الْمِيْرَاتِ لَا يَسْتَحِقُهَا الصبى وَأفْرِدَ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّهُ إِذَا كَانَ كَذَالِكَ فَلا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُحْرَمَ عَنِ الْمَيْرَاتِ بِهَا لَيْسَ مِنْ بَابِ الْجَزَاءِ بَلْ لِعَدَمِ الأَهْلِيَةِ إذَ الْكُفْرُ وَالرِّقْ يُنَافِي أَهْلِيَةَ الْمِيرَاثِ مِنَ المُسلِم الْحُرِّ وَالْجُنُونِ عَطَفٌ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ الصَّغَرُ وَهُوَ آفَةً تَحَلُّ بِالدِّمَاغِ بِحَيْتُ يَبْعَثُ عَلَى أَفْعَالِ خِلَافِ مُقْتَضَى الْعَقْلِ مِنْ غَيْرِ ضَعْفٍ فِي أَعْضَائِهِ وَتَسَنقُطُ
And there is no benefit in delaying the obligation because insanity has no end, so it would be harmful for a Muslim woman to be under a kafir and that is not permissible. But when he understands, i.e., becomes inclined, then he has acquired a type of capacity of performance, meaning the deficient capacity, not the complete one, due to his minority. And it is an excuse by which what is possible to be dropped from the adult is dropped, from the rights of Allah like acts of worship, hudud, and expiations, because they can be dropped without excuse and they accept nullification and substitution in themselves. And the obligation of faith is not dropped from him, so that when he believes, it will be obligatory, and the rulings applicable to believers will follow, such as separation between him and his polytheist wife, deprivation of inheritance from her, and inheritance between him and his Muslim relatives. And the obligation of performance is placed from him, meaning the obligation of faith is removed from the child, so if he did not affirm during childhood or did not recite the Shahada after puberty, he is not considered an apostate. And the summary of the matter is that responsibility is removed from him. The conclusion of the rulings on minority is that all that can be forgiven is dropped from him, meaning all acts of worship and punishments except apostasy, and it is valid from him if he performs it by himself without responsibility and claim. And when you understand this, now he mentions the types of accidental causes. So he says: 'It is minority.' Minority is among the accidental causes. The author has counted it among the interfering causes, although it is inherent in creation, because minority is not intrinsic to the reality of man, since Adam was created an adult, so minority is accidental in his offspring. And it is in its initial state like insanity. Do you not know that when a minor's wife becomes Muslim, the order to present Islam to his parents is not given, rather it is delayed until he becomes mature, then presented. If one of the parents becomes Muslim, the minor is made to follow him; if both refuse, separation is made between the wife and the minor. And there is no benefit in delaying the obligation (i.e., delaying the presentation of Islam until insanity ends) because insanity has no end, so delay would cause harm to the Muslim woman who is under a kafir, and that is not permissible. But when he becomes intelligent, i.e., becomes discerning, then he acquires a type of capacity of performance, i.e., deficient capacity appears, not complete, because he still has minority, and this is an excuse for him. So with it is dropped what can be dropped from the adult, i.e., from the rights of Allah such as prayers, hudud, and expiations, because they can be dropped when an excuse occurs, and they accept annulment and substitution in themselves. And the obligation of faith is not dropped from him. So when he believes after becoming intelligent, it will be obligatory, and all rulings that apply to believers will apply, such as separation between him and his polytheist wife, deprivation of inheritance from her, and inheritance between him and his Muslim relatives. And the obligation of performance is removed from him, meaning the compulsion to believe is removed, so if he did not affirm during childhood or recite the Shahada after puberty, he is not considered an apostate. The summary is that responsibility is removed from him. The conclusion about minority is that all rulings that can be forgiven are dropped from him, i.e., all acts of worship and punishments except apostasy, and it is valid from him if he does it by himself without responsibility and claim. And for him is that which has no liability, i.e., it is permissible for the minor to accept property in which there is no harm, like gifts and charity and similar pure benefits, and this has been mentioned in the discussion of capacity. Then his statement: 'So he is not deprived of inheritance by killing according to us' is a branch of his statement that responsibility is removed from him, meaning if a minor kills his testator intentionally or accidentally, he is not deprived of his inheritance because it is a punishment and responsibility, unlike the case of disbelief and slavery. He answered with his statement: 'Unlike disbelief and slavery' because deprivation of inheritance is not incurred by the minor, and it is argued that if that is the case, he should not be deprived of inheritance by them; this is not from the category of penalty but due to lack of capacity, since disbelief and slavery contradict the capacity of inheritance from a free Muslim. And insanity is joined to his statement 'minority', and it is a disease that takes hold of the brain such that it impels actions contrary to reason without weakness in its limbs, and it drops...
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the legal effects of minority (sighar) as an accidental cause ('arid) affecting legal capacity. The commentator explains that minority, like insanity, initially suspends many obligations. The key principle is that a minor is not held responsible for acts of worship (prayer, fasting), hudud punishments, and expiations because these can be dropped due to an excuse. However, the obligation of faith (iman) is never dropped; if the minor reaches the age of discernment (tamyiz) and believes, it counts as an obligation fulfilled, and all marital and inheritance consequences apply. The minor cannot be forced to believe; the obligation of performance is lifted. A summary is given: all that can be forgiven (except apostasy) is removed from the minor, but if he performs an act voluntarily without compulsion, it is valid. The minor may accept pure benefits like gifts and charity. A specific furu' is discussed: if a minor kills his testator (the person from whom he inherits), he is not deprived of inheritance because that would be a punishment, and punishment is dropped from the minor. This is contrasted with an adult who would be deprived. The passage distinguishes this from disbelief and slavery, which prevent inheritance due to lack of capacity (ahliyyat al-irth), not as a penalty. Finally, insanity is defined as a disease affecting the brain that leads to irrational actions.

Key Terms
الصغر (al-sighar): Minority; the state of being a minor before puberty. It is an accidental cause ('arid) that suspends legal capacity for obligations and punishments.
الأهلية القاصرة (al-ahliyyat al-qasira): Deficient capacity; the capacity of a discerning minor (mumayyiz) who can perform some actions validly but is not held liable for obligatory acts.
العهدة (al-uhda): Legal responsibility or liability for actions; specifically the accountability for fulfilling obligations and penalties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the obligation of faith (iman) for a minor?
A) It is dropped entirely like other obligations.
B) It is not dropped; if he believes after discernment, it is obligatory.
C) It is delayed until puberty.
D) It is only required if his parents are Muslim.

Key Takeaway
Minority is an accidental cause that drops all obligations and punishments except faith, and a discerning minor's acts are valid but not obligatory.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
15 min
Removal of Responsibility (Uhdah) from Minors and Insane Persons
Explaining the removal of responsibility from minors and insane persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that obligations bearing the possibility of dropping are removed from minors and insane persons, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding congenital insanity.

Core Idea
Minors and insane are not liable for punitive obligations but remain bound by essential duties and financial liabilities.

In Hanafi usul, legal capacity (ahliyah) is the foundation for accountability. This passage examines how incomplete capacity removes responsibility (uhdah) for obligations that may drop, such as hudud and kaffarat, while preserving fundamental duties like faith. Understanding this principle clarifies numerous rulings on the legal status of minors and the insane.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key principle
Locate the statement that responsibility (uhdah) is removed from the minor and insane. Note which obligations are explicitly mentioned as dropping (hudud, kaffarat) and which are not (iman).
The phrase 'تُوضعُ عَنْهُ الْعُهْدَة' is central.
2
Distinguish between dropping and non-dropping obligations
Explain why hudud and kaffarat can drop (they are purely punitive or expiatory) while iman and financial liabilities cannot (they are foundational or compensatory).
Use the text's contrast between 'rights of Allah' and 'rights of servants'.
3
Apply the principle to specific cases
Work through the examples given: a minor's acceptance of gifts, killing of a testator (inheritance), and liability for damages. Confirm whether each falls under removal of uhdah.
The text explicitly says killing does not bar inheritance; damages are not removed.
4
Analyze the internal dispute on congenital insanity
Compare Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's positions on qada' for worship missed during congenital insanity. Identify the basis of each analogy (minor vs. temporary insane) and determine the mufta bihi.
The text states 'وَقِيلَ الاِخْتِلافُ عَلَى الْعَكْس' indicating variant reports.

عَقُوبَةٌ وَعُهْدَةً بالكفر وَالرِّقَ فَاجَابَ عَنْهُ بَقَوْلِهِ بِخِلَافِ الكُفْرِ وَالرّقِ لأنَّ حِرْمَانَ الْمِيْرَاتِ لَا يَسْتَحِقُهَا الصبى وَأفْرِدَ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّهُ إِذَا كَانَ كَذَالِكَ فَلا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُحْرَمَ عَنِ الْمَيْرَاتِ بِهَا لَيْسَ مِنْ بَابِ الْجَزَاءِ بَلْ لِعَدَمِ الأَهْلِيَةِ إذَ الْكُفْرُ وَالرِّقْ يُنَافِي أَهْلِيَةَ الْمِيرَاثِ مِنَ المُسلِم الْحُرِّ وَالْجُنُونِ الْمُحْتَمِلَةُ للسقُوطِ لَأَصْحَانَ الْمُثْلِفَاتِ وَنَفَقَةِ الأَقَارِبِ وَالدِّيَةِ كَمَا فى الصبي بعَيْنِهِ وَكَذَا الطلاق وَالْعِتَاقَ وَنَحْوِهِمَا مِنَ الْمَصَارِ غَيْرِ مَشرُوع في حقه لكِنه إذا لَمْ يَمْتَدُ الْحَقِّ بِالنَّوْمِ عِنْدَ عَلَمَائِنَا الثلثة فَيَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ قَضَاءُ العِبَادَاتِ كَمَا عَلَى النَّائِمِ إِذْ لأخرَجَ فِي قَضَاءِ الْقَلِيْلِ وَهَذَا فِي الْجُنونِ الْعَارَضِي بِأَنْ بَلَغَ عَاقِلاً ثُمَّ جُنَّ وَأَمَّا فِي الْجُنُونِ الأَصْلِى بِأَنْ بَلَغَ مَجْنُونًا فَعِنْدَ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ هُوَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الصَّبَاحَتَّى لَوْ أَفَاقَ قَبْلَ مُضَى الشَّهْرِ فِي الصَّوْمِ أَوْ قَبْلَ تَمَامِ يَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ فِي الصلوة لايَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ الْقَضاءُ وَعِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ هُوَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْعَارِضِي فَيَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ الْقَضاءُ وَقِيلَ الاِخْتِلافُ عَلَى الْعَكْس ثُمَّ أَرَادَ أَنْ يُبَيِّنَ حَدَّ الْأَمْتِدَادِ وَعَدَمِهِ لِيَبْتَنِي عَلَيْهِ وَجُوْبَ الْقَصَاءِ وَعَدَمَهُ ولَمَّا كَانَ ذَالِكَ أَمْرًا غَيْرَ مَصْبُوطٍ بَيْنَ صَابِطَةٌ بِالحَرَج فِي كُلِّ الْعِبَادَاتِ فَقَالَ وَحَدُ الإِمْتَدَادِ فِي الصَّلَوَةِ أَن يَزِيدَ عَلَى يَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ. ولَهُ مَالاً عُهْدَة فیہ اور اس کے لئے وہ تصرف جس میں ہار نہ ہو یعنی میں کے لئے وہ تصرف ترجمه و تشریح کرنا جائز ہے جس میں اس کا ضرر اور نقصان نہ ہو کلابیہ قبول کرنا صدقہ قبول کرنا اور اسی طرح دوسری وہ چیز ہیں جن میں نفع محض ہے اس کا تفصیلی بیان اہمیت کے باب میں گزر چکا ہے۔ پھر منصب کا قول فَلا يُحْرُمُ عَنِ الْمِيْرَاتِ بِالْقَتْلِ عِنْدَه چنانچہ قتل کرنے کے جب سے ہمارے نزدیک وہ میراث سے محروم نہ ہو گا یہ اس بات پر تفریح ہے کہ نبی سے ہر قسم کی بار ذمہ داری (عہدہ) ساقط ہے یعنی اگر کسی میں نے اپنے مورث کو عمداً یا خطاء قتل کر دیا تو اس کی میراث سے محروم نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہ نوبت ہے (سزا) جس کا میں مستحق نہیں ہے واقدِرَ عَلَيْهِ الخ اس پر ایک اعتراض دارد کیا گیا ہے کہا گر ایسا ہی ہے تو کفر اور رقیت کی وجہ سے اس کو میراث سے محروم نہ ہونا چاہیے تو مصنف نے اس اعتراض کا جواب اپنے اس قول سے دیا ہے کہ بخلاف الكفر والرق لیکن کفر اور رقیت کا مسئلہ اس سے مختلف ہے کیونکہ کفر اور رقیت کیوجہ سے میراث سے محروم ہونا از باب میرات بطور جزاء کے نہیں ہے بلکہ وجہ یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں امور کی وجہ سے بچہ اہل نہیں رہتا کیونکہ کفر اور رقیت مسلمان آزادی کی میراث پانے کی اہمیت کے منافی ہے۔ والجنون اور جنون (۲) اس کا عطف الصفر پر ہے جنون ایک آفت اور مصیبت ہے جو دماغ میں داخل ہو جاتی ہے اس طور پر کہ وہ فعل دماغی انسان کو منتفی عقل کے خلاف کرنے پر آمادہ کر تا رہتا ہے مگر اس سے اعضاء بدن و قوی میں کوئی ضعف یا کمزوری واقع نہیں ہو جاتی۔ وتسقط به العبادات المحتملة للسقوط۔ اس جنون کے سبب سے سقوط کا احتمال رکھنے والی تمام عباد میں اس سے ساقط ہو جاتی ہیں لیکن دوسرے کا مال ضائع کرنے اور تلف کرنے کا تاوان اور اقرباء کا نفقہ اور دیت ساقط نہیں ہوتے جس طرح
A kind of etiquette: this imparts a degree of importance to performance, meaning limited capacity arises, perfect capacity does not arise because childhood remains, and it is an excuse for him. So by it those rulings drop that bear the possibility of dropping from the adult. After that, only those rulings drop from the child that bear the possibility of dropping from the adult, i.e., of the rights of Allah like hudud and kaffarat, because at the occurrence of the excuse they drop, and these rights in themselves bear the possibility of annulment and change. And the obligation of faith does not drop from him, so that when after being sane he brings faith, it will be counted as an obligation, and all rulings that become established for other believers due to faith become established for him, for example separation between him and his polytheist wife, and deprivation of inheritance from the polytheist wife, and the establishment of mutual inheritance between him and his Muslim relatives. And the obligation of performance is dropped from him, meaning the obligation to bring faith is dropped from him. So if in childhood he does not make verbal affirmation or recite the shahada before Muslims, after becoming adult he will not be considered a disbeliever. The summary of the statement is: the responsibility of the minor is dropped; the gist of the matter regarding the minor is that the obligations that bear the possibility of forgiveness, i.e., all hudud and punishments except apostasy, and the burden of their responsibility is dropped from the minor. And it is valid from him, meaning despite the absence of requirement of rulings and his responsibility for adherence to rulings, if he does it voluntarily it is valid. And for him is whatever has no liability, meaning it is permissible for the minor to do that in which no harm, like accepting gifts and charity and the like which are pure benefit; and this has passed in the discussion of capacity. Then his statement: so he is not deprived of inheritance by killing according to us, is a branching from his statement: that responsibility is removed from him. So if a minor kills his testator intentionally or unintentionally, he is not deprived of his inheritance because it is a punishment and a liability, unlike kufr and riqq. He answered it by his statement: unlike kufr and riqq, because deprivation of inheritance by the minor does not deserve it, and it was specified that if it is so, then he should not be deprived of inheritance by them; it is not from the category of retribution but due to lack of capacity, because kufr and riqq oppose the capacity of inheritance from a free Muslim. And junun is a conjunction to his statement saghar; it is a calamity that settles in the brain such that it incites the person to actions contrary to the dictates of reason without weakness in his limbs. And there drop by it the acts of worship that bear the possibility of dropping, but not the damages for property, maintenance of relatives, and diya, just as in the case of the minor. And similarly divorce and manumission and the like from the disposals are not legislated in his right. But if the period does not extend with sleep according to our three scholars, it is necessary for him to make up the acts of worship as for the sleeper. And this is in the case of temporary insanity, i.e., he reaches puberty sane then becomes insane. As for congenital insanity, i.e., he reaches puberty insane, according to Abu Yusuf he is like a minor, so if he regains sanity before the month passes in fasting or before completing a day and night in prayer, qada' is not necessary for him. And according to Muhammad, he is like the temporary, so qada' is necessary for him. And it is said the disagreement is the opposite. Then he intended to explain the limit of extension and its absence so that based on it the obligation of qada' and its non-obligation may be built. And since that is a matter not fixed by a fixed measure that would cause difficulty in all acts of worship, he said: and the limit of extension in prayer is that it exceeds a day and night. And for him is whatever has no liability, and for him it is permissible to do such action in which there is no loss, i.e., for the minor it is permissible to engage in such actions in which there is no harm or loss, like accepting gifts, accepting charity, and similarly other things that are pure benefit. Its detailed explanation has passed in the chapter on capacity. Then the author's statement: so he is not deprived of inheritance by killing according to us, is a branching on his statement that all types of responsibility are removed from the minor, i.e., if a minor kills his testator intentionally or unintentionally, he will not be deprived of his inheritance because it is a punishment that the minor does not deserve. An objection was raised: if so, then he should not be deprived of inheritance due to kufr and riqq. The author answered by his statement: unlike kufr and riqq. The matter of kufr and riqq is different because deprivation of inheritance due to kufr and riqq is not by way of retribution but due to the fact that due to these two matters the child is not eligible, because kufr and riqq are contrary to the capacity to receive inheritance from a free Muslim. And junun is a conjunction of saghar; junun is a calamity that enters the brain such that it incites a person to actions contrary to the dictates of reason without any weakness occurring in his limbs and faculties. And there drop by it all acts of worship that bear the possibility of dropping, but the compensation for causing loss to another's property, and the maintenance of relatives, and diya do not drop, just as in the case of the minor.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage deals with the legal capacity (ahliyah) of minors and insane persons, specifically the removal of responsibility (uhdah) for certain obligations. The author begins by explaining that a minor's capacity is limited; he is excused due to childhood. As a result, obligations that can potentially be dropped (like hudud and kaffarat) are removed from him. However, essential duties like the obligation of faith are not dropped; if he later becomes sane and believes, it counts as obligatory. Similarly, the obligation to perform acts of worship is not imposed on him during minority, but if he performs them voluntarily, they are valid. The passage then discusses that a minor may engage in transactions that are purely beneficial, such as accepting gifts and charity, without liability. A key ruling is that if a minor kills his testator, he is not deprived of inheritance because it is a punishment, and he is not liable for punishments due to his lack of capacity. An objection about kufr and riqq is addressed: deprivation of inheritance due to kufr or riqq is not by way of punishment but due to lack of eligibility. The passage then moves to junun (insanity), defining it as a brain affliction that leads to actions contrary to reason. Insanity, like childhood, removes obligations that can be dropped, but not financial liabilities. The text also covers the important internal Hanafi dispute regarding congenital insanity: Abu Yusuf treats it like childhood (no qada' if recovery is brief), while Muhammad treats it like temporary insanity (qada' required). The limit for extension in prayer is specified as more than a day and night. The overall theme is the legal principle that those lacking full legal capacity are not burdened with punitive or strictly devotional obligations, but remain liable for compensatory duties.

Key Terms
عهدة ('uhdah): Responsibility or liability for obligations; the text states that for minors and insane persons, 'uhdah is removed for obligations that bear the possibility of dropping.
صبي (sabi): A minor who has not reached puberty; his legal capacity is incomplete (ahliyah qasirah).
جنون (junun): Insanity, defined as an affliction of the brain that leads to actions contrary to reason without physical weakness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, if a minor kills his testator intentionally, what is the ruling regarding inheritance?
A) He is deprived of inheritance because it is a crime.
B) He is not deprived of inheritance because he is not liable for punishments.
C) He is deprived only if the killing was intentional, not if accidental.
D) He inherits only if the testator was a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the removal of 'uhdah from minors and insane persons applies only to obligations that can potentially drop, not to all duties, and financial liabilities remain intact.

Duration of Insanity and Qada of Worship
Defining durations for qada after insanity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi thresholds of insanity (hadd al-imtidad) to determine whether qada of prayers, fasts, and zakat is wajib upon recovery.

Core Idea
The obligation of qada after insanity depends on the duration relative to the specific act’s threshold: a day and night for prayer, a month for fasting, a year for zakat.

This lesson explores the Hanafi treatment of insanity as an excuse from ritual obligations. The scholars distinguish between temporary insanity (al-junūn al-‘āriḍī), which is like sleep and requires qada, and permanent insanity (al-junūn al-aṣlī), which gives rise to an internal difference. To operationalize this, the author defines a precise legal duration (ḥadd al-imtidād) for each act of worship, beyond which qada becomes obligatory upon recovery. The passage then applies these thresholds to specific scenarios involving prayer, fasting, and zakat, noting exceptions and the rulings of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of insanity
Identify temporary insanity (occurring after sanity) and permanent insanity (from birth or puberty). Understand that temporary insanity is akin to sleep: all missed acts require qada. For permanent insanity, there is a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
Temporary insanity: qada wajib. Permanent insanity: ikhtilaf.
2
Learn the general threshold (ḥadd al-imtidād) for prayer
For prayer, the insanity must exceed a day and a night (24 hours). The calculation differs: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf count total hours; Muhammad counts the number of missed prayers, requiring that prayers become six (i.e., exceed five prayer times) before qada is dropped.
Threshold: must exceed one full day and night.
3
Apply the threshold for fasting
For fasting, the insanity must cover the entire month of Ramadan. However, if the person was conscious on the first night and then insane for the rest, qada is not required (a sahih narration from Halwani). If recovery occurs during a day of Ramadan, recovery before noon triggers qada; after noon, no qada.
Full month coverage, with exception for first night.
4
Apply the threshold for zakat
For zakat, the insanity must cover the entire year. Abu Yusuf eases this by considering the majority of the year as the full year, to prevent hardship.
Entire year threshold; majority suffices per Abu Yusuf.
5
Evaluate the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf on permanent insanity
Abu Yusuf treats permanent insanity like childhood: if recovery occurs before the threshold (one month for fast, one day for prayer), no qada. Muhammad treats it like temporary insanity: qada is always wajib. Understand the practical consequence (thamarah).
No overall tarjih given; relies on Zahir al-Riwayah for fasting.

أَوْلِ لَيْلَةٍ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ فَاصْبَحَ مَجْنُونًا ثُمَّ اسْتَوْعَبَ بَاقِي الشهْرِ لا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ الْقَضاءُ وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ لان اللَّيْلَ لِأَيْصَامُ فِيْهِ فَكَانَ الإفَاقَةُ وَالْجُنُونُ فِيْهِ سَوَاءٌ وَلَوْ أَفَاقَ فِي يَوْمٍ مِّنْ رَمَضَانَ فَلَوْ كَانَ قَبْلَ الزَّوَالِ يَلْزَمَة القَضاءُ وَلَوْ كَانَ بَعْدَهُ لايَلْزَمُهُ فِي الصَّحِيحِ وَفِي الزَّكَوةِ باستغْراقِ الْحَوْلِ And this is regarding temporary insanity... Then he intended to explain the limit of duration... The limit of duration for prayer is that it exceeds a day and a night. But according to Muhammad, by consideration of prayer, meaning as long as prayers do not become six, qada is not dropped. By consideration of hours according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), such that if one becomes insane before noon and then recovers on the second day after noon, qada is not required according to them because by hours it is more than a day and a night. According to him (Muhammad), qada is required as long as it does not extend to Asr time such that prayers become six and enter the limit of repetition. For fasting, by covering the whole month, such that if he recovers in any part of the month, day or night, qada is wajib according to Zahir al-Riwayah. From Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani: if he was conscious on the first night of Ramadan and then became insane at dawn and covered the rest of the month, qada is not required, and that is sahih because the night is not for fasting, so consciousness and insanity are equal in it. If he recovers on a day of Ramadan, if before noon, qada is necessary; if after noon, it is not necessary in the sahih. For zakat, by covering the whole year, because it does not enter the limit of repetition until the second year enters, and Abu Yusuf considered the majority of the year as the whole for ease and to prevent hardship on the mukallaf.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage deals with the definition of the duration of insanity that excuses one from qada of missed acts of worship. The author first distinguishes between temporary (aarid) and permanent (asli) insanity. For temporary insanity, the ruling is like sleep: qada is wajib. For permanent insanity, there is a difference between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. Abu Yusuf treats it like childhood: if the person recovers before a month (for fasts) or a day and night (for prayers), qada is not required. Muhammad treats it like temporary insanity: qada is wajib. Then the author defines the limit of duration for prayer: it must exceed a day and a night. There is a difference in how to count this: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider total hours, while Muhammad considers the number of prayers missed (six prayers threshold). For fasting, the limit is covering the entire month of Ramadan, but with exceptions: if the person was conscious on the first night, then became insane and remained so for the rest, qada is not wajib according to a sahih narration. For zakat, the limit is covering the entire year, but Abu Yusuf considers the majority of the year as sufficient. This passage belongs to the furu' al-fiqh discussion of qada' al-ibadat and illustrates how usul principles like tahdid al-hadd are applied to actual rulings.

Key Terms
الجنون العارضی (al-junūn al-‘āriḍī): Temporary insanity that occurs after having been sane, such that recovery is expected.
الجنون الاصلی (al-junūn al-aṣlī): Permanent insanity present from birth or from the onset of puberty.
حد الامتداد (ḥadd al-imtidād): The legal duration that separates trivial from significant insanity, affecting qada obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One day
B) A day and a night
C) Six prayers
D) Two days

Key Takeaway
The obligation to make up missed acts of worship after insanity depends on precise temporal thresholds set by the Hanafi school, which differ for prayer, fasting, and zakat.

Junun's Effect on Fasting Qada and Zakat: Hanafi Usul Analysis
Rulings on junun's effect on qada of fasting and zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that junun covering an entire day or year voids the obligation of qada and identify the ikhtilaf regarding post-noon awakening and the majority-year concession.

Core Idea
Insanity spanning a full day or year eliminates the need to make up missed worship.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar addresses when junun (insanity) relieves a person from making up missed fasts and from zakat. The key is whether the entire period of obligation was covered by junun. For fasting, if consciousness returns before noon, qada is required; after noon, it is not. For zakat, the entire year must be covered, but Abu Yusuf allowed a concession for most of the year. Understanding these rulings reveals how Hanafi usul balances textual rules with practical ease.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline rule for fasting
If a person is insane for the entire day of Ramadan, no qada is required. The passage states that consciousness and insanity are equal in this regard.
This applies only when junun covers the whole day.
2
Note the exception for pre-noon awakening
If the person regains consciousness before noon (zawal), qada becomes obligatory. After noon, it is not obligatory according to the sahih (sound) view.
The dividing line is noon, not fajr or any other time.
3
Understand the talil (rationale) for the exception
The day is considered a single unit of worship. If junun covers it entirely, no qada; but if consciousness returns before the day is half over, the person had capacity for part of it, so qada is due.
This reasoning supports the pre-noon/post-noon distinction.
4
Recognize the ikhtilaf with Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad reportedly considered the number of prayers missed. If six prayers accumulate due to junun, qada becomes required regardless of the time of awakening. The Hanafi sahih view is the post-noon exemption.
The text declares the post-noon view as sahih (sound).
5
Apply the rule to zakat with the intra-Hanafi dispute
For zakat, the entire year must pass in junun for no zakat to be due. Abu Yusuf ruled that if most of the year is covered by junun, it is treated as the whole year for ease, but the general Hanafi position requires the full year.
Abu Yusuf's view is based on the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَكَانَ الإفَاقَةُ وَالْجُنُونُ فِيْهِ سَوَاءٌ وَلَوْ أَفَاقَ فِي يَوْمٍ مِّنْ رَمَضَانَ فَلَوْ كَانَ قَبْلَ الزَّوَالِ يَلْزَمَة القَضاءُ وَلَوْ كَانَ بَعْدَهُ لايَلْزَمُهُ فِي الصَّحِيحِ وَفِي الزَّكَوةِ باستغْراقِ الْحَوْلِ لأَنْهَا لأَتَدْخُلُ فِي حَدُ التَّكْرَارِ مَالَمْ تَدْخُلِ السَّنَةُ الثَّانِيَةُ وَأَبُو يُوسُفَ أَقَامَ أَكْثَرَ الْحَوْلِ مَقَامَ الكُلِّ تَيْسِيرًا وَدَفْعًا لِلْحَرَجِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُكَلْفِ
So consciousness and insanity in it are equal. If he becomes conscious during a day of Ramadan, then if it was before noon, qada is obligatory upon him; if after noon, it is not obligatory upon him according to the correct opinion. And regarding zakat, by the entire year passing, because it does not enter the limit of repetition until the second year enters. And Abu Yusuf considered most of the year as the whole year, for ease and to remove hardship for the responsible person.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on how junun (insanity) affects obligations of fasting and zakat. The source states that for fasting, if a person regains consciousness during a day of Ramadan, they must make up that fast if they awoke before noon; if after noon, no qada is required. This is the relied-upon view (sahih). For zakat, the entire year must pass in insanity for no zakat to be due; otherwise, if the person regains consciousness during the year, zakat becomes obligatory. Abu Yusuf ruled that if a person is insane for most of the year, it is treated as the whole year to ease the burden on the obligated person.

Key Terms
الجنون (al-junūn): Insanity; a legal impediment that removes responsibility for obligations.
القضاء (al-qaḍāʾ): Making up a missed obligatory act of worship after its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is insane for the entire day of Ramadan except for a brief moment after noon, what is the ruling on qada according to the sahih view?
A) Qada is obligatory
B) Qada is not obligatory
C) Qada is recommended
D) The day must be repeated with kaffarah

Key Takeaway
Junun covering an entire period of worship (day/year) removes the obligation of qada; only awareness before the midpoint changes that.

Definition and Legal Capacity of the Ma'tuh (Feeble-Minded)
Defines 'at-it'h and details its legal effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'at-it'h, distinguish it from insanity and childhood, and apply its partial legal capacity to determine which acts are valid or invalid.

Core Idea
The ma'tuh has basic intellect but lacks full contractual liability; valid worship and agency but invalid divorce without guardian.

This passage defines feeble-mindedness (al-'at'hu) as a post-puberty defect that impairs intellect without removing it entirely. The author then explains the legal capacity of the ma'tuh by analogy to a child with intellect (sabi ma'a al-'aql), listing acts that are valid (e.g., worship, accepting Islam) and those that are invalid (e.g., divorce, sale without guardian). The text also addresses an objection: why is the ma'tuh liable for property he destroys if he is like a child? The answer distinguishes between contractual guarantee ('uhdah) and tort liability (daman).

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and cause
Locate the definition of 'at-it'h in the text. Note that it is a post-puberty defect causing intellectual confusion and mixed speech. The cause (sabab) is a deficiency in intellect.
Compare with complete insanity (junun) where intellect is absent entirely.
2
Understand the analogy to a child with intellect
The text states the ma'tuh is 'like a child with intellect' (ka al-sabi ma'a al-'aql). Identify the shared characteristic: existence of basic intellect but vulnerability to error. This analogy governs many rulings.
The asl (original case) is the child with intellect; the far' (new case) is the ma'tuh.
3
Categorize valid and invalid acts
List the acts mentioned: valid (worship, accepting Islam, agency for others, freeing slaves, accepting allegiance) and invalid (divorce, freeing slaves without guardian?, sale/purchase without guardian, demands in agency, defect returns, litigation). Note the common thread: acts requiring 'uhdah (contractual guarantee) are invalid.
Freeing slaves appears twice; check consistency: it says 'freeing his slave' is valid in one line but invalid later. The text likely means freeing without guardian permission is invalid, but with permission? The passage needs clarification.
4
Analyze the objection and response on liability
The objection: if ma'tuh is like a child, why is he liable for property he consumes? The response distinguishes between 'uhdah (contractual, requires capacity) and daman (tort, based on property inviolability). The ma'tuh must compensate for damage even without capacity.
This is a key distinction in Hanafi law: property protection (ismat al-mal) is absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْعِتْهُ بَعْدَ الْبُلُوغ وَأَعَطَفَ عَلَى مَا قَبْلَهُ وَهُوَ آفَةٌ تُوْجِبْ خَلَلاً فِي الْعَقْلِ فَيَصِيرُ صاحبة مُخْتَلَط الكلام يَشْبَهُ بَعْضُ كَلامِهِ بِكَلامِ الْمُقَلَاءِ وَبَعْضَهُ بِكَلام الْمَجَانِيْنَ فَهُوَ أَيْضًا كَالْصَبَا فِي وُجُوْدِ أَصْلِ الْعَقْلِ وَتَمَكُنِ المَللِ عَلَى مَا قَالَ وقر كالصبا مَعَ الْعَقْلِ فِي كُلِّ الأحكام حتى لايَصْنَعُ صحةُ الْقَوْلِ وَالْفِعْلِ فَيَصحُ عِبَادَالة وإستلامهُ وَتَوَكَّلُهُ بِبَيْعِ مَالٍ غَيْرِهِ وإِعْتَانِ عَهْدِهِ وَيُصِيحُ مِنْهُ قُبُول البيَةِ كَمَا يُصبح من الصبى لكِنَّهُ يَصْنَعُ العَهْدَةَ فَلا يَصِيحُ طَلَاقَ امْرَاتِهِ وَلَا إعْتَالَ عِبْدَهِ أصلاً وَلا بَيْعَهُ وَلَا شراءً ، بِدُونِ إِذْنِ الْوَلِي وَلَا يُطَالِبُ فِي الْوَكَالَةِ يتسلِيمِ الْمَبِيْعِ وَلَا يُرَدُّ عَلَيْهِ بِالْعَيْبِ وَلَا يُؤْمَرُ بِالْحُصُومَة. ثُمَّ أَفْرِدَ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّهُ إِذَا كَانَ كَذَالِكَ فَيَنْبَغِي أَلا يُوَاخَذَ الْمَعْتُوْهُ بِضِمَانِ مَا سْتَهْلَكَهُ مِنْ الأمْوَالِ فَأَجَابَ عَنْهُ بِقَوْلِهِ وَأَمَّا ضِمَانُ مَا اسْتَمْلَكَهُ مِنَ الْأَمْوَالِ فَلَيْسَ بِعُهْدَةٍ وَكَوْنُة صَبِيًّا أَوْ عَبْدًا أَوْ مَعْتُوْهَا لاَيْنَا فِي عِصْمَةَ الْمَحَلُ يَعْنِي أَنَّ ضِمَانَ الْمَالِ لَيْسَ بِطَرِيْقِ الْعُهْدَةِ بَلْ بِطَرِيْقِ جَبْرِمَا قَوَتُهُ مِنَ الْمَالِ الْمَعْصُوْمِ وَعِصْعَتُهُ لَمْ تَزَلَ مِنْ أَجَلٍ كَونَ الْمُسْتَهْلِكَ صَبيًا أَوْ مَعْتُوهَا بِخِلَافِ حَقُوقِ اللهِ فَإِنَّ ضمَانَهَا إِنَّمَا يَجِبُ جَزَاءَ لِلأَفْعَالِ دُونَ الْمَحَالِ وَهُوَ مَوْقُوْفُ عَلَى كَمَالِ الْعَقْلِ وَيُوْضِعُ عَنْهُ الْخِطَاب كالصبي حَتَّى لا تجب عَلَيهِ الْعِبَادَات وَلَا تَثْبُتْ فِي حَقْهِ الْعُقُوبَاتِ وَيُولَى عَلَيْهِ كَمَا يُولَى عَلَى الْصَغِيرِ نَظَرًا لَهُ وَشَفْقَةٌ عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يُلْى عَلَى
And al-'at'hu after puberty, and it is attached to what preceded it. It is a defect that causes a deficiency in the intellect, so its owner's speech becomes mixed, some of his speech resembling the speech of sane people and some like the speech of madmen. So it is also like being a child in terms of existence of basic intellect and possibility of defect, as he said: it is like being a child with intellect in all rulings, so that soundness of statement and action is not prevented. So his acts of worship are valid, and his accepting Islam, and his being appointed as agent to sell property of another, and his freeing of his slave, and his acceptance of the pledge of allegiance is valid as it is valid from a child. But he cannot fulfill the guarantee (daman al-'uhdah), so the divorce of his wife and the freeing of his slave are not valid at all, nor his sale and purchase without the guardian's permission, nor can he be demanded in agency to deliver the sold item, nor can the item be returned to him due to defect, nor can he be ordered to litigate. Then it was pointed out to him that if it is so, then the ma'tuh should not be held liable for what he consumes of wealth. So he answered by saying: As for liability for what he consumes of wealth, it is not by way of guarantee (al-'uhdah), and his being a child, slave, or ma'tuh does not affect the inviolability of the property. Meaning that liability for wealth is not by way of guarantee but by way of compensation for what he has destroyed of protected wealth, and its inviolability is not removed because the consumer is a child or ma'tuh, unlike the rights of Allah, for their liability is only due as a recompense for actions, not for the property, and it depends on complete intellect. And the address is removed from him like a child, so that acts of worship are not obligatory upon him, nor are punishments established against him, and a guardian is appointed over him as a guardian is appointed over a child, out of consideration and compassion for him, and he is not appointed over...
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage defines 'at-it'h (feeble-mindedness) as a post-puberty defect that impairs intellect but does not remove it entirely. The ma'tuh's speech mixes sane and insane elements. The text analogizes the ma'tuh to a child with intellect (sabi ma'a al-'aql), meaning they have basic intellect but are vulnerable to error. As a result, their valid acts (like worship, accepting Islam, agency for others, and accepting allegiance) are sound because they have sufficient intellect. However, they lack the capacity for legal transactions that involve 'uhdah (liability/guarantee) — thus they cannot divorce, free slaves, buy/sell without guardian permission, nor can they be sued for delivery of goods or for defects. The text then addresses an objection: if the ma'tuh is like a child, why is he liable for property he destroys? The answer distinguishes between 'uhdah (contractual guarantee) and daman (tortious liability for damages). The latter is based on the inviolability of property, which remains regardless of the consumer's status. In contrast, rights of Allah (like acts of worship) are based on capacity and thus are suspended for the ma'tuh.

Key Terms
العته (al-ʿit'hu): Feeble-mindedness; a mental deficiency after puberty causing mixed speech and impaired judgment.
العُهْدَة (al-ʿuhdah): Liability or guarantee that arises from contractual obligations; the ma'tuh cannot fulfill this.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT valid from a ma'tuh without guardian permission?
A) Accepting Islam
B) Performing acts of worship
C) Selling his property
D) Being appointed as an agent to sell another's property

Key Takeaway
The ma'tuh has partial legal capacity: valid for acts requiring basic intellect, invalid for acts requiring contractual guarantee ('uhdah), but liable for property damage due to the inviolability of property.

The Ma'tuh: Definition and Legal Effects in Hanafi Usul
Defining al-ʿatah and its legal effects in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-ʿatah and apply the Hanafi rulings on the maʿtūh's legal capacity across acts of worship, transactions, and liability.

Core Idea
The maʿtūh is like a child with intellect: valid worship, but no liability undertakings without a guardian.

في هذا الدرس، نتعرف على تعريف العته عند الحنفية وأثره في أهلية الأداء. يشرح النص أن المعتوه كالصبي مع العقل، فتثبت له بعض التصرفات دون غيرها. سنحلل التفريق بين العهدة والضمان ونتعرف على الحكمة من إلزام المعتوه بضمان الأموال دون حقوق الله.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Definition of al-ʿatah
From the source text, locate the definition of al-ʿatah (العته). Note its characteristics: occurs after puberty, causes intellectual weakness, incoherent speech, but retains some rationality.
Distinguish from junun (madness) where intellect is completely absent.
2
Classify the Hukm of the Maʿtūh
The text analogizes the maʿtūh to a child with intellect (كالصبي مع العقل). This determines the legal capacity: partially addressable (ahlīyat al-adā’ nāqiṣa).
In Hanafi usul, this classification leads to specific rulings.
3
Extract Valid and Invalid Acts
From the text, list acts that are valid (e.g., ibadat, accepting Islam, agency, gifts) and invalid (e.g., divorce, manumission, sale without guardian).
The key principle is whether the act involves ʿuhdah (warranty causing potential harm).
4
Analyze the Distinction between ʿUhdah and Ḍamān
The text addresses an objection: why is the maʿtūh liable for property destruction? It clarifies that ḍamān (compensation) is not ʿuhdah but based on the inviolability of property.
Rights of Allah are excused due to dependency on intellect; rights of men are not.
5
Apply the Ruling to New Scenarios
Using the principles from this passage, determine the legal effect of a maʿtūh's actions in transactions, torts, and family law.
Remember: the maʿtūh cannot be a guardian over others (marriage, discipline, orphans' wealth).

بِخِلَافِ حَقُوقِ اللهِ فَإِنَّ ضمَانَهَا إِنَّمَا يَجِبُ جَزَاءَ لِلأَفْعَالِ دُونَ الْمَحَالِ وَهُوَ مَوْقُوْفُ عَلَى كَمَالِ الْعَقْلِ وَيُوْضِعُ عَنْهُ الْخِطَاب كالصبي حَتَّى لا تجب عَلَيهِ الْعِبَادَات وَلَا تَثْبُتْ فِي حَقْهِ الْعُقُوبَاتِ وَيُولَى عَلَيْهِ كَمَا يُولَى عَلى الصنفِي نَظرًا لَهُ وَشَفْقَةٌ عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يُلْى عَلَى غَيْرِهِ بِالإِنْكَاحِ والتَّادِيْبِ وَحِفْظِ أَمْوَالِ اليَتَامَى كَمَا أَنَّ الصَّبْيَ كَذَالِكَ
And al-ʿatah (intellectual confusion) after puberty: it is a condition that causes excess and light in the intellect, such that a person speaks incoherently; some of his words resemble those of sensible people, others resemble madmen. Since there is intellect but with weakness, he is considered in the ruling of one with intellect like a child with intellect, as the author said: 'like a child with intellect in all rulings.' Therefore his acts of worship are valid, his acceptance of Islam, his agency for selling another's property or freeing another's slave, and his acceptance of a gift are valid. But he is prevented from undertaking liability that entails harm; thus divorcing his wife, freeing his slave, selling or buying without permission are not valid. If he is an agent for sale, delivery cannot be demanded from him, nor can the price be returned due to defect, nor can he be appointed for litigation. Then an objection was raised: if so, the maʿtūh should not be held liable for property he destroys. He answered: 'As for liability for property he destroys, it is not by way of warranty; his being a child, slave, or maʿtūh does not affect the inviolability of property.' Meaning that liability for property is not via warranty but by way of compensating the protected property, and its inviolability is not removed because the consumer is a child or maʿtūh. Unlike the rights of Allah, for which liability is necessarily a recompense for actions, not property, and is dependent on complete intellect. The address is removed from him like a child, so obligations are not obligatory upon him, nor are punishments established. He is placed under guardianship like a child, out of consideration and compassion, and he does not have guardianship over others in marriage, discipline, or safeguarding orphans' wealth, just as a child is like that.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Anwar defines the legal category of al-ʿatah (ʿintah) and the maʿtūh (person afflicted with it). The author explains that ʿatah is a divine affliction (ʿāriḍ samāwī) that occurs after puberty, characterized by a weakness in the intellect that leads to incoherent speech, though the person retains some rational capacity. This places the maʿtūh in a middle position: like a child (ṣabī) with intellect (ṣabī maʿa al-ʿaql). As a result, the maʿtūh's acts of worship (ʿibādāt) are valid, and he can validly accept Islam, act as an agent for sale or manumission of another's property, and accept gifts. However, he cannot perform acts that entail liability (ʿuhdah) causing harm, such as divorcing his wife, freeing his own slave, or engaging in financial transactions without a guardian. If he is appointed as an agent for sale, the buyer cannot demand delivery from him nor return the item due to defect, and he cannot be sued. The text then addresses an objection: why is the maʿtūh still liable for property he destroys? The answer is that liability for damages (ḍamān) to property is not based on the concept of ʿuhdah (warranty/guarantee) but on the principle of compensating for destroyed protected property (māl maʿṣūm). The inviolability of property remains regardless of the consumer's capacity, unlike the rights of Allah (ḥuqūq Allāh) where liability is tied to the act and requires full intellect. Therefore, the maʿtūh is not addressed by divine commands like a child; obligations are not obligatory, punishments do not apply, and he is placed under guardianship. He cannot be a guardian over others for marriage, discipline, or orphans' wealth. This is a clear statement of Hanafi position, analogous to the child.

Key Terms
العته (al-ʿatah): A condition of intellectual weakness after puberty, causing incoherent speech but retaining some rationality.
المعتوه (al-maʿtūh): Person afflicted with al-ʿatah; has partial legal capacity.
العهدة (al-ʿuhdah): Warranty or guarantee that entails responsibility for defects or losses.
الضمان (al-ḍamān): Liability for property damage, based on compensating protected property, not warranty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling on the ma'tuh, which of the following actions is VALID without a guardian?
A) Divorcing his wife
B) Freeing his own slave
C) Accepting a gift
D) Selling his own property

Key Takeaway
The ma'tuh is like a child with intellect: valid in worship and agency, but invalid in transactions with harm, and liable for property damage due to inviolability of property.

Forgetfulness as a Legal Impediment in Hanafi Usul
Defines forgetfulness and its legal effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define forgetfulness (al-nisyān) according to Hanafi usul, distinguish it from madness, and apply its legal effect on obligation and performance to specific acts of worship and transactions.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness does not remove obligation but may excuse performance when predominant in worship.

Forgetfulness (al-nisyān) is a common human experience, but in Islamic law it has specific boundaries. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition of forgetfulness as a necessary ignorance due to a defect, separating it from madness and sleep. We'll explore when forgetfulness excuses performance and when it does not, particularly in rights of Allah versus rights of people.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi definition of forgetfulness
Locate the statement that defines nisyān as 'necessary ignorance of what one knew due to a defect (āfah)' and note how it excludes madness (junūn) and sleep (nawm).
The author distinguishes by 'without a defect' and 'with his knowledge'.
2
Classify forgetfulness as an impediment to performance not obligation
Understand that forgetfulness does not prevent the underlying obligation (wujūb) from attaching; rather, it may excuse the timely performance (adā') under certain conditions.
The text states: 'It does not prevent obligation in the rights of Allah.'
3
Recognize the exception of predominant forgetfulness
When forgetfulness is predominant (ghālib), it excuses performance in specific acts of worship like fasting, slaughter, and the first sitting of prayer.
The author gives examples and qualifies with 'predominant' to exclude normal forgetfulness.
4
Apply the rule to rights of people
Forgetfulness is never an excuse in huqūq al-ʿibād; if property is destroyed forgetfully, compensation (ḍamān) is obligatory.
This contrasts with huqūq Allāh where predominant forgetfulness may excuse.
5
Analyze the reasoning behind each example
For each excused case (fasting, slaughter, first sitting), identify the ʿillah (cause) that makes forgetfulness natural and thus excusable.
E.g., nature inclines to eating, fear in slaughter, resemblance to last sitting.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

آنجا نیکہ اور دوسری بہت سی چیزوں کا علم رکھتا ہو لہذا مصنفہ کے قول "لا جافة " سے جنون خارج ہو گیا اور ہمارے قول " مع علمه " کی قید سے نوم " اور الماء خارج ہو گئے وَهُوَلَا يُنَا فِي الْوُجُوْبِ فِي حَقَّ اللَّهِ تغالی اور یہ حقوق اللہ کے وجوب کو نہیں روکتا ہے لہذا انماز اور روزہ اس سے ساقط نہ ہوں گے جبکہ یہ ان دونوں کو بھول گیا ہو بلکہ اس کے ذمہ ان کی قضاء واجب ہو گی لكنه اذا كان غالباً كما في الصوم ليكن جن طاعتوں میں نسیان کا غلبہ ہو ان میں نسیان معاف ہے جیسے روزہ، ذبح کرتے وقت بسم اللہ کہنے میں اور سلام پھر دینا بھول کر قعدہ اولی میں وغیرہ یہ سب اس سے معاف ہیں پس روزہ میں نفس طبعا خود ہی کھانے پینے کی طرف مائل ہوتا ہے لہذہ ا نفس نے اس میں نسیان واجب کیا ہے بس معاف کمجا جائے گا اور اس سے اس کا روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا اور ذبیحہ جانور پرندہ میں ذریج ایک قسم کی ہیبت اور خوف پیدا کر دیتا ہے جس سے کہ طبیعت اس سے نفرت کرنے لگتی ہے ارو اس کی حالت متغیر ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے بسم اللہ پڑھنے سے طبیعت غافل ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے ہمارے نزدیک نسیان اس میں معاف ہے اور نماز کے قعدہ اولی میں ناسی کا سلام پھیر دیتا در حقیقت قعدہ اخیرہ سے غالباً الشعراہ پیدا کر دیتا ہے اس لئے بھول کر سلام پھر دیتا ہے اس لئے اس حد تک اس میں معافی ہے کہ سلام پھیر دینے کے بعد کسی سے کلام نہ کرلے اسکو مصنف نے اپنے قول غالبا سے مقید اس سے کیا ہے تا کہ سلام و کلام بھول کر بحالت صلوۃ اس سے خارج ہو جائے کیونکہ اس کا و توع اکثر و بیشتر اور غالبا نہیں ہوا کرنا کیونکہ نماز کی حالت اور اس کی جیت کذائی اس نسیان کو یاد دلانے والی ہوتی ہے لہذا ہمارے نزدیک یہ معاف نہیں ہے۔ وَلَا يُجْعَلُ عُدْرًا فِي حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ فَإِنْ أَتْلَف مَالَ إِنسَانِ نَاسِيًا يَجِبْ عَلَيْهِ الضمَانُ وَالنُّوْمُ عَطَفْ عَلَى مَأَقَبْلَهُ وَهُوَ عِجْرٌ عَنْ اسْتِعْمَالِ الْقُدْرَةِ تَعْرِيف بالحكم والآثرِ وَحْدَهُ الصَّحِيحُ أنه فِتْرَةٌ طَبِيعِيَّة تَحْدِث للأنسان بلا اختيار فَارْجَبَ تَاخِيْرَ الْخِطَابِ وَلَا يَمْنَعُ الْوُجُوْبَ فَيَثْبُتُ عَلَيْهِ نَفْسُ الْوُجُوب لاجل الْوَقْتِ وَلَا يَثْبَت عَلَيْهِ وُجُوبُ الأَدَاءِ لِعَدَمِ الْخِطَابِ فِي حَقِّهِ فَإِنْ انْتَبَة في الوقت يُؤدِى وَ إِلا يَقْضِي وَيُنَا فِي الاخْتِيَارَ حَتَّى بَطَلَتْ عِبَارَتُه في الطلاق والعتاق وَالإسلام وَالرِّدَّةِ فَلَوْ طَلْقَ أَوْ إِعْتَقَ أَوْ أَسْلَمَ أوْ ارْتَدُ فِي النّوْم لا يثبت حكم شَيْءٍ مِنْهُ وَلَمْ يَتَعَلُقُ بَقَرَاءَ بِهِ وَكَلامِهِ وَقَهْقَتِهِ فِى الصلوة حكم فاذا قرأ القائم في صلوتِهِ لَمْ تَصبح قِرَاءَتُه وَلَا يُعْتَدُ قِيَامَهُ وَرُكُوْعُهُ وَسُجُودُهُ لِصَدُورِهَا لَا عَنْ أخْتِيَارَ وَكَذَا إِذَا تُكلّم في الصلوة لم تفسد صلوتُهُ لأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِكَلامٍ حَقِيْقَةٌ وَإِذَا قَيْقَةَ فِي الصَّلوة لأيَكُونُ حَدَثًا نَاقِضًا لِلْوُضُوْءِ وَالاِعْمَاءُ عَطَفٌ عَلَى مَا قَبْلَهُ وَلَمَّا كَانَ مُسْتَبِها بِالْجُنُونِ عَرْفَهُ لِلإمْتِيانِ فَقَالَ وَهُوَ ضَرْبُ مَرَضِ وَقَوْتُ قُوَّةٍ يَضعَفُ الْقُوى وَلاَ يُزِيلُ الْحِجَى أَى الْعَقْلِ بِخِلافِ الْجُنُونِ فَإِنَّهُ يُزِيلُهُ وَهُوَ كالنوم حَتَّى بَطَلَتْ عِبَادَتُهُ بَل أشتد مِنْهُ أَى بَل الاعْمَاءُ أَشدُّ من النوم فِى قَوْتِ الاِخْتِيَارِ فَكَانَ حَدئًا بِكُلِّ حَالٍ أَي سَوَاءٌ كَانَ مُضطَجِعًا أَوْ مُتَّكِئًا أَوْ قَائِمًا أَوْ قَائِدًا أَوْ رَاكِبًا أَوْ سَاجِدًا بَخِلافِ النُّوْمِ فَإِنَّهَ لا يُنْقِصُ إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَ مُضطَجِعًا أوْسُتَكِنَا أَوْمُسْتَها لأمَا إِذَا كَانَ قَائِمًا أَوْ قَائِداً أَوْ رَاكِعًا أَوْ سَاجِدًا وَقَدْ يَحْتَمِلُ الاِمْتِدَادَ وَإِنْ كَانَ الأصْلُ فِيهِ عَدَمُ الاِمْتِدَادِ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَمْتَدَّ الْحق بالنوم في وُجُوبِ قَضاءِ الصَّلوةِ وَإِنْ اِمْتَدَّ فَيُلْحَقُ بِالْجُنُونِ فَيَسْقُطُ بِهِ الأَدَاءُ كَمَا فِي الملوة إذا زادَ عَلى يَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ بِاعْتِبَارِ الصَّلوةِ عِنْدَ مَحَمَّدٍ وَبِاعْتِبَارِ السَّاعَاتِ عِنْدَهُمَا كَمَا بَيْنَا فِي الْجُنُونِ. وَلا يُجْعَلُ عُدْرًا فِي حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ اور نسیان حقوق العباد میں عذر شمار نہیں کیا جاتا پس ترجمه و تشریح اگر کسی نے بھول کر کسی کا مال ہلاک کر دیا تو اس کا تاوان واجب ہو گا۔ والنوم (۵) اور قوم اس کا بھی عطف صفر پر ہے اور نوم یہ ہے کہ انسان اپنی قدرت کے استعمال سے عاجز ہو جائے یہاں پر قوم کی تعریف اس کا حکم اور اسکا اثر بیان کیا گیا ہے ورنہ اصل تعریف قوم کی یہ ہے کہ نیند ایسی سستی اور کسل کو کہتے ہیں کہ جو انسان میں (ممکن اور تعب کی وجہ سے غیر اختیاری طور پر پیدا ہوتی ہے فاوْجَبْ تَاخِيْرُ الْخِطَابِ وَلَا يَمْنَعُ الوُجُوبُ جس بناء پر سونے والے ( نائم) کے حق میں خطاب موخر ہو جاتا ہے مگر یہ نوم وجوب احکام کے لئے مانع نہیں ہوتی پیس ٹائم پر نفس وجوب وقت کی بناء پر ثابت ہو جاتا ہے اور وجوب اداء اس پر ثابت نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ اس کے حق میں خطاب محقق نہیں ہو تائیس اگر نیند سے وقت باقی رہتے ہوئے بیدار ہو جائے تو اداء کر لے ورنہ قضاء کرے - وَيُنَا فِي الاخْتِيَارِ حَتَّى بِطَلَت عِبَارَتُهُ في الطلاق الخ البترہ نوم میں اختیار سلب ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے ٹائم کا الفاظ طلاق، عشاق، کلمہ اسلام اور کلمه ارتداد کا استعمال کرنا باطل ہے پس اگر حالت قوم میں کسی شخص نے طلاق دیدی یا غلام کو آزاد کر دیا۔ یا اسلام لے آیا۔ یا مرتد ہو گیا تو ان میں سے کوئی علم بھی اس پر ثابت نہ ہو گا۔ حکم وَلَمْ يَتَعَلَّقَ بِقِرَالْتِهِ وَكَلامِهِ And forgetfulness (4) is also an 'ataf on sickness; it is a necessary ignorance of what one knew due to a defect. So without any affliction or illness, one becomes ignorant and unaware of some definitely known things, while still knowing many other things. Therefore, by the author's saying 'without a defect' madness is excluded, and by our saying 'with his knowledge' sleep and water are excluded. And it does not prevent obligation in the rights of Allah, so prayer and fasting are not dropped if one forgets them, but qada' is obligatory. However, if it is predominant as in fasting, then forgetfulness is excused in acts of worship like fasting, saying Bismillah at slaughter, and forgetting to say the salam in the first sitting of prayer. These are all excused. In fasting, nature inclines to eating, so forgetfulness is caused by the soul, thus it is excused and does not invalidate the fast. In slaughter, the animal creates fear, so the mind becomes heedless of Bismillah, hence forgetfulness is excused. In prayer, if one forgetfully says salam in the first sitting, it is similar to the last sitting, so it is excused as long as one does not speak after. The author qualified with 'predominant' to exclude forgetfulness that is not predominant in prayer, because prayer's state reminds one, so it is not excused. And it is not considered an excuse in rights of people: if one destroys someone's property forgetfully, compensation is obligatory. And sleep (5) is also an 'ataf on what precedes, and it is inability to use power, defined by its ruling and effect. The correct definition is that it is a natural lethargy that occurs to a person involuntarily. It necessitates postponement of address. It does not prevent obligation, so the obligation itself is established due to the time, but the obligation of performance is not established because the address is not addressed to him. If he wakes up during the time, he performs; otherwise he makes qada'. And it nullifies choice, so his expressions are invalid in divorce, manumission, Islam, and apostasy. If he divorces, frees, accepts Islam, or apostatizes during sleep, none of these rulings are established. And his recitation, speech, and laughter in prayer have no legal effect. If a standing person recites in prayer, his recitation is not valid, nor is his standing, bowing, and prostration counted because they occur without choice. Similarly, if he speaks in prayer, his prayer is not invalidated because it is not real speech. If he laughs in prayer, it is not an event that nullifies wudu'. And fainting is an 'ataf on what precedes. Since it resembles madness, it is defined for distinction: it is a kind of illness and weakness of strength that does not remove intellect, unlike madness which does. It is like sleep in that his acts of worship are invalid, but stronger than sleep in nullifying choice. So it is an event in every state, whether lying, leaning, standing, sitting, riding, or prostrating, unlike sleep which only nullifies when lying, leaning, or reclining, not when standing, sitting, bowing, or prostrating. And it may be prolonged, although the principle is that it is not prolonged. If it does not prolong, the ruling of sleep applies regarding obligation of qada' of prayer; if it prolongs, it is treated like madness, so performance is dropped as in prayer if it exceeds a day and night according to Muhammad, or according to hours according to the two, as we explained in madness. And it is not considered an excuse in rights of people: forgetfulness is not accepted as an excuse. So if someone forgetfully destroys another's property, compensation is obligatory. And sleep (5) is an 'ataf on what precedes. Sleep is that a person becomes incapable of using his power. Here the definition of sleep is given by its ruling and effect; otherwise the real definition is that sleep is a state of lethargy and laziness that occurs in a person involuntarily due to possible causes and fatigue. It necessitates postponement of address and does not prevent obligation. So the obligation itself is established due to time, but the obligation of performance is not established because the address is not actualized for him. If he wakes up during the remaining time, he performs; otherwise he makes qada'. And it nullifies choice, so his expressions are invalid in divorce, etc. In sleep, choice is removed, so using words of divorce, manumission, declaration of Islam, and apostasy is void. If a person divorces, frees, accepts Islam, or apostatizes while sleeping, none of these rulings are established. And his recitation, speech, and laughter in prayer have no legal effect. Thus, during sleep in prayer...

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Anwar deals with two legal impediments: forgetfulness (nisyan) and sleep (nawm). The author first defines forgetfulness as a necessary ignorance of what one previously knew due to a defect (such as illness or intoxication), distinguishing it from madness (which removes knowledge entirely) and sleep (which is not a true ignorance). The key ruling is that forgetfulness does not prevent obligation (wujub) in rights of Allah—so if one forgets a prayer or fast, it must be made up (qada'). However, if forgetfulness is predominant (ghalib) in certain acts, it is excused: examples include eating forgetfully while fasting (does not break the fast), forgetting to say Bismillah while slaughtering (the meat is still halal), and unintentionally saying salam in the first sitting of prayer (as long as one does not speak afterward). The reasoning is that human nature tends towards these forgetfulnesses, so shari'ah grants leniency. In contrast, forgetfulness in rights of people is never an excuse: if one damages someone's property forgetfully, compensation is obligatory. The passage then defines sleep as a natural involuntary lethargy. Its legal effect is that the address (khitab) of shari'ah is postponed—the sleeper is not obliged to perform actions during sleep, but the obligation itself remains attached to the time, so if he wakes up he must perform; if not, he makes up later. Sleep also nullifies choice (ikhtiyar), so any verbal acts (divorce, manumission, conversion, apostasy) performed during sleep are invalid. Additionally, recitation, speech, and laughter during sleep in prayer do not affect the prayer because they lack intention. Finally, fainting (i'ma') is similar to sleep but stronger: it nullifies worship and is always an event (naqid) for wudu', regardless of position, unlike sleep which only nullifies wudu' when lying down. Fainting also has the same rulings as sleep regarding obligation of prayer. The passage emphasizes that these rulings are based on the Hanafi usul principle that legal obligations are tied to capacity and address.

Key Terms
النسیان (al-nisyān): A necessary ignorance of what one knew due to a defect (afah), without complete removal of knowledge.
النوم (al-nawm): A natural involuntary lethargy that makes a person incapable of using his power.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a person who forgetfully says the salam in the first sitting of prayer?
A) His prayer is invalid and he must repeat it.
B) It is excused as long as he does not speak afterwards.
C) He must perform sajdat al-sahw regardless.
D) His prayer is valid but he must make up the rest.

Key Takeaway
Forgetfulness does not remove obligation but may excuse performance when predominant in acts of worship.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Sleep as a Legal Impediment: Effects on Obligation and Choice
Defines sleep and fainting and their legal effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sleep (al-nawm) and fainting (al-iʿmā') according to Hanafi usul, explain their effects on obligation, choice, and acts of worship, and distinguish between them in terms of nullifying wudu' and voiding worship.

Core Idea
Sleep removes choice and postpones the address, but does not prevent obligation; fainting is stronger and always an event for wudu'.

Sleep is a natural state that suspends human agency, but Islamic law carefully delineates its consequences. This lesson explains the Hanafi definition of sleep, its effect on the address of shari'ah, and how it nullifies choice in verbal acts. We also compare sleep with fainting, which is more severe in nullifying worship and wudu'.

Guided Path
1
Define sleep and its essential features
Extract the definition from the passage: sleep is a natural involuntary lethargy that incapacitates the use of power. Note that it is not a defect but a temporal state.
The author defines sleep by its ruling and effect, not just its nature.
2
Understand the postponement of address
Sleep does not prevent the obligation from attaching to the time, but it postpones the address (khitab) so that performance is not obligatory during sleep.
The text: 'It necessitates postponement of address. It does not prevent obligation.'
3
Analyze the nullification of choice
Sleep removes choice (ikhtiyar). Therefore, any verbal act performed during sleep (divorce, manumission, conversion, apostasy) is invalid and has no legal effect.
Examples: divorce, freeing a slave, accepting Islam, apostasy.
4
Evaluate sleep's effect on prayer
Recitation, speech, and laughter during sleep in prayer have no legal consequence; the prayer is not invalidated, and laughter does not nullify wudu'.
Because these actions lack intention and choice.
5
Compare fainting with sleep
Fainting is similar to sleep but stronger in nullifying choice. It is always an event (naqid) for wudu' regardless of position, whereas sleep only nullifies wudu' when lying down. Prolonged fainting is treated like madness.
The author distinguishes by saying fainting removes choice more severely.
