الصوم ليكن جن طاعتوں میں نسیان کا غلبہ ہو ان میں نسیان معاف ہے جیسے روزہ، ذبح کرتے وقت بسم اللہ کہنے میں اور سلام پھر دینا بھول کر قعدہ اولی میں وغیرہ یہ سب اس سے معاف ہیں پس روزہ میں نفس طبعا خود ہی کھانے پینے کی طرف مائل ہوتا ہے لہذہ ا نفس نے اس میں نسیان واجب کیا ہے بس معاف کمجا جائے گا اور اس سے اس کا روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا اور ذبیحہ جانور پرندہ میں ذریج ایک قسم کی ہیبت اور خوف پیدا کر دیتا ہے جس سے کہ طبیعت اس سے نفرت کرنے لگتی ہے ارو اس کی حالت متغیر ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے بسم اللہ پڑھنے سے طبیعت غافل ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے ہمارے نزدیک نسیان اس میں معاف ہے اور نماز کے قعدہ اولی میں ناسی کا سلام پھیر دیتا در حقیقت قعدہ اخیرہ سے غالباً الشعراہ پیدا کر دیتا ہے اس لئے بھول کر سلام پھر دیتا ہے اس لئے اس حد تک اس میں معافی ہے کہ سلام پھیر دینے کے بعد کسی سے کلام نہ کرلے اسکو مصنف نے اپنے قول غالبا سے مقید اس سے کیا ہے تا کہ سلام و کلام بھول کر بحالت صلوۃ اس سے خارج ہو جائے کیونکہ اس کا و توع اکثر و بیشتر اور غالبا نہیں ہوا کرنا کیونکہ نماز کی حالت اور اس کی جیت کذائی اس نسیان کو یاد دلانے والی ہوتی ہے لہذا ہمارے نزدیک یہ معاف نہیں ہے۔ وَلَا يُجْعَلُ عُدْرًا فِي حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ فَإِنْ أَتْلَف مَالَ إِنسَانِ نَاسِيًا يَجِبْ عَلَيْهِ الضمَانُ وَالنُّوْمُ عَطَفْ عَلَى مَأَقَبْلَهُ وَهُوَ عِجْرٌ عَنْ اسْتِعْمَالِ الْقُدْرَةِ تَعْرِيف بالحكم والآثرِ وَحْدَهُ الصَّحِيحُ أنه فِتْرَةٌ طَبِيعِيَّة تَحْدِث للأنسان بلا اختيار فَارْجَبَ تَاخِيْرَ الْخِطَابِ وَلَا يَمْنَعُ الْوُجُوْبَ فَيَثْبُتُ عَلَيْهِ نَفْسُ الْوُجُوب لاجل الْوَقْتِ وَلَا يَثْبَت عَلَيْهِ وُجُوبُ الأَدَاءِ لِعَدَمِ الْخِطَابِ فِي حَقِّهِ فَإِنْ انْتَبَة في الوقت يُؤدِى وَ إِلا يَقْضِي وَيُنَا فِي الاخْتِيَارَ حَتَّى بَطَلَتْ عِبَارَتُه في الطلاق والعتاق وَالإسلام وَالرِّدَّةِ فَلَوْ طَلْقَ أَوْ إِعْتَقَ أَوْ أَسْلَمَ أوْ ارْتَدُ فِي النّوْم لا يثبت حكم شَيْءٍ مِنْهُ وَلَمْ يَتَعَلُقُ بَقَرَاءَ بِهِ وَكَلامِهِ وَقَهْقَتِهِ فِى الصلوة حكم فاذا قرأ القائم في صلوتِهِ لَمْ تَصبح قِرَاءَتُه وَلَا يُعْتَدُ قِيَامَهُ وَرُكُوْعُهُ وَسُجُودُهُ لِصَدُورِهَا لَا عَنْ أخْتِيَارَ وَكَذَا إِذَا تُكلّم في الصلوة لم تفسد صلوتُهُ لأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِكَلامٍ حَقِيْقَةٌ وَإِذَا قَيْقَةَ فِي الصَّلوة لأيَكُونُ حَدَثًا نَاقِضًا لِلْوُضُوْءِ وَالاِعْمَاءُ عَطَفٌ عَلَى مَا قَبْلَهُ وَلَمَّا كَانَ مُسْتَبِها بِالْجُنُونِ عَرْفَهُ لِلإمْتِيانِ فَقَالَ وَهُوَ ضَرْبُ مَرَضِ وَقَوْتُ قُوَّةٍ يَضعَفُ الْقُوى وَلاَ يُزِيلُ الْحِجَى أَى الْعَقْلِ بِخِلافِ الْجُنُونِ فَإِنَّهُ يُزِيلُهُ وَهُوَ كالنوم حَتَّى بَطَلَتْ عِبَادَتُهُ بَل أشتد مِنْهُ أَى بَل الاعْمَاءُ أَشدُّ من النوم فِى قَوْتِ الاِخْتِيَارِ فَكَانَ حَدئًا بِكُلِّ حَالٍ أَي سَوَاءٌ كَانَ مُضطَجِعًا أَوْ مُتَّكِئًا أَوْ قَائِمًا أَوْ قَائِدًا أَوْ رَاكِبًا أَوْ سَاجِدًا بَخِلافِ النُّوْمِ فَإِنَّهَ لا يُنْقِصُ إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَ مُضطَجِعًا أوْسُتَكِنَا أَوْمُسْتَها لأمَا إِذَا كَانَ قَائِمًا أَوْ قَائِداً أَوْ رَاكِعًا أَوْ سَاجِدًا وَقَدْ يَحْتَمِلُ الاِمْتِدَادَ وَإِنْ كَانَ الأصْلُ فِيهِ عَدَمُ الاِمْتِدَادِ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَمْتَدَّ الْحق بالنوم في وُجُوبِ قَضاءِ الصَّلوةِ وَإِنْ اِمْتَدَّ فَيُلْحَقُ بِالْجُنُونِ فَيَسْقُطُ بِهِ الأَدَاءُ كَمَا فِي الملوة إذا زادَ عَلى يَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ بِاعْتِبَارِ الصَّلوةِ عِنْدَ مَحَمَّدٍ وَبِاعْتِبَارِ السَّاعَاتِ عِنْدَهُمَا كَمَا بَيْنَا فِي الْجُنُونِ. وَلا يُجْعَلُ عُدْرًا فِي حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ اور نسیان حقوق العباد میں عذر شمار نہیں کیا جاتا پس ترجمه و تشریح اگر کسی نے بھول کر کسی کا مال ہلاک کر دیا تو اس کا تاوان واجب ہو گا۔ والنوم (۵) اور قوم اس کا بھی عطف صفر پر ہے اور نوم یہ ہے کہ انسان اپنی قدرت کے استعمال سے عاجز ہو جائے یہاں پر قوم کی تعریف اس کا حکم اور اسکا اثر بیان کیا گیا ہے ورنہ اصل تعریف قوم کی یہ ہے کہ نیند ایسی سستی اور کسل کو کہتے ہیں کہ جو انسان میں (ممکن اور تعب کی وجہ سے غیر اختیاری طور پر پیدا ہوتی ہے فاوْجَبْ تَاخِيْرُ الْخِطَابِ وَلَا يَمْنَعُ الوُجُوبُ جس بناء پر سونے والے ( نائم) کے حق میں خطاب موخر ہو جاتا ہے مگر یہ نوم وجوب احکام کے لئے مانع نہیں ہوتی پیس ٹائم پر نفس وجوب وقت کی بناء پر ثابت ہو جاتا ہے اور وجوب اداء اس پر ثابت نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ اس کے حق میں خطاب محقق نہیں ہو تائیس اگر نیند سے وقت باقی رہتے ہوئے بیدار ہو جائے تو اداء باطل ہے پس اگر حالت قوم میں کسی شخص نے طلاق دیدی یا غلام کو آزاد کر دیا۔ یا اسلام لے آیا۔ یا مرتد ہو گیا تو ان میں سے کوئی علم بھی اس پر ثابت نہ ہو گا۔ حکم وَلَمْ يَتَعَلَّقَ بِقِرَالْتِهِ وَكَلامِهِ And forgetfulness (4) is also an 'ataf on sickness; it is a necessary ignorance of what one knew due to a defect. So without any affliction or illness, one becomes ignorant and unaware of some definitely known things, while still knowing many other things. Therefore, by the author's saying 'without a defect' madness is excluded, and by our saying 'with his knowledge' sleep and water are excluded. And it does not prevent obligation in the rights of Allah, so prayer and fasting are not dropped if one forgets them, but qada' is obligatory. However, if it is predominant as in fasting, then forgetfulness is excused in acts of worship like fasting, saying Bismillah at slaughter, and forgetting to say the salam in the first sitting of prayer. These are all excused. In fasting, nature inclines to eating, so forgetfulness is caused by the soul, thus it is excused and does not invalidate the fast. In slaughter, the animal creates fear, so the mind becomes heedless of Bismillah, hence forgetfulness is excused. In prayer, if one forgetfully says salam in the first sitting, it is similar to the last sitting, so it is excused as long as one does not speak after. The author qualified with 'predominant' to exclude forgetfulness that is not predominant in prayer, because prayer's state reminds one, so it is not excused. And it is not considered an excuse in rights of people: if one destroys someone's property forgetfully, compensation is obligatory. And sleep (5) is also an 'ataf on what precedes, and it is inability to use power, defined by its ruling and effect. The correct definition is that it is a natural lethargy that occurs to a person involuntarily. It necessitates postponement of address. It does not prevent obligation, so the obligation itself is established due to the time, but the obligation of performance is not established because the address is not addressed to him. If he wakes up during the time, he performs; otherwise he makes qada'. And it nullifies choice, so his expressions are invalid in divorce, manumission, Islam, and apostasy. If he divorces, frees, accepts Islam, or apostatizes during sleep, none of these rulings are established. And his recitation, speech, and laughter in prayer have no legal effect. If a standing person recites in prayer, his recitation is not valid, nor is his standing, bowing, and prostration counted because they occur without choice. Similarly, if he speaks in prayer, his prayer is not invalidated because it is not real speech. If he laughs in prayer, it is not an event that nullifies wudu'. And fainting is an 'ataf on what precedes. Since it resembles madness, it is defined for distinction: it is a kind of illness and weakness of strength that does not remove intellect, unlike madness which does. It is like sleep in that his acts of worship are invalid, but stronger than sleep in nullifying choice. So it is an event in every state, whether lying, leaning, standing, sitting, riding, or prostrating, unlike sleep which only nullifies when lying, leaning, or reclining, not when standing, sitting, bowing, or prostrating. And it may be prolonged, although the principle is that it is not prolonged. If it does not prolong, the ruling of sleep applies regarding obligation of qada' of prayer; if it prolongs, it is treated like madness, so performance is dropped as in prayer if it exceeds a day and night according to Muhammad, or according to hours according to the two, as we explained in madness. And it is not considered an excuse in rights of people: forgetfulness is not accepted as an excuse. So if someone forgetfully destroys another's property, compensation is obligatory. And sleep (5) is an 'ataf on what precedes. Sleep is that a person becomes incapable of using his power. Here the definition of sleep is given by its ruling and effect; otherwise the real definition is that sleep is a state of lethargy and laziness that occurs in a person involuntarily due to possible causes and fatigue. It necessitates postponement of address and does not prevent obligation. So the obligation itself is established due to time, but the obligation of performance is not established because the address is not actualized for him. If he wakes up during the remaining time, he performs; otherwise he makes qada'. And it nullifies choice, so his expressions are invalid in divorce, etc. In sleep, choice is removed, so using words of divorce, manumission, declaration of Islam, and apostasy is void. If a person divorces, frees, accepts Islam, or apostatizes while sleeping, none of these rulings are established. And his recitation, speech, and laughter in prayer have no legal effect. Thus, during sleep in prayer...

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Anwar deals with two legal impediments: forgetfulness (nisyan) and sleep (nawm). The author first defines forgetfulness as a necessary ignorance of what one previously knew due to a defect (such as illness or intoxication), distinguishing it from madness (which removes knowledge entirely) and sleep (which is not a true ignorance). The key ruling is that forgetfulness does not prevent obligation (wujub) in rights of Allah—so if one forgets a prayer or fast, it must be made up (qada'). However, if forgetfulness is predominant (ghalib) in certain acts, it is excused: examples include eating forgetfully while fasting (does not break the fast), forgetting to say Bismillah while slaughtering (the meat is still halal), and unintentionally saying salam in the first sitting of prayer (as long as one does not speak afterward). The reasoning is that human nature tends towards these forgetfulnesses, so shari'ah grants leniency. In contrast, forgetfulness in rights of people is never an excuse: if one damages someone's property forgetfully, compensation is obligatory. The passage then defines sleep as a natural involuntary lethargy. Its legal effect is that the address (khitab) of shari'ah is postponed—the sleeper is not obliged to perform actions during sleep, but the obligation itself remains attached to the time, so if he wakes up he must perform; if not, he makes up later. Sleep also nullifies choice (ikhtiyar), so any verbal acts (divorce, manumission, conversion, apostasy) performed during sleep are invalid. Additionally, recitation, speech, and laughter during sleep in prayer do not affect the prayer because they lack intention. Finally, fainting (i'ma') is similar to sleep but stronger: it nullifies worship and is always an event (naqid) for wudu', regardless of position, unlike sleep which only nullifies wudu' when lying down. Fainting also has the same rulings as sleep regarding obligation of prayer. The passage emphasizes that these rulings are based on the Hanafi usul principle that legal obligations are tied to capacity and address.

Key Terms
النسیان (al-nisyān): A necessary ignorance of what one knew due to a defect (afah), without complete removal of knowledge.
النوم (al-nawm): A natural involuntary lethargy that makes a person incapable of using his power.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a divorce pronounced during sleep?
A) The divorce is valid because words were uttered.
B) The divorce is invalid because sleep nullifies choice.
C) The divorce is valid if the sleeping person had previously intended to divorce.
D) The divorce is suspended until the person wakes up.

Key Takeaway
Sleep removes choice and postpones the address, but does not prevent obligation; fainting is stronger and always an event for wudu'.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
The Legal Definition and Rulings of Unconsciousness (Ighma)
Defines ighma and discusses its effect on wudu and prayer obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ighma, distinguish it from sleep and insanity, state its effect on wudu, and apply the Hanafi ruling on prayer qada when ighma is extended or not.

Core Idea
Ighma nullifies wudu in all states but only drops the duty of immediate prayer if it extends beyond a day and night.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwaar defines the legal disability of unconsciousness (ighma) and distinguishes it from sleep and insanity. It explains that ighma is a hadath that nullifies wudu regardless of position, unlike sleep which has conditions. It then addresses the critical question of when ighma excuses missed prayers, presenting the Hanafi position based on the actions of Companions and istihsan, in contrast to the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Define ighma using the text's criteria
Identify the two key characteristics: ighma is a kind of illness that weakens the faculties but does not remove intellect. Contrast with insanity which removes intellect.
The author defines ighma separately because it resembles insanity but differs in the preservation of intellect.
2
Compare ighma to sleep regarding wudu nullification
Note that ighma is a hadath in every state (standing, sitting, lying, leaning, prostrating), while sleep only nullifies wudu when the person is reclining or leaning on something that if removed would cause a fall.
Ighma is stronger than sleep in loss of choice, hence it nullifies wudu universally.
3
Understand the dispute on prayer obligation
Trace the Hanafi differentiation: if ighma is not extended (less than a day and night), it is annexed to sleep and qada is required; if extended beyond a day and night, it is like insanity and the duty of immediate performance (ada) drops. Compare with Shafi'i who says any complete prayer time missed drops qada.
Imam Muhammad says extension means exceeding a day and night; the two masters (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider the number of hours.
4
Analyze the istihsan argument
Examine how the Comapnions' actions (Ammar ibn Yasir made up after a day and night; Ibn Umar did not after longer) provide the basis for distinguishing extension. Then note that for fasting, even if ighma extends the whole month, qada is still required because extension is rare; by priority, it is even rarer for zakat to span a year.
Istihsan overrides a general principle because of the specific precedent from the Companions.

حالت میں سو گیا تو جا قض وضوء نہیں ہے۔ وَقَدْ يَحْتَمِلُ الإمتداد البتہ یہ بے ہوشی کبھی زیر تک [؟] محمد ہو جاتی ہے اگر چہ اصل اس میں یہی ہے کہ محمد نہیں ہوتی پس اگر بے ہوشی ممتد نہ ہو تو وہ نیند کے ساتھ ملحق کردی جائے گی نماز کے واجب ہونے کے حق میں اور اگر محمد ہو گئی تو اس کو جنون کا حکم دے دیا جاتا ہے فَيَسْقُطُ بِهِ الْآدَاءُ كَمَا فِي الصَّلَوَةِ إِذَا زَادَ عَلى يَوْم وَلَيْلَةٍ پس اگر ایک رات ایک دن سے تجاوز کر جائے تو نماز کا وجوب اداء اس سے ساقط ہو جائے گا البتہ امام محمد کے نزدیک ایک دن ایک رات ہے زائد ہونا نماز کے اعتبار سے ہے اور شیخین کے نزدیک گھنٹوں کے لحاظ سے جیسا کہ ہم نے جنون میں بیان کر دیا ہے۔ وَعِنْدَ الشَّافَعِي إِذا أُغْمِيَ عَلَيْهِ وَقْت صَلَوَةٍ كَامِلَةٍ لاَيَجِبُ الْقَضاءُ وَلَكِنا اسْتِحْسَبَنَّا بِالْفَرْقِ بَيْنَ الاِمْتِدَادِ وَعَدَمِهِ لأَنَّ عَمَّار بن ياسر أُعْمِيَ عَلَيْهِ يَوْمًا وَلَيْلَةً فَقَضى الصلوة وابْن عُمرَ أغْمِيَ عَلَيْهِ أكْثَرَ مِنْ يَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ فَلَمْ يَقْضِ الصَّلوةَ وَابْتِدَادُهُ فِي الصَّوْمِ نَادِرٌ فَلاَ يُعْتَبَرُ حَتَّى لَوْ أُغْمِيَ عَلَيْهِ فِي جَمِيعِ الشهْرِ ثُمَّ أَفَاقَ بَعْدَ مَصْيِهِ يَلْزَمُهُ الْقَضَاءُ وَإِذَا كَانَ اِمْتِدَادُهُ فِي الصُّوْمِ نَادِرًا فَفِيُّ الرَّكُوةِ أَوْلى أَنْ يَنْدَرَ اسْتِفْرَاتُهُ الحَوْلَ
And [the ruling of] unconsciousness: this is also an addition to the previous disability. Since ighma resembles insanity, the author defined it separately: "It is a kind of illness and loss of strength that weakens the faculties but does not remove intellect." Contrary to insanity which removes intellect. Ighma is like sleep in that all speech during it is void; indeed it is stronger than sleep in loss of choice. So it is a hadath in every state, so it nullifies wudu in all states: standing, sitting, lying on side, leaning, in prostration, etc., unlike sleep which nullifies only when lying on side or leaning on something that if removed the person would fall. When ighma does not extend, it is annexed to sleep regarding prayer obligation; if it extends (controversy: Imam Muhammad says exceeding a day and night regarding prayer, the two masters say by hours), then it drops the duty of performance (ada) like insanity. According to Shafi'i, if one is unconscious for a complete prayer time, qada is not obligatory. But we (Hanafis) made istihsan by differentiating between extended and non-extended, because Ammar ibn Yasir was unconscious for a day and night and made up prayers, while Ibn Umar was unconscious for more and did not make up. Its extension in fasting is rare, so if one is unconscious for a whole month, qada is still obligatory. If extension in fasting is rare, then in zakat it is even more rare to extend for a year.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage defines ighma (unconsciousness) as a legal disability. The author first distinguishes it from insanity: ighma weakens the senses but does not remove intellect, while insanity removes intellect. Ighma is treated like sleep in that both involve loss of volition, but ighma is stricter: it nullifies wudu in all positions, while sleep only nullifies when the person is reclining or leaning. The passage then addresses the effect of ighma on prayer obligation: if ighma is brief (not extended), it is like sleep and does not drop the obligation; if it extends beyond a day and night (by Imam Muhammad's view) or a certain number of hours (by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), it is like insanity and drops the duty to perform the prayer on time, but qada may still be required. A dispute with Shafi'i is presented: Shafi'i holds that unconsciousness for one complete prayer time drops qada altogether. The Hanafi response uses istihsan to differentiate between extended and non-extended ighma, citing the actions of the Companions Ammar ibn Yasir (who made up after a day and night) and Ibn Umar (who did not make up after longer). For fasting, even if ighma extends the whole month, qada is still required because such extension is rare; and by priority, if it rarely extends a month, it almost never extends a full year for zakat.

Key Terms
إغماء (ighma): A state of unconsciousness due to illness where strength is lost but intellect remains
جنون (junun): Insanity that removes intellect entirely
حدث (hadath): Legal impurity that nullifies wudu

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person is unconscious for 12 hours and misses one prayer, is qada (making up the prayer) obligatory?
A) Yes, because the unconsciousness was not extended beyond a day and night.
B) No, because any complete prayer time missed due to unconsciousness drops qada.
C) Yes, because unconsciousness always requires qada regardless of duration.
D) No, because unconsciousness is like insanity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan based on the Companions' actions to distinguish between short and extended unconsciousness, affecting whether missed prayers must be made up.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Slavery (Riq) as a Legal Disability: Definition and Distinction from Ownership
Defines riq as a legal disability and distinguishes it from ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define riq as a legal disability, state its characteristics (indivisibility, origin as punishment, persistence after Islam), and distinguish it from ownership (milk).

Core Idea
Slavery (riq) is a legal disability, not physical; it is indivisible because it is a right of Allah, unlike ownership which can be partial.

In this passage, the author explains the nature of slavery (riq) as a legal disability (ʻujr ḥukmī). He clarifies that riq is not based on physical incapacity but on a legal status imposed as punishment for disbelief. The passage also distinguishes riq from ownership (milk), highlighting that riq is indivisible while milk can be partial. This distinction has significant consequences for legal transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its classification
Recognize that riq is defined as a legal disability (ʻujr ḥukmī) — a status that hinders the slave from performing legal transactions, regardless of physical ability.
The author explicitly states that the slave is 'incapable of transactions' even if physically stronger.
2
Understand the cause (sabab) and persistence
Riq is originally established on disbelievers as punishment for arrogance. However, once established, it persists even if the slave converts to Islam and is inherited by children. Emancipation is the only way to remove it.
Compare with kharaj: initially on disbelievers but continues after Muslim purchase.
3
Compare with ownership (milk)
Ownership is a right of the slave (the owner's right over the slave) and can be partial: a slave can be sold to two persons, or half of a slave can be sold. Riq is a right of Allah and is indivisible — a person cannot be 'partly a slave'.
The text uses consensus (ijma) on selling half a slave to illustrate divisibility of milk.
4
Analyze the analogy to kharaj
The author draws a parallel between the persistence of riq and kharaj land tax: both are initially imposed on disbelievers but remain after Islam. This analogy reinforces that riq's continuation is a legal matter, not tied to the original punishment.
This is an example of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in usul al-fiqh.
5
Reflect on the implications
Because riq is a legal disability, a slave cannot own property, enter contracts, or perform independent transactions. This affects many subsidiary rulings (furu') such as the slave's capacity for testimony, marriage, and business.
The definition serves as a basis for deriving rulings in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالرِّقَ عَطْف عَلَى مَا قَبْلَهُ وَهُوَ عِجْرٌ حُكْمِي أَن بِحُكْم الشرْعِ وَهُوَ عَاجِرُ لا يَقْدِرُ التَّصَرُّفَاتِ وَإِنْ كَانَ بِحَسَبِ الْحِس أَقْوى وَأَجْسَمُ مِنَ الْحُرِّ شَرِعَ جَزَاءً عَلَى الْكُفْرِ لأَن الكُفَّارَ اسْتَنْكَفُوا عِبَادَةُ اللهِ تَعَالَى فَجَعَلَهُمْ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَبِيْدَ عَبِيْدِهِ وَهَذَا فِي الْأَصْلِ أَنْ أصل وضعه وَابْتِدَائِهِ إِذا الرَّقية لآتَرِدُ ابْتِدَاهُ إِلا عَلَى الْكَفَّارِ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ ذلِكَ وَإِنْ أسْلَمَ بَقِيَ عَلَيْهِ وَعَلَى أَوْلادِهِ وَلَا يَنْفَكُ عَنْهُ مَالَمْ يُعْتَى كَالْخِرَاج لايُثْبُتُ ابْتِدَاءَ إِلا عَلَى الْكَافِرِ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ إِنِ اسْتَرَى الْمُسْلِمُ أَرْضِ خِرَاجٍ بَقِيَ عَلَى حَالِهِ وَلَا يَتَغَيْرُ وَإِلَيْهِ أَشْتَارَ بَقَوْلِهِ لَكِنَّهُ فِي الْبَقَاءِ صَارَ مِنَ الأُمُورِ الْحُكْمِيَةِ أَنْ صَارَ فِي الْبَقَاءِ حُكْمًا مِنْ أَحْكَام الشرْعِ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يُرَاعِي فِيْهِ مَعْنَى الْجَزَاءِ بِهِ يَصِيرُ الْمَرْأَ عَرْضَةً لِلتَّمْلُكِ وَالابْتِدَالِ أَى بِسبب هذ الرِّقْ يَصِيْرُ الْعَبْدُ مَحَلَا لِكَوْنِهِ مَعْلُوكًا وَمُبْتَزِلاً وَالْفَرْضَةُ فِي الأَصْلِ خِرْقَةُ الْقَصَابِ الَّتِي يَمْسَحُ بِهَا دُسُومَةً يَدِهِ وَهُوَ وَصنف لا يَتَجَزاءُ ثُبُوتًا وَدَوَالا لأنه حق الله تَعَالَى فَلا يَصح أن يُوصَف الْعَبْدُ بِكَوْنِهِ مَرْقُوقِ الْبَعْضِ دُونَ البَعْضِ بِخِلافِ الْمِلْكِ اللأَزِمِ لَهُ فَإِنَّهُ حَقَّ الْعَبْدِ يُوْصَفُ بالتَّجَزُئ زَوَالاً وَثُبُوتًا فَإِنَّ الرَّجُلَ لَوْ بَاعَ عَبْدَهُ مِنْ اثْنَيْن جاز بِالإِجْمَاعِ وَلَوْ بَاعَ نِصْفَ الْعَبْدِ يَبْقَى الْمِلْكُ لَهُ فِي النَّصْفِ الآخِرِ بِالإِجْمَاعِ وَهُوَ اعَمُ مِنَ الرّقَ اذْقَدْ يُوصَفُ بِهُ غَيْرَ الإِنسان من العروض دُونَ الرق.
And slavery (riq) is an addition to what preceded. It is a legal disability: by divine law, the slave is incapable of transactions, even though physically stronger and larger than a free person. It was legislated as a punishment for disbelief, because the disbelievers were arrogant in worshipping Allah, so Allah made them slaves of His slaves. Originally, slavery is only initiated upon disbelievers. Then after that, if he accepts Islam, it remains on him and his children, and he does not become free unless emancipated. Like kharaj land tax: it is only levied on disbelievers initially, then if a Muslim buys it, it remains. So in its continuation, it became a legal matter without regard to the original punishment. By this, a person becomes a subject for ownership and possession. The original form (al-farda) is a butcher's cloth with which he wipes grease from his hand. And it (riq) is a category that does not admit of partiality in establishment or removal because it is a right of Allah; so it is not correct to describe a slave as partly enslaved. Unlike ownership (milk) which is a right of the slave and admits of partiality: if a man sells his slave to two persons, it is permissible by consensus; if he sells half, ownership remains in the other half by consensus. And ownership is more general than slavery, as it can be applied to inanimate objects, unlike slavery.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage defines riq (slavery) as a legal disability (ʻujr ḥukmī). Even though a slave may be physically stronger than a free man, he is legally incapable of independent transactions. The author explains the origin of slavery as a punishment for disbelief, as the Quran indicates that disbelievers' arrogance led to their subjugation. Initially, slavery is only established on disbelievers, but once established, it persists even after Islam and is inherited by children unless emancipation occurs. The author analogizes to kharaj land tax: it is originally imposed on unbelievers but continues after a Muslim acquires the land. In essence, in its continuation, slavery becomes a legal status without requiring the original punitive meaning. Importantly, slavery (riq) is indivisible in establishment and removal because it is a right of Allah; a person cannot be partially slave. In contrast, ownership (milk) is a right of the slave and can be partial—e.g., selling a slave to two persons or selling half. Thus ownership is more general than slavery, as it can apply to inanimate objects.

Key Terms
الرق (al-riqq): A legal disability that renders a person incapable of legal transactions, established as a punishment for disbelief
الملك (al-milk): Ownership: a legal right that can be partial and applies to both humans and objects

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is riq (slavery) considered indivisible?
A) Because a slave is owned by only one person.
B) Because it is a right of Allah.
C) Because slaves are physically incapable.
D) Because emancipation is impossible.

Key Takeaway
Riq is a legal disability, not a physical condition; it is an indivisible right of Allah, whereas ownership (milk) is a divisible human right.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Legal Definition of Riqq (Slavery) and Its Characteristics
Definition and characteristics of riqq with analogies and internal dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the legal definition of riqq, explain its origin and continuity, apply the rule of its indivisibility, distinguish riqq from milk, and compare Abu Hanifa's view on itq with that of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Riqq is a right of Allah, indivisible; milk is a right of humans, divisible.

This lesson examines the legal nature of riqq (slavery) as defined in the Hanafi school. We explore its origin as a punishment for disbelief, its continuity even after the slave embraces Islam, and its crucial property of indivisibility, which distinguishes it from ownership (milk). The lesson also delves into the internal Hanafi dispute regarding the divisibility of emancipation (itq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition of riqq
Find and state the definition given in the text: riqq is a legal incapacity (عجز حكمي) that renders a person unable to perform legal dispositions, regardless of physical strength.
Note the contrast between physical capability and legal incapacity.
2
Trace the origin and continuity of riqq
The text states riqq is legislated as a punishment for disbelief, but once established, it continues even after the person embraces Islam, like kharaj on land.
The origin is punitive, but continuity is a pure legal ruling.
3
Analyze the indivisibility of riqq
Riqq is a right of Allah, so it cannot be partial: a slave cannot be partially free. Provide examples from the text (selling a slave to two persons is allowed; selling half leaves ownership divisible).
Contrast with milk, which is divisible because it is a human right.
4
Distinguish riqq from milk and its effects
Milk applies to both humans and commodities; riqq only to humans. Milk can be divided in ownership; riqq cannot.
This distinction has practical implications in sales and inheritance.
5
Examine the internal Hanafi dispute on itq
The text presents the disagreement: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that i'taq (act of emancipating) is indivisible because it establishes freedom, while Abu Hanifa views it as removal of ownership and thus divisible.
This affects partial emancipation scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نور الانوار جلد سوم
اشرف الانوار شرح اردو في الصَّوْمِ نَادِرًا فَفِي الزَّكَاةِ أَوْلى أَنْ يَنْدَرَ اسْتِفْرَاتُهُ الْحَوْلَ وَالرِّقَ عَطْف عَلَى مَا قَبْلَهُ وَهُوَ عَجْزٌ حُكْمِيٌّ أَيْ بِحُكْمِ الشَّرْعِ وَهُوَ عَاجِزٌ لَا يَقْدِرُ التَّصَرُّفَاتِ وَإِنْ كَانَ بِحَسَبِ الْحِسِّ أَقْوَى وَأَجْسَمُ مِنَ الْحُرِّ شُرِعَ جَزَاءً عَلَى الْكُفْرِ لِأَنَّ الْكُفَّارَ اسْتَنْكَفُوا عِبَادَةَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى فَجَعَلَهُمُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَبِيدَ عَبِيدِهِ وَهَذَا فِي الْأَصْلِ أَيْ أَصْلُ وَضْعِهِ وَابْتِدَائِهِ إِذِ الرِّقَّةُ لَا يَرِدُ ابْتِدَاؤُهُ إِلَّا عَلَى الْكُفَّارِ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ وَإِنْ أَسْلَمَ بَقِيَ عَلَيْهِ وَعَلَى أَوْلَادِهِ وَلَا يَنْفَكُّ عَنْهُ مَا لَمْ يُعْتَقْ كَالْخَرَاجِ لَا يُثْبَتُ ابْتِدَاءً إِلَّا عَلَى الْكَافِرِ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ إِنِ اشْتَرَى الْمُسْلِمُ أَرْضَ خَرَاجٍ بَقِيَ عَلَى حَالِهِ وَلَا يَتَغَيَّرُ وَإِلَيْهِ أَشَارَ بِقَوْلِهِ لَكِنَّهُ فِي الْبَقَاءِ صَارَ مِنَ الْأُمُورِ الْحُكْمِيَةِ إِذْ صَارَ فِي الْبَقَاءِ حُكْمًا مِنْ أَحْكَامِ الشَّرْعِ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يُرَاعَى فِيهِ مَعْنَى الْجَزَاءِ بِهِ يَصِيرُ الْمَرْءُ عُرْضَةً لِلتَّمْلُكِ وَالِابْتِذَالِ أَيْ بِسَبَبِ هَذَا الرِّقِّ يَصِيرُ الْعَبْدُ مَحَلًّا لِكَوْنِهِ مَمْلُوكًا وَمُبْتَذَلًا وَالْعَرَضَةُ فِي الْأَصْلِ خِرْقَةُ الْقَصَّابِ الَّتِي يَمْسَحُ بِهَا دَسَمَةَ يَدِهِ وَهُوَ وَصْفٌ لَا يَتَجَزَّأُ ثُبُوتًا وَزَوَالًا لِأَنَّهُ حَقُّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى فَلَا يَصِحُّ أَنْ يُوصَفَ الْعَبْدُ بِكَوْنِهِ مَرْقُوقًا بَعْضِهِ دُونَ بَعْضٍ بِخِلَافِ الْمِلْكِ اللَّازِمِ لَهُ فَإِنَّهُ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ يُوصَفُ بِالتَّجَزِّي زَوَالًا وَثُبُوتًا فَإِنَّ الرَّجُلَ لَوْ بَاعَ عَبْدَهُ مِنَ اثْنَيْنِ جَازَ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ وَلَوْ بَاعَ نِصْفَ الْعَبْدِ يَبْقَى الْمِلْكُ لَهُ فِي النِّصْفِ الْآخَرِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ وَهُوَ أَعَمُّ مِنَ الرِّقِّ إِذْ قَدْ يُوصَفُ بِهِ غَيْرُ الْإِنْسَانِ مِنَ الْعُرُوضِ دُونَ الرِّقِّ. اور امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک جب کسی پر انماء طاری رہا نماز کے کامل وقت میں تو ترجمہ تشریح قضاء واجب نہیں ہوتی اور ہم نے ستحسن بجا ہے کہ اغماء محمد اور الماء غیر محمد کے در میان فرق کر دیں کیونکہ حضرت عمار بن یا سٹر ایک دن ایک رات بے ہوش رہے پھر جب افاقہ ہوا تو انھوں نے ان کی قضاء کی اس طرح حضرت ابن عمر ایک دن ایک رات سے زائد بے ہوش رہے تو انھوں نے نماز کی قضاء نہیں فرمائی۔ وامتداد في الصوم نادر لیکن روزہ کے سلسلے میں پورے ماہ بے ہوشی کا امتداد بالکل شاذ اور نادر ہے اس لئے (روزہ ساقط ہونے میں) اس کا اعتبار نہ کیا جائے گا حتی کہ اگر کوئی شخص پورے مہینے بے ہوش رہے پھر مہینہ گذر جانے کے بعد ہوش آ جائے تو اس پر قضاء کرنا واجب ہو گا جب روزہ میں اعتماء کا امتداد نادر اور شاذ ہے تو زکوۃ کے بارے میں تو بدرجہ اولی نادر ہے کہ کوئی پورے سال ہی بے ہوش رہے۔ والذق (۷) اور رقیت اس کا بھی صفر پر عطف ہے وھو عج مکھی اور وہ ایک عذر کی ہے یعنی بحکم شرع عجز ہے یعنی غلام اور رقیت شرعاً ایسا عاجز ہے کہ تصرفات پر قادر نہیں ہے اگر چہ بظاہر غلام جسمانی اعتبار سے
اشرف الانوار شرح اردو (120) نور الانوار جلد سوم بمقابلہ حر (آزاد) کے زیادہ جسم اور قوت والا ہے شرعَ جَزَاء عَلى الكُفْرِ جو کفر کی سزاء کے طور پر مشروع ہوتی ہے کیونکہ کفار نے اللہ تعالی کی عبادت سے اپنے کو روکا ہے اس لئے (اس کی سزا) میں اللہ تعالی نے ان کو اپنے غلاموں کا غلام بنا دیا ہے و مراقی الاصل اور یہی غلامی کی اصل حقیقت ہے یعنی غلامی کی اصل وضع اور ابتداء یہی ہے کیونکہ ابتداء میں غلامی کا ور دو صرف کفار کے حق میں ہوا ہے پھر اس کے بعد اگرچہ وہ (کافر) مسلمان ہی کیوں نہ ہو گیا ہو مگر رقیت پر باقی رکھا گیا ہے جس طرح مالک کا غلام ہے اسی طرح اس کی اولاد کا بھی غلام ہے اور یہ غلامی اس سے اس وقت نیک جدا نہیں ہوتی جب تک کہ اس کو آزاد نہ کر دیا جائے۔ جس طرح خراج (زمین کا ٹیکس) ابتداء میں صرف کفار پر لاگو کیا گیا پھر اس کے بعد اگر کسی مسلمان نے خراجی زمین کو خرید لیا ہے تو بھی خراج اپنی اصل حالت پر بر قرار رہتا ہے اور متغیر نہیں ہو تا مصنف نے اسی طرف اپنے اس قول میں اشارہ کیا ہے وَلكِنَّهُ فِي البَقَاءِ صَارَ من الأمور الحِكْمِيةِ لكن حالت بقاء میں یہ ایک مسلمی امر ہے یعنی بعد کی حالت میں جزاء کے معنی کی رعایت کئے بغیر شریعت کے دوسرے احکام کی طرح یہ بھی ایک محکم شرع کی بطور جاری رہتا ہے۔ به يَصِيرُ المَرْءُ عُرضة للتملك والابتدال اس غلامی کے سبب سے آدمی ملکیت اور حقارت کا نشانہ بنارہتا ہے یعنی اس غلامی کی وجہ سے مملوک اور ذلیل ہونے کا محل باقی رہتا ہے اور عرضہ در حقیت قصائی کے اس چیتھڑے کو کہتے ہیں کہ جس سے وہ ہاتھوں میں لگی ہوئی آلائش و چربی کو صاف کرتا ہے۔ وَهُوَ وَصَف لَا يَتَجَری اور یہ ایک ایسا وصف ہے جس میں تجزیہ نہیں ہوتا نہ ثبوت میں اور نہ زوال میں اس کے اندر تجربی نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ اگر ایک شخص اپنے غلام کو دو آدمی کے ہاتھ شروخت کر دے تو بالا جماع یہ بیع جائز ہے اور اگر اپنے نصف غلام کو فروخت کر دے تو دوسرے نصف پر اس کی ملکیت باقی رہتی ہے بالا جماع اور ملک عام ہے اور برقی اسکے مقابلے میں خاص ہے اور ملکیت رقیت سے عام ہے کیونکہ ملکیت کے ساتھ انسان کے علاوہ دوسری اشیاء بھی ملکیت کے ساتھ متصف ہو سکتی ہے مگر رقیت صرف انسان ہی کے ساتھ خاص ہے۔ كَالْعِتْقِ الَّذِي هُوَ ضِدُّهُ فَإِنَّهُ أَيْضًا لَأَيْقَبَلُ التَّجْزِيَةَ وَهُوَ قُوَّةً حُكْمِيَةٌ يُصِيرُ بها الشخص أهلاً لِلْمَالِكِيَّةِ وَالوِلايَةِ مِنَ الشَّهَادَةِ وَالْقَضَاءِ وَنَحْوَهِ وَكَذَا لِاعْتَاق عِنْدَهُمَا أَنْ عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوْسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ أَيْضًا لَا يَتَجَزَّأَ لَأَنَّ الإِعْتَاقَ إِثْبَاتُ الْعِتْقِ فَالْعِتْقِ أَثَرَهُ فَلَوْ كَانَ الاِعْتَاق مُجَتَزَيًا وَأُعْتِقَ الْبَعْضُ فَلَا يُخْلُوْا إِمَّا أَنْ يَثْبُت العتق في الكل فيلم الأثرُ بِدُونِ الْمُؤثرِ أَوْ الْمُؤثرِ بِدُونِ الأَثَرِ أَوْ تَجَزى الْعِتْقِ وَفِي بِعْض النسخ لَمْ يُوْجَدْ قَوْلَهُ أَوْ تَجَزَى الْعِتَقَ أَوْ تَحْزِيرُهُ لا يَخْلُو عَنْ تَمَرُّل يَخْلُوْعَنْ وَقَالَ أَبِي حَنَيْفَةَ إِنَّهُ زَالَةُ الْمِلْكِ وَهُوَ مُتَجَرى لإسقاط الرِّقَ أَوْ إِثْبَات الْعِتْقِ
Nur al-Anwar Volume 3, Ashraf al-Anwar Urdu commentary: Regarding fasting, it is rare, so regarding zakat it is more likely that its completion of a year is rare. And 'al-riqq' is coordinated with what preceded it, and it is a legal incapacity, meaning by Shari'ah law, and he is incapable, unable to dispose, even if according to physical strength he is stronger and larger than a free person. It is legislated as a punishment for disbelief because the disbelievers refrained from worshipping Allah Almighty, so Allah Almighty made them slaves of His slaves. This is in origin, i.e., the origin of its establishment and its beginning, because slavery does not apply initially except to the disbelievers. Then after that, even if he becomes Muslim, it remains upon him and upon his children, and he is not freed from it unless he is emancipated, like the kharaj (land tax) which is not established initially except upon the disbeliever; then after that, if a Muslim purchases kharaj land, it remains in its state and does not change. And to this the author pointed with his saying: 'But in continuation it became from the legal matters' because in continuation it became a ruling from the rulings of Shari'ah without considering in it the meaning of punishment. By it a person becomes subject to ownership and humiliation, i.e., because of this slavery the slave becomes a place for being owned and degraded. And 'al-'aradah' originally is the butcher's rag with which he wipes the grease from his hand. And it is a description that is not divisible in establishment or removal because it is a right of Allah Almighty, so it is not valid to describe the slave as being partially enslaved without part, contrary to ownership that is necessary for him, for it is a right of the slave and is described as divisible in removal and establishment. For if a man sells his slave to two persons, it is permissible by consensus; and if he sells half the slave, ownership remains for him in the other half by consensus. And it (milk) is more general than riqq, as it may describe other than humans among commodities, unlike riqq. And according to Imam Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, when unconsciousness (ighma) occurs upon someone at the complete time of prayer, the translation/explanation: qada' is not obligatory. And we have done istihsan to differentiate between unconsciousness of Muhammad (peace be upon him) and unconsciousness of other than Muhammad, because 'Ammar ibn Yasir (may Allah be pleased with him) remained unconscious for a day and a night, then when he regained consciousness, he performed qada' of the prayers. Similarly, Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) remained unconscious for more than a day and a night, and he did not perform qada' of the prayers. And the duration in fasting is rare: but in the matter of fasting, the duration of unconsciousness for a whole month is completely rare and unusual, therefore it (that it exempts from fasting) will not be considered. Even if a person remains unconscious for a whole month, then after the month passes he regains consciousness, then performing qada' becomes obligatory upon him. Since in fasting the duration of unconsciousness is rare and unusual, then regarding zakat, it is even more rare that someone remains unconscious for a whole year. And the number (7): And 'riqqiyyah' (slavery) is also coordinated with what preceded it, and it is a legal incapacity, and it is a legal excuse, meaning by Shari'ah law it is incapacity, i.e., a slave and slavery is a disability in Shari'ah such that he is unable to perform transactions, although apparently the slave is physically... Ashraf al-Anwar Urdu commentary (120) Nur al-Anwar Volume 3: Compared to a free person, (the slave) has more physical strength and power. It is legislated as a punishment for disbelief, because the disbelievers prevented themselves from worshiping Allah Almighty, so Allah Almighty made them slaves of His slaves. And the origin of slavery: this is the true reality of slavery, i.e., the original establishment and beginning of slavery is this: because initially the entry of slavery occurred only for the disbelievers. Then after that, even if that disbeliever became Muslim, slavery is retained upon him, just as he is a slave of the master, similarly his children are also slaves. And this slavery does not separate from him until he is manumitted. Just as kharaj (land tax) initially applied only to disbelievers, then after that, if a Muslim purchases kharaj land, the kharaj remains in its original state and does not change. The author pointed to this with his saying: 'But in continuation it became from the legal matters' meaning in the state of continuation, it is a regulatory matter, i.e., in the later state, without considering the meaning of punishment, like other rulings of Shari'ah, it also continues as a ruling of Shari'ah. By it a person becomes subject to ownership and humiliation: due to this slavery, a person remains the target of ownership and contempt, i.e., due to this slavery he remains a place for being owned and degraded. And 'al-'aradah' originally is the butcher's rag with which he cleans the grease and fat on his hands. And it is a description that is not divisible: this is a description in which there is no division, neither in establishment nor in removal. Because if a person sells his slave to two people, by consensus this sale is valid. And if he sells half of his slave, his ownership remains on the other half by consensus. And ownership (milk) is general and riqq is specific in contrast to it, and ownership is more general than slavery because besides humans, other things can also be described with ownership, but slavery is specific only to humans. Like emancipation (itq) which is its opposite, for it also does not accept division, and it is a legal power by which a person becomes eligible for ownership and guardianship such as testimony and judiciary and the like. Similarly, emancipation (i'taq) according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) also does not divide because emancipation is the establishment of freedom, so freedom is its effect. If emancipation were divisible and part was emancipated, then it would either lead to the establishment of freedom in the whole without the effect of the cause, or the cause without the effect, or the division of freedom itself. In some copies, his words 'or the division of freedom' are not found, and its estimation is not free from distortion. And Abu Hanifa said: it (emancipation) is the removal of ownership, and it is divisible for removing slavery or establishing freedom.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the legal definition and characteristics of riqq (slavery) as a legal description (wasf). The author begins by explaining that riqq is a legal incapacity (ajz hukmi) that renders a person unable to perform legal dispositions, even if physically stronger than a free person. This incapacity is legislated as a punishment for disbelief, as disbelievers refused to worship Allah, so He made them slaves. However, this punishment aspect is only at the origin; once slavery is established, it continues even if the slave embraces Islam, like kharaj tax on land. The text then emphasizes that riqq is indivisible (la yatajazzau) because it is a right of Allah; a slave cannot be partially free and partially slave. This is contrasted with ownership (milk), which is divisible—one can own half a slave—because ownership is a right of the human. Milk is more general than riqq as it applies to inanimate objects as well. The latter part discusses itq (emancipation) as the opposite of riqq, and a dispute among the Hanafi imams: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that i'taq (the act of emancipating) is also indivisible because it establishes freedom, while Abu Hanifa considers i'taq as the removal of ownership (izalat al-milk), which is divisible. The commentary includes an Urdu explanation of these points.

Key Terms
الرق (al-riqq): Legal slavery, a description (wasf) that is a legal incapacity established as a punishment for disbelief, indivisible in both establishment and removal.
الملك (al-milk): Ownership, a right of the human, divisible in establishment and removal, applicable to humans and other things.
العتق (al-ʻitq): Emancipation, the opposite of riqq, a legal power that makes a person eligible for ownership and guardianship. Divisible according to Abu Hanifa (as removal of ownership), indivisible according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is riqq considered indivisible?
A) Because a slave is always owned by the state, not an individual.
B) Because riqq is a right of Allah, and rights of Allah are not divisible.
C) Because the slave is physically inseparable from himself.
D) Because the consensus of the Sahibayn overrules Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
Riqq is a legal incapacity, a right of Allah that is indivisible in establishment and removal, distinct from ownership which is divisible and applies more broadly.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
Two Types of Blood Immunity (Ismah) in Hanafi Usul
Usul rule on blood immunity types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'ismah mu'aththimah and 'ismah muqawwimah, and apply each to determine whether compensation is due for killing.

Core Idea
Blood immunity has two levels: one by faith alone (sinful killing), one by residence in Dar al-Islam (entailing compensation).

In this passage from the commentary on Nur al-Anwar, the author explains how slavery does not affect a person's blood immunity, but more importantly, he clarifies that there are two distinct types of blood immunity in the Hanafi school: one that simply makes killing a sin (mu'aththimah) and one that also imposes financial or retaliatory liability (muqawwimah). This distinction is crucial for understanding when a killer must pay blood-money or face qisas, versus when only expiation is required. The lesson will unpack the sabab (cause) for each type, using the examples of a believer in Dar al-Islam and a believer who remains in Dar al-Harb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of ismah
Find in the passage where the author mentions 'ismah mu'aththimah' and 'ismah muqawwimah'. Note the Arabic terms and their English equivalents: 'ismah mu'aththimah' (immunity that makes killing sinful) and 'ismah muqawwimah' (immunity that entails compensation).
The phrase 'الْعِصْمَةُ الْمُؤْثِمَةُ' and 'الْمُقَوَّمَةُ' appear near the end.
2
Determine the sabab (cause) for each type
The passage states that ismah mu'aththimah is established by faith (iman) alone: 'الْعِصْمَةَ بِالإِيمَانِ'. For ismah muqawwimah, it says it is established by the abode of faith (dar al-iman): 'الْمُقَوَّمَةُ بِدَارِهِ أَى الْعِصْمَةُ الَّتِى تُوْجِبُ القِيْمَةَ تَثْبُتُ بِدَارِ الْإِيْمَانِ'. So the sabab for the full immunity is residence in Dar al-Islam.
Note that 'dar al-iman' is synonymous with Dar al-Islam in this context.
3
Apply to the example of a convert in Dar al-Harb
The passage contrasts a Muslim in Dar al-Islam with a person who accepts Islam in Dar al-Harb but does not migrate. For the latter, only ismah mu'aththimah applies: his killer incurs sin and must give kaffarah, but no diyah or qisas. Trace this reasoning: since he lacks residence in Dar al-Islam, the sabab for muqawwimah is absent.
This highlights that legal consequence (athar) varies based on the sabab present.
4
Derive the general usul rule
From this analysis, formulate a general rule: 'Blood immunity that only prohibits killing (makes it sinful) is caused by faith; blood immunity that also requires compensation or retaliation is caused by residence in Dar al-Islam.' This is a Hanafi legal principle regarding the sanctity of life.
This rule can be applied to determine rights of protection for various individuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حتى لا يملك العبد والمكاتب التسرى (یعنی غلام اور مکاتب کو تسری کی اجازت نہیں ہے) ولا تصحُّ مِنْهُمَا حَجَّةُ الإسلام حَتَّى لَوْ حَجَّا يَقَعُ نَقْلاً وَإِنْ كَانَ بِإِذْنِ الْمَوْلَى لان مَنَافِعَهُمَا سِوَى الصلوةِ وَالصَّيَام تَبْقَى لِلْمَوْلَى وَلَا تَكُونُ لَهُمَا قَدْرِةً على أدائه بخلاف الفقير إذا حَجَّ ثُمَّ اسْتَغْنى حَيْثُ يَقَعُ مَا أَدَّىٰ عَنِ الْفَرْضِ لَأَنْ ملك الْمَال لَيْس بشرط لِذَاتِهِ وَإِنَّمَا شَرْطٌ للتَّمَكُن عَنِ الآدَاءِ وَلَا يُنَافِي مَا لَكِيَةُ غَيْرِ الْمَالِ كَالنِّكَاحِ والدم فإنّهُ مَالِكَ لِلنِّكَاح لإنْ قَضَاءَ شَهْوَةِ الْفَرْجِ فَرْضٌ ولا سبيلَ لَهُ فِي التُسَرِّي فَتَعَيَّنَ النِّكَاحِ وَلَكِنَّهُ مَوْقوفٌ عَلَى رَضَاءِ الْمَوْلَى لَأَنْ الْمَهْرَ يَتَعَلَّقَ بِرَقَبَتِهِ فَيُبَاعُ فِيْهِ وَفِي ذَالِكَ إِصْرَارٌ لِلْمَوْلَى فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ رِضَائِهِ وكذا هُوَ مَالِك لِدَمِهِ لأنه مُحتاج إلى الْبَقَاءِ وَلَا بَقَاءَ إلا به وَلِهَذَا لَا يَمْلِكُ الْمَوْلَى إِتْلَاف دَمِهِ وَصَحَّ إِقْرَارُ الْعَبْدِ بِالْقِصَاصِ لَأَنَّهُ فِي ذَالِكَ مِثْلُ الْحُرِّ وَيُنَافِي فِي كَمَالَ الْحَالِ فِي أَهْلِيَةِ الْكَرَامَاتِ الْمَوْضُوعَةِ لِلْبَشَرِ كَالذِّمَّةِ وَالْوِلَايَةِ وَالْحِلِ فَإِنْ ذِمَّتَهُ نَاقِصَةٌ لَا تَقْبَلُ إِنْ [؟] يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ دَيْنٌ مَالَمْ يُعْتَقَ أَو لَمْ يُكَاتِبُ وَلَا وِلايَةَ لَهُ عَلَى [؟] بِالنِّكَاحِ وَلَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ مِنَ النِّساءِ مِثْلَ مَا حَلُ لِلْحُرِّ فَانَّ لِلْحُرِّ أَنْ تَحِلَّ أَرْبَعُ نِساءِ والرقيق يَصْفُ ذَالِكَ وَإِنَّه أَي الرِّقَ لايؤثر فِي عَصْمَةِ الدَّم أَى إِزَالَةَ عِصْمَةِ الدم بَلْ دَمُهُ مَعْصُومُ كَمَا كَانَ دَمُ الْحَرِّ مَعْصُوْمًا لَاَنَّ الْعِصْمَةَ بِالإِيمَانِ أَنْ مَنْ كَانَ مُؤْمِنًا يَسْتَحِقُ الإِثْمَ قَاتِلُهُ فَتَجِبَ الْكَفَّارَةُ عَلَيْهِ وَالْمُقَوَّمَةُ بِدَارِهِ أَى الْعِصْمَةُ الَّتِى تُوْجِبُ القِيْمَةَ تَثْبُتُ بِدَارِ الْإِيْمَانِ فَمَنْ قَتَلَ مِنْ الْمُسْلِمِيْنَ فِي دَارِ الاِسلام تَجِبُ الدِّيَّةُ وَالْقِصَاصِ عَلَى قَاتِلِهِ بِخِلافِ مَنْ أَسْلَمَ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ وَلَمْ يُهَاجِرُ الى دار الإسلام فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَجِبُ عَلَى قَاتِلِهِ إِلَّا الكَفَّارَةُ دَوْنَ الدِّيَّةِ وَالْقِصَاصِ إِذْ لَيْسَ لَهُ إِلَّا الْعِصْمَةُ الْمُؤْثِمَةُ دُونَ الْمُقَوَّمَةِ.
A slave and a mukatab do not own concubinage. And Hajj al-Islam is not valid from them; even if they perform Hajj, it counts as nafl, even if with the master's permission, because their benefits apart from prayer and fasting remain for the master, and they have no ability to perform it. Unlike the poor person who performs Hajj then becomes rich, his performance counts as obligatory, because ownership of wealth is not a condition in itself but is a condition for ability to perform. And it does not contradict ownership of other than wealth, like marriage and blood: indeed he is an owner of marriage because fulfilling the desire of the private part is obligatory, and he has no way to concubinage, so marriage is determined, but it is dependent on the master's consent because the dower is attached to his neck and he is sold for it, and in that there is harm to the master, so his consent is necessary. And likewise, he is owner of his blood because he needs survival and there is no survival except by it, and therefore the master does not own the destruction of his blood, and the slave's confession of retaliation is valid because in that he is like a free person. And it [slavery] prevents perfection in the capacity for honors placed for humans, like legal personality, guardianship, and halal: indeed his legal personality is deficient; it does not accept that a debt becomes obligatory on him unless he is freed or a mukatab, and he has no guardianship over marriage, and it is not permissible for him from women like what is permissible for a free person, for a free person may marry four women, and a slave is limited from that. And slavery does not affect the immunity of blood, i.e., removal of blood immunity; rather his blood is inviolate just as the free person's blood is inviolate, because immunity is by faith: whoever is a believer, his killer deserves sin, so expiation is obligatory on him. And the immunity that entails compensation is established by the abode of faith. So whoever kills a Muslim in the abode of Islam, blood-money and retaliation are obligatory on his killer, contrary to one who became Muslim in the abode of war and did not migrate to the abode of Islam, for nothing is obligatory on his killer except expiation without blood-money and retaliation, since he has only the immunity that makes sinful without the immunity that entails compensation.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Anwar discusses the legal capacity of a slave ('abd) and a mukatab (slave under contract of manumission). It opens by stating that they do not have the right to take a concubine (tasrri). Next, it addresses Hajj: even if they perform Hajj with the master's permission, it counts only as a voluntary (nafl) act, not as the obligatory Hajj of Islam. The reason is that their time and labor (manafi') belong to the master except for prayer and fasting, so they lack full ability. This contrasts with a poor free person who performs Hajj and later becomes rich—his Hajj suffices for the obligation because wealth is a condition for ability, not for the essence. The commentary then clarifies that a slave does have ownership in matters other than wealth: he owns his marriage (can marry) and his blood (dhim). Regarding marriage, because fulfilling sexual desire is obligatory and a slave cannot own a concubine, marriage becomes the means, but it requires the master's consent because the dower becomes a debt on the slave's neck, potentially causing loss to the master. Similarly, a slave owns his blood (life) because he needs to survive, and thus the master cannot kill him. The slave's confession in qisas is valid like a free person. However, slavery does impair full legal capacity: the slave's dhimma (legal personality) is deficient—he cannot incur debt unless freed or made a mukatab; he has no guardianship over marriage; and he is limited to fewer wives than a free man. The passage concludes by distinguishing two types of blood immunity: 'ismah mu'aththimah' (making killing sinful) due to faith, and 'ismah muqawwimah' (entailing compensation) linked to residence in dar al-Islam. A Muslim in dar al-Islam has both; a convert in dar al-harb who does not migrate only has the former, so his killer only owes kaffarah, not diyah or qisas.

Key Terms
عصمة (ismah): Immunity or inviolability of blood, protecting one from being killed lawlessly.
عصمة مؤثمة (ismah mu'aththimah): Blood immunity that only makes killing a sin; does not require diyah or qisas.
عصمة مقومة (ismah muqawwimah): Blood immunity that entails compensation (diyah or qisas).
دار الإسلام (dar al-Islam): Abode of Islam; territory under Muslim rule where Islamic law prevails.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle in the passage, what is required for a person's blood to have full immunity (including diyah/qisas)?
A) Being a Muslim only.
B) Being a Muslim and residing in Dar al-Islam.
C) Being a Muslim and being a free person.
D) Being a Muslim and having a valid dhimma.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul distinguishes blood immunity into two types: mu'aththimah (by iman, only sinful) and muqawwimah (by residence in Dar al-Islam, entailing diyah/qisas).

Slavery and Blood Sanctity: The Basis for Qisas Equality
Explaining that slavery does not affect blood sanctity and the slave is equal to the free in qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a free person is executed in qisas for killing a slave, and distinguish the two types of blood sanctity.

Core Idea
Slavery does not remove blood sanctity; the slave's blood is equally inviolable, making qisas applicable.

This passage from a Hanafi usul work distinguishes two types of blood sanctity (ismat al-dam): one based on faith (incurs sin) and one based on abode (incurs monetary liability). It argues that slavery, while affecting certain capacities like dhimma and wilaya, does not affect either type of sanctity. Therefore, the slave is equal to the free in the essential meaning upon which qisas is based.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of blood sanctity
Read the passage and locate where the author distinguishes between al-ismat al-muthima (sanctity that incurs sin) and al-ismat al-muqawwama (sanctity that incurs value). Understand the basis of each.
The first is based on faith alone, the second on residence in Dar al-Islam.
2
Note the capacities slavery does affect
The passage mentions that a slave's dhimma is deficient, he has no marriage guardianship, and his marriage limit is two wives. This shows that slavery does affect some legal capacities, but not blood sanctity.
These are contrasts to highlight that blood sanctity is separate.
3
Understand the slave's equality in both sanctities
The author asserts that the slave is like the free in each of the two sanctities: in faith, it is obvious; in residence, he follows his master in Dar al-Islam.
Thus the slave has both sanctities fully.
4
Derive the ruling on qisas
Because the slave's blood is fully sanctified, the essential meaning (al-ma'na al-asli) for qisas—equality in blood sanctity—is present. Therefore, a free person is killed for killing a slave.
This is the Hanafi position, stated with 'عندنا' (according to us).
5
Engage with the Shafi'i opposition
The Shafi'i school argues from Quran 2:178 that qisas applies only free for free. The Hanafi response is that the verse is general and the specific proof of equality in essential meaning overrides it.
The practical difference: in the Hanafi school, qisas is applied; in Shafi'i, only diya is paid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِتْلَاف دَمِهِ وَصَحْ أَقْرَارُ الْعَبْدِ بِالْقِصَاصِ لَأَنَّهُ فِي ذَالِكَ مِثْلُ الْحُرِّ وَيُنَا فِي كَمَالَ الْحَالِ فِي أَهْلِيَةِ الْكَرَامَاتِ الْمَوْضُوعَةِ لِلْبَشَرِ كَالذِّمَّةِ وَالْوِلَايَةِ وَالْحِلُ فَإِنْ ذِمْتَهُ نَاقِصَةٌ لَا تَقْبَلُ إِنْ يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ دَيْنٌ مَالَمْ يُعْتَقَ أَو لَمْ يُكَاتِبُ وَلَا وِلايَةَ لَهُ عَلَى بِالنِّكَاحِ وَلَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ مِنَ النِّساءِ مِثْلَ مَا حَلُ لِلْحُرْفَانَ لِلْحُرُ أَنْ تَحِلَّ أَرْبَعُ نِساءِ والرقيق يصنف ذالِكَ وَإِنْه أَي الرِّقَ لايؤثر فِي عَصْمَةِ الدَّم أى إِزَالَةٍ عِصْمَةِ الدم بَلْ دَمُهُ مَعْصُومُ كَمَا كَانَ دَمُ الْحَرِّ مَعْصُوْمًا لَاَنَّ الْعِصْمَةَ البُوثِمَة بِالْإِيْمَانِ أَنْ مَنْ كَانَ مُؤْمِنًا يَسْتَحِقُ الإِثْمَ قَاتِلُهُ فَتَجِبَ الْكَفَّارَةُ عَلَيْهِ وَالْمُقَوْمَةُ بدَارِهِ أَى الْعِصْمَةُ الَّتِى تُوْجِبُ القِيْمَةَ تَثْبُتُ بِدَارِ الْإِيْمَانِ فَمَنْ قَتَلَ مِنْ الْمُسْلِمِيْنِ فِي دَارِ الاِسلام تَجِبُ الديَّةُ وَالْقِصَاصِ عَلَى قَاتِلِهِ بِخِلافِ مَنْ أَسْلَمَ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ وَلَمْ يُهَاجِرُ الى دار الإسلام فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَجِبُ عَلَى قَاتِلِهِ إِلَّا الكَفَّارَةُ دَوْنَ الدِّيَّةِ وَالْقِصَاصِ إِذْ لَيْسَ لَهُ إِلَّا الْعِصْمَةُ الْمُؤْثِمَةُ دُونَ الْمُقَوْمَةِ.
وَالْعَبْدُ فِيْهِ أَيْ فِي كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْعِصْمَتَيْنِ كَالْحُرْ أَمَّا فِي الْإِيْمَانِ فَظَاهِرٌ وَأَمَّا فِي الاحْتِرَازِ فِى دار الإسلام فَلاتُه تَبْعٌ لِلْمَوْلى فَإِذَا كَانَ الْمَوْلَى مُحْدِرًا فِي دَارِ الإسلام كَانَ الْعَبْدُ أيضًا مُحْدِرًا فِيهِ إِمَّا بالإسلام أَوْ بِقُبُولِ الذِّمَّةِ وَإِنَّمَا فِي قِيْمَتِه أَى إِنَّمَا يُوثُرُ الرِّقَ فِي نُقْصَانِ قِيْمَتِهِ حَتَّى إِذَا بِلَغَتْ قِيْمَتُهُ عَشْرَةٌ الآفِ دِرْهَم يَنْبَغِى أَنْ يَنْقُصِ مِنْهُ عَشرَةُ دَارَهِمَ حَطَّا المَرْتَبَةِ عَنْ مَرْتَبَةِ الْحُرُ وَلِهَذَا أَى لِكَوْنِ الْعَبْدِ مِثْلُ الْحُرُ فِي العِصْمَةِ يُقْتَلُ الْحُرُّ بِالْعَبْدِ قِصَاصَا عِنْدَنَا إِذَا قَدَرَ وُجِدَتِ الْمُسَاوَاةُ فِي الْمَعْنى الأَصْلِيُّ الَّذِي يَبْتَنِي عَلَيْهِ الْقِصَاصِ
The destruction of his blood, and the slave's confession to qisas is valid because he is like a free person in that. But it opposes completeness of state in the capacity for dignities placed for humans, such as dhimma, wilaya, and hilla. For his dhimma is deficient, it does not accept that debt become obligatory upon him unless he is freed or made a mukatib. And he has no guardianship in marriage, and women are not permissible for him like what is permissible for the free. For the free person, four women are permissible, and the slave is limited to that. And indeed slavery does not affect the sanctity of blood, meaning removal of the sanctity of blood; rather his blood is sanctified just as the blood of the free is sanctified, because the sanctity that incurs sin is by faith: whoever is a believer, his killer deserves sin, so expiation becomes obligatory upon him. And the sanctity that incurs value is by his abode: the sanctity that necessitates (blood money) value is established by the abode of faith. So whoever is killed among Muslims in the abode of Islam, blood money and qisas become obligatory upon his killer. Contrary to one who accepted Islam in the abode of war and did not migrate to the abode of Islam, for upon his killer only expiation is obligatory without blood money and qisas, since he only has the sanctity that incurs sin, not the one that incurs value. And the slave is like the free in each of the two sanctities: as for faith, it is apparent; as for being protected in the abode of Islam, he is a follower of his master. So if the master is residing in the abode of Islam, the slave is also residing there, either by Islam or by accepting dhimma. Slavery only affects the reduction of his monetary value, so that if his value reaches ten thousand dirhams, ten dirhams should be deducted from it due to lowering his rank from the rank of a free person. And because the slave is like the free in sanctity, a free person is killed for a slave in qisas according to us, when equality is found in the essential meaning upon which qisas is based.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a ruling explaining the effect of slavery on blood sanctity and qisas. It begins by stating that a slave's confession to qisas is valid, as he owns his life in a way similar to a free person. However, slavery does affect other capacities: dhimma is deficient (debt does not bind without freedom or kitaba), he has no marriage guardianship, and he is limited to two wives (half of the free man's four). Then the main point: slavery does not remove blood sanctity. There are two types of sanctity: (1) al-ismat al-muthima (sanctity that incurs sin) – established by faith alone, making the killer sinful and requiring kaffara; (2) al-ismat al-muqawwama (sanctity that incurs monetary liability) – established by residence in Dar al-Islam (or under dhimma), requiring diya or qisas. A slave has both sanctities: he is a believer (faith) and resides in Dar al-Islam (following his master). Therefore, if a free person kills a slave, qisas is obligatory because equality in the essential meaning (blood sanctity) exists. Slavery only affects monetary value, not the sanctity of blood. This is the Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa and his disciples).

Key Terms
عصمة الدم (ismat al-dam): Blood sanctity; the inviolability of human life that makes killing unlawful.
الذمة (al-dhimma): Legal capacity to bear obligations; in a slave it is deficient, not fully accepting debt.
الولاية (al-wilaya): Guardianship; a slave has no guardianship over marriage because of his deficiency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following does slavery affect?
A) Blood sanctity (ismat al-dam)
B) Legal capacity (dhimma)
C) Qisas applicability
D) Faith

Key Takeaway
Slavery does not remove blood sanctity; the slave is equal to the free in both the sin-incurring and value-incurring sanctities, so qisas is established.

Definition of Marad and Its Legal Effects
Definition of marad as a legal cause of partial restriction (hajr)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define marad (illness) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, identify its classification as a cause of hajr, and apply the condition of marad al-mawt to determine when financial restriction applies.

Core Idea
Illness preserves legal capacity for speech acts but, when mortal, triggers partial financial restriction retroactively.

This passage defines 'marad' as a bodily state that disrupts natural balance but does not negate a person's capacity for legal rulings and expressions (ahliyyat al-hukm wa al-ibarah). However, because mortal illness is a cause of death, it becomes a cause of partial restriction (hajr) in financial matters to protect the rights of creditors and heirs. Understanding this definition is essential for grasping the Hanafi position on the legal capacity of a sick person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Definition of Marad
Extract from the Arabic that marad is a 'state of the body by which the natural balance is removed' (حالة للبدن يزول بها اعتدال المزاج). Note that this is a physical state, not a legal construct in itself.
The term used is 'المزاج' (temperament) in correct Arabic; the OCR shows 'المُبْعِيَةِ'.
2
Distinguish Effects on Capacity
Marad does not negate ahliyyat al-hukm (capacity for rulings) or al-ibarah (capacity for speech acts). The sick person can still perform marriage, divorce, etc. But it does affect the capacity for financial transactions beyond certain limits.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi usul: illness only partially restricts financial capacity.
3
Determine the Condition for Hajr
Hajr (restriction) applies only when the illness is mortal (marad al-mawt) and connected to death. If the person recovers, no retroactive restriction applies.
The phrase 'إِنَّهُ لَايُنَافِى أَهْلِيَةً الحكم' clarifies that general illness does not restrict.
4
Understand the Retroactive Effect
When a person dies from a mortal illness, the restriction is retroactive from the onset of that illness. Transactions made during the illness that exceed one-third or are for debts are invalid.
The text says 'يُقَالُ عِنْدَ الْمَوْتِ إِنَّهُ مَحْجُورٌ عَنِ التَّصَرُّفِ مِنْ أَوَّلَ الْمَرَضِ'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمَرَضِ عَطَفٌ عَلى مَا قَبْلَة وَهُوَ حَالَةٌ لِلْبَدَنِ يَزُولُ بِهَا اعْتِدَالُ الْمُبْعِيَةِ فَإِنَّهُ لَايُنَافِى أَهْلِيَةً الحكم وَالْعِبَارَةُ أنْ يَكُونُ أَهْلاً لِوُجُوبِ الْحُكْمِ لِلتَّعْبِيرِ عَنِ الْمَقَاصدِ بِالْعِبَارَةِ حتى صنع نِكَاحَة وَطَلَاقَة وَسَائِرُ مَا يَتَعَلَّقَ بِعِبَارَتِهِ وَلَكِنَّهُ لَمَّا كَانَ سَبَبُ الْمَوْتِ وَإِنْه أى وَالْحَالَ أَنَّ الْمَوْتَ عِجْرٌ خَالِصٌ كَانَ الْمَرْضَ مِنْ أَسْبَابِ الْعِجْزِ فَتُرعَتِ الْعِبَادَات عَلَيْهِ بَالْقُدْرَةِ الْمُمْكِنَةِ فَيُصَلِّي قَاعِدًا أَنْ لَمْ يَقْدِرْ عَلَى الْقِيَامَةِ وَمُسْتَلْقِيًا إنْ لَمْ يَقْدِرُ عَلى القُعُودِ وَلَمَّا كَانَ الْمَوْتِ مِلَّةَ الْخَلافَةِ أَنْ خِلافَةِ الْوَارِثِ وَالغُرَمَاءِ فِى مَالِهِ كَانَ الْمَرَضُ مِنْ اسْتَبَاب تَعَلى حَقَّ الْوَارِثِ. وَالْعَزِيم بِمَالِهِ فَيَكُونُ مِنْ أَسْبَابِ الْحَجَرِ بِقَدْرِ مَا يَتَعَلَّقَ بِهِ صِيَانَةُ الْحَقِّ أَي حَق الْغُرَيْم وَلُّوارَثَ وَيَكُونُ الْمَرِيضِ مَحْجُورًا لِقَدْرِ الدِّيْنِ الَّذِي هُوَ حَقُّ الْعَزِيمِ وَمِنَ الثَّلْثِيْنَ الَّذِي هُوَ حَق الْمَوَارِثِ وَلَكِنْ لأَمْطَلَقًا بَلْ إِذَا اتَّصَلَ بِالْمَوْتِ وَيَمُوتُ مِنْ ذالِكَ الْمَرَضِ فَحِينَئِذٍ يَظْهَرُ كَوْتُهُ مَحْجُورًا ولَكِنْ يَكُونُ مُسْتَتَبَدًا إِلَى أَوْلِهِ أَيْ يُقَالُ عِنْدَ الْمَوْتِ إِنَّهُ مَحْجُورٌ عَنِ التَّصَرُّفِ مِنْ أَوَّلَ الْمَرَضِ. اور مرض (۸) اور مرض اس کا بھی ماقبل یعنی صفر پر عطف ہے بیماری بدن کی ایک خاص کیفیت کا نام ہے جس کی وجہ سے بدن کا طبیعی اعتدال زائل ہو جاتا ہے۔ وانه لا ينافي اهلية الحكم والعبادة اور یہ
And 'al-marad' (illness) is connected by conjunction to what precedes it. It is a state of the body by which the natural balance of temperament is removed. Indeed, it does not negate the capacity (ahliyyah) for legal rulings and speech acts (ibarah) that one is qualified for the obligation of rulings, to express intentions through speech, such as marriage, divorce, and all that pertains to his expression. But because it is a cause of death, and death is pure incapacity, illness is among the causes of incapacity. So acts of worship are imposed upon him according to possible ability: he prays sitting if unable to stand, and lying down if unable to sit. And since death is the time of succession—the succession of the heir and creditors over his wealth—illness is among the causes that necessitate the right of the heir and creditor over his wealth. So it becomes a cause of restriction (hajr) to the extent of preserving the right, i.e., the right of the creditor and heir. Thus, the sick person is restricted to the extent of the debt which is the right of the creditor, and to the extent of one-third which is the right of the heirs. But not absolutely; rather, if the illness is connected to death and he dies from that illness, then his being restricted becomes apparent; but it is retroactive from its beginning, i.e., at the time of death it is said that he was restricted from transactions from the beginning of the illness. And illness (8): Illness is also connected to what precedes it, i.e., to 'safar'? It is a specific quality of the body by which the natural balance of the body is removed. And it does not negate the capacity for legal rulings and worship.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage defines 'marad' (illness) in legal terms as a bodily state that disrupts normal balance but does not remove legal capacity (ahliyyah) for rulings and speech acts—hence a sick person can still conclude marriage, divorce, etc. However, because illness is a cause of death (pure incapacity), it becomes a cause of restriction (hajr) in financial matters to protect the rights of creditors and heirs. The restriction is not absolute; it only becomes effective when the illness is mortal (marad al-mawt) and results in death. At that point, the restriction is retroactive from the onset of that illness. The Urdu commentary further explains that illness is a specific condition that disturbs the body's equilibrium but does not negate capacity for legal actions and worship.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A mortal illness that ends in death, triggering hajr in financial matters.
حجر (hajr): Legal restriction disallowing certain transactions to protect the rights of creditors and heirs.
أهلية الحكم (ahliyyat al-hukm): Capacity to receive legal rulings (obligations, rights).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only when the illness causes loss of speech.
D) Only when a judge declares the person incompetent.

Key Takeaway
Marad al-mawt is a cause of hajr in financial transactions, but it does not remove general legal capacity or the ability to perform speech acts.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Legal Effect of Death Illness on Capacity and Transactions
Commentary on death illness restrictions in Hanafi fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sabab and illa of the restriction on transactions in death illness, and apply the Hanafi rule distinguishing between voidable and non-voidable transactions.

Core Idea
Death illness triggers partial interdiction to protect heirs and creditors, but capacity remains for essential acts.

This passage explores the legal construct of marad al-mawt in Hanafi usul. While a sick person retains full capacity for speech acts (marriage, divorce), death illness becomes a sabab that imposes qayd (restrictions) on financial transactions to safeguard the rights of creditors and heirs. Understanding which transactions are voidable (qabil al-faskh) and which are suspended as tadbir is critical for the mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sabab (cause) of restriction
The text states that death illness is a cause for restricting transactions because death itself is the cause for substitution (khilafah) of creditors and heirs. Recognize that the illness is a sabab connected to death, not a direct cause.
The restriction is only triggered if the illness ends in death; otherwise, no interdiction.
2
Distinguish between full capacity and restrictions
Note that the sick person remains qualified for obligations (ahliyyat al-wujub) and can perform worship (prayer sitting/lying) and validly marry, divorce, etc. Restrictions only apply to transactions that affect the rights of others (ghayr).
Marriage with proper mahr is exempt because it is a basic need; the right of others attaches only to surplus wealth.
3
Classify transactions into voidable and non-voidable
Voidable (yāḥtamil al-faskh) transactions like gifts and sales below market value (muḥābāt) are valid at the time but can be rescinded after death if needed. Non-voidable transactions like freeing a slave when the estate is insolvent or the slave’s value exceeds one-third are treated as mudabbir (suspended on death).
The distinction depends on whether the transaction can be undone without harm to the counterparty.
4
Apply the principle of ta'līq and naqd
Understand that voidable transactions are effective until the need for rescission arises at death, while non-voidable ones are suspended and become effective after death but with obligation to compensate creditors/heirs.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of protective restriction without complete interdiction.

معاملات جن کا تعلق تعبیر مہارت و الفاظ ہے ہے سب بیج ہے۔ وَلَكِنَّهُ لَمَّا كَانَ سَبَبُ المَوتِ اور چونکہ مرض موت کا سبب ہے اور بلا شبہ یہ یعنی اس موت کا حال یہ ہے کہ وہ خالص بجز اور مجبوری ہے لہذا چت لیٹ کر پڑھ سکتا ہے اگر بیٹھنے پر قادر نہ ہو۔ ولَمَّا كَانَ الْمَوْتُ عِلَّة الخلافة اور چونکہ موت قائم مقامی کی علت ہے لہذ امر نے والے کے مال میں اس کے قرض خواہ اور اس کے وارث اس کے قائم مقام ہو جاتے ہیں كَانَ الْمَرَضُ مِنْ أَسْبَابِ تَعَلُّقِ الوارث میت کے مال میں لہذا میت کا قرض اس کے مال سے وارث اور قرض خواہوں کا حق متعلق ہونے کا سبب بن گیا جس کے نتیجے میں یہی مرض جتنی مقدار مال سے اس حق کی حفاظت کا تعلق ہے اس میں مریض کے تصرف کو روکنے کا سبب ہو جائیگا یعنی قرض خواہ کا حق اور وارث کا حق محفوظ رکھنے کے لئے مریض کے تصرف سے مجبور ہو جاتا ہے مقدار قرض میں جو کہ قرض خواہ کا حق ہے اور دو ٹمبٹ جو کہ وارثوں کا حق ہے مگر مطلقاً محجور نہیں کیا جاتا بلکہ اذا اتصل بالموت جب یہ مرض موت سے متصل ہو اور اسی مرض سے مریض مر جائے تو اس وقت اسکا مجور ہونا ظاہر ہوگا البتہ يكون مستنداً الى اوله اول مرض کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے یہ حجر ثابت ہو گا یعنی موت کے وقت کیا جائے گا کہ یہ اول مرض سے مجبور ہے یعنی مرنے کے وقت یہ حکم لگایا جائے گا کہ اس بیماری کی ابتداء ہی سے اس کا تصرف نافذ نہیں ہے۔ حَتَّى لاَ يُوثْرَ الْمَرَض مُتَعَلِّقَ بَقَوْلِهِ بِقَدْرِ مَا يَتعلَّق بِه صِيَانَةُ الْحَقِّ أَيْ إِنَّمَا يُؤثر الْمَرَضُ فِيْمَا تَعَلَّقَ بِه حَقَّ الْغَيْرِ وَلَا يُوثُرُ فِيْمَا لَا يَتَعَلَّقَ بِهِ حَقٌّ غَرِيْمَ وَوَارِتْ كَالنِّكَاحِ بِعَهْرِ الْمِثْلِ فَإِنَّهُ مِنَ الْجَوائج الأصلِيَةِ وَحَقِّهِمْ يَتَعَلْقُ فِيمَا يَقْضَلُ مِنْهَا فَيَصيحُ في الحال كُلُّ تَصَرُّفٍ يَحْتَمِلُ الْفَسعَ كَالْهِبَةِ وَالْمُحَابَاتِ وَهُوَ الْبَيْعُ بَاقَلْ مِنَ الْقِيْمَةِ اذ الْمَوْتُ مَشكُوكَ فِي الْحَالِ وَلَيْسَ فِي صحة هذا التَّصَرُفِ فِي الْحَالِ ضَرْرٌ بِأَحَدٍ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَصِحُ ثُمَّ يَنْقُضُ إِنْ اِحْتِيْجَ إِلَيْهِ أَنْ إلى النَّقْضِ عِنْدَ تَحَقَّقِ الْحَاجَةِ وَمَالَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْفَسَبْحُ جُعِلَ كَالْمُعَلِّقِ بِالْمَوْتِ وَهُوَ الْمُدَبِّرُ كَالإِعْتَاقِ إِذَا وَقَعَ عَلى حَق عَرِيْمٍ أَوْ وَارِثَ بِأَنْ أَعْتَقَ عَبْدًا مِنْ مَالِهِ الْمُسْتَغْرَقِ بِالدَيْنِ أَوْ أَعْتَقَ عَبْدًا قِيْمَتُهُ تَزِيْدُ عَلَى الظُّلْثِ فَحُكْمُ هَذَا الْمُعْتَقِ حُكْمُ الْمُدَيْرِ قَبْلَ الْمَوْتِ فَيَكُونُ عَبْدًا فِي جَمِيعِ الأَحْكَامِ الْمُعَلَّقَةِ بِالْحُزْيَةِ مِنَ الْكَرَامَاتِ وَبَعْدَ الْمَوْتُ يَكُونُ حُرًّا وَيَسْعَى فِي قِيْمَتِهِ لِلْغُرَمَاءِ وَالْوَرَكة
The importance of rulings and correct expressions is not contradictory; a person is qualified for the obligation of the Sharia ruling and can express his intention through words, so his marriage, divorce, and all transactions related to expression and words are valid. But because death illness is a cause of death, and undoubtedly this death is pure compulsion, so illness became among the causes. Therefore, considering ability to perform, worship is commanded for the sick person; he can pray sitting if unable to stand, and lying down if unable to sit. And because death is the cause of substitution, the creditors and heirs substitute him in his wealth, so illness became a cause for the attachment of heirs' rights in the deceased's wealth. Thus, the illness prevents the sick person's transactions to the extent necessary to protect that right, i.e., the right of creditors and heirs, but he is not completely interdicted. Only when the illness is connected to death and he dies from it does his interdiction become apparent, but it is attributed to the beginning, so at the time of death it is judged that he was interdicted from the start. So illness only affects what involves the right of another, and does not affect what does not involve the right of creditor and heir, like marriage with proper mahr because it is among original needs, and their right attaches only to surplus. So every voidable transaction like gift and sale below market value is valid immediately, because death is uncertain at present and there is no harm to anyone in its immediate validity. Then it is rescinded if needed, i.e., when the need for rescission arises. And what is not voidable is treated as suspended on death, like a mudabbir: in freeing a slave when it affects the right of a creditor or heir, e.g., freeing a slave from wealth entirely covered by debt, or freeing a slave whose value exceeds one-third; the ruling of such freed slave is like a mudabbir before death: he remains a slave in all rulings attached to ownership, and after death he becomes free and pays his value to creditors and heirs.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of death illness (marad al-mawt) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by affirming that a sick person retains full legal capacity for contracts and speech acts; thus his marriage and divorce are valid. However, because death illness is a cause of death, which forces the substitution of the deceased by creditors and heirs, the illness becomes a reason to restrict the sick person's transactions to protect the rights of those who will have claims on the estate. This restriction is not absolute interdiction (hajr) — it only applies when the illness ends in death. At the moment of death, his transactions during illness are deemed to have been under restriction from the start, but only to the extent needed to safeguard creditors' and heirs' rights. The text then specifies that illness only affects transactions involving others' rights; transactions like marriage with proper mahr (which is a basic need) are valid because the right of others only attaches to surplus wealth. All voidable transactions (like gifts and sales below market value) are valid immediately because death is uncertain and there is no immediate harm, but they can be rescinded later if necessary to fulfill debts or protect the bequest limit (one-third). Non-voidable transactions, such as freeing a slave when the estate is insolvent or the slave's value exceeds one-third, are treated like a mudabbir (slave promised freedom upon death): the freed slave remains a slave before death and after death becomes free, but must pay his value to creditors and heirs.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): An illness from which the patient dies; it triggers restrictions on transactions to protect creditors and heirs.
حجر (hajr): Legal interdiction restricting a person's financial transactions.
محابات (muḥābāt): Selling goods below market value; considered a voidable transaction in death illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling of a gift (hibah) made by a person in death illness?
A) It is invalid immediately and no legal effect.
B) It is valid but can be rescinded after death if needed to protect creditors' or heirs' rights.
C) It is valid only if made in writing.
D) It is valid only if the recipient is a relative.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats death illness (marad al-mawt) as a sabab for partial interdiction: transaction restrictions only apply to protect third-party rights, and voidable transactions are valid but rescindable upon need.
