Payment of Kitabah by Heirs of Mukatab
Clarifying the obligation of heirs to pay kitabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qiyas-based derivation to determine the obligation of heirs to pay kitabah upon the death of a mukatab.

Core Idea
The heirs of a mukatab must pay his kitabah from his estate by analogy to the master's need for the payment.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar clarifies the obligation when a mukatab (a slave with a manumission contract) dies before completing payment. The ruling is derived by qiyas (analogy): just as the master requires the kitabah to complete freedom and gain wala (guardianship) from a living mukatab, so too the heirs must pay from the deceased's estate to realize the same goal. Understanding this analogy illuminates how Hanafi usul extends rulings through effective cause (illa).

Guided Path
1
Identify the original case (asl)
The original case is a living mukatab who owes kitabah. The ruling is that the master has the right to demand payment because the master needs the payment to achieve freedom and wala.
The asl is explicit: the master is in need of the kitabah.
2
Extract the effective cause (illa)
The illa is the master's need for the kitabah to complete the manumission and secure wala. This need is the operative reason for the obligation.
The text literally says 'because the master needs wala and the kitabah'.
3
Identify the new case (far')
The new case is a mukatab who dies before completing the kitabah, leaving behind an estate sufficient to cover the remaining amount, while the master is still alive.
The condition: the master is alive and the estate suffices.
4
Apply the analogy
Since the illa (master's need) is present in both cases, the ruling of obligation to pay is transferred. The heirs must pay the kitabah from the estate.
After payment, the remaining wealth is inherited, and the mukatab's children become free.
5
Note the scope and conditions
The analogy holds only if the master is alive and the estate covers the kitabah. If the master is dead or the estate is insufficient, the ruling may differ.
The passage mentions 'an wafa' to emphasize that children should not delay payment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نور الانوار جلد نوم اشرف الانوار شرح اردو کر دے کیونکہ مولی ولاء اور بدل کتابت کا محتاج ہے ایسے ہی جب مکاتب مر جائے اور بدل کتابت کے سلسلے میں استمال چھوڑ جائے جو بدل کتابت کو پورا کر سکے اور آقا زندہ ہے تو مکاتب کے ورثہ اس کو اداہ کردیں موٹی کو دیدیں کیونکہ مولی مکاتب کی آزادی دینے کے لئے بدل کتابت کا ضرورت مند ہے یہاں تک بدل کتابت ادا کرنے کے بعد جو مال مکاتب کا باقی بچے گا وہ ورثہ میں تقسیم کیا جائے گا اور مکاتب کی وہ اولاد جو پیدا ہوئی اور خریدی گئی مکاتب کے زمانہ میں وہ سب آزاد ہو جائیں گے اور وہ خود اپنی زندگی کی آخری لحات میں آزاد ہو جائے گا اور ہم نے " عن وفاء " کا لفظ اس لئے کہا ہے کہ کیونکہ مکاحب کی اولاد کے لئے مناسب نہیں ہے کہ وہ کب کریں اور مکاتب باپ کی بدل کتابت ادا کریں۔
Nur al-Anwar, volume nine, Ashraf al-Anwar, Urdu commentary: because the master needs wala and the kitabah. Similarly, when a mukatab dies and leaves behind in the matter of kitabah something that can fulfill the kitabah and the master is alive, then the heirs of the mukatab should pay it to the master. Because the master is in need of the kitabah to free the mukatab. After paying the kitabah, whatever wealth of the mukatab remains will be divided among the heirs. And the children of the mukatab who were born or purchased during the time of kitabah will all be freed, and he himself will be freed in the last moments of his life. And we said the word 'an wafa' because it is not appropriate for the children of the mukatab to delay and for the mukatab's father to pay the kitabah.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a ruling regarding the mukatab (a slave who has a contract of manumission upon payment of a sum). The author explains that if the mukatab dies before completing the kitabah, his heirs must pay the remaining amount from his estate to the master. The master's need for the payment is analogous to his need for wala (guardianship). After the kitabah is paid, the remaining estate is distributed among the heirs. The children of the mukatab born or acquired during the kitabah period become free automatically. The author mentions 'an wafa' to emphasize that the children should not delay payment.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered a contract with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
بدل کتابت (badal al-kitabah): The agreed sum to be paid for manumission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) His heirs from his estate
B) The master forfeits the amount
C) The mukatab's children must work to pay
D) The state pays the master

Key Takeaway
The obligation of heirs to pay kitabah is established by qiyas on the master's need, ensuring freedom for the mukatab and his children upon payment from the estate.

Types of Ignorance (Jahl) and Their Legal Effects in Hanafi Usul
Classifying ignorance and its legal effects on liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the types of ignorance (jahl) according to Hanafi usul and determine which types excuse liability in matters of hadd and kaffarah.

Core Idea
Ignorance is only an excuse in matters of valid ijtihad or shubha, not when clear texts from Quran and Sunnah are available.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between ignorance that is excusable and ignorance that is not. This classification is fundamental for understanding when a person's lack of knowledge can mitigate legal responsibility in areas like hudud punishments and expiations. In this lesson, we examine the four types of 'invalid ignorance' that do not excuse, and the one type of 'excusable ignorance' that averts punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories of ignorance
The text first states that ignorance (jahl) is of types: jahl batil (invalid ignorance) and jahl fi mawdi' al-ijtihad (ignorance in a place of valid ijtihad). Recognize that the former is never an excuse, while the latter can be.
Jahl batil includes four subtypes listed below.
2
List the four subtypes of jahl batil
The text enumerates: (1) ignorance of a disbeliever after evidences; (2) ignorance of a follower of desire regarding Allah's attributes; (3) ignorance of a rebel regarding liability for property; (4) ignorance of a mujtahid who contradicts clear texts. Note that all share the trait of opposing clear evidence.
These are not accepted as excuses on the Day of Judgment.
3
Understand the legal effect of jahl batil
Jahl batil does not avert liability in this world or the Hereafter. The person remains fully accountable, and hudud and kaffarah apply.
Example: the mujtahid who contradicts a clear Quranic verse is not excused.
4
Understand the legal effect of jahl fi mawdi' al-ijtihad
This type of ignorance is a valid excuse and creates a shubha (doubt) that averts hadd and kaffarah. The text gives examples: a fasting person who thinks cupping breaks the fast (based on a valid ijtihad) and a person who commits zina with his father's slave girl due to doubt about permissibility from interconnected property rights.
Key condition: the person must have a plausible basis for his ignorance, such as a fatwa from a reliable scholar.
5
Apply the classification to the examples and note conditions
For the cupping example, if the fasting person obtained a fatwa from a trusted jurist before breaking the fast, kaffarah is not required. If he did not, he is liable. For the zina case, if the person genuinely believed the slave girl was permissible due to the father-son property connection, hadd is averted; if he knew it was haram, it is imposed.
This shows that ignorance is only excusable when it arises from a legitimate doubt or a valid ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو انواع جهل باطل لا يصح عذراً في الآخرة وجهل صاحب الهوى في صفات الله وجهل الباغي حتى يضمن مال العادل وتقسمه اذا تلفه وجهل من خالف في اجتهاده الكتاب كجهل الشافعي في حل ماتروك التسمية عامداً قياساً على ماتروك التسمية ناسياً فإنه مخالف لقول تعالى {ولا تاكلوا مما لم يذكر اسم الله عليه} والسنة المشهورة كالفتوى ببيع أمهات الأولاد ونحره فالجهل بفتوى بيع أمهات الأولاد جمل من داود الأصفاني وتابعه حيث ذهبوا إلى جواز بيعها لحديث جابر كنا نبيع أمهات الأولاد على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو مخالف للحديث المشهور أعني قوله عليه السلام لامرأة ولدت من سيدها هي معتقة عن دبر منه والجمل في نحوه كجهل الشامي في جواز القضاء بشاهد ويمين فإنه مخالف للحديث المشهور وهو قوله عليه السلام البينة على المدعي واليمين على من أنكر ولو لا من قضى به معاوية وقد نقلنا كل هذا على نحوها قال أسلافنا وإن كنا لم نجر عليه والثاني الجمل في موضع الاجتهاد الصحيح أو في موضع الشبهة وإنه يصلح عذراً وشبهة دارئة للحد والكفارة كالمحتجم الصائم إذا أفطر عمداً بعد الحجامة على ظن أنها فطرته أي إن الحجامة فطرت الصوم حيث لا تلزمه الكفارة لأنه جهل في موضع الاجتهاد الصحيح لأن عند الأوزاعي الحجامة تفطر الصوم لقوله عليه السلام أفطر الحاجم والمحجوم ولكن قال شيخ الإسلام لو لم يستفت فقيها ولم يبلغه الحديث أو بلغه وعرض تأويله تجب عليه الكفارة لأن ظنه حصل في غير موضعه وأما إذا استفتى فقيها يعتمد على فتواه فأفتاه بالقضيب فأفطر بعده عمدا لا تجب الكفارة وكم زنى بجارية والده على ظن أنها تحل له فإن الحد لا يلزمه لأنه ظن في موضع الشبهة إذ الأملاك بين الآباء والأبناء متصلة فيصير شبهة أن ينتفع أحدهم بمال الآخر وأما إذا ظن أنها لا تحل له فإنه يجب الحد حينئذ.
And it (ignorance) is types: (1) Invalid ignorance that is not an excuse in the Hereafter; (2) Ignorance of the follower of desire in matters of Allah's attributes; (3) Ignorance of the rebel until he guarantees the property of the just and divides it if it is destroyed; (4) Ignorance of one who opposes the Book in his ijtihad, like the ignorance of al-Shafi'i regarding the permissibility of [eating] an animal upon which the name [of Allah] was intentionally omitted, analogizing to one who omitted it forgetfully, for it contradicts His saying: {And do not eat from that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned} and the well-known sunnah. Also like the fatwa permitting the sale of ummahat al-awlad (mothers of children), so the ignorance of the fatwa regarding the sale of ummahat al-awlad is a case [like that] of Dawud al-Asfahani and his followers, as they went to the permissibility of selling them based on the hadith of Jabir: 'We used to sell ummahat al-awlad during the time of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him,' but this contradicts the well-known hadith, namely his saying, peace be upon him, to a woman who gave birth from her master: 'She is free upon his death.' And a similar case is like the ignorance of al-Shami regarding the permissibility of judging by one witness and an oath, for it contradicts the well-known hadith, namely his saying, peace be upon him, 'The burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the one who denies,' were it not that Mu'awiyah judged by it. We have narrated all this in its manner; our predecessors said, 'And if we did not dare to [oppose] him.' The second type is ignorance in a place of valid ijtihad or in a place of shubha, and it constitutes a valid excuse and a doubt that averts hadd (fixed punishment) and kaffarah (expiation), like the cupped fasting person who intentionally breaks his fast after cupping, thinking that cupping breaks his fast, so kaffarah is not incumbent upon him because it is ignorance in a place of valid ijtihad, since according to al-Awza'i, cupping breaks the fast due to his saying, peace be upon him, 'The cupper and the cupped have broken their fast.' But Shaykh al-Islam said: If he did not seek a fatwa from a jurist and the hadith did not reach him, or it reached him and he interpreted it away, then kaffarah is incumbent upon him because his assumption occurred outside its proper place. But if he sought a fatwa from a jurist whom he relies upon, and he gave him a fatwa [that it breaks the fast], and he intentionally broke his fast after that, then kaffarah is not obligatory. And likewise, one who commits zina with his father's slave girl thinking she is permissible for him—the hadd is not imposed on him because it is an assumption in a place of shubha, since property rights between fathers and sons are interconnected, thus it becomes a shubha that one of them may benefit from the other's property. But if he assumed that she is not permissible for him, then the hadd is obligatory at that time.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar defines four types of ignorance (jahl) that are not valid excuses in the Hereafter, followed by a fifth type that is a valid excuse. The classification is crucial for understanding when ignorance can mitigate legal liability in Hanafi fiqh. The first type is batil (invalid) ignorance, such as a disbeliever's ignorance of tawhid after clear evidences—it is not accepted on the Day of Judgment. The second is ignorance of the ahl al-hawa (those who follow desires), like the Mu'tazila who deny Allah's attributes, punishment of the grave, seeing Allah, and intercession. The third is ignorance of the baghi (rebel) who rejects a just imam based on a corrupt argument; if he destroys property without an armed force, he is liable, but if he has power, the liability is like that of harbi enemies. The fourth is ignorance of a mujtahid who contradicts the clear text of the Quran or authentic hadith in his ijtihad. The Sharh gives the example of Imam al-Shafi'i's ruling that an animal slaughtered without deliberately pronouncing tasmiyah is halal, by analogy with one who forgets. The Hanafi response argues that this contradicts the Quranic verse (6:121) and the established sunnah. Similarly, Dawud al-Asfahani (Zahiri) permitted selling ummahat al-awlad based on a hadith, but the Hanafis argue against it using the hadith that such a woman becomes free upon the master's death. The Shami (likely referring to a Hanafi) permitted qada' with one witness and an oath, but the author notes that this contradicts the well-known hadith about burden of proof being on the claimant and oath on the denier. The second major category is jahl in a place of valid ijtihad or shubha, which does serve as an excuse. For example, a fasting person who thinks cupping invalidates the fast (following al-Awza'i) and intentionally breaks the fast is not required to perform kaffarah, because his assumption is based on a valid ijtihad. However, Shaykh al-Islam (likely Abu Yusuf or Muhammad) clarifies that if he acted without proper knowledge or seeking fatwa, he is liable. Another example is a person who commits zina with his father's slave girl thinking she is permissible due to the interconnectedness of property between father and son—this doubt averts the hadd punishment. But if he knows she is not permissible, the hadd is imposed. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi principle that ignorance is only an excuse in matters of ijtihad where there is room for legitimate difference of opinion, not when clear texts are available.

Key Terms
جهل باطل (jahl batil): Ignorance that is not accepted as an excuse on the Day of Judgment, such as a disbeliever's ignorance of tawhid after evidences.
جهل في موضع الاجتهاد (jahl fi mawdi' al-ijtihad): Ignorance in a matter that is subject to valid ijtihad, where multiple scholarly opinions exist—this can serve as an excuse.
شبهة (shubha): A doubt or ambiguity that resembles legality, sufficient to avert fixed punishments (hudud).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul text, what is the ruling on eating meat from an animal slaughtered without intentionally pronouncing the name of Allah (tasmiyah) based on analogy with forgetfulness?
A) Halal, by analogy with one who forgets.
B) Haram, because it contradicts the Quranic verse.
C) Permissible only if the slaughterer is a Muslim.
D) The ruling depends on the intention of the butcher.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, ignorance is only a valid excuse when it occurs in matters of legitimate ijtihad or shubha, not when clear textual evidence is available.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Ignorance in Matters of Valid Ijtihad
Second category of excusable ignorance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which ignorance in matters of valid ijtihad serves as a legal excuse (udhr) and apply them to the cupping (hijama) and zina examples.

Core Idea
Ignorance excuses only in matters where valid ijtihad exists, not contradicting clear texts.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi usul principle: ignorance can be a legal excuse, but only when the matter involves a legitimate difference of scholarly opinion. The passage from Nur al-Anwar uses the example of cupping during fasting and zina with a father's slave-girl to illustrate when ignorance removes liability for hadd and kaffarah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
State the rule: ignorance (jahl) is an excusable legal excuse (udhr) in matters where valid ijtihad permits differing opinions, as long as the ijtihad does not contradict the clear Quran and well-known Sunnah.
2
Examine the cupping example
Read the example: a fasting person takes cupping (hijama) believing it breaks the fast (based on a hadith and some scholars' view). After cupping, he intentionally breaks his fast. Apply the principle: does his ignorance excuse him from kaffarah?
The hadith: 'The cupper and the cupped have broken their fast.'
3
Analyse the zina example
Consider a person who commits zina with his father's slave-girl assuming she is permissible. The assumption stems from common property between father and son, creating doubt. Evaluate whether ignorance excuses him from hadd.
The distinction: if he knew she was not permissible, hadd applies.
4
Apply the Khwahar Zadah distinction
Note that not all ijtihad-based ignorance is automatically excused. If the person acted on his own assumption without consulting a scholar, kaffarah may be due. Only if he followed a reliable fatwa does his ignorance become excusable.
This clarifies the boundary: ignorance must arise from following valid ijtihad, not mere whim.
5
State the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a person who cupped and then ate intentionally may or may not owe kaffarah depending on whether he relied on a fatwa or acted independently.

وَالثَّانِي الجمل في موضع الاجتهاد الصحيح (ب) جہل جو ( قرآن و حدیث مشہورہ کے وہ غیر مخالف) اجتہادی مسائل سے یا محل استعباد سے متعلق ہو ان مواقع کا جاہل عذر قرار دیئے جانے کے قابل ہے جس شبہ سے جد اور کفارہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے کا حجم جیسے سینگی لگانے والا روزہ دار اذا الفطر جبکہ افطار کرے میکی لگانے کے بعد جان بوجھ کر علی ظن انها فطرتہ اس گمان ہے کہ اس نے اس کا روزہ توڑ دیا ہے یعنی یہ کہ پچھنے لگوانے سے روزہ ٹوٹ جاتا کہ اس پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ جہالت ایسے موقع پر پائی گئی ہے جس میں بعض مجتہد کا قیاس صحیح (یعنی کتاب اور سنت مشہورہ کے غیر مخالف بھی موجود ہے کیونکہ امام اور اعلی کے نزدیک پچھنے لگوانے سے روزہ ٹوٹ جاتا ہے اس لئے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا افطر الحاجم والمحجوم پچھنے لگانے والا اور لگوانے والا دونوں کا روزہ ٹوٹ گیا لیکن شیخ الاسلام خواہر زادہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ (ماشن کی تقسیم کے بر خلاف) فرمایا ہے کہ حجامت لگانے والے نے افطار سے پہلے اگر کسی فقیہ سے مسئلہ دریافت نہیں کیا اور نہ اس کو مذکورہ حدیث معلوم ہے اگر معلوم تو ہے مگر اس کی صحیح تاویل بھی وہ جانتا ہے ایسی حالت میں اگر اس نے عمد افطار کر لیا ہے تو اس پر کفارہ واجب ہوگا کیونکہ اس صورت میں اس کا گمان بےجا نا قابل اعتبار ہے اور بہر حال جب اس نے کسی نقیہ سے فتوی معلوم کیا جس کے فتوی پر اس کو اعتماد ہے اور اس نے اس کو فتوی دید یا پھر اس نے اس کے بعد محمد افطار کر لیا تو کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ و کمن زنى بجارية والده على ظن أنها تحل له : یا جیسے کوئی شخص اپنے باپ کی باندی سے زنا کر ڈالے اس گمان سے کہ یہ باندی اس کے حق میں بھی حلال ہے تو اس پر حد لازم نہ ہو گی کیونکہ اس نے شبہ کے مقام پر گمان کیا ہے کیونکہ ملکیتیں باپ اور بیٹوں کے درمیان ملی ہوئی ہوتی ہیں اس لئے شبہ پیدا ہو تا یا ہے ایک دوسرے کی چیز سے نفع اٹھا لے لیکن اگر بینے کا گمان یہ تھا کہ یہ باندی میرے لئے حلال نہیں ہے تو اس پر ایسی صورت میں حد جاری ہو گی۔
بِخِلَافِ جَارَيَةِ وَلَدِهِ فَإِنَّهَا تَجِلُّ بِكُلِّ حَالٍ سَوَاءٌ ظَنْ أَنْهَا تَحِلُّ لَهُ أَوْ لَا بِخِلاف جَارَيَةٍ أَخِيْهِ فَإِنَّهَا لا تَحِلُّ لَهُ بِكُلِّ حَالٍ فَلايَسْقُطُ الْحَدُ عَنْهُ لأَن الأَمْلاكَ مُتَبَايِنَةٌ عَادَةُ وَالثَّالِثُ الجَهْلُ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ مِنْ مُسْلِمٍ لَمْ يُهَاجِرُ إِلَيْنَا بِالشَّرَائِمِ وَالْعِبَادَات وَإِنَّهُ يَكُونُ عُدْرًا حَتى لَوْلَمْ يُصَلِّ وَلَمْ يَصتُمْ مُدَةً لَمْ تَبْلُغَة الدعوة لا يَجِبُ قَضاؤُهُمَا لأَنْ دَارُ الْحَرْبِ لَيْسَتْ بِمَحَلٍ لِشهْرَةِ أحكام الإسلام بِخِلافِ الَّذِي إِذَا أَسْلَمَ فِي دَارِ الإسلام فَإِنْ جَهْلَةٌ بِالسَّرَائِمِ لَا يَكُونَ هُدْرًا اِذْرُبَّمَا يُمْكِنُهُ السَّوَالُ عَنْ أَجْكَام الإسلام فَيَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ الْقَضاءُ الصَّلوة وَالصَّوْمِ مِنْ وَقْتِ الإِسْلامِ وَيَلْحَقُ بِهِ أَنْ يَجْهْلِ مَنْ أَسْلَمَ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ فِي كَوْنِهِ عُدْرًا جَهْلُ السَّفِيعِ بِالْبَيْعِ فَإِنَّهُ إِذَا لَمْ يَعْلَمُ بِالْبَيْعِ فَسَكُوتِهِ مَنْ طَلَبِ الشفْعَةِ يَكُونُ عُدْرًا لايَبْطِلُهَا بَعْدَ مَا عَلِمَ بِهِ لا يَكُونُ سُكُوتُهُ عُدْرًا بَلْ تَبْطُلْ بِهِ الشفْعَةُ وَجَهْلُ الآمَةِ بِالإعْتَاقِ أَوْ بِالْخِيَارِ فَإِنَّهُ يَكُونُ عُدْرًا فِي السَّكُوتِ يَعْنِي إِذَا اعْتِقَتِ الأمةُ الْمَنْكُوحَةُ يَثْبُتُ لِهَا الْخِيَارُ بَيْنَ أَن تَبْقَى تَحْتَ تَصَرُّفِ الزوج أَوْلَمْ تَبْقَ فَإِذَا لَمْ تَعْلَمْ بِخَيْرِ الاِعْتَاقِ أَوْ بِأَنَّ الشَّرْعَ أَعْطَاهَا الْخِيَارُ كَانَ جَهْلُهَا عُدْرًا ثُمَّ إِذَا عَلِمَتْ بِالأَعْتَاقِ أَوْ بِمِسْئَلَةِ الْخَيَارِ يَكُونُ لَهَا الْخِيَارُ الآن لأنَّ الْمَوْلَى يَستَبِدُ بِالإعْتَاقِ وَلَعَلَّهُ لَمْ يُخْبِرُهَا بِهِ وَلَأَنْهَا مَشْغُوْلَةٌ بِخِدْمَتِهِ فَلَا تَتَفَرُعُ لِمَعْرِفَةِ أَحْكَام الشرع الَّتِي مِنْ جُمْلَتِهَا الْخِيَارُ وَجَهْلُ الْبِكْرِ بِانْكَاحِ الْوَلَىٰ فَإِنَّهُ يَكُونُ أَيْضًا عُدْرًا فِي السَّكُوتِ يَعْنِى إِذَا زَوْجَ الصَّغِيرَ أَوِ الصَّغْرَةُ غَيْرُ الْآبِ وَالْجَدْ يَصحُ النَّكَاحُ وَيَثْبُتُ لَهُمَا الْخِيَارُ بَعْدَ الْبُلُوغ فَإِنْ جَهْلاً بِخَبَرِ النِّكَاحِ يَكُونُ عُدْرًا حَتَّى يَعْلَمَا وَإِنْ عَلِمًا بِالنِّكَاحِ وَلَمْ يَعْلَمَا بَان الشرْعَ خَيْرَهُمَا لَا يَكُونُ عُدْرًا لأن الدار دَارُ الإِسْلَامِ وَالْمَانِعُ مِنَ التَعَلُّم مَعْدُوْمُ فَلا يَعْدُرُ هَدَ الْجَمَلُ
And the well-known Sunnah: (opposes the famous tradition) like giving a fatwa permitting the sale of 'ummahat al-awlad' (mothers of children) and similar issues. The ignorance of Wali al-Isfahani and his followers regarding the fatwa of selling them arises because they believe in its permissibility based on the hadith of Jabir that they used to sell 'ummahat al-awlad' during the time of the Prophet (PBUH), although this hadith contradicts the well-known hadith: the saying of the Prophet (PBUH) concerning a woman who gave birth from her master's sperm: 'She is free upon his death' and other such issues. An example of ignorance is Imam al-Shafi'i's ignorance regarding the issue of judging based on a single arrow, which contradicts the famous hadith: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the one who denies.' Contrary to this hadith, Amir Muawiyah was the first to judge based on it. Note that we have only transmitted what the early scholars said about the dignity of the imams; we would never dare to call their ijtihad based on ignorance, as there is room for interpretation.
And the second: ignorance in a place of correct ijtihad — ignorance related to matters of ijtihad that are not contrary to the clear Quran and well-known Sunnah, or to matters of istibdad (personal opinion), such a person is excusable. This is because of the doubt that removes the obligation of hadd (punishment) and kaffarah (expiation). For example, a fasting person who takes cupping and then intentionally breaks his fast after cupping, under the assumption that cupping breaks the fast — kaffarah is not obligatory. This is because this ignorance occurs in a place where some mujtahid's valid analogy exists (i.e., not contrary to the clear Quran and well-known Sunnah), because according to Imam Abu Hanifah, cupping breaks the fast, as the Prophet (PBUH) said: 'The cupper and the cupped have broken their fast.' However, Shaykh al-Islam Khwahar Zadah said contrary to the division of the matn: if the cupper did not ask a faqih before breaking his fast, and does not know the above hadith, or knows it but also knows its correct interpretation, then if he intentionally breaks his fast, kaffarah is obligatory because his assumption is invalid. But if he asked a trusted faqih and was given a fatwa, and then intentionally broke his fast, kaffarah is not obligatory. And likewise, a person who commits zina with his father's slave-girl under the assumption that she is permissible for him — hadd punishment is not obligatory because he had doubt; since property is shared between father and son, it creates a doubt. But if his assumption was that she was not permissible for him, then hadd applies. In contrast, the slave-girl of his own son is permissible absolutely, whether he thinks she is permissible or not. The slave-girl of his brother is never permissible, so hadd is not dropped because properties are usually separate. And the third: ignorance in the Abode of War (Dar al-Harb) concerning Islamic laws and worship for a Muslim who did not migrate to us — it is an excuse. If he did not pray or fast for a period because the call of Islam did not reach him, he is not required to make them up because Dar al-Harb is not a place where Islamic rulings are widespread. In contrast, if one embraces Islam in the Abode of Islam, his ignorance of the laws is not an excuse because he can ask about them; so he must make up missed prayers and fasts from the time of his Islam. Attached to this is the ignorance of one who embraces Islam in Dar al-Harb: it is an excuse. Ignorance of the pre-emptor (shafi') about the sale — if he did not know about the sale, his silence regarding shuf'a is an excuse and does not invalidate it. After he knows, his silence is not an excuse and invalidates shuf'a. Ignorance of a slave-woman about her emancipation or about the option (khiyar) — that is an excuse for silence. Meaning, if a married slave-woman is emancipated, she has the option to stay with her husband or leave. If she did not know about the emancipation or that the Shari'ah gave her the option, her ignorance is an excuse. Then when she knows about the emancipation or the issue of option, she has the option now because the master may have secretly emancipated her without telling her, and she is busy with his service so she does not have time to learn applied rulings including the option. Ignorance of a virgin about the marriage contract made by a guardian — it is also an excuse for silence. If a minor boy or girl (other than father or grandfather) is married, the marriage is valid and they have the option upon reaching puberty. If they were ignorant of the marriage, it is an excuse until they know. But if they knew of the marriage and did not know that the Shari'ah gave them an option, that is not an excuse because this is the Abode of Islam and there is no barrier to learning; so they are not excused.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage discusses the categories of ignorance (jahl) that constitute a legal excuse (udhr) in Hanafi fiqh. The author, commenting on the matn of Nur al-Anwar, explains that ignorance can be a legitimate defense in certain contexts, particularly when it involves matters of ijtihad (independent legal reasoning) where a contrary opinion based on valid evidence exists. The first category is ignorance in matters of ijtihad that are not contrary to the clear Quran and well-known Sunnah. An example given is the case of 'ummahat al-awlad' (slave women who have borne children to their master): some scholars, like Wali al-Isfahani, permitted their sale based on a hadith of Jabir, but this contradicts the well-known hadith that such women are free upon the master's death. The author notes that such ignorance from scholars is not blameworthy because it arises from differing ijtihad, not from rejecting clear evidence.

The second category is ignorance in a place where there is a valid ijtihad that is not contrary to explicit texts. The main example is cupping (hijama) during fasting. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, cupping breaks the fast based on a hadith, so a person who breaks his fast after cupping under the assumption that it already broke his fast is excused from kaffarah because there is a valid ijtihad supporting that view. However, Shaykh al-Islam Khwahar Zadah adds that if the person did not consult a scholar and acted on his own assumption, kaffarah is due. But if he consulted a reliable scholar and followed his fatwa, then kaffarah is not due. Another example is zina with the father's slave-girl: if someone assumes she is permissible due to shared ownership, they are excused from the hadd punishment.

The third category is ignorance in Dar al-Harb (a non-Muslim territory where Islamic law is not applied) for a Muslim who did not migrate. His ignorance of prayer and fasting obligations is an excuse because the call of Islam may not have reached him fully. If he converts in Dar al-Harb, he does not have to make up missed acts. However, if he converts in Dar al-Islam, he must make up missed prayers and fasts because he could have learned the rules.

The passage then discusses other specific cases: ignorance of a pre-emptor (shafi') about a sale — if he remains silent due to ignorance, his right of pre-emption is not lost; but once he knows, silence invalidates it. Ignorance of a slave-woman about her emancipation or the option to leave her marriage — she is excused for not immediately exercising her option because she may not have known. Similarly, ignorance of a minor (married by a guardian other than father or grandfather) about the marriage contract itself is an excuse, and they can exercise their option upon puberty. However, if they knew about the marriage but were ignorant of the legal option, that is not an excuse because they could have learned in Dar al-Islam.

Throughout, the author emphasizes that ignorance is evaluated based on context: whether the person could have known, whether there is conflicting scholarly opinion, and whether they acted on genuine doubt.

Key Terms
الجهل (al-jahl): Lack of knowledge or awareness of a ruling.
العذر (al-udhr): A legal excuse that removes culpability or obligation.
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): Independent legal reasoning based on valid sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a fasting person who cupped and then ate intentionally NOT liable for kaffarah?
A) If he assumed cupping breaks the fast but did not ask a scholar.
B) If he asked a reliable scholar and followed his fatwa that cupping breaks the fast.
C) If he knows cupping does not break the fast but eats anyway.
D) Only if he lives in Dar al-Harb.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance excuses only when it arises from following a valid ijtihad-based fatwa in a matter where scholars differ.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
Ignorance in Dar al-Harb as a Legal Excuse
Third category of excusable ignorance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that ignorance of Islamic rulings in Dar al-Harb is an excuse for a Muslim who did not migrate, and distinguish it from the case of conversion in Dar al-Islam.

Core Idea
Ignorance in Dar al-Harb excuses missed prayers and fasts if the call of Islam did not reach the person.

This lesson covers the third category of excusable ignorance in Hanafi usul: ignorance in Dar al-Harb (non-Muslim territory). The rule is lenient because Islamic rulings may not be widespread. The passage also explains that a convert in Dar al-Islam is not excused due to the availability of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Define Dar al-Harb and the condition
Dar al-Harb is a territory where Islamic law is not applied, and the call of Islam may not be effectively propagated. The person in question is a Muslim who did not migrate to Muslim lands.
2
Identify the ruling on missed prayers and fasts
If such a person did not pray or fast for a period because the call of Islam did not reach him, he is not required to make them up (qada) because his ignorance is excusable.
The principle: 'Dar al-Harb is not a place where Islamic rulings are widespread.'
3
Contrast with conversion in Dar al-Islam
If a person embraces Islam in Dar al-Islam, his ignorance of laws is not an excuse because he can ask and learn. He must make up missed prayers and fasts from the time of his conversion.
The availability of knowledge removes the excuse.
4
Apply the rule to Muslims who convert in Dar al-Harb
A person who converts in Dar al-Harb is treated with the same leniency: his ignorance while still in Dar al-Harb is excusable.
This is attached to the third category.
5
State the practical consequence
The difference is significant for making up missed acts: a convert in Dar al-Islam must calculate and make up all missed prayers/fasts; a convert in Dar al-Harb does not.

وَالسَّنَّةُ المَشْهُورَةُ: يا سفت مشہور کی مخالفت کرے) جیسے امہات اولاد کی بیچ کے درست ہونے کا فتوی دینا اسی طرح اس قسم کے دوسرے مسائل میں تو امہات الاولاد کی بیچ کے فتوی کی جہالت و ولز و اصفہانی اور ان کے متبعین سے صادر ہوتی ہے کیونکہ وہ ان کی بیچ کے جواز کے قائل ہیں حدیث جابر کی بناء پر کہ جناب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانے میں ہم احبات الاولاد کی بھی کیا کرتے تھے حالانکہ یہ حدیث، حدیث مشہور کے مخالف ہے یعنی رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا فرمان اس عورت کے متعلق فرمایا جس نے اپنے آتا کے نطفہ سے بچہ جنا تھا ہی معتقة عن دبر منه (یعنی مولی کے مرنے کے بعد یہ آزاد ہے) اور اس قسم کے دوسرے مسائل میں جہالت کی مثال جیسے امام شافعی کی جہالت قضاء کے جواز کے مسئلے میں ایک گولہ اور ایک قسم کی بنیاد پر یہ حدیث مشہور کے مخالف ہے اور وہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا فرمان ہے البينة على المدعى واليمين على من انکر شہادت پیش کرنا صرف مدعی کے ذمہ ہے (اور نیند نہ ہو پر ) قسم مد عاعلیہ کر ہے اور اس حدیث کے بر خلاف سب سے پہلے حضرت امیر معاویہ نے فیصلے فرمائے ہیں واضح رہے کہ اس مقام پر ائمہ مجتہدین کی شان میں علماء سلف نے جو کچھ فرمایا ہے ہم نے صرف اسی کو نقل کر دیا ہے ورنہ ہم ہر گز اس پر جرائت نہیں کر سکتے تھے کہ ایسے ائمہ عظام کے اجتہاد کو مبنی بر جہالت بتائیں باوجود یکہ ان میں تاویلات کی گنجائش بھی موجود ہے۔
وَالثَّانِي الجمل في موضع الاجتهاد الصحيح (ب) جہل جو ( قرآن و حدیث مشہورہ کے وہ غیر مخالف) اجتہادی مسائل سے یا محل استعباد سے متعلق ہو ان مواقع کا جاہل عذر قرار دیئے جانے کے قابل ہے جس شبہ سے جد اور کفارہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے کا حجم جیسے سینگی لگانے والا روزہ دار اذا الفطر جبکہ افطار کرے میکی لگانے کے بعد جان بوجھ کر علی ظن انها فطرتہ اس گمان ہے کہ اس نے اس کا روزہ توڑ دیا ہے یعنی یہ کہ پچھنے لگوانے سے روزہ ٹوٹ جاتا کہ اس پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ جہالت ایسے موقع پر پائی گئی ہے جس میں بعض مجتہد کا قیاس صحیح (یعنی کتاب اور سنت مشہورہ کے غیر مخالف بھی موجود ہے کیونکہ امام اور اعلی کے نزدیک پچھنے لگوانے سے روزہ ٹوٹ جاتا ہے اس لئے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا افطر الحاجم والمحجوم پچھنے لگانے والا اور لگوانے والا دونوں کا روزہ ٹوٹ گیا لیکن شیخ الاسلام خواہر زادہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ (ماشن کی تقسیم کے بر خلاف) فرمایا ہے کہ حجامت لگانے والے نے افطار سے پہلے اگر کسی فقیہ سے مسئلہ دریافت نہیں کیا اور نہ اس کو مذکورہ حدیث معلوم ہے اگر معلوم تو ہے مگر اس کی صحیح تاویل بھی وہ جانتا ہے ایسی حالت میں اگر اس نے عمد افطار کر لیا ہے تو اس پر کفارہ واجب ہوگا کیونکہ اس صورت میں اس کا گمان بےجا نا قابل اعتبار ہے اور بہر حال جب اس نے کسی نقیہ سے فتوی معلوم کیا جس کے فتوی پر اس کو اعتماد ہے اور اس نے اس کو فتوی دید یا پھر اس نے اس کے بعد محمد افطار کر لیا تو کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ و کمن زنى بجارية والده على ظن أنها تحل له : یا جیسے کوئی شخص اپنے باپ کی باندی سے زنا کر ڈالے اس گمان سے کہ یہ باندی اس کے حق میں بھی حلال ہے تو اس پر حد لازم نہ ہو گی کیونکہ اس نے شبہ کے مقام پر گمان کیا ہے کیونکہ ملکیتیں باپ اور بیٹوں کے درمیان ملی ہوئی ہوتی ہیں اس لئے شبہ پیدا ہو تا یا ہے ایک دوسرے کی چیز سے نفع اٹھا لے لیکن اگر بینے کا گمان یہ تھا کہ یہ باندی میرے لئے حلال نہیں ہے تو اس پر ایسی صورت میں حد جاری ہو گی۔
بِخِلَافِ جَارَيَةِ وَلَدِهِ فَإِنَّهَا تَجِلُّ بِكُلِّ حَالٍ سَوَاءٌ ظَنْ أَنْهَا تَحِلُّ لَهُ أَوْ لَا بِخِلاف جَارَيَةٍ أَخِيْهِ فَإِنَّهَا لا تَحِلُّ لَهُ بِكُلِّ حَالٍ فَلايَسْقُطُ الْحَدُ عَنْهُ لأَن الأَمْلاكَ مُتَبَايِنَةٌ عَادَةُ وَالثَّالِثُ الجَهْلُ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ مِنْ مُسْلِمٍ لَمْ يُهَاجِرُ إِلَيْنَا بِالشَّرَائِمِ وَالْعِبَادَات وَإِنَّهُ يَكُونُ عُدْرًا حَتى لَوْلَمْ يُصَلِّ وَلَمْ يَصتُمْ مُدَةً لَمْ تَبْلُغَة الدعوة لا يَجِبُ قَضاؤُهُمَا لأَنْ دَارُ الْحَرْبِ لَيْسَتْ بِمَحَلٍ لِشهْرَةِ أحكام الإسلام بِخِلافِ الَّذِي إِذَا أَسْلَمَ فِي دَارِ الإسلام فَإِنْ جَهْلَةٌ بِالسَّرَائِمِ لَا يَكُونَ هُدْرًا اِذْرُبَّمَا يُمْكِنُهُ السَّوَالُ عَنْ أَجْكَام الإسلام فَيَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ الْقَضاءُ الصَّلوة وَالصَّوْمِ مِنْ وَقْتِ الإِسْلامِ وَيَلْحَقُ بِهِ أَنْ يَجْهْلِ مَنْ أَسْلَمَ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ فِي كَوْنِهِ عُدْرًا جَهْلُ السَّفِيعِ بِالْبَيْعِ فَإِنَّهُ إِذَا لَمْ يَعْلَمُ بِالْبَيْعِ فَسَكُوتِهِ مَنْ طَلَبِ الشفْعَةِ يَكُونُ عُدْرًا لايَبْطِلُهَا بَعْدَ مَا عَلِمَ بِهِ لا يَكُونُ سُكُوتُهُ عُدْرًا بَلْ تَبْطُلْ بِهِ الشفْعَةُ وَجَهْلُ الآمَةِ بِالإعْتَاقِ أَوْ بِالْخِيَارِ فَإِنَّهُ يَكُونُ عُدْرًا فِي السَّكُوتِ يَعْنِي إِذَا اعْتِقَتِ الأمةُ الْمَنْكُوحَةُ يَثْبُتُ لِهَا الْخِيَارُ بَيْنَ أَن تَبْقَى تَحْتَ تَصَرُّفِ الزوج أَوْلَمْ تَبْقَ فَإِذَا لَمْ تَعْلَمْ بِخَيْرِ الاِعْتَاقِ أَوْ بِأَنَّ الشَّرْعَ أَعْطَاهَا الْخِيَارُ كَانَ جَهْلُهَا عُدْرًا ثُمَّ إِذَا عَلِمَتْ بِالأَعْتَاقِ أَوْ بِمِسْئَلَةِ الْخَيَارِ يَكُونُ لَهَا الْخِيَارُ الآن لأنَّ الْمَوْلَى يَستَبِدُ بِالإعْتَاقِ وَلَعَلَّهُ لَمْ يُخْبِرُهَا بِهِ وَلَأَنْهَا مَشْغُوْلَةٌ بِخِدْمَتِهِ فَلَا تَتَفَرُعُ لِمَعْرِفَةِ أَحْكَام الشرع الَّتِي مِنْ جُمْلَتِهَا الْخِيَارُ وَجَهْلُ الْبِكْرِ بِانْكَاحِ الْوَلَىٰ فَإِنَّهُ يَكُونُ أَيْضًا عُدْرًا فِي السَّكُوتِ يَعْنِى إِذَا زَوْجَ الصَّغِيرَ أَوِ الصَّغْرَةُ غَيْرُ الْآبِ وَالْجَدْ يَصحُ النَّكَاحُ وَيَثْبُتُ لَهُمَا الْخِيَارُ بَعْدَ الْبُلُوغ فَإِنْ جَهْلاً بِخَبَرِ النِّكَاحِ يَكُونُ عُدْرًا حَتَّى يَعْلَمَا وَإِنْ عَلِمًا بِالنِّكَاحِ وَلَمْ يَعْلَمَا بَان الشرْعَ خَيْرَهُمَا لَا يَكُونُ عُدْرًا لأن الدار دَارُ الإِسْلَامِ وَالْمَانِعُ مِنَ التَعَلُّم مَعْدُوْمُ فَلا يَعْدُرُ هَدَ الْجَمَلُ
And the well-known Sunnah: (opposes the famous tradition) like giving a fatwa permitting the sale of 'ummahat al-awlad' (mothers of children) and similar issues. The ignorance of Wali al-Isfahani and his followers regarding the fatwa of selling them arises because they believe in its permissibility based on the hadith of Jabir that they used to sell 'ummahat al-awlad' during the time of the Prophet (PBUH), although this hadith contradicts the well-known hadith: the saying of the Prophet (PBUH) concerning a woman who gave birth from her master's sperm: 'She is free upon his death' and other such issues. An example of ignorance is Imam al-Shafi'i's ignorance regarding the issue of judging based on a single arrow, which contradicts the famous hadith: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the one who denies.' Contrary to this hadith, Amir Muawiyah was the first to judge based on it. Note that we have only transmitted what the early scholars said about the dignity of the imams; we would never dare to call their ijtihad based on ignorance, as there is room for interpretation.
And the second: ignorance in a place of correct ijtihad — ignorance related to matters of ijtihad that are not contrary to the clear Quran and well-known Sunnah, or to matters of istibdad (personal opinion), such a person is excusable. This is because of the doubt that removes the obligation of hadd (punishment) and kaffarah (expiation). For example, a fasting person who takes cupping and then intentionally breaks his fast after cupping, under the assumption that cupping breaks the fast — kaffarah is not obligatory. This is because this ignorance occurs in a place where some mujtahid's valid analogy exists (i.e., not contrary to the clear Quran and well-known Sunnah), because according to Imam Abu Hanifah, cupping breaks the fast, as the Prophet (PBUH) said: 'The cupper and the cupped have broken their fast.' However, Shaykh al-Islam Khwahar Zadah said contrary to the division of the matn: if the cupper did not ask a faqih before breaking his fast, and does not know the above hadith, or knows it but also knows its correct interpretation, then if he intentionally breaks his fast, kaffarah is obligatory because his assumption is invalid. But if he asked a trusted faqih and was given a fatwa, and then intentionally broke his fast, kaffarah is not obligatory. And likewise, a person who commits zina with his father's slave-girl under the assumption that she is permissible for him — hadd punishment is not obligatory because he had doubt; since property is shared between father and son, it creates a doubt. But if his assumption was that she was not permissible for him, then hadd applies. In contrast, the slave-girl of his own son is permissible absolutely, whether he thinks she is permissible or not. The slave-girl of his brother is never permissible, so hadd is not dropped because properties are usually separate. And the third: ignorance in the Abode of War (Dar al-Harb) concerning Islamic laws and worship for a Muslim who did not migrate to us — it is an excuse. If he did not pray or fast for a period because the call of Islam did not reach him, he is not required to make them up because Dar al-Harb is not a place where Islamic rulings are widespread. In contrast, if one embraces Islam in the Abode of Islam, his ignorance of the laws is not an excuse because he can ask about them; so he must make up missed prayers and fasts from the time of his Islam. Attached to this is the ignorance of one who embraces Islam in Dar al-Harb: it is an excuse. Ignorance of the pre-emptor (shafi') about the sale — if he did not know about the sale, his silence regarding shuf'a is an excuse and does not invalidate it. After he knows, his silence is not an excuse and invalidates shuf'a. Ignorance of a slave-woman about her emancipation or about the option (khiyar) — that is an excuse for silence. Meaning, if a married slave-woman is emancipated, she has the option to stay with her husband or leave. If she did not know about the emancipation or that the Shari'ah gave her the option, her ignorance is an excuse. Then when she knows about the emancipation or the issue of option, she has the option now because the master may have secretly emancipated her without telling her, and she is busy with his service so she does not have time to learn applied rulings including the option. Ignorance of a virgin about the marriage contract made by a guardian — it is also an excuse for silence. If a minor boy or girl (other than father or grandfather) is married, the marriage is valid and they have the option upon reaching puberty. If they were ignorant of the marriage, it is an excuse until they know. But if they knew of the marriage and did not know that the Shari'ah gave them an option, that is not an excuse because this is the Abode of Islam and there is no barrier to learning; so they are not excused.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage discusses the categories of ignorance (jahl) that constitute a legal excuse (udhr) in Hanafi fiqh. The author, commenting on the matn of Nur al-Anwar, explains that ignorance can be a legitimate defense in certain contexts, particularly when it involves matters of ijtihad (independent legal reasoning) where a contrary opinion based on valid evidence exists. The first category is ignorance in matters of ijtihad that are not contrary to the clear Quran and well-known Sunnah. An example given is the case of 'ummahat al-awlad' (slave women who have borne children to their master): some scholars, like Wali al-Isfahani, permitted their sale based on a hadith of Jabir, but this contradicts the well-known hadith that such women are free upon the master's death. The author notes that such ignorance from scholars is not blameworthy because it arises from differing ijtihad, not from rejecting clear evidence.

The second category is ignorance in a place where there is a valid ijtihad that is not contrary to explicit texts. The main example is cupping (hijama) during fasting. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, cupping breaks the fast based on a hadith, so a person who breaks his fast after cupping under the assumption that it already broke his fast is excused from kaffarah because there is a valid ijtihad supporting that view. However, Shaykh al-Islam Khwahar Zadah adds that if the person did not consult a scholar and acted on his own assumption, kaffarah is due. But if he consulted a reliable scholar and followed his fatwa, then kaffarah is not due. Another example is zina with the father's slave-girl: if someone assumes she is permissible due to shared ownership, they are excused from the hadd punishment.

The third category is ignorance in Dar al-Harb (a non-Muslim territory where Islamic law is not applied) for a Muslim who did not migrate. His ignorance of prayer and fasting obligations is an excuse because the call of Islam may not have reached him fully. If he converts in Dar al-Harb, he does not have to make up missed acts. However, if he converts in Dar al-Islam, he must make up missed prayers and fasts because he could have learned the rules.

The passage then discusses other specific cases: ignorance of a pre-emptor (shafi') about a sale — if he remains silent due to ignorance, his right of pre-emption is not lost; but once he knows, silence invalidates it. Ignorance of a slave-woman about her emancipation or the option to leave her marriage — she is excused for not immediately exercising her option because she may not have known. Similarly, ignorance of a minor (married by a guardian other than father or grandfather) about the marriage contract itself is an excuse, and they can exercise their option upon puberty. However, if they knew about the marriage but were ignorant of the legal option, that is not an excuse because they could have learned in Dar al-Islam.

Throughout, the author emphasizes that ignorance is evaluated based on context: whether the person could have known, whether there is conflicting scholarly opinion, and whether they acted on genuine doubt.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (Dar al-Harb): Territory where Islamic law is not applied and Muslims may face persecution or lack of Islamic education.
الدعوة (al-da'wa): The call of Islam; propagation of Islamic teachings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for ignorance to excuse missed prayers in Dar al-Harb?
A) The person must have intended to migrate.
B) The person must have been Muslim before entering Dar al-Harb.
C) The call of Islam must not have reached the person.
D) The person must not have access to any schools.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance in Dar al-Harb excuses missed acts of worship only if the Islamic call did not reach the individual.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Ignorance in Specific Legal Situations: Shuf'a, Khiyar, and Marriage Options
Specific applications of excusable ignorance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of excusable ignorance to the cases of shuf'a (pre-emption), khiyar (option) for a emancipated slave-woman, and khiyar for a minor upon puberty.

Core Idea
Ignorance of a right or option can excuse silence; once knowledge is obtained, silence is no longer excused.

The passage concludes with three specific applications of excusable ignorance: the right of pre-emption when unaware of a sale, a slave-woman's option after emancipation, and a minor's option after being married by a guardian. These illustrate how ignorance affects the validity of silence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general principle
Silence (sukut) has legal effects: if a person with a right remains silent while knowing their right, it may indicate consent or forfeit. Ignorance of the right excuses silence and preserves the right.
2
Examine the shuf'a (pre-emption) case
A person entitled to shuf'a (right of first refusal when a neighboring property is sold) remains silent because he did not know about the sale. His ignorance is an excuse, he does not lose his right. Once he knows, any further silence invalidates his right.
3
Examine the slave-woman's option
A married slave-woman is emancipated. She has the option to stay with her husband or leave. If she did not know about her emancipation or the legal option, her silence is excused. When she finds out, she can exercise the option.
She is busy with service; may not have time to learn legal details.
4
Examine the minor's option
A minor boy or girl married by a guardian other than father/grandfather has an option upon puberty. If they were ignorant of the marriage itself, their silence is excused. Once they know, they must exercise the option quickly.
If they knew about the marriage but not the legal option, that ignorance is not excused because they could have learned in Dar al-Islam.
5
Extract the underlying rule
The rule: ignorance is an excuse for silence regarding rights when it is genuinely hard to know (e.g., not informed, preoccupied with service). But in Dar al-Islam, ignorance of the legal consequence (khiyar) after knowing the event is not excused.

وَالسَّنَّةُ المَشْهُورَةُ: يا سفت مشہور کی مخالفت کرے) جیسے امہات اولاد کی بیچ کے درست ہونے کا فتوی دینا اسی طرح اس قسم کے دوسرے مسائل میں تو امہات الاولاد کی بیچ کے فتوی کی جہالت و ولز و اصفہانی اور ان کے متبعین سے صادر ہوتی ہے کیونکہ وہ ان کی بیچ کے جواز کے قائل ہیں حدیث جابر کی بناء پر کہ جناب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانے میں ہم احبات الاولاد کی بھی کیا کرتے تھے حالانکہ یہ حدیث، حدیث مشہور کے مخالف ہے یعنی رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا فرمان اس عورت کے متعلق فرمایا جس نے اپنے آتا کے نطفہ سے بچہ جنا تھا ہی معتقة عن دبر منه (یعنی مولی کے مرنے کے بعد یہ آزاد ہے) اور اس قسم کے دوسرے مسائل میں جہالت کی مثال جیسے امام شافعی کی جہالت قضاء کے جواز کے مسئلے میں ایک گولہ اور ایک قسم کی بنیاد پر یہ حدیث مشہور کے مخالف ہے اور وہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا فرمان ہے البينة على المدعى واليمين على من انکر شہادت پیش کرنا صرف مدعی کے ذمہ ہے (اور نیند نہ ہو پر ) قسم مد عاعلیہ کر ہے اور اس حدیث کے بر خلاف سب سے پہلے حضرت امیر معاویہ نے فیصلے فرمائے ہیں واضح رہے کہ اس مقام پر ائمہ مجتہدین کی شان میں علماء سلف نے جو کچھ فرمایا ہے ہم نے صرف اسی کو نقل کر دیا ہے ورنہ ہم ہر گز اس پر جرائت نہیں کر سکتے تھے کہ ایسے ائمہ عظام کے اجتہاد کو مبنی بر جہالت بتائیں باوجود یکہ ان میں تاویلات کی گنجائش بھی موجود ہے۔
وَالثَّانِي الجمل في موضع الاجتهاد الصحيح (ب) جہل جو ( قرآن و حدیث مشہورہ کے وہ غیر مخالف) اجتہادی مسائل سے یا محل استعباد سے متعلق ہو ان مواقع کا جاہل عذر قرار دیئے جانے کے قابل ہے جس شبہ سے جد اور کفارہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے کا حجم جیسے سینگی لگانے والا روزہ دار اذا الفطر جبکہ افطار کرے میکی لگانے کے بعد جان بوجھ کر علی ظن انها فطرتہ اس گمان ہے کہ اس نے اس کا روزہ توڑ دیا ہے یعنی یہ کہ پچھنے لگوانے سے روزہ ٹوٹ جاتا کہ اس پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ جہالت ایسے موقع پر پائی گئی ہے جس میں بعض مجتہد کا قیاس صحیح (یعنی کتاب اور سنت مشہورہ کے غیر مخالف بھی موجود ہے کیونکہ امام اور اعلی کے نزدیک پچھنے لگوانے سے روزہ ٹوٹ جاتا ہے اس لئے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا افطر الحاجم والمحجوم پچھنے لگانے والا اور لگوانے والا دونوں کا روزہ ٹوٹ گیا لیکن شیخ الاسلام خواہر زادہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ (ماشن کی تقسیم کے بر خلاف) فرمایا ہے کہ حجامت لگانے والے نے افطار سے پہلے اگر کسی فقیہ سے مسئلہ دریافت نہیں کیا اور نہ اس کو مذکورہ حدیث معلوم ہے اگر معلوم تو ہے مگر اس کی صحیح تاویل بھی وہ جانتا ہے ایسی حالت میں اگر اس نے عمد افطار کر لیا ہے تو اس پر کفارہ واجب ہوگا کیونکہ اس صورت میں اس کا گمان بےجا نا قابل اعتبار ہے اور بہر حال جب اس نے کسی نقیہ سے فتوی معلوم کیا جس کے فتوی پر اس کو اعتماد ہے اور اس نے اس کو فتوی دید یا پھر اس نے اس کے بعد محمد افطار کر لیا تو کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ و کمن زنى بجارية والده على ظن أنها تحل له : یا جیسے کوئی شخص اپنے باپ کی باندی سے زنا کر ڈالے اس گمان سے کہ یہ باندی اس کے حق میں بھی حلال ہے تو اس پر حد لازم نہ ہو گی کیونکہ اس نے شبہ کے مقام پر گمان کیا ہے کیونکہ ملکیتیں باپ اور بیٹوں کے درمیان ملی ہوئی ہوتی ہیں اس لئے شبہ پیدا ہو تا یا ہے ایک دوسرے کی چیز سے نفع اٹھا لے لیکن اگر بینے کا گمان یہ تھا کہ یہ باندی میرے لئے حلال نہیں ہے تو اس پر ایسی صورت میں حد جاری ہو گی۔
بِخِلَافِ جَارَيَةِ وَلَدِهِ فَإِنَّهَا تَجِلُّ بِكُلِّ حَالٍ سَوَاءٌ ظَنْ أَنْهَا تَحِلُّ لَهُ أَوْ لَا بِخِلاف جَارَيَةٍ أَخِيْهِ فَإِنَّهَا لا تَحِلُّ لَهُ بِكُلِّ حَالٍ فَلايَسْقُطُ الْحَدُ عَنْهُ لأَن الأَمْلاكَ مُتَبَايِنَةٌ عَادَةُ وَالثَّالِثُ الجَهْلُ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ مِنْ مُسْلِمٍ لَمْ يُهَاجِرُ إِلَيْنَا بِالشَّرَائِمِ وَالْعِبَادَات وَإِنَّهُ يَكُونُ عُدْرًا حَتى لَوْلَمْ يُصَلِّ وَلَمْ يَصتُمْ مُدَةً لَمْ تَبْلُغَة الدعوة لا يَجِبُ قَضاؤُهُمَا لأَنْ دَارُ الْحَرْبِ لَيْسَتْ بِمَحَلٍ لِشهْرَةِ أحكام الإسلام بِخِلافِ الَّذِي إِذَا أَسْلَمَ فِي دَارِ الإسلام فَإِنْ جَهْلَةٌ بِالسَّرَائِمِ لَا يَكُونَ هُدْرًا اِذْرُبَّمَا يُمْكِنُهُ السَّوَالُ عَنْ أَجْكَام الإسلام فَيَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ الْقَضاءُ الصَّلوة وَالصَّوْمِ مِنْ وَقْتِ الإِسْلامِ وَيَلْحَقُ بِهِ أَنْ يَجْهْلِ مَنْ أَسْلَمَ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ فِي كَوْنِهِ عُدْرًا جَهْلُ السَّفِيعِ بِالْبَيْعِ فَإِنَّهُ إِذَا لَمْ يَعْلَمُ بِالْبَيْعِ فَسَكُوتِهِ مَنْ طَلَبِ الشفْعَةِ يَكُونُ عُدْرًا لايَبْطِلُهَا بَعْدَ مَا عَلِمَ بِهِ لا يَكُونُ سُكُوتُهُ عُدْرًا بَلْ تَبْطُلْ بِهِ الشفْعَةُ وَجَهْلُ الآمَةِ بِالإعْتَاقِ أَوْ بِالْخِيَارِ فَإِنَّهُ يَكُونُ عُدْرًا فِي السَّكُوتِ يَعْنِي إِذَا اعْتِقَتِ الأمةُ الْمَنْكُوحَةُ يَثْبُتُ لِهَا الْخِيَارُ بَيْنَ أَن تَبْقَى تَحْتَ تَصَرُّفِ الزوج أَوْلَمْ تَبْقَ فَإِذَا لَمْ تَعْلَمْ بِخَيْرِ الاِعْتَاقِ أَوْ بِأَنَّ الشَّرْعَ أَعْطَاهَا الْخِيَارُ كَانَ جَهْلُهَا عُدْرًا ثُمَّ إِذَا عَلِمَتْ بِالأَعْتَاقِ أَوْ بِمِسْئَلَةِ الْخَيَارِ يَكُونُ لَهَا الْخِيَارُ الآن لأنَّ الْمَوْلَى يَستَبِدُ بِالإعْتَاقِ وَلَعَلَّهُ لَمْ يُخْبِرُهَا بِهِ وَلَأَنْهَا مَشْغُوْلَةٌ بِخِدْمَتِهِ فَلَا تَتَفَرُعُ لِمَعْرِفَةِ أَحْكَام الشرع الَّتِي مِنْ جُمْلَتِهَا الْخِيَارُ وَجَهْلُ الْبِكْرِ بِانْكَاحِ الْوَلَىٰ فَإِنَّهُ يَكُونُ أَيْضًا عُدْرًا فِي السَّكُوتِ يَعْنِى إِذَا زَوْجَ الصَّغِيرَ أَوِ الصَّغْرَةُ غَيْرُ الْآبِ وَالْجَدْ يَصحُ النَّكَاحُ وَيَثْبُتُ لَهُمَا الْخِيَارُ بَعْدَ الْبُلُوغ فَإِنْ جَهْلاً بِخَبَرِ النِّكَاحِ يَكُونُ عُدْرًا حَتَّى يَعْلَمَا وَإِنْ عَلِمًا بِالنِّكَاحِ وَلَمْ يَعْلَمَا بَان الشرْعَ خَيْرَهُمَا لَا يَكُونُ عُدْرًا لأن الدار دَارُ الإِسْلَامِ وَالْمَانِعُ مِنَ التَعَلُّم مَعْدُوْمُ فَلا يَعْدُرُ هَدَ الْجَمَلُ
And the well-known Sunnah: (opposes the famous tradition) like giving a fatwa permitting the sale of 'ummahat al-awlad' (mothers of children) and similar issues. The ignorance of Wali al-Isfahani and his followers regarding the fatwa of selling them arises because they believe in its permissibility based on the hadith of Jabir that they used to sell 'ummahat al-awlad' during the time of the Prophet (PBUH), although this hadith contradicts the well-known hadith: the saying of the Prophet (PBUH) concerning a woman who gave birth from her master's sperm: 'She is free upon his death' and other such issues. An example of ignorance is Imam al-Shafi'i's ignorance regarding the issue of judging based on a single arrow, which contradicts the famous hadith: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the one who denies.' Contrary to this hadith, Amir Muawiyah was the first to judge based on it. Note that we have only transmitted what the early scholars said about the dignity of the imams; we would never dare to call their ijtihad based on ignorance, as there is room for interpretation.
And the second: ignorance in a place of correct ijtihad — ignorance related to matters of ijtihad that are not contrary to the clear Quran and well-known Sunnah, or to matters of istibdad (personal opinion), such a person is excusable. This is because of the doubt that removes the obligation of hadd (punishment) and kaffarah (expiation). For example, a fasting person who takes cupping and then intentionally breaks his fast after cupping, under the assumption that cupping breaks the fast — kaffarah is not obligatory. This is because this ignorance occurs in a place where some mujtahid's valid analogy exists (i.e., not contrary to the clear Quran and well-known Sunnah), because according to Imam Abu Hanifah, cupping breaks the fast, as the Prophet (PBUH) said: 'The cupper and the cupped have broken their fast.' However, Shaykh al-Islam Khwahar Zadah said contrary to the division of the matn: if the cupper did not ask a faqih before breaking his fast, and does not know the above hadith, or knows it but also knows its correct interpretation, then if he intentionally breaks his fast, kaffarah is obligatory because his assumption is invalid. But if he asked a trusted faqih and was given a fatwa, and then intentionally broke his fast, kaffarah is not obligatory. And likewise, a person who commits zina with his father's slave-girl under the assumption that she is permissible for him — hadd punishment is not obligatory because he had doubt; since property is shared between father and son, it creates a doubt. But if his assumption was that she was not permissible for him, then hadd applies. In contrast, the slave-girl of his own son is permissible absolutely, whether he thinks she is permissible or not. The slave-girl of his brother is never permissible, so hadd is not dropped because properties are usually separate. And the third: ignorance in the Abode of War (Dar al-Harb) concerning Islamic laws and worship for a Muslim who did not migrate to us — it is an excuse. If he did not pray or fast for a period because the call of Islam did not reach him, he is not required to make them up because Dar al-Harb is not a place where Islamic rulings are widespread. In contrast, if one embraces Islam in the Abode of Islam, his ignorance of the laws is not an excuse because he can ask about them; so he must make up missed prayers and fasts from the time of his Islam. Attached to this is the ignorance of one who embraces Islam in Dar al-Harb: it is an excuse. Ignorance of the pre-emptor (shafi') about the sale — if he did not know about the sale, his silence regarding shuf'a is an excuse and does not invalidate it. After he knows, his silence is not an excuse and invalidates shuf'a. Ignorance of a slave-woman about her emancipation or about the option (khiyar) — that is an excuse for silence. Meaning, if a married slave-woman is emancipated, she has the option to stay with her husband or leave. If she did not know about the emancipation or that the Shari'ah gave her the option, her ignorance is an excuse. Then when she knows about the emancipation or the issue of option, she has the option now because the master may have secretly emancipated her without telling her, and she is busy with his service so she does not have time to learn applied rulings including the option. Ignorance of a virgin about the marriage contract made by a guardian — it is also an excuse for silence. If a minor boy or girl (other than father or grandfather) is married, the marriage is valid and they have the option upon reaching puberty. If they were ignorant of the marriage, it is an excuse until they know. But if they knew of the marriage and did not know that the Shari'ah gave them an option, that is not an excuse because this is the Abode of Islam and there is no barrier to learning; so they are not excused.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage discusses the categories of ignorance (jahl) that constitute a legal excuse (udhr) in Hanafi fiqh. The author, commenting on the matn of Nur al-Anwar, explains that ignorance can be a legitimate defense in certain contexts, particularly when it involves matters of ijtihad (independent legal reasoning) where a contrary opinion based on valid evidence exists. The first category is ignorance in matters of ijtihad that are not contrary to the clear Quran and well-known Sunnah. An example given is the case of 'ummahat al-awlad' (slave women who have borne children to their master): some scholars, like Wali al-Isfahani, permitted their sale based on a hadith of Jabir, but this contradicts the well-known hadith that such women are free upon the master's death. The author notes that such ignorance from scholars is not blameworthy because it arises from differing ijtihad, not from rejecting clear evidence.

The second category is ignorance in a place where there is a valid ijtihad that is not contrary to explicit texts. The main example is cupping (hijama) during fasting. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, cupping breaks the fast based on a hadith, so a person who breaks his fast after cupping under the assumption that it already broke his fast is excused from kaffarah because there is a valid ijtihad supporting that view. However, Shaykh al-Islam Khwahar Zadah adds that if the person did not consult a scholar and acted on his own assumption, kaffarah is due. But if he consulted a reliable scholar and followed his fatwa, then kaffarah is not due. Another example is zina with the father's slave-girl: if someone assumes she is permissible due to shared ownership, they are excused from the hadd punishment.

The third category is ignorance in Dar al-Harb (a non-Muslim territory where Islamic law is not applied) for a Muslim who did not migrate. His ignorance of prayer and fasting obligations is an excuse because the call of Islam may not have reached him fully. If he converts in Dar al-Harb, he does not have to make up missed acts. However, if he converts in Dar al-Islam, he must make up missed prayers and fasts because he could have learned the rules.

The passage then discusses other specific cases: ignorance of a pre-emptor (shafi') about a sale — if he remains silent due to ignorance, his right of pre-emption is not lost; but once he knows, silence invalidates it. Ignorance of a slave-woman about her emancipation or the option to leave her marriage — she is excused for not immediately exercising her option because she may not have known. Similarly, ignorance of a minor (married by a guardian other than father or grandfather) about the marriage contract itself is an excuse, and they can exercise their option upon puberty. However, if they knew about the marriage but were ignorant of the legal option, that is not an excuse because they could have learned in Dar al-Islam.

Throughout, the author emphasizes that ignorance is evaluated based on context: whether the person could have known, whether there is conflicting scholarly opinion, and whether they acted on genuine doubt.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): Right of pre-emption: an owner of a property to step into the shoes of the buyer and acquire the sold property under the same conditions.
الخيار (al-khiyar): Option or choice; especially the option to annul a marriage or stay.
السكوت (al-sukut): Silence; legally significant when it indicates consent or abandonment of a right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a minor knows about his marriage but does not know he has an option to annul upon puberty?
A) He loses the option because ignorance is not excused in Dar al-Islam.
B) He retains the option because ignorance is excused.
C) He loses the option only if he was an adult.
D) He retains the option if no one told him about it.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance of a fact (event) excuses silence and preserves rights; ignorance of a legal consequence (after knowing the fact) is not excused in Dar al-Islam.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Shubha and Custom in Hadd for Zina
Ruling on shubha as a bar to hadd in zina with father's slave-girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of shubha to determine whether hadd punishment is dropped, based on the presence of intermixing (khultat) or distinct ownership (mubayanah).

Core Idea
A shubha that bars hadd must be objectively reasonable based on custom, not just a personal mistake.

In this lesson, we examine a classic Hanafi ruling on how the concept of shubha (legal doubt) operates as a bar to the hadd punishment for zina. The passage from Ashraf al-Anwar uses three scenarios—father's, son's, and brother's slave-girl—to illustrate when shubha is present and when it is not. By analyzing these cases, you will understand the Hanafi method of evaluating custom (urf) in determining shubha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three cases
List the three distinct scenarios presented: zina with father's slave-girl, with son's slave-girl, and with brother's slave-girl.
2
Determine the ruling for each case
For father's: no hadd; for son's: no hadd (since permissible); for brother's: hadd applies.
Note that the son's case is dropped because the act is inherently permissible, not due to shubha.
3
Extract the underlying criterion
Identify the factor that distinguishes father's case from brother's: intermixing of properties (khultat) vs. distinct ownership (mubayanah) based on custom.
Custom (urf) is the basis for evaluating shubha.
4
Apply the principle to new scenarios
Generalize: any situation where custom suggests possible permissibility due to ownership intermixing may create shubha and bar hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و كمن زنى بجارية والده على ظن أنها تحل له : فلا حد عليه لأن شبهة الخلطة توجب الشبهة . بخلاف جارية ولده فإنها تجل بكل حال سواء ظن أنها تحل له أو لا . بخلاف جارية أخيه فإنها لا تحل له بكل حال فلا يسقط الحد عنه لأن الأموال متباينة عادة .
And like one who commits zina with his father's slave-girl, thinking she is permissible for him: then no hadd is upon him because the doubt of intermixing causes doubt. Unlike his son's slave-girl, for she is permissible in every case, whether he thinks she is permissible for him or not. Unlike his brother's slave-girl, for she is not permissible for him in any case, so the hadd is not dropped from him because properties are customarily distinct.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the effect of shubha (doubt) in criminal law, specifically regarding the hadd punishment for zina. The author states that if a man commits zina with his father's slave-girl, mistakenly believing she is permissible for him (due to shared ownership in the household), he is not liable for hadd because the shubha arises from the intermixing of properties between father and son. In contrast, a father's zina with his son's slave-girl is not punishable because she is halal for the father in all circumstances (ownership transfers). As for a brother's slave-girl, she is never halal for the brother, and since properties of brothers are customarily distinct, no shubha exists, so hadd is applied. The ruling illustrates how the Hanafi school considers social customs and likely possibilities when determining the presence of shubha that bars punishment.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubhah): A legal doubt that prevents application of hadd punishment; here it is caused by the intermixing of ownership.
خلطة (khultah): Intermixing or intermingling of property, which creates a reasonable doubt of permissibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on hadd for a man who commits zina with his brother's slave-girl?
A) Hadd is applied because properties of brothers are customarily distinct.
B) Hadd is dropped because of shubha from family relationship.
C) Hadd is applied only if the man admits guilt.
D) Hadd is dropped if the man was ignorant of the prohibition.

Key Takeaway
Shubha that bars hadd must be objectively grounded in custom, not mere personal mistake.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Ignorance as a Legal Excuse in Hanafi Fiqh: Types and Conditions
Explains the Hanafi rule on ignorance as an excuse through multiple case studies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify types of ignorance (jahl) that serve as legal excuses ('udhr) in Hanafi fiqh and apply the condition of ease of knowledge to determine when ignorance is excused.

Core Idea
Ignorance excuses only when obtaining knowledge is impossible or extremely difficult.

In Hanafi legal theory, ignorance of a ruling or fact can sometimes exempt a person from liability. But this is not universal: the key is whether the person had reasonable access to knowledge. This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Anwar illustrates several scenarios where ignorance is accepted as an excuse and others where it is not. By studying these examples, we derive the underlying principle: al-'udhr bi al-jahl muqayyad bi al-imkan (excuse by ignorance is conditioned on possibility of knowledge).

Guided Path
1
Identify the person and the fact
For each case, note who is ignorant and what they are ignorant of (fact or ruling).
E.g., father ignorant of prohibition regarding son's slave-girl, Muslim in dar al-harb ignorant of prayer obligation.
2
Assess the context
Determine the environment: dar al-harb vs dar al-islam, ease of obtaining knowledge, social customs (urf).
3
Classify the ignorance
Distinguish between jahl al-hukm (ignorance of the ruling) and jahl al-waqi' (ignorance of the fact), as each may be treated differently.
Example: slave-girl's ignorance of her freedom is jahl al-waqi‘; virgin's ignorance of the option is jahl al-hukm.
4
Apply the principle of istita‘a
If the person could not reasonably acquire knowledge (due to location, circumstances, or custom), ignorance is an excuse. If they could have learned, it is not.
This aligns with Quran 2:286: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond what it can bear.'
5
Determine the legal consequence
If excused, liability is dropped (e.g., no hadd, no qada'). If not excused, the default ruling applies (e.g., qada' obligatory, right lost).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الانواز شریح حامد دو نور الانوار جلد سوم ترجمه تشریح بخلاف جَارِبَةِ وَلَدِهِ الح: - البتہ لڑکے کی باندی کا حکم اس کے خلاف ہے (کہ باپ اگر اس سے زنا کرلے تو حدیث کی رونے) تو یہ باندی باپ کے حق میں ہر حال میں حلال ہے خواہ باپ نے اپنے لئے اس کے حلال ہونے کا گمان کیا ہو یا نہ کیا ہو بخلاف اپنے بھائی کی باندی کے کہ یہ بھائی کے لئے کسی حال میں حلال نہیں ہے لہذا اس سے صد ساقط نہ ہو گی کیونکہ عادت اور عرف یہ ہے کہ بھائیوں کی املاک جدا جدا ہوتی ہیں۔ والثالث الجَمَلُ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ مِنْ مُسلِم لَمْ يُبَاجِرُ إِلَيْنَا :- (ج) وہ جہل جو دار الحرب میں کسی مسلمان سے پایا جائے جس نے اب تک دار الاسلام کی طرف ہجرت نہیں کی ہے۔ یعنی عبادات اور احکام شرعیہ سے متعلق وانہ یکون عذر ابلا شبہ اس کا جہل عذر ہے حتی کہ اگر اس نے نماز نہیں پڑھی یا روزہ نہیں رکھا اس مدت تک کہ اس کو دعوت اسلام نہیں پہونچ سکی تو ان دونوں کی قضاء اس پر واجب نہیں ہیں کیونکہ دار الحرب اسلامی احکام کی شہرت کا مقام نہیں ہے اس کے بر خلاف کوئی ذمی اگر وابر الاسلام میں رہ کر ایمان قبول کر لے تو احکام شرعیہ سے اس کی جہالت عذر نہ بھی جائے گی کیونکہ موقع بہ موقع پوچھ پانچھ کر اسلام کے احکام معلوم کر سکتا ہے۔ لہذا اس کے ذمہ اسلام قبول کرنے کے وقت سے نماز روزہ کی قضاء واجب ہو گئی ولحق بہ اور ملحق ہے اس کے ساتھ یعنی دار الحرب میں رہ کر اسلام قبول کر لینے سے مسلمان کے عذر کے ساتھ جهل الشفيع بالبيع شفیع کی جہالت بیچ کے بارے میں کیو نکہ جب شفیع نے بیچ کو نہیں جانا تو حق سکوت عذر شمار نہ ہو گا بلکہ اس سکوت سے حق شفع باطل ہو جائے گا۔ وَجَمل الأمة بِالأعْتَاقِ او بالخيار: اور باندی کی جہالت آزاد ہونے یا خیار حق ہے کہ اس کا سکوت بھی عذر شمار ہوگا صورت یہ ہے کہ جب منکوحہ باندی کو آزادی مل گئی تو اس بات کا اختیار حاصل ہو جاتا ہے کہ موجودہ شوہر کے تصرف میں ہاتی رہے یا باقی نہ رہے اور جب اس نے اپنے آزاد ہونے کی خبر نہیں جانا یا اس مسئلے کو نہیں جان سکی کہ شریعت اسلام نے ایسے موقع پر باندی کو خیار کا حق دیا ہے تو اس کی جہالت عذر کبھی جائے گی پھر جب اپنی آزادی کو جان گئی یا اس مسئلے سے واقف ہو گئی تو اب اس کو اختیار حاصل ہو گا کیونکہ آتا ہی اس کے آزاد کرنے کا تنہا مالک ہے اس لئے باندی کو خبر نہ کرنے کا امکان موجود ہے نیز چونکہ باندی ہر وقت آقا کی خدمتوں میں مصروف کار ہے اس لئے اس کو احکام شریعت سے واقف ہونے کا موقع نہ مل سکا اور انہیں احکام میں سے خیار کا حق بھی ہے۔ وَجَهْلُ البِكْرِ بِالْكَاحِ الوَلی: - اور باکرہ (بالغہ ) کی ناواقفیت ولی کے نکاح کر دینے کے سلسلے میں تو یہ صورت بھی سکوت میں عذر شمار ہو گی۔ یعنی جب باپ اور دادا کے سواء کسی دوسرے ولی نے صغیر یا صغیرہ کو نکاح کر دیا تو نکاح درست ہے مگر دونوں خیار حاصل رہیگا کہ بالغ ہونے کے بعد اس نکاح کو باقی رکھیں یا ضخ کر دیں۔ پس اگر یہ نکاح کئے جانے کی خبر سے ناواقف اور جاہل رہے تو یہ جہالت عذر شمار ہو گی۔ حتی کہ دونوں اس خبر کو جان جائیں اور اگر دونوں نے نکاح کی خبر تو سن لی اور نکاح سے واقف ہو گئے مگر مسئلہ خیار کا معلوم نہیں تھا یہ معلوم نہ تھا کہ شریعت نے نکاح باقی رکھنے یا توڑنے کا اختیار ان کو بالغ ہونے کے بعد عطا کیا ہے تو اس جہالت کو عذر نہ قرار دیا جائیگا، اس واسطے کہ دار، دار الاسلام ہے اور علوم دینیہ کے حاصل کرنے سے رکاوٹ معدوم ہے جہاں چاہتے اور جب چاہتے علم دین حاصل کر سکتے تھے لہذا یہ جہالت عذر میں شمار نہ ہو گی۔ وَجَهْلُ الوَكِيلِ وَالْمَادُونَ بِالإِطْلَاقِ وَضِدْهِ فَإِنَّ الْوَكِيلُ وَالْمَادُونَ إِذَا لَمْ يَعْلَمَا بالإطلاق أى بالوَكَالةِ وَالإِذْنِ وَضَدْهِ أَى بِالْعَزلِ وَالْحَجْرِ فَتَصَرْفَا قَبْلَ بُلُوغ الخبر اليْمَا فَهَذَا الجَملُ مِنْهُمَا يَكُونُ عُدْرًا فَلَمْ يَنْقُدْ تَصرفُهُما عَلى المُؤكل والمولى في الصورة الأولى لأنهُمَا لَمْ يَعْلَمَا بِأَمْرِهِمَا وَيَنْقُذُ تَصَرُّفَهُمَا عَلَيْهِمَا الصورَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ لأَنَّهُمَا لَمْ يَعْلَمَا بِحِجْرِهِمَا
The commentary explains: Contrary to the son's slave-girl, the father's ruling is different (if the father commits zina with her, the hadd punishment is not applied); this slave-girl is lawful for the father in all cases, whether he assumed she was lawful for him or not, unlike the brother's slave-girl who is not lawful for the brother in any case, so the hadd is not dropped because custom and ‘urf are that brothers' properties are separate. Third: ignorance in dar al-harb of a Muslim who has not migrated to us: that is ignorance found in a Muslim in dar al-harb who has not yet migrated to dar al-islam, concerning worship and shari‘ah rulings, and it is an excuse. If he did not pray or fast until the da‘wah of Islam reached him, then qada' of these is not obligatory on him because dar al-harb is not a place where Islamic rulings are well-known. In contrast, a dhimmi who accepts Islam while in dar al-islam, his ignorance of shari‘ah rulings is not an excuse because he could inquire and learn. So qada' of prayer and fast becomes obligatory from the time of acceptance of Islam. Attached to this is the ignorance of the shafi‘ (pre-emptor) regarding the sale: when the shafi‘ did not know about the sale, his silence is not an excuse but rather his right of pre-emption becomes void. And the ignorance of the slave-girl regarding emancipation or option: her silence is an excuse. When a married slave-girl is freed, she has the option to remain with her husband or not. If she did not know of her freedom or the legal ruling, her ignorance is an excuse; once she knows, she has the option. And the ignorance of the virgin (adult) regarding marriage by a guardian: when a guardian other than father/grandfather marries a minor, the marriage is valid but both have the option upon reaching majority. If they were ignorant of the marriage, that ignorance is an excuse; if they knew of the marriage but not the option, ignorance is not an excuse in dar al-islam because they could learn. And the ignorance of the agent and the slave regarding authorization and its opposite: if the agent or slave did not know of the authorization or its revocation, and acted before news reached them, that ignorance is an excuse. In the first case (not knowing they were authorized) their actions are not binding on the principal/master; in the second case (not knowing they were revoked) their actions are binding.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Anwar enumerates various situations where ignorance (jahl) serves as a legal excuse ('udhr) in Hanafi fiqh. The author begins with the case of a father and his son's slave-girl: due to common practice, the father's access is presumed, so ignorance of prohibition excuses him from hadd. Then, the text introduces the third type of ignorance (after previous categories) — a Muslim living in dar al-harb who has not migrated. Because Islamic rulings are not well-known there, his failure to pray or fast is excused. In contrast, a dhimmi who converts in dar al-islam must make up missed acts because he could have learned. Similarly, the pre-emptor's ignorance of a sale does not excuse his silence; his right lapses. For a married slave-girl who is freed, ignorance of the fact or the option is an excuse because she is busy serving her master. For a virgin married by a guardian other than father/grandfather, ignorance of the marriage is an excuse, but ignorance of the option is not if she could have learned. Finally, agents and slaves who act without knowledge of their authorization or revocation are excused; the legal effects depend on which fact they were ignorant of.

Key Terms
جهل (jahl): Lack of knowledge of a fact or legal ruling that may serve as an excuse
عذر ('udhr): A legal excuse that exempts from liability or consequences
شفيع (shafi‘): Pre-emptor in property (shuf‘a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, is the ignorance of a Muslim who never migrated from dar al-harb regarding prayer and fasting an excuse?
A) Yes, because dar al-harb is not a place of Islamic knowledge.
B) No, because Islam obligates prayer and fasting everywhere.
C) Yes, but only if he was forced to stay.
D) No, because he could have asked Muslims there.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ignorance excuses only when obtaining knowledge is so difficult that the person cannot be blamed for not knowing.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
