Usul Rule: The Legal Capacity of an Intoxicated Person
Distinguishes intoxication types and their legal effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and prohibited intoxication in Hanafi usul, state the effect on legal capacity, and apply the exception for apostasy and hudud acknowledgments.

Core Idea
Prohibited intoxication does not excuse legal consequences; permitted intoxication suspends capacity like unconsciousness.

This passage from Ashraf ul-Anwar explains a critical usul rule about the mahkum alayh (legal subject). Intoxication is not a single category; its legal effect depends on its cause. We'll unpack the Hanafi position, the Quranic proof, and the important exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of intoxication
The passage distinguishes between intoxication from a permissible cause (e.g., medicine, being forced to drink, or drinking out of necessity) and from a prohibited cause (e.g., voluntarily drinking wine). Identify the specific examples given for each type.
Also note the difference between early and later scholars regarding hashish and opium.
2
Determine the effect on legal capacity
For permissible intoxication, the person is treated like someone unconscious: his legal acts (divorce, manumission, etc.) are suspended. For prohibited intoxication, he remains fully accountable; his statements are valid except for apostasy and acknowledgment of private hudud.
The passage explicitly states 'by consensus' that he is not excused from the address (khitab).
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
The proof cited is Quran 4:43 'Do not approach prayer while you are intoxicated'. The Hanafi interpretation is that this is a valid address to the drunk in his state of intoxication, implying he is still legally addressed. If it were conditional ('when drunk, do not pray'), it would be invalid because it attributes address to a contradictory state.
This reasoning rejects the analogy with a madman because drunkenness is self-inflicted.
4
Note the exceptions
Two exceptions are made for prohibited intoxication: (1) if he utters words of disbelief, he is not deemed an apostate because his belief hasn't changed; (2) if he confesses to a purely divine hadd (drinking wine, zina), the hadd is not inflicted because his confession is unreliable and intoxication suggests retraction.
These exceptions show that even for prohibited intoxication, full accountability is not absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالسَّكْرَ عَطْف عَلَى الْجَهْلِ وَهُوَ إن كَانَ مِنْ مَبَاحٍ أَي حَصَلَ مِنْ شَرْب شَتَّى مُبَاحٍ كَشَرْبِ الدَّوَاءِ وَالْمُسكِرِ مِثْلُ الْبَنْعِ وَالأَفْيُونِ عَلَى رَائى الْمُتَقَدِّمِيْنَ دَوْنَ الْمُتَاخَرِينَ وَشَرَبُ الْمُكْرَةِ وَالْمُضْطَرَ أَى شَرْبِ الْمُكْرَةِ بِالنَّقْلِ أَوْ يَقْطَعَ الْعَصْرِ الْخَمْرِ وَشَرْبِ الْمُصْطَرُ للعطش إيَّاهُ فَهُوَ كَالإِغْمَاءُ يَعْنِي يُجْعَلُ مَانعًا فَيَمْتَعُ صَحَةُ الطَّلَاقِ وَالْعِقَاقِ وسائر التصرُّفَاتِ كَالاِغْمَاءِ كَذَالِكَ وَإِنْ كَانَ مِنْ مَحْظُورًا أَنْ حَصَلَ مِنْ شرْب شَيْءٍ مُحَرَّمٍ كَالْحَمَرِ وَالسَّكْرِ وَنَحْوِهِ فَلا يَنَا فِي الْخِطَابِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ لَأَنْ قَوْلَهُ تَعَالَى لَاتَقْرَبُوا الصَّلوةَ وأَنْتُمْ سُكَارَىٰ إِنْ كَانَ خِطَابًا فِي حَالِ السَّكْرِ فهو المَطوب لأنَّه لايُنَافِى الْخِطَابَ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي حَالِ الصَّحْرِ فَهُوَنَاسِدٌ إِذْ يَصِيْرُ الْمَعْنَى إِذَا سَكَرْتُمْ فَلا تَقْرَبُوا الصَّلوةَ كَقَوْلِهِ لِلْعَاقِلِ إِذَا أَجَنَتَ فَلا تَفْعَلُ كَذَا وَهُوَ اِضافَةُ الخَطَابِ إِلى حَالٍ مُنَافٍ لَهُ فَلا يَجُوزُ وَتَلْزَمُهُ أَحْكَامُ الشَّرْعِ وتُصحُ عِبَارَتُهُ فِي الطِّلاقِ وَالْعِتَاقِ وَالْبَيْعِ وَالشَّرَاءِ وَالْأَقَارِيرِدُ جُرَّاً لَهُ عَنْ ارتكاب الْمِنْهى عَنْهُ وَتَنْبِيْها لَهُ عَلى أنْ مِثْلَ هذ السكر المحرم لا يَكُونُ عُذرا لَهُ فِي إِبْطَالٍ أَحكام الشرع إِلا لِرُدَّةَ وَالإِقْرَارَ بِالْحُدُودِ الْخَالِصةِ فَإِنَّهُ إِذَا ارْتَدْ السكْرَانُ وَتَكلم بكَلِمَةِ الْكُفْرِ لَا يُحْكَمُ بِكُفْرِهِ لأَنَّ الرِّدَةَ عِبَارَةٌ عَنْ تَبَدُّلِ الْأَعْتِقَادِ وَهُوَ غَيْرُ مُعْتَقِدٍ لَمَا يَقُولُهُ وَكَذَا إِذَا أَقَرْ بِالْحُدُودِ الْخَالِصَةِ اللهِ كَشْرُبِ الْخَمَرِ وَالزِّنَا لا يُحَدُّ لأَن الرُّجُوعَ عَنْهُ صَحِيح والسكَرُ دَلِيلُ الرُّجوع
And intoxication is appended to ignorance. If it results from permissible drinking, such as drinking medicine or an intoxicant like hashish and opium according to the early scholars (not the later), and drinking under compulsion or necessity—i.e., forced to drink or compelled to drink wine, or drinking it due to extreme thirst—then it is like unconsciousness, meaning it is treated as a preventive (mani‘), so it prevents the validity of divorce, manumission, and all other transactions like unconsciousness. And if it is from a prohibited source, i.e., resulting from drinking something forbidden, like wine and similar intoxicants, then he is not excused from address (khitab) by consensus, because the verse 'Do not approach prayer while you are intoxicated' (Quran 4:43): if it is an address while in intoxication, it is valid because it does not contradict the address; if it is an address while sober, it is invalid because it would mean 'when you become intoxicated, do not approach prayer', like telling a sane person 'when you go mad, do not do such-and-such', and that is attributing address to a state that contradicts it, which is impermissible. So the rulings of shari‘ah are binding on him, and his statements in divorce, manumission, sale, purchase, and acknowledgments are valid, as a deterrent from committing prohibited acts and to remind him that such prohibited intoxication is not an excuse for invalidating shari‘ah rulings, except for apostasy and acknowledgment of private hudud (prescribed punishments). For if an intoxicated person apostatizes and speaks words of disbelief, he is not judged to be a disbeliever because apostasy indicates a change of belief, and he does not believe what he says. Similarly, if he acknowledges private hudud like drinking wine or zina, he is not punished because retraction is valid, and intoxication indicates retraction.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of intoxication (sukr) as an excuse in Hanafi law. It distinguishes between intoxication from permissible causes (e.g., medicine, hashish/opium according to early scholars, or being forced/dying of thirst) and from prohibited causes (e.g., wine). For permissible intoxication, the legal capacity for acts like divorce and manumission is suspended, similar to unconsciousness. For prohibited intoxication, the drunkard is still held fully accountable for his actions, because the Quranic address to avoid prayer while drunk is a valid address in that state, not a conditional one. Thus, his divorces, manumissions, sales, and acknowledgments are effective. However, two exceptions are made: if he utters words of disbelief, he is not deemed an apostate because his belief has not changed; and if he confesses to a purely divine hadd (like drinking wine or zina), the hadd is not applied because his confession is not reliable, and intoxication suggests retraction.

Key Terms
السكر (al-sukr): Intoxication, whether from permissible or prohibited substances.
الإغما (al-ighma'): Unconsciousness, a state that prevents valid legal acts.
الحدود الخالصة (al-hudud al-khalisah): Purely divine prescribed punishments that have no personal right involved.
المكره (al-mukrah): A person under compulsion (ikrah).
المضطر (al-mudtarr): A person in dire necessity (darurah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a divorce pronounced by a person who voluntarily drank wine?
A) The divorce is invalid because he is not sane.
B) The divorce is valid as a deterrent and reminder.
C) The divorce is valid only if he remembers it later.
D) The divorce is suspended until he sobers up.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, intoxication from a prohibited source does not excuse legal consequences; only intoxication from a permissible source suspends capacity like unconsciousness, with narrow exceptions for apostasy and hudud confessions.

Intoxication and Legal Pronouncements
Ruling on validity of intoxicated person's talaq, i'taq, etc.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule regarding an intoxicated person's pronouncements and identify the exceptions for apostasy and acknowledgment of pure hudud.

Core Idea
Intoxication does not invalidate legal pronouncements except for apostasy and acknowledgment of pure hudud.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the validity of actions performed while intoxicated. While the general rule is that such actions are binding, there are key exceptions rooted in the nature of the act and the rights involved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Read the first part of the passage: it states that the intoxicated person's pronouncements in talaq, i'taq, sale, purchase, and acknowledgment are valid and binding.
The general rule emphasizes legal stability and deterrence from intoxication.
2
Note the exceptions
The passage mentions two exceptions: apostasy (ridda) and acknowledgment of pure hudud (ḥudūd khāliṣa).
Apostasy requires intentional change of belief, lacking in intoxication.
3
Distinguish pure vs non-pure hudud
For pure hudud (e.g., hadd for zina and drinking), retraction after acknowledgment is allowed. For impure hudud (e.g., qadhf, qisas), retraction is not accepted because a personal right is involved.
The passage illustrates this with examples: qadhf and qisas cannot be retracted.
4
Understand the rationale (talil)
The exception for pure hudud exists because intoxication suggests the acknowledgment may be unreliable, and the right is solely God's. For impure hudud, the victim's right prevents retraction.
This distinction shows how the Hanafi school balances divine and personal rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلزمه أحكام الشرع وتصح عبارته في الطلاق والعتاق والبيع والشراء والإقرار... سوء الردة والإقرار بالحدود الخالصة ... بأنه إذا أقر بالحدود غير الخالصة لله كالقذف أو القصاص فإنه لا يصح الرجوع إذ صاحب الحق يكذبه فيؤاخذ بالحدود والقصاص. وبخلاف ما إذا زنى في حال سكره وثبت من غير إقرار فيه فإنه يحد صاحبا.
The rulings of the Sharia are binding upon him and his expression is valid in divorce, manumission, sale, purchase, and acknowledgment... except apostasy and acknowledgment of pure hudud... if he acknowledges impure hudud like slander or retaliation, he cannot retract because the owner of the right belies him, so he is bound by the hudud and retaliation. And unlike if he committed adultery while intoxicated and it was established without his acknowledgment, then he is punished.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage states the general rule that an intoxicated person's legal pronouncements are valid and binding. The rationale is to deter from intoxication and to affirm that drunkenness does not nullify sharia rulings. Exceptions: apostasy (because it requires belief change) and acknowledgment of pure hudud (hadd punishments solely for God, like zina or drinking) where retraction is allowed because intoxication indicates possible retraction. For non-pure hudud (like qadhf or qisas), retraction is not accepted because the victim's right is involved and they deny the retraction. If zina occurs while intoxicated but is proven without confession, the hadd is applied after sobriety.

Key Terms
حُدُودٌ خَالِصَةٌ (ḥudūd khāliṣa): Penalties that are solely the right of God, such as hadd for zina and drinking.
رِدَّة (ridda): Apostasy from Islam.
حُدُود غَيْر خَالِصَة (ḥudūd ghayr khāliṣa): Penalties that involve a personal right, such as hadd for qadhf (slander) or qisas (retaliation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the acknowledgment was not made in front of a judge.

Key Takeaway
An intoxicated person's pronouncements are valid except for apostasy and acknowledgment of pure hudud, reflecting the Hanafi principle that intoxication does not negate legal capacity for most actions.

Definition and Conditions of Jest (Hazl) in Contracts
Defining hazl and its condition of explicit stipulation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of hazl (jest) in usul al-fiqh, differentiate it from seriousness (jidd) and from the option of condition (khiyar al-shart), and identify the condition that makes hazl effective.

Core Idea
Hazl is pure play: words without intent, invalidating the contract unless explicitly declared before the agreement.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, understanding the intention behind contractual words is essential. This passage defines hazl (jest) — a situation where parties speak without meaning what they say. It is the opposite of jidd (seriousness). We will parse the definition, compare it to a similar concept (khiyar al-shart), and learn the specific condition that distinguishes a void jest from a valid contract.

Guided Path
1
State the definition of hazl
Identify the key elements: the intended meaning is neither literal nor metaphorical; it is pure play (la'b mahd). The speaker does not intend the ruling nor is pleased with it.
Note the contrast with jidd: seriousness means intending the literal (haqiqi) or metaphorical (majazi) meaning.
2
Contrast hazl with jidd
Jidd is when the speaker intends the actual meaning of the words; hazl is the opposite. This is the core distinction in contractual intent.
3
Compare hazl with khiyar al-shart
In both, the person is not pleased with the ruling of the sale. However, hazl invalidates the sale outright, while khiyar al-shart does not. The similarity is in the lack of pleasure with the legal effect; the difference is in the effect on validity.
Khiyar al-shart is a valid option that suspends binding effect; hazl destroys the contract.
4
Identify the condition of hazl
Hazl must be explicitly stipulated by both parties before the contract (using their tongues). It cannot be inferred from circumstances (dalala al-hal). It does not need to be mentioned within the contract itself, unlike khiyar al-shart.
The condition is a preventive measure: without it, the contract is presumed serious.
5
Derive the ruling on hazl
Because the parties do not choose the ruling (hukm) of the contract, the contract is invalid (batil). The Hanafi school holds that hazl nullifies the sale, even though the utterance itself is based on choice and pleasure.
This ruling applies to all contracts, not just sales.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والهزل عطف على ما قبلة وهو أن يراد بالشيء ما لم يوضع له ولا ما صلح له اللفظ استعارة يعنى لا يكون اللفظ محمولا على معناه الحقيقي أو المجازي بل يكون لعبا محضا... وهو ضد الجد وهو أن يراد بالشيء ما وضع له أو ما يصلح له اللفظ استعارة وإنه ينافي اختيار الحكم والرضاء به ولا ينافي الرضاء بالمباشرة يعني أن الهازل لا يختار الحكم ولا يرضى به ولكنه يرضى بمباشرة السبب إذا التلفظ إنما هو عن رضاء واختيار صحيح لكنه غير قاصد ولا راض للحكم فصار الهزل بمعنى خيار الشرط أبدا في البيع لعدم الرضاء بحكم البيع ولا بعدم الرضاء بنفس البيع ولكن بينهما فرق من حيث أن الهزل يفسد البيع وخيار الشرط لا يفسده. وشرطه أن يكون صريحا مشروطا باللسان بأن يذكر العاقدان قبل العقد أنهما يهزلان في العقد ولا يثبت ذلك بدلالة الحال فقط إلا أنه لم يشترط ذكره في العقد بخلاف خيار الشرط لأن غرضهما من البيع مازلا أن يعتقد الناس ذلك بيعا وليس ببيع في الحقيقة وهذا لا يحصل بذكره في العقد.
And jest is coordinated with what preceded it: it is that the intended meaning of an expression is what it was not placed for and what the word is not suitable for even metaphorically, meaning the word is not carried on its literal or metaphorical meaning, but is pure play... It is the opposite of seriousness, which is that the intended meaning is what it was placed for or what the word is suitable for metaphorically. And it contradicts choosing the ruling and being pleased with it, but does not contradict being pleased with direct action. That is, the jesting person does not choose the ruling nor is pleased with it, but is pleased with performing the cause (uttering the words) because the utterance is based on pleasure and valid choice, but he does not intend nor is pleased with the ruling. So jest becomes like the option of condition permanently in sale, due to lack of pleasure with the ruling of sale, but not due to lack of pleasure with the sale itself. However, there is a difference: jest invalidates the sale, while the option of condition does not invalidate it. And its condition is that it must be explicitly stipulated by tongue, by the two contractors mentioning before the contract that they are jesting in the contract. It is not established by circumstantial evidence alone, except that it is not required to mention it in the contract itself, unlike the option of condition, because their purpose from the sale is to make people think it is a sale while it is not actually a sale, and this cannot be achieved by mentioning it in the contract.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage defines hazl (jest) as using words without intending either their literal or metaphorical meanings, but pure play. Its opposite is jidd (seriousness), where the speaker intends the actual meaning (literal or metaphorical). Hazl is similar to khiyar al-shart (option of condition) in that the person is not pleased with the legal effect, but differs in that hazl invalidates the contract entirely, while option of condition keeps it valid. The key condition for hazl is that the parties must explicitly declare before the contract that they are jesting; this cannot be inferred from circumstances. It does not need to be stated within the contract itself, unlike khiyar al-shart which must be stipulated within the contract to inform the public.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Using words without intending their real or metaphorical meaning, i.e., jest or play.
خيار الشرط (khiyār al-sharṭ): Option of condition: a stipulated period to confirm or cancel a sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Hazl must be stated in the contract, while khiyar al-shart can be stated before.
B) Hazl invalidates the sale, while khiyar al-shart does not invalidate it.
C) Hazl does not require explicit stipulation, while khiyar al-shart does.
D) Hazl is only about divorce while khiyar al-shart is about sales.

Key Takeaway
Hazl invalidates the contract because there is no genuine intent; it must be declared before the contract to be recognized.

Jest and Compulsion in Sale: Default Validity Principle
Explaining legal effect and conditions of jest and compulsion in sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a contract made in jest is invalid due to lack of real consent, and distinguish it from khiyar al-shart.

Core Idea
Jest in a contract voids it; only explicit verbal agreement can establish jest.

This passage from Ashrāf al-Anwār examines the critical distinction between jest (hazl) and the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart). While both involve an inner intent different from the outward expression, jest fundamentally lacks the real consent (rida) required for a valid contract. The text also presents a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two students regarding the effect of a prior agreement to jest when parties later disagree about their intent.

Guided Path
1
Define hazl and talji'ah
Understand that hazl (jest) is when a speaker intends a meaning not placed for the word nor suitable as metaphor, while talji'ah (compulsion) is when external pressure causes a person to act contrary to apparent meaning. Both negate real consent.
Distinguish from khiyar al-shart, which suspends but does not invalidate the contract.
2
Identify the condition for valid jest
Jest must be explicitly agreed upon orally before the contract; contextual clues are insufficient. This is because the purpose of jest is to mislead others, which requires explicit verbal agreement.
Contrast with khiyar al-shart, which is effective by stipulation in the contract itself.
3
Trace the legal effect of a jest sale
A jest sale is invalid (fasid) and does not transfer ownership, even if delivery occurs. Any subsequent actions by the buyer (e.g., freeing a slave) are ineffective because ownership never passed.
The text compares this to a sale with perpetual option, which also prevents ownership transfer despite being valid.
4
Analyze the four scenarios after a secret agreement to jest
The passage outlines four cases: (1) they proceed with the jest – invalid; (2) they abandon the jest and contract seriously – valid; (3) they had no specific intent – valid by default; (4) they differ on whether they built on the jest or abandoned it – Abu Hanifa rules valid, contrary to the Sahibayn.
Note that in cases 3 and 4, the principle of default validity (as-sihhah fi al-asl) applies.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa holds that when parties differ, the one claiming seriousness (abandonment of jest) is more entitled because validity is the original ruling in contracts. The Sahibayn apparently hold that the prior agreement casts doubt, making the contract invalid.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether the sale is valid or invalid in such a dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الانوار شرح اردو
نور الانوار جلد سوم
الْبَيْعَ مَازَلاً أَنْ يَعتَقَدَ النَّاسُ ذَالِكَ بَيْعًا وَلَيْسَ يَبِيعُ فِي الْحَقِيقَةِ وَهَذَا لايحصل بذِكْرِه فِى العَقْدِ وَأَمَّا خِيَارُ الشَّرَطِ فَالْفَرْضُ مِنْهُ إعْلَامُ النَّاسِ بِأَنْ الْبَيْعَ لَيْسَ بأتابلٌ [؟] مُعَلَّقًا بِالْخِيَارِ وَذَالِكَ إِنْمَا يَعْصِلُ بِذِكْرِهِ فِي عَيْنِ الْقَعْدِ ترجمه تشریح بخلافِ مَا لَوْ أَمر بِالْحُدُودِ الغَيْرِ الخالصة بخلاف ایسی حدود کے جو خالص اللہ کے حقوق نہیں ہیں جیسے نذف کسی پر تہمت لگانا یا قصاص تو اس اقرار سے رجوع صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ جس کا حق ہے وہ اس کی تکذیب کر دے گا لہذا اس پر حد اور قصاص دونوں جاری ہوں گے بخلاف اس کے کہ اس نے ارتکاب زنا بحالت نشہ کیا ہو اور زنا بغیر اس کے اقرار کے ثابت ہو ا ہو تو نشہ زائل ہونے کے بعد اس پر حد جاری کی جائے گی۔ وَالْبَزَلُ : ۔ (۳) اور ہنرل (مذاق) اس کا بھی ماقبل پر عطف ہے یعنی جہل پر وهو ان يراد بالشتی مالم يوضع له ولا ما لصلح له اللفظ استعارة : برل کہتے ہیں اپنے کلام سے ایسا مطلب مراد لینا جس کے لئے یہ کلام موضوع نہیں ہے اور نہ دو مطلب اس کے معنی مجازی ہونے کے قابل ہے یعنی اس کے الفاظ حقیقی معنی پر محمول نہیں ہو سکتے نہ معنی مجازی پر محمول ہو سکتے ہیں بلکہ محض مذاق پر محمول ہوں گے۔ مصنف کی یہ عبارت تکلف سے خالی نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان کا قول و لا ما صلح کہ میں اگر مالا صلح لہ کہنا زیادہ بہتر تھا تا کہ مالم يوضع له پر عطف ہو جاتا ہے یا پھر لفظ ہا کو حذف کر کے ولا صلح لہ کہتے تو بہتر تھا اسکا بھی مالم يوضع له پر عطف ہو جاتا۔
وَهُوَ ضد الجِدْ وَهُوَ أنْ يُرَادَ بِالشلي مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ أَوْ مَا يَصلَحُ لَهُ الخ:- یہ لفظ جد کی ضد ہے جد کہتے ہیں لفظ سے معنی موضوع لہ یا معنی مجازی مراد لینا اور یہ ہنرل کلام کے حکم کو قبول کرنے اور اس حکم پر راضی ہونے کے منافی ہے لیکن کلام کے استعمال پر راضی ہونے کے منافی نہیں یعنی مذاق کا کرنے والا کلام کے حکم کو اختیار نہیں کرتا نہ اس کے حکم سے راضی ہوتا ہے لیکن اس کی رضا الفاظ کے صرف استعمال میں ہوتی ہے اس وجہ سے کہ وہ راضی خوشی سے الفاظ بولتا ہے اگر چہ حکم کا ارادہ نہیں کرتا نہ اس کے حکم پر راضی ہوتا ہے فصار المزل بمعني خيار الشرط لبزانداق کا تصرف بیچ میں دیکر شریط کے مانند ہے جو خیار کو مرید ہو کیونکہ حکم بیچ سے وہ راضی نہیں ہوتا اور نہ نفس بیچ سے اس کی عدم رضاء ہوتی ہے البتہ ان دونوں کے مفہوم اور حکم میں فرق ہے کیونکہ مذاق بیچ کو فاسد کر دیتا ہے۔ اور خیار شرط فاسد نہیں کرتا۔ وشرطة :- اور اس کی شرط یعنی مذاق کو معتبر ہونے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ ان يكون صريحا مشروطا باللسان زبانی طور پر صراحہ باہم ملے شدہ ہو بائیں صورت دونوں عاقد ( بائع اور مشتری) بیچ کا معاملہ کرنے سے پہلے یہ ذکر لسانی کر دیں کہ دونوں بیچ کے معاملے میں مذاق کر رہے ہیں دلالت حال سے مذاق ثابت نہیں ہوتا ان لم يشترط في العقد بخلاف خيار الشرط البتہ عقد کے اندر اس کاذکر کرنا ضروری۔

ا شرف الانوار شرح اردو
نور الانوار جلد سوم
نہیں ہے بخلاف خیار شرط کے کیونکہ مذاقیہ عقد بیع کرنے والوں کا مقصد یہ ہوتا ہے کہ لوگ تو الفاظ کو دیکھ کر عقد بیچ ہی سمجھ جائیں حالانکہ حقیقت میں یہ بیچ نہیں ہے یہ مفہوم عقد میں ذکر کرنے سے حاصل نہیں ہوتا اور بہر حال خیار شرط تو اس سے مقصد لوگوں کو بتلانا ہوتا ہے کہ بیچ تام نہیں ہے بلکہ خیار پر معلق ہے اور یہ معنی خیار کے عقد بیع میں ذکر کرنے سے حاصل ہوں گے۔
وَالتَّلْجِيَّةُ كَالهَزْلِ فَلا يُنَافِى الأَهْلِيَةِ وَهِيَ فِي اللُّغَةِ مَاخُونَةٌ مِنَ الإِنْجَاءِ أَنْ الاِصْطَرَارُ فَحَاصِلُهَا أَنْ يَلْجِيءَ شَيْءٌ إِلى أَن يَأْتِي أَمْرًا بَاطِئًا بِخِلافِ ظَاهِره فَيَظْهَرُ يَحُضُورِ الْخَلْقِ أَنَّهُمَا يَعْتَقِدُ أَنِ الْبَيْعَ بَيْنَهُمَا لأَجَلِ مَصْلِحَةٍ دَعَتْ إِلَيْهِ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ فِي الْوَاقَعِ بَيْنَهُمَا بَيْعٌ وَالْمَوْلُ أَعَمُ مِنْهُمَا وَلَكِنَّ الْحُكْمَ فِيْهِمَا سِوَاءٌ فِي أَنَّهُ لَايُنَافِى الأَدْلِيَةِ ثُمَّ اِعْلَمْ أَنَّ مَبْنِى هَذَا الْهَزْلِ عَلَى أَنْ يَتَّفِقُ الْعَاقِدَ أَن فِي السر أن  ُتظهر العَقْدُ بحُضُورِ النَّاسِ وَلَا عَقْدَ بَيْنَهُمَا فِي الْوَاقِعِ فَعَقَدَا بُحُضُورِ النَّاسِ ثُم بَعْدَ تَفَرُّقِ النَّاسِ لاَيَعْلُوْا عَنْ أَرْبَعِ حالات بَيْنَهُمَا فِي كُلِّ عَقْدٍ وَقَدْ تنهُمَا المُصنّف بالتفصيل فَقَالَ فَاِنْ تَوَاضَعًا عَلى المزل باصل البيع أى الْبَيْعِ اِتِّفَقَا فِي السِّرِّ عَلَى أَنْ يَظْهَرَ البَيْعَ بِحُضُورِ النَّاسِ وَلَا يَكُونُ بَيْنَهُمَا أَصلُ الْبَيْعِ فَعَقَداً بِحُضُورِهِمْ وَتَفَرَّقَ الْمَجْلِسُ ثُمَّ جَاءَ أوإتفقا على البناء أى أنهما كانا بانينِ عَلَى تِلْكَ الْمُوَاضَعَةِ وَليَزكَ يُفْسِدُ البَيْعَ وَلا يُوجب الملك وَإنْ: اِتَّصَلَ بِهِ الْقَيْضُ لِعَدَمِ الرِّضَاءِ حَتَّى لَوْ كَانَ الْمَبِيْعُ عَبْدًا فَاعْتَقَةَ الْمُشْقِرِئُ بَعْدَ الْقَبَض لايَنْفُذُ كَالْبَيْع بشرطِ الْخِيَارِ اَبَدًا فَإِنَّهُ يَمْنَعُ ثُبُوت الْمِلْكِ مَعَ كَوْنِ البيع صَحِيْحًا فَفِي الْفَاسِدِ أَوْلى وَإِنِ اِتَّفَقَا عَلَى الأَعْرَاضٍ أَيْ عَلَى أَنَّهُمَا أَعْرَضَا عَنِ الْمُوَاضِعَةِ الْمُتَقَدِّمَةِ وَعَقْدَا البَيعَ عَلَى سَبِيْلِ الْجِدْ فَالْبَيْعُ صَحِيحُ وَالْمَزْلُ بَاطِلٌ وَإِنْ اِتَّفَقَا عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَحْضُرُهُمَا شَيءٌ عِنْدَ الْبَيْمِ مِنَ الْبِنَاءِ عَلي الْمَوَاضِعَةِ وَالأعْرَاضِ بَلْ كَانَا خَالِيَ الدُّهْنِ عَنْهُ أَوْ اخْتَلَفَا فِي الْبِنَاءِ الأَعْرَاضِ فَقَالَ أَحَدُهُمَا بَيْتُنَا الْعَقْدُ عَلى المَوَاضِةِ الْمُتَعَدَّمَةِ وَقَالَ الْآخَرُ عَقْدُنَا عَلَى سبيل الجد فَالْعَقْدُ صَحِيحٌ عِند أبي حنيفة خلاقًا لَهُمَا فَجَعَلَ أَبو حَنِيفَةً صحة الايجاب أولى لأن الصحة فِي الأَصْلُ فِى الْعُقُود فَيُحْمَلُ عَلَيْهَا مالم يُوجِدُ مُغيَرُ وَهُوَ فِيْمَا إِذَا اتَّفَقَا عَلَى أَنَّهُمَا كَانَا خَالِى الذَّهْنِ وَأَمَّا اذَا اخْتَلَفا فَمْدَعِي الإِعْرَاضِ مُتَمَسَك بالأصل فَهُوَ أَوْلى
The sale as jest: that people believe it is a sale while in reality it is not a sale, and this is not achieved by mentioning it in the contract. As for the option of stipulation, its purpose is to inform people that the sale is not complete but is contingent on the option, and that is achieved by mentioning it in the contract itself. Translation commentary: Contrary to the case where he orders non-exclusive punishments... And al-hazl: (3) And jest (mazaq) is also linked to what precedes it, i.e., ignorance, and it is that one intends by speech what it was not placed for, nor what the word is suitable for as a metaphor... And it is the opposite of seriousness, and it is that one intends by the word its literal or metaphorical meaning. And this jest is contrary to accepting the ruling of speech and being satisfied with it, but not contrary to being satisfied with the use of speech. So the jest becomes like khiyar al-shart... And its condition: that it be explicit and verbal, so that both parties mention verbally before the contract that they are jesting in the transaction; context does not prove jest if not stipulated in the contract, unlike khiyar al-shart where mentioning it in the contract is necessary. And al-talji'ah is like al-hazl: it does not affect legal capacity. In language it is derived from 'compulsion'. Its essence is that something compels a person to do a thing contrary to its apparent meaning, so it appears in the presence of people that they consider a sale between them for a benefit that led to it, while in reality there is no sale between them. The ruling on both is the same: they do not affect legal capacity. Then know that the basis of this jest is that the two contracting parties agree in secret to show the contract in the presence of people while there is no actual contract between them. Then they contract in the presence of people. Then after the people disperse, it does not go beyond four cases between them in every contract, and the author detailed them: If they agreed on jest from the beginning of the sale, i.e., they agreed in secret to show the sale in the presence of people and there is no basis of sale between them, then they contracted in their presence and the session ended, then the sale is invalid and does not cause ownership even if delivery is connected, due to lack of consent. So if the sold item was a slave and the buyer freed him after delivery, it is not effective, like a sale with perpetual option, which prevents ownership despite the sale being valid, so in a corrupt sale it is more so. And if they agreed on abandonment, i.e., they abandoned the prior agreement and contracted the sale seriously, the sale is valid and the jest is void. And if they agreed that nothing occurred at the time of sale regarding building on the agreement or abandonment, but they were free of it, or they differed regarding building and abandonment, one saying 'we built on the prior agreement' and the other saying 'we contracted seriously', then the contract is valid according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). He (Abu Hanifa) considered the validity of the offer more appropriate because validity is the original ruling in contracts, so it is applied as long as there is no changing factor. This is when they agree that they were free-minded. If they differ, the one claiming abandonment holds the original principle, so he is more entitled.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-based commentary comparing the effects of jest (hazl) and compulsion (talji'ah) in sale contracts with the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart). The author first distinguishes between them: in a jest sale, the parties intend only an outward appearance of a sale without real consent, so the contract is invalid (fasid) regardless of whether the jest is mentioned in the contract. In khiyar al-shart, the purpose is to inform others that the sale is contingent; this is achieved by stipulation. The condition for valid jest is that it must be explicitly agreed upon orally before the contract; contextual clues are insufficient. Then talji'ah is introduced as similar to jest in that it does not affect legal capacity and also results in an invalid sale. The passage then details four scenarios after a secret agreement to jest: (1) If they agreed on jest from the start and never revoked, the sale is invalid even if possession is taken; any act like freeing a slave by the buyer is ineffective because ownership did not transfer. (2) If they later abandon the jest and perform the sale seriously, it becomes valid. (3) If they had no specific intent or they differ (one claiming jest, the other seriousness), Abu Hanifa rules the contract valid because the default principle in contracts is validity. The one who claims seriousness (abandonment of jest) relies on this original principle, so his claim is stronger. This is a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), who apparently held a different view on this specific scenario. The passage concludes by affirming Abu Hanifa's position as the relied-upon one.

Key Terms
الْهَزْلُ (al-hazl): Jest: uttering the words of a contract without intending its legal effects, i.e., merely playing with words.
التَّلْجِيَّةُ (al-talji'ah): Compulsion: performing a contract outwardly while internally intending something else due to external pressure or fear.
خِيَارُ الشَّرْطِ (khiyar al-shart): Option of stipulation: the right to rescind a sale within a specified period, explicitly mentioned in the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if two parties secretly agree to a jest sale, then they contract in public, and later the buyer frees the slave he received?
A) The sale is valid and the freeing takes effect.
B) The sale is invalid and the freeing does not take effect.
C) The sale is valid but the freeing is only effective if the seller agrees.
D) The sale is suspended until the option period expires.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi default in contracts is validity (as-sihhah), and jest must be explicitly agreed to override it; otherwise, the contract stands.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
Rulings on Jest (Hazl) in Sale Contracts
Explaining the effect of prior jest agreement on sale validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principles of asl (default) and zahir (apparent) to determine the validity of a sale contract when prior jest (muwada'a) is alleged, and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A prior jest agreement invalidates a sale only if both parties actively intend it at the time; otherwise, default validity prevails.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar expands on the rulings of hazl (jest) in sale contracts. It presents four scenarios regarding the original sale when a prior secret agreement to jest exists. The commentary clarifies how Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Sahibayn) differ in applying the usul principles of default validity (asalat al-sihhah) versus the apparent nature of the prior agreement. Understanding this intra-madhhab dispute sharpens your ability to reason from usul to furu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling and its expansion
The base text (Nur al-Anwar) states a ruling on talji'ah and hazl. The commentary expands with four hypotheticals regarding the original sale (asl al-bay'). Identify these scenarios: (1) both agree to build upon jest, (2) both agree to turn away, (3) both have no recollection, (4) they differ.
The first two scenarios have consensus; the last two involve ikhtilaf.
2
Understand the Usul Principle invoked by Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa holds the sale valid in the last two scenarios. The principle: the default (asl) in contracts is validity and seriousness. Absence of evidence of jest means the contract is treated as valid.
This principle is: 'الأصل في العقود الصحة'.
3
Understand the Usul Principle invoked by the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn consider the prior agreement as the apparent (zahir) that governs. They give precedence to the prior agreement over the default, making the sale void unless both parties explicitly turn away.
They rely on: 'المواضعة المتقدمة هي الظاهر'.
4
Apply the same delineation to variations in amount and type
The commentary extends the four scenarios to cases where the jest concerns the price amount (qadr) or the type of currency (jins). Notice how the ruling changes with istihsan when the type differs.
For jins, the sale is valid in all scenarios by istihsan.

Source Text

اشرف الانوار شرح اردو نور الانوار جلد سوم
ترجمه و تشریح و التلجيَةُ كَالبَدْلِ فَلَا يُنَافِي الأَهْلَيَة : ۔ اور مجبوری (کی مصلحت کا معاملہ ) مذاق کے حکم ۔ میں ہے کہ یہ بھی اہمیت کے منافی نہیں ہے تلجیه لفظ الجاء سے ماخوذ ہے معنی اضطرار اور مجبوری کے ہیں حاصل یہ ہے کہ آدمی کسی مجبوری سے ایسا معاملہ کرنے پر مجبور ہو جائے، جس کا ظاہر اس کے باطن کے بر خلاف ہو یعنی کسی مصلحت کے پیش نظر (سابقہ پو شیدہ مقصد کے پیش نظر ) لوگوں کے سامنے یہ ظاہر کرے کہ یہ دونوں عقد بیچ کر رہے ہیں حالانکہ فی الواقع دونوں کے درمیان کوئی عقد بیچ نہ ہو۔ یہ مذاق کو تلجہ سے عام ہے کہ مجبوری اور غیر مجبوری دونوں میں اس کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے) مگر اہمیت کے منافی نہ ہونے میں دونوں برابر ہیں ۔
پھر جانو تم کہ مذاق کا معنی اس پر ہے کہ پہلے دونوں عاقدین تنہائی میں اس بات پر اتفاق کر لیں کہ لوگوں کے سامنے تو عقد بیع کا اظہار کریں گے حالانکہ واقع میں یہ معالمہ کی کا نہیں شمار ہو گا اس خفیہ منصوبہ کے تحت دونوں نے لوگوں کے سامنے عقد بیچ کر لیا پھر لوگوں کے منتشر ہو جانے کے بعد ان حال کا چار صورتوں سے خالی نہیں ہے جن کو مصنف نے یہ تفصیل بیان کیا ہے فرمایا: خان تواضعا على المزل بأصل البيع (۱) اگر دونوں عاقد اصل بیچ میں مذاق کرنا طے کر لیں یعنی تخفیہ طور پر دونوں شروع میں یہ طے کرلیں کہ لوگوں کے سامنے تو بیع کا اظہار کریں گے حالانکہ وہ عقد بیچ نہیں ہے لہذا ان لوگوں کے سامنے عقد بیع کیا ہو اور مجلس بدل گئی پھر دونوں واپس آئے۔ اتفاقا على النساء اور دونوں میں اتفاق ہو گیا اس پر بناء کرنے میں یعنی سابقہ ملے شدہ مذاق ہی پر دونوں نے عقد بیچ کر دیا يفسد البيع تو بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی اور ملک کو واجب نہ کرے گا اگرچہ عقد بیع کے ساتھ متصلا قبضہ ہی کیوں نہ کر لیا گیا ہو کیونکہ دونوں راضی نہ تھے حتی کہ اس بیچ نما مذاق میں اگر مشتری نے بیچ پر یعنی غلام پر قبضہ کر لیا اور اس کو قبضہ کے بعد آزاد کر دیا تو محق نافذ نہ ہوگا كالبيع بشرط الخيار ابداً جیسے غیر معینہ مدتک کی شرط کے ساتھ بیچ کرنا شرط موبد ثبوت ملک کو روک دیتی ہے باوجود یکہ نفس پیچ در سیست ہے تو بیع فاسد میں بدرجہ اولی یہ خیار باقی رہے گاوان اتفقا علی الاعراض اور اگر دونوں اعراض پر تو ہو جائیں یعنی دونوں اس بات پر متفق ہو جائیں کہ ہم دونوں نے سابقہ مفارق والی بات سے اعراض کر لیا اور صحیح طور پر عقد بیع کو انجام دیا ہے۔ فالبيع صحيح والهزل باطل وانما اتفقا على أنه يحضرهما :- تو بیچ درست ہے اور مذاق باطل ہے اور اگر دونوں کا اس میں اتفاق ہو کہ کچھ بھی متحضر نہیں تھا عقد بیچ کرنے کے وقت نہ مذاق پر بناء کرنے کا خیال آیا اور نہ اسکو نظر انداز کرنے کا خیال آیا بلکہ دونوں اس مذاق سے خالی ذہن رہے او اختلفا في البناء والاعراض یا نفاق پر بناء کرنے اور اس سے اعراض کرنے میں باہم اختلاف ہو ایک تو ان دونوں میں سے یہ کہے کہ یہ عقدہم دونوں کے درمیان سابقہ ملے شدہ مذاق پر ہوتی ہے اور دوسرا کہے کہ ہم نے صحیح طور پر بیچ کیا ہے فالعقد صحيح عند ابي حنيفة خلافا لهما تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک بھی درست ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک صحیح نہیں ہے سو امام ابو حنیفہ نے جانب بیچ کو قابل ترجیح قرار دیا ہے کیونکہ عقد کے اندر اصل صحبت ہے لہذا اس معاملہ کو صحیح عقد پر ہی محمول کیا جائے گا جب تک اس سے بتبدیلی کرنے والی چیز نہ موجود ہو اور یہ اس صورت میں ہے کہ دونوں خالی ذہن ہوں اور اگر دونوں میں اختلاف ہو بیع سے اعراض کرنے والا حقیقت اصل سے استدلال کر رہا ہے پس وہی بہتر اولی ہے۔ وَهُمَا اعْتَبَرَ الْمُوَاضِعَةَ الْمُتَقَدِّمَة لأنَّ الْبِنَاءَ عَلَيْهَا هُوَ الظَّاهِرُ فَفِي صَوْرِةِ عَدَم حضورِ شَيْءٍ تَكُونُ الْمَوَاضِعَةُ هُوَ الأَصْلُ وَفِي صُوَرَةِ الاِخْتِلَافِ يُرَجُحُ قَوْلَ مَنْ بَنَى عَلَى الْمَوَاضِعَةِ فَهْذِهِ أَرْبَعَةُ أَقْسَمَام لَلْمَوَاضِعَةِ باصلِ الْبَيْعِ وَإِنْ كَانَ ذَالِكَ الْقَدْرِ بِأَنْ يَقُوْلاً إِنَّ البَيْعَ بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَكَ تَامٌ وَلكِنْ تَوَاضِيعُ فِي الْقَدْرِ وَنَظْهِرُ بِحُضُورِ الْخَلقِ أَن الثَّمَنَ أَلْفَانِ وَفِي الْوَاقَع يَكُونُ الثَّمَنَ الْقَا فَدِهِ أَيْضًا أَرْبَعَةُ أَقْسامٍ فَإِنْ اِثْفَقَا عَلى الأَرْضِ كَانَ الثَّمَنُ الْفَيْنِ لَأَنْهُمَا لَمَّا أَعْرَضَا عَنِ المَوَاضِعَةِ وَالْهَزْلِ يَكُونُ الاِعْتِبَارُ بِالتُسْمِيَةِ وَهَذَا القِسْمُ لِظُهُورِهِ لَمْ يَذْكُرُهُ فِي بَعْض النسخ وَإِنْ اِثْفَقَا عَلى أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَحْضُرُهُمَا شَيْءٌ أَوْ إِخْتَلَفَا فَالْهَرْلُ بِاطِلُ والتسمية صَحِيحَةٌ عِنْدَهُ وَعِنْدَهُمَا الْعَمَلُ بالمَوَاضِعَة وَاجَبْ وَالألْفِ الَّذِي هُوَ لابه بَاطِل فَيَكُونُ الثَّمَن عِنْدَهُ الْفَيْنِ وَعِنْدَهُمَا أَلف بِنَاءً عَلَى مَا تَقَدَمُ مِنْ أَصْلِهِ وَأَصْلِهمَا وَإِنْ اتفقا عَلَى الْبِنَاءِ عَلَى الْمَوَاضِعَةِ فَالثَّمَنُ الْفَانِ عِنْدَهُ لأنه أوجعل الثَّمَنَ الْفَايَكُونُ قَبُوْلُ الأَلْفِ الَّذِي هُوَ غَيْرُ دَاخِل فِي الْبَيْعِ شَرْطًا لِقُبُولِ الْآخَرِ فيُفْسيدُ الْبَيْعَ بمَنْزِلَةِ مَالَوْ جَمَعَ بَيْنَ جُرٌ وَعَبْدٍ فَلا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ الثَّمَنُ الْفَيْنِ ليصحَ الْعَقْدُ وَعِنْدَهُمَا الثَّمَنُ اَلْ لأَنَّ غَرَضَهُ مِنْ ذِكْر الألف هؤلاً هُوَ الْمُقَابَلَةُ بالمبيع فَكَانَ ذِكْرُهُ وَالسُّكُوتُ عَنْهُ سَوَاءٌ كَمَا فِي النِّكَاحِ وَهُوَ رِوَايَةٌ عَنْ أَبِي حنيفة ايضا وان كان ذالك فِى الجنس بأن يُوَاضعًا عَلَى أَنْ تَعْقِدَ بِحُضَيْرٍ الخلق على مائة دينار وَالْعَقْدُ بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَكُمْ عَلى مِائَةٍ دَرَهِمَ فَالْبَيْعَ جَائِرٌ عَلَى مثل حال من الاحوال الأرْبَعَةِ سَوَاءٌ إِتَّفقا على الأغراض أوْ عَلَى الْبِنَاءِ أَوْ عَلَى أَنَّهُ لم يحضرهما شيءٌ اوْ اخْتَلَفًا في البناء أو الأَعْرَاضِ اسْتِحْسَانًا وَذَالِكَ لأَنَّ البيع لا يصح بلا تسلمية البدلِ وَهُمَا جَدًا في أَصْلِي الْعَقْدِ فَلا بُدْ مِنَ اللَّـ وذالك بالانقاد مما سيما وهذا ذا بالاتفاق بَيْنِ أَبِي غَةِ وَصَاحِبَ
(Urdu commentary on Nur al-Anwar Volume 3) Translation and explanation: And al-talji'ah is like al-badl, so it does not contradict capability. The matter of compulsion (maslahah) is in the ruling of jest (mazaq). This too is not contrary to importance. Talji'ah is derived from ilja' meaning compulsion and necessity. The summary is that a person is compelled by necessity to do an act whose outward appearance is contrary to his inner state, i.e., due to some maslahah (hidden purpose) he shows people that both are concluding a sale contract while in reality there is no sale contract. This jest is more general than talji'ah because it applies both in compulsion and non-compulsion, but they are equal in not opposing importance. Then know that the meaning of jest is that the two contracting parties first agree privately that they will outwardly declare a sale contract while in reality it will not be considered a transaction. Under this secret plan, both perform the sale contract in front of people. Then after people disperse, the state is not free from four situations which the author has detailed. He said: If both agree to jest in the original sale, i.e., secretly both initially agree that they will declare a sale in front of people while it is not a sale contract. So they perform the sale contract in front of people and the gathering changes. Then both return. They agree on building upon (al-nisa'), i.e., both agree to conclude the sale upon the previous jest. The sale is fasid (void), and it will not effect ownership even if possession is taken immediately with the contract, because both were not satisfied. So if the buyer takes possession of the slave and frees him after possession, the emancipation is not effective, like a sale with a perpetual option (bishart al-khiyar abadan). Just as a condition of perpetual option prevents the establishment of ownership, though the contract itself is valid, so in a fasid sale this option remains a fortiori. If both agree on turning away (al-i'rad), i.e., both agree that they have turned away from the previous matter and properly performed the sale, then the sale is sahih (valid) and the jest is batil (void). If both agree that nothing occurred to them at the time of the contract, neither the thought of building upon jest nor the thought of disregarding it, but both were free from jest, and they differ over building upon or turning away, one saying the contract was upon the previous jest and the other saying they performed a valid sale. In both these situations, according to Imam Abu Hanifah it is valid, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Imam Abu Hanifah considered the side of sale as preferable because the default in contracts is validity; hence this transaction will be regarded as a valid contract unless something appears to change it. And this is when both are free in mind. But if they differ, the one claiming turning away is relying on the default, so that is better. The two (Sahibayn) considered the prior agreement because building upon it is the apparent (zahir). In the case of nothing occurring, the prior agreement is the default. In the case of dispute, the statement of the one who built upon the agreement is preferred. So these are four divisions for the prior agreement regarding the original sale. And if it is concerning the amount, such that they say, 'The sale between us is complete, but we have agreed on the amount and we will show in front of people that the price is two thousand, while in reality the price is [one] thousand' — this also has four divisions. If they agree on turning away (i'rad), the price is two thousand because when they turn away from the prior agreement and jest, consideration is given to the named amount. This division, due to its obviousness, he did not mention in some copies. If they agree that nothing occurred to them, or they differ, then according to him (Abu Hanifah) the jest is void and the named amount is valid, while according to them (Sahibayn) acting upon the prior agreement is wajib and the thousand which is [the real price?] is void. So according to him the price is two thousand, and according to them one thousand, based on their respective principles mentioned earlier. If they agree on building upon the prior agreement, then the price is [only?] two thousand? Actually text says: 'the price is [??] according to him' — OCR unclear. He said: the price is two thousand? Actually the text says: 'فَالثلاثَنُ الْفَانِ عِنْدَهُ' — 'the price is two thousand according to him'. Because he made the price two thousand? Actually it says: 'لأنه أوجعل الثَّمَنَ الْفَايَكُونُ' unclear. The gist: according to him, the price must be two thousand for the contract to be valid; according to them, the price is [one?] thousand because the mention of the extra is like silence, as in marriage. This is also a narration from Abu Hanifah. And if it is concerning the type (jins), such as they agree to contract in front of people for one hundred dinars while the contract between them is for one hundred dirhams, then the sale is ja'iz (permissible) in any of the four states — whether they agree on turning away, building upon, nothing occurring, or differ — by istihsan. Because a sale is not valid without a known substitute (badal), and they were serious (jadd) in the original contract, so there must be specification, which is achieved by acceptance, especially since this is by agreement between Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is an Urdu commentary from 'Ashraf al-Anwar' explaining a section of 'Nur al-Anwar' on the rulings of hazl (jest) and muwada'a (mutual agreement) in sale contracts. The commentator first distinguishes talji'ah (compulsion) from hazl, noting both do not contradict legal capacity. The main issue: when two parties secretly agree to make a pretended sale (hazl) before witnesses, but later their actual intentions differ. There are four scenarios regarding the original sale (asl al-bay'): (1) both agree to build upon (bina') the jest — the sale is fasid (void) by consensus, as they did not genuinely consent; (2) both agree to disregard (i'rad) the jest — the sale is sahih (valid); (3) both state they had no prior agreement in mind — Abu Hanifa rules the sale valid because the default in contracts is validity and there is no evidence of jest, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider the prior agreement as the default, so the sale is fasid; (4) they differ (one claims jest, the other denies) — Abu Hanifa says the sale is valid, giving weight to the party claiming seriousness because the default is validity, and the one claiming i'rad is relying on the original principle (asl). The Sahibayn say the prior agreement is apparent (zahir), so the claim of building upon it is preferred. The passage then discusses analogous four divisions when the jest concerns the amount (qadr) — e.g., they agree to say the price is 2000 but really it is 1000. Again, if they agree on i'rad, the named price (2000) is effective; if they agree on bina', the sale is fasid according to Abu Hanifa because the extra 1000 is a condition that invalidates, but according to Sahibayn it is valid because the extra mention is like silence, similar to marriage. When the jest is about the type (jins) — e.g., they declare dinars but intend dirhams — the sale is valid in all four scenarios by istihsan, because the substitute (badal) is specified by the actual intent (jadd) and the declaration is a mere formality. This is agreed upon by all. The key usul principle: the default in contracts is validity (as-sihhah), and intent (niyyah) can override external form when known. The lesson demonstrates how Hanafi usul applies to a practical fiqh issue, highlighting the difference between Abu Hanifa's reliance on the default (asl) and the Sahibayn's reliance on the apparent (zahir).

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest; an act or utterance not meant seriously, especially in contracts.
المواضعة (al-muwada'a): Mutual prior agreement to pretend a sale while intending otherwise.
البناء (al-bina'): Building upon the prior jest; i.e., both parties intend to execute the jest at the time of contract.
الإعراض (al-i'rad): Turning away from the prior jest; i.e., both parties now intend a serious contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where prior jest (muwada'a) concerns the amount (e.g., they agree to say the price is $2000 but actually $1000), and both parties agree to build upon (bina') the jest at the time of contract, what is the ruling according to Abu Hanifa?
A) The sale is valid and the price is $1000.
B) The sale is fasid because the extra $1000 is a condition that invalidates.
C) The sale is valid and the price is $2000.
D) The sale is makruh.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the default in contracts is validity; a prior jest agreement only invalidates if both parties actively intend it at the time of contract.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Effect of Jest (Hazl) on Marriage Dower: Istihsan vs. Qiyas
Explains rulings on jest in contracts, especially marriage and divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of istihsan to distinguish the ruling on jest in marriage dower from jest in sale price, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Jest in marriage dower is ignored; the contract stands with the true amount because dower is subsidiary.

The effect of jest (hazl) on contracts is a key usul topic that demonstrates the interaction between textual evidence (hadith) and juristic reasoning (istihsan). In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on marriage contracts where the dower amount is stated jokingly. The hadith establishes that jest in marriage, divorce, and oaths is treated as serious, but the school uses istihsan to differentiate between marriage and sale due to the subsidiary nature of dower. This leads to an important intra-Hanafi difference between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its legal implication
Locate the hadith 'ثلاث جدهن جد وهزلهن جد: النكاح والطلاق واليمين'. Explain that it proves these contracts are valid even if uttered in jest (hazl is not considered). This is an 'amm (general) text that applies to all three matters.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is qati (definitive) for the obligation of treating these as serious.
2
Classify the types of contracts
The author distinguishes three categories: (1) contracts without money (divorce, manumission, oath), (2) contracts with money as subsidiary (marriage), and (3) contracts with money as primary (sale). For each, jest has different effects.
Focus on marriage where dower (mahr) is subsidiary to the main purpose (istimta').
3
Apply istihsan to marriage dower
According to Abu Hanifa (via Muhammad), if the parties jest in the amount of dower (e.g., state 2000 but intend 1000), the contract is valid with the true amount (1000) because the jested amount is void. This is based on istihsan: since dower is subsidiary, preferring the named amount (the jested one) would make dower primary, which contradicts its original nature.
Contrast with sale: if the price is jested, the contract becomes fasid (voidable) because the jested amount is a corrupt condition, and price is primary.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one via Muhammad (istihsan) and one via Abu Yusuf (qiyas on sale). Abu Yusuf analogizes marriage to sale, requiring the jested amount to be paid to preserve the contract. The author (Ashraf al-Anwar) favors the first narration.
Thamarah al-khilaf: in case of disagreement, one narration gives 1000 (true), the other 2000 (jest).
5
Synthesize the usul principle
The ruling demonstrates that istihsan can override qiyas when the 'illa (effective cause) differs. In marriage, the subsidiary nature of dower allows ignoring the jest, whereas in sale the primary nature of price requires upholding the named amount.
This is a key example of Hanafi usul where maslahah and custom (as part of istihsan) modify strict analogy.

نور الانوار جلد سوم
اِبْتِغَاءُ البُضْعِ فَإِنْ مَوْلاً بِاصْلِهِ بِأَنْ يَقُولَ لَهَا إِنَّى أَنْكَحْكِ بِحُضُورِ الْخَلْقِ وَلَيْسَ بَيْنَنَا نِكَاحَ فَالْعَقْدُ لازم والمَالُ بِاطِل سَوَاءٌ إِثْفَقَا عَلَى الْبِنَاءِ أَوِ الأَعْرَاضَ أو عَدَم حُضُورِ شَيْءٍ مِنْهُمَا أَوْ اكْتَلَنَا فِيهِ وَإِنْ هَزَلَا فِي القَدْرِ بِأَنْ يُزَوجَهَا عَلَا نِيَةٌ بِالْيَقِيْنِ وَيَكُونُ الْعَبْرُ فِى الْوَاقِع ألفًا فَإِنْ اِثْفَقَا عَلَى الْإِعْرَاضِ فَالْمَهْرُ أَلْفَانِ بالاتفاق لأن لَهَا وِلايَةُ الأَعْرَاضِ عَنِ المَزْل.
اوجهُ الفَرْقِ لَهُمَا الح: باقی صاحبین نے مذاق في القدر ( مقدار ممن) والی صورت میں ترجمه و تشریح و ہزار پر کیچ کو منعقد بابا ہے اور مذافی فی الجنس ( سو دینار اصل قیمت اور سو درہم مذاق دالی صورت میں انعقاد اول پر تسلیم فرمایا ہے اس فرق کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اول صورت میں اصل پیچ کو قطعی قرار دے کر مذاق جو کہ طے شدہ تھا کا اعتبار مکن قرار دیا ہے اس لئے کہ مذاقی والے ہزار کو باطل کر کے بھی اصل مقدار مسمی ہزار باقی رہ جاتی ہے جو میچ کا بدل بن سکتی ہے اور رہی یہ بات کہ دوسرے ہزار کو قبول کرنا شرط ہونا لازم آتا ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ دیتے ہیں کہ چونکہ اس شرط کا کوئی مطالبہ کرنے والا نہیں ہے لہذا یہ پیچ کو فاسد نہ کرے گا۔ اس کو پر خلاف صورت و ثانیہ میں اگر طے شدہ نداق کو معتبر مان لیا جائے تو مسمی ہی باطل ہو جاتا ہے اور بیچ کے عقد کا خالی حسن البدل ہونا لازم آتا ہے جو کہ مفسد کی ہے اس عقد کو صحیح کرنے کے لئے تسمیہ لازم اور مذاق کو باطل کر دیا گیا ہے۔
اب مصنف ما لا يحتمل النقض کی قسمیں بیان کر رہے ہیں وان كان في الذي لا مال فيه كالطلاق والعتاق واليمين الخ (۱) اگر ایسے تصرف میں مذاق پایا جائے جس میں مال کا لین دین نہیں ہے مثلا طلاق ، حتاق، تعلیق بالشرط میں تو یہ نص حدیث تصرف صحیح اور مذاق باطل ہے حدیث سے آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا یہ ارشاد مراد ہے ثلث جد من جد وهزلهن جد النكاح والطلاق واليمين ( تمن معالى ایسے ہیں کہ ان کو بیچ بیچ انجام دیتا تو بیچ بیچ ہے ہی مذاق بھی بیچ بچی پر محمول ہے نکاح ، طلاق، یمین ) اور دوسری روایت میں نکاح، مشتاق اور یمین ہے مواضعہ (نداق کے انداز میں گفتگو کرنا) کی صورت یہ ہے کہ دو مرد عورت آپس میں طے کر لیں کہ لوگوں کے سامنے نکاح کرے گا اور اس کو طلاق دیگا یا غلام کو آزاد کرے گا۔ حالانکہ واقع میں ایسا نہیں ہے صرف مذاق میں ایسا کرتا ہے اور یمین سے مراد تعلیق ہے صورت اس کی یہ ہے ایک شخص اپنی بیوی یا اپنے غلام سے کہے میں طلاق اور عناق کو لوگوں سے سامنے معلق کروں گا مگر واقع میں یہ ایسا نہیں ہے یمین سے یمین باللہ مراد نہیں ہے کیونکہ یمین باللہ میں مواضعہ کی صورت نہیں پائی جاتی لہذا ان تینوں صورتوں میں ہر حال میں (خواہ مذاق یا سچ مچ ) نکاح یا طلاق وغیرہ زبان سے کہے گا تو واقع ہو جائیں گے ۔ اور مذاق باطل ہو گل ان تینوں صورتوں کے ساتھ قصاص کی معافی کا مسئلہ نذر ماننے کا مسئلہ یا اس

طرح کے دوسرے مسائل بھی ملحق کئے گئے ہیں۔

نور الانوار جلد سوم
وَإِنْ كَانَ الْمَالُ فِيهِ تَبْعًا كَالنِّكَاحِ (۲) اور اگر اس عقد میں مال بھی ہو ( اگر اصالنا نہیں) جتا ہو جیسے نکاح کیونکہ نکاح میں اصل مقصود مبر نہیں ہوتا نکاح کا اصلی مقصد ابتغاء البضع ملك بضع كا حاصل کرنا ہوتا ہے فان هزلاً بنفسہ تو اگر اصل عقد میں مذاق ہو مثلاً مرد عورت سے کہے کہ میں لوگوں کے سامنے مجھ سے نکاح کروں گا مگر اصل میں وہ مذاق ہو گا نکاح نہ ہو گا فالعقد لازم والمزل بأطل - تو عقد لازم اور ہنرل باطل ہے اسکا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہوگا برابر ہے کہ دونوں نے مذاق پر بتاؤ کر کے عقد کیا ہو یا پھر مذاق کو نظر انداز کر کے ایسا کیا ہو یا دونوں بوقت نکاح بالکل خالی الذہ ہن تھے یا مذاق پر نکاح کی بناء ہونے نہ ہونے کا بعد میں اختلاف پیدا ہو جائے بہر صورت نکاح درست ہے اور منرل باطل ہے۔ وَإِن هَزَلَاً فِي الْقَدْرِ: اور اگر مقدار مہر میں فراق ہو مثلاً مرد نے علانیہ طور پر دو ہزار میں نکاح کیا ہے مگر اصل میں نکاح کا مہر صرف ایک ہزار ہو فان اتفقا على الاعراض فالمہر الفان اس صورت میں اگر مذاق کو نظر انداز کرنے پر دونوں کا اتفاق ہو تو مہر دو ہزار ثابت ہو گا اس وجہ سے کہ دونوں کو مذاق سے اعراض کر لینے کا حق حاصل ہے۔
وإِنْ اِثْفَقَا عَلَى الْبِنَاءِ فَالْمَهْرُ أَلف بِالإنْفَاقِ لانْ ذِكْرَ أَحَدٍ الْأَلْفَيْنِ كَانَ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الْهَزْلِ وَالْمَالَ لا يَثْبُتُ مَعَ الْهَزْلِ وَالْفَرْق لأبِي حَنِيْقَةِ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الْبَيْمِ حَيْثُ أَوْجَبَ الأَلْقَيْنِ فِي الْبَيْعِ وَالألْتُ فِي النِّكَاحِ أَنَّهُ لَوْ لَمْ يَجْعَلِ الثَّمَنَ الْفَيْنِ لَكَانَ شَرْطًا فَاسِدًا وَهُوَ يُؤْثِّرُ فِي فَسَادِ الْبَيْعِ وَلَا يُؤثْرُ فِي فَساديِ النُكَاحِ لَا فِي أصلِ الْعَقْدِ وَلا فِي الصَّدَاقِ وَإِنْ اِثْفَقَا عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَحْضُرُهُمَا شَلَّى أَوْ اخْتَلَفَا فَالنّكَاحُ جَائِرٌ بِأَلْفِ فِي رِوَايَةٍ مُحَمَّدٍ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقِيْلَ بِالْقَيْنِ فِي رِوَايَةِ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ عَنْهُ وَجْهُ الرِّوَايَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ هُوَ القَيَاسُ عَلَى البَيْعِ وَوَجْهُ الرِّوَايَةِ الأَوْلَى وَهُوَ الاسْتِحْسَانُ أنْ العَهْرَ فِى النِّكَاحِ تَابِعٌ فَلا يَجُوزُ تَرْجِيْحُ جَانِبِ التُسْمِيَةِ عَلَى الم لأنْ يَكُونَ المَبْرُ حِينَئِذٍ مَقْصُورًا بِالذَّاتِ وَهُوَ خِلافُ الأَصلِ بِخِلافِ البيع لأن الثَّمَنَ مَقْصُودٌ فِيهِ فَيَكُونَ تَصَحِيحَة أَيْضًا مَقْصَوْدًا فَيُرَجُحُ جَانِبُ السنمِيَةِ عَلى الهَدْلِ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي الْجِنْسِ بِأَنْ تَوَاضَمَا عَلَى الدُّنَانِهْرِ وَالْعَهْرُ فِي الْحَقِيقَةِ دَرَاهِمُ فَإِنْ اتَّفَقَا عَلى الإِعْرَاضِ فَالْعَهْرُ مَا سَمْيَا وَإِنْ إِثْفَقَا عَلَى الْبِنَاءِ وَاتَّفَقَا عَلى أَنه لَمْ يَحْضُرُ هُمَا شئلى أوْ اخْتَلَفَا يَجِبُ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ فِى الصور الثلث أما في الأولى فَبِالإجْمَاعِ لأَنَّهُمَا قَصَدًا الْمَوْلُ بِالْمُسَمَّى وَالْمَالَ
Seeking intercourse; if the master [intends] the original [woman] by saying to her: 'I marry you in front of people while there is no marriage between us,' then the contract is binding and the money is void, whether they agree on the building or disregarding or absence of any of them or they differ in it. And if they jest in the amount, such as he marries her publicly [stating] one thousand while the actual amount is one thousand, then if they agree on disregarding, the dower is two thousand by agreement because she has the authority to disregard the jest. The aspect of distinction for them: ... [Urdu commentary]. Now the author is explaining the types of things that do not bear abrogation: 'And if it is in that which has no money like divorce, manumission, and oath' (1) If jest occurs in a transaction that does not involve money, such as divorce, manumission, conditional suspension, then by the text of hadith the transaction is valid and the jest is void. The hadith is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Three things whose seriousness is serious and whose jest is serious: marriage, divorce, and oath.' ... And if money is subsidiary in it, like marriage (2) ... 'fa in hazala binafsihi' then if jest is in itself, the contract is binding and the dower is void. 'Wa in hazala fi al-qadri' and if they jest in the amount, then if they agree on disregarding, the dower is two thousand. If they agree on building [upon the jest], the dower is one thousand by agreement because the mention of one of the two thousand was in jest, and money is not established with jest. The distinction for Abu Hanifa between this and sale, where he required two thousand in sale and one thousand in marriage, is that if he did not make the price two thousand, it would be a corrupt condition, and it affects the invalidity of the sale but does not affect the invalidity of marriage, neither in the essence of the contract nor in the dower. And if they agree that nothing was present to them or they differ, then the marriage is permissible with one thousand in a narration from Muhammad from Abu Hanifa, and it is said with two thousand in a narration of Abu Yusuf from him. The face of the second narration is analogy to sale, and the face of the first narration is istihsan: that the dower in marriage is subsidiary, so it is not permissible to prefer the side of naming over jest so that the dower would then be intended in itself, which is contrary to the original, unlike sale because the price is intended in it, so its correction is also intended, so the side of naming is preferred over jest. And if it is in the genus, such as they agree on dinars while the dower is actually dirhams, then if they agree on disregarding, the dower is what they named; if they agree on building and they agree that nothing was present to them or they differ, then the fair dower is obligatory in the three images. As for the first, by consensus because they intended jest with the named and the money...
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar, a commentary (sharh) on Nur al-Anwar, discusses the effect of jest (hazl) in various contracts. The author first distinguishes contracts without monetary consideration (like divorce, manumission, and oaths) where, based on a hadith, jest does not affect the validity—the contract is upheld and the jest is void. Then it addresses contracts with subsidiary monetary consideration, like marriage, where the primary aim is not money but the right to marital relations. In marriage, if jest is in the essence (i.e., pretending to marry while not intending), the contract is nonetheless binding, and any specified dower (mahr) is also valid because the jest does not affect the substance. However, if the jest is in the amount of dower (e.g., stating a higher amount jokingly while intending a lower one), the default ruling according to Abu Hanifa is that the contract is valid with the true intended amount, not the jested one. The passage details scenarios where the parties agree to overlook the jest (then the stated amount is due) or rely on it (then the true amount is due). A key point is the distinction between marriage and sale: in sale, if the price is jested, the condition affects the validity because price is a primary object; in marriage, the dower is subsidiary, so the contract remains valid. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas (analogy). The passage also reports a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the ruling when there is uncertainty about the jest, with Muhammad preferring istihsan (one thousand) and Abu Yusuf preferring qiyas on sale (two thousand). Finally, it discusses jest in the genus (type) of dower, where the named type is different from the actual. If they agree to disregard the jest, the named type is due; otherwise, the fair dower (mahr al-mithl) is due by consensus.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest or joking in the utterance of a contract, without serious intention.
المهر (al-mahr): The dower or bride-gift given by the husband to the wife as part of the marriage contract.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that allows departing from a strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling based on a stronger evidence or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a marriage contract where the husband jokingly names a dower of 2000 dirhams but actually intends 1000, and both parties later agree to disregard the jest, what is the dower according to Abu Hanifa?
A) 2000 dirhams
B) 1000 dirhams
C) The contract is invalid
D) Mahr al-mithl (fair dower)

Key Takeaway
Jest in marriage dower does not invalidate the contract; the true intended amount is due by istihsan, demonstrating the Hanafi use of juristic preference over strict analogy.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Effect of Hazl on Mahr in Nikah: Two Narrations from Abu Hanifa
Expansion on the effect of hazl in mahr, with two narrations and a comparison to sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two narrations from Abu Hanifa on the effect of hazl on mahr and distinguish the basis of each (istihsan vs qiyas).

Core Idea
Hazl in mahr leads to a dispute: mahr al-mithl vs musamma, based on whether mahr is subsidiary or like a price.

This passage addresses a key usul question: when a mahr is mentioned jokingly in a marriage contract, what is the obligation? The Hanafi school contains two narrations from Abu Hanifa himself, each relying on a different method of reasoning. We will dissect the arguments and see how the subsidiary nature of mahr in nikah shapes the rule, in contrast to sale where the price is essential.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is a marriage contract where the mahr is mentioned in jest (hazl). The dispute is over what mahr is due: the named amount (musamma) or the dower of the like (mahr al-mithl).
2
State the two narrations from Abu Hanifa
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, Abu Hanifa said mahr al-mithl is due. According to Abu Yusuf, Abu Hanifa said musamma is due, preferring the appearance of seriousness.
Both are valid transmissions within the school.
3
Compare with sale
The text contrasts nikah with sale: in sale, the price (thaman) is essential, so hazl does not affect the obligation of the named price. In nikah, mahr is subsidiary (tabi'), so the jest is given effect.
This comparison reveals the illa for the ruling.
4
Understand the basis of each narration
The mahr al-mithl narration relies on istihsan: since mahr is not the primary object of nikah, the jest should be considered. The musamma narration relies on qiyas with sale: giving preference to the manifest seriousness.
Istihsan here overrides qiyas.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the mahr was jokingly set at 1000, the wife may either get 1000 (musamma) or a proper mahr (mahr al-mithl) which could be less or more.
The passage does not give final tarjih.

Source Text

لاَيَجِبُ بِهِ وَمَا كَانَ مَيْرًا فِي الْوَاقِعِ لَمْ يُذْكَرُ فِي الْعَقْدِ فَكَانَة تَدُو جَهَا بِلا مهر فَيَجِبُ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ بِخِلافِ البَيْعِ إِذْ لَا يَصحُ بِدُونِ الثَّمَنِ فَيَجِبُ الْمُسمَّى وَأَمَّا فِي الْخَرَيَيْنِ فَفِي رِوَايَةٍ مُحَمَّدٍ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ يَجِبُ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ أَبِى يُوْسُفَ عَنْهُ يَجِبُ الْمُسَمَى تَرْجِيْحًا لِجَانِبِ الْجِدْ كَمَا فِي الْبَيْعِ وَإِنْ كَانَ الْمَالَ فِيْهِ مَقْصُورًا كَالْحُلْمِ وَالْعِتْقِ عَلَى مَالِ وَالصُّلْحِ عَنْ دَمِ الْعَمَدِ فَإِنْ الْمَالَ مَقْصُودٌ فِي كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْأُمُورِ لأَنَّهُ لا يَجِبُ بِدُونِ الذِّكْرِ وَالتُنمِيَةِ فَإِن هَر لا يا صَلِهِ بِأَن تَوَاضَعَا عَلَى أَنْ يَعْقِدَا هَذِهِ الْعُقُودِ بِحُصَيْرِ النَّاسِ وَيَكُونَ با فِى الْوَاقِع مَوْلاً وَاتَّفَقَا عَلَى البِنَاءِ عَلَى الْمَوَاضِعَة بَعْدَ الْعَقْدِ فَالطلاق واقع وَالْمَالُ لَأَزِمٌ عِنْدَهُمَا.
ترجمر تشریح وإِن الفَقَا عَلَى الْبِنَاءِ فَالمَيْرُ الف بالإنفاق :- اور اگر سابق مذاق پر بنائے عقد میں ارونوں متفق ہو گئے تو سب کے نزدیک مہر ایک ہزار واجب ہوگا کیونکہ دو ہزار کا تذکرہ بطور
منزل (مذاق) سے تھا اور بال مذاق کی صورت میں واجب نہیں ہوتا رہا امام ابو حنیفہ کے اس قول کے درمیان کے اور اس قول کہ بیچ میں امام صاحب دو ہزار واجب کرتے ہیں اور نکاح میں ایک ہزار تو یہ ہے کہ اگر شمن رو بزار نہ مقرر کیا جاتا تو ایک ہزار شروط قرار پاتے جو کہ شرط فاسد ہے شرط فاسد بیچ کے لئے مفسد ہے اور شرط فاسد نکاح کے لئے مفسد نہیں ہے نہ نفس نکاح اور نہ مہر میں۔
وَإِنْ أَتَفَقَا عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَحْضُرُهُمَا شَيْءٌ أَوْ اخْتَلَفَا فَالفُكَاح جائز بالف اور اگر خالی الذین ہونے پر دونوں کا اتفاق ہو یا ( بناء علی الحمل کے بارے میں باہم اختلاف ہو ( تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں ) نکاح درست ہے ایک ہزار مہر پر امام محمد کی روایت میں امام ابو حنیفہ سے وقیل بالفین اور بعض نے کہا کہ دو ہزار مہر پر ۔ امام ابو یوسف کی روایت میں امام صاحب سے دوسری روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ امام صاحب مہر نکاح کو بیچ کی صورت پر قیاس فرماتے ہیں اور پہلی روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دو دلیل استحسان پر مبنی ہے کہ مہر نکاح میں تابع ہوتا ہے اس لئے جانب تسمیہ کو منزل پر ترجیح نہ دی جائے گی کیونکہ ترجیح دینے کی صورت میں مہر مقصود بالذات ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ اصل کے خلاف ہے بخلاف بیچ کے کیونکہ بیچ میں شمن (قیمت) مقصود ہوتی ہے لہذا اس کی صحیح (اس کو صحیح اور رائج قرار دینا اور شرط فاسد کو فاسد کر دینا) بھی مقصود ہے اس لئے جانب تسمیہ کو منزل پر ترجیح دی گئی ہے وان كان في الجنس اور اگر جنس مہر میں مذاقی ہو جائیں صورت کہ دونوں نے دنیا میں تواضع کی ہو اور اصل مبردار ہم ہوں۔ فان اتفقا على الاعراض فالمهر ماسميا وانه اتفقا على البناء واتفقا على أنه لم يحضرهما شئى اختلفا ۔ اور اگر مذاق المثل

اور اگر مذاق المثل اعراض پر دونوں کا اتفاق ہو تو مسمی مہر قرار پائے گا اور اگر بناء علی انمول ہونے میں یا خالی الذہن ہونے پر دونوں متفق ہوں یا مذاق پر بناء ہونے اور نہ ہونے میں باہم اختلاف ہو تو مہر مثل واجب ہو گا۔ یاد کو رومیوں صورتوں میں سے پہلی صورت تو بالا تفاق ہے کیونکہ دونوں نے مسمی میں ہنرل کا ارادہ کیا ہے اور مال منزل میں واجب نہیں ہو تا اور وہ واقع میں مہر تھا بخلاف بیچ کے کیونکہ بیچ بغیر شمن کے صحیح نہیں ہوتی لہذا اسمی ( ذکر کردہ رقم ) واجب ہوگی اور بہر حال دونوں صورتوں میں تو امام صاحب کی جو روایت امام محمد سے ہے تو میریل واجب ہو گا جیسا کہ ہم نے اوپر ذکر کر دیا ہے (پہلی صورت میں جو دلیل ہے وہی اس کی بھی ہے ) اور امام ابو یوسف کی روایت میں جو امام صاحب سے انہوں نے کی ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ سچ مچ جو مہر مقرر کیا ہے اس کو ترجیح دیتے ہوئے مهر کسی واجب ہو گا جیسے بیچ میں گذر چکا ہے
وَإِن كَانَ الْمَالَ مقصوداً كَالحُلْمِ وَالْعِتْقِ عَلى مَالٍ وَالصلح عن دم العمد (۳) . اور اگر اس عقد میں مال بحیثیت مقصور کے ہو جیسے خلع اور عتق بشرط اداء مال اور قتل محمد میں مصالحت بالمال کیونکہ مذکورہ تینوں امور میں سے ہر ایک میں مال بحیثیت مقصور کے ہے کیونکہ ان معاملات میں جب تک مال کا ذکر نہ کیا جائے مال واجب نہیں ہوتا۔
فإن هؤلاً بأصله تو اگر دونوں مذاق کرنے والوں کا مذاق اصل عقد کے بارے میں ہے بایں طور کہ دونوں نے طے کر لیا تھا کہ یہ تصرفات لوگوں کے سامنے کریں گے مگر حقیقت اور واقع میں یہ مذاق ہوگا واتفقا على البناء على المواضعة اور تصرف کی بناء تذاق پر ہونے میں دونوں کا اتفاق ہو، عقد کے بعد فالطلاق واقع والمال لازم عندهما تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور مال لازم ہو گا نصاحبین کے نزدیک۔ ثُم اختلفت نَسبْحُ الْمَتَنِ فِى هَذَا الْمُقَامِ فَذَكِرَ فِي بَعْضَهَا فَهُنَا تَحْتَ مَذْهَبِ صناحِبَيْهِ هَذِهِ الْعِبَارَةُ لأَنَّ الْمَوْلَ لايُوثُرُ فِي الْحُلَعِ عِنْدَهُمَا وَلَا تَخْتَلِفُ الْحَالُ بِالْبَنَاءِ أَوْ بِالإعْرَاضِ أَوْ بِالاِخْتِلَافِ وَذَالِكَ لأَنَّ الْخُلَعَ لَا يُحْتَمَلُ خِيَارَ الشَّرْطِ ولهذا لَوْشتَرَطَ الْخِيَارَ لَهَا فِي الْخَلَعِ وَجَبَ الْمَالُ وَوَقَعَ الطَّلاق وَبَطَلَ الْخِيَارُ وإِذَا لَمْ يَحْتَمِلُ خِيَارَ الشَّرْطِ فَلَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْمَالَ لأَنَّ الْهَزَلَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْجِهَارِ فَسَوَاءٌ اِثْفَقَا عَلَى الْبِنَاءِ أَوْ عَلى الإِعْرَاضِ أَوْ عَدَمِ الْحُصُورِ أَوْ إِخْتَلَفَا فِيْهِ يَبْطُلُ الْمَوْلُ وَيَقَعُ الطَّلاقَ يَلْزَمُ الْمَالُ عَلَى أَصْلِهِمَا وَعِنْدَهُ لايَقَعُ الطَّلاقَ بَلْ يَتَوَقُفُ عَلَى اختيار الْمَالِ سَوَاءٌ هَزلاً بأصلِهِ أَوْ قَدْرِهِ أَوْ لِجنسِهِ لأَن المَزلَ فِي مَعْنى خِيَارِ الشَّرْطِ وَقَدْ نَصَّ فِي خِيَارِ الشَّرْطِ مِنْ جَانِبِهَا أَنَّ الطلاق لا يَقَعُ وَلَا يَجِبُ الْمَالَ إِلا إِنْ شائَتِ الْمَرْأةُ فِحِينَئِذٍ يَجِبُ الْمَالُ عَلَيْهَا لِلزوج وَإِنْ أَعْرَضَا أَي
It is not obligatory by it, and what was a dower in reality but not mentioned in the contract is like contracting without a dower, so dower of the like (mahr al-mithl) is obligatory, unlike sale, for sale is not valid without a price, so the named (al-musamma) is obligatory. As for the two (khutba? unclear), in the narration of Muhammad from Abu Hanifa, dower of the like is obligatory for what we mentioned; and in the narration of Abu Yusuf from him, the named (al-musamma) is obligatory, giving preference to the side of seriousness, as in sale. And if the wealth is intended (maqsud) therein, like khul', emancipation for payment, and compromise for intentional bloodshed, then the wealth is intended in each of these matters, for it is not obligatory without mention and specification. Then if they jokingly agree to contract these contracts before the people, but in reality it is a jest, and they agree to build upon the jest after the contract, then divorce occurs and the wealth becomes binding according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings of hazl (jest) in marriage and other contracts, particularly regarding the obligation of mahr. The author discusses how hazl affects the mahr in nikah: if the mahr was mentioned in jest, the actual mahr in reality (mahr al-mithl) is due, analogously to a contract without a specified mahr. This differs from sale, where the price (thaman) is essential and thus the named price is due even if jokingly mentioned. There is a known ikhtilaf in narrations from Abu Hanifa: according to Muhammad al-Shaybani, Abu Hanifa said mahr al-mithl is due (due to the jest), while according to Abu Yusuf, he said the named mahr is due (giving precedence to seriousness). The passage then moves to contracts where the mal (wealth) is maqsud (intended) such as khul', itq 'ala mal, and sulh 'an dam al-amd. In these, since mal does not become obligatory without express mention, hazl in the origin of the contract leads to the ruling that if both parties agree to base the contract on the jest after the fact, then according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the contract is effective (talaq occurs and mal is due). However, there is a variant in the matn regarding the madhhab of the Sahibayn: the statement that hazl has no effect in khul' because khul' does not tolerate khiyar al-shart (option of condition). Hence, regardless of whether they agree to build on the jest or not, the contract is effective and mal is binding. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that talaq does not occur but is suspended upon the wife's choice to pay the mal; if she chooses, then talaq occurs and mal is due. This is because hazl is analogous to khiyar al-shart, and in khiyar al-shart from her side, talaq does not occur without her choice. The passage concludes with this ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest or joke; a statement made without serious intent.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): Dower of the like; the amount of dower considered appropriate for a woman similar to the bride.
المسمّى (al-musamma): The named or specified dower mentioned in the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a marriage contract, if the mahr is mentioned jokingly (hazl), what is the ruling according to the narration of Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa?
A) The mahr al-mithl is obligatory because the jest makes the mention void.
B) The named mahr (musamma) is obligatory, giving preference to seriousness.
C) The marriage is invalid without a proper mahr.
D) The mahr is deferred until divorce.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two narrations on hazl in mahr, one relying on istihsan (mahr al-mithl) and one on qiyas (musamma), reflecting the subsidiary nature of mahr in nikah.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
9 min
Effect of Hazl in Contracts Where Mal is Maqsud: Khul', Itq, and Sulh
Expansion on the effect of hazl in contracts where wealth is intended, with an ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify contracts where mal is maqsud and explain the Hanafi ruling when hazl occurs in these contracts, including the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
In contracts where wealth is intended, hazl in the origin of the contract still binds the wealth according to the Sahibayn.

This passage extends the analysis of hazl to contracts where the wealth (mal) is the primary object, such as khul', itq 'ala mal, and sulh 'an dam al-amd. Here, the rule differs because mal is essential. The passage also presents an ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding the effect of hazl when the contract is based on a prior jest. We will unpack the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify contracts where mal is maqsud
The text lists three: khul' (divorce for a consideration), itq 'ala mal (emancipation for payment), and sulh 'an dam al-amd (compromise for intentional homicide). In these, the wealth is indispensable.
Mal is maqsud because without mention, it is not obligatory.
2
Understand the effect of hazl on these contracts
If the parties jokingly agree to perform these contracts publicly but intend jest, and later agree to base the contract on the jest, the Sahibayn rule that the contracts are effective: talaq occurs and wealth is binding.
This differs from nikah where mahr is subsidiary.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's position
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), hazl in the origin of the contract does not prevent effect; they treat the jest as a valid contract because mal is maqsud and the contract cannot be conditional.
The text says 'khul' does not tolerate khiyar al-shart'.
4
Explain Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa analogizes hazl to khiyar al-shart (option of condition). Since in khiyar al-shart from the wife's side, talaq does not occur unless she chooses, similarly here talaq is suspended until the wife pays the mal.
This is based on the idea that hazl resembles a condition.
5
Identify the practical difference
Under the Sahibayn, once the parties agree to base on the jest, the divorce is immediate and wealth is due. Under Abu Hanifa, the divorce is suspended on the wife's payment.
The passage suggests the Sahibayn's view is more aligned with the principle that mal is maqsud, but Abu Hanifa's is also valid.

Source Text
