لاَيَجِبُ بِهِ وَمَا كَانَ مَيْرًا فِي الْوَاقِعِ لَمْ يُذْكَرُ فِي الْعَقْدِ فَكَانَة تَدُو جَهَا بِلا مهر فَيَجِبُ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ بِخِلافِ البَيْعِ إِذْ لَا يَصحُ بِدُونِ الثَّمَنِ فَيَجِبُ الْمُسمَّى وَأَمَّا فِي الْخَرَيَيْنِ فَفِي رِوَايَةٍ مُحَمَّدٍ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ يَجِبُ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ أَبِى يُوْسُفَ عَنْهُ يَجِبُ الْمُسَمَى تَرْجِيْحًا لِجَانِبِ الْجِدْ كَمَا فِي الْبَيْعِ وَإِنْ كَانَ الْمَالَ فِيْهِ مَقْصُورًا كَالْحُلْمِ وَالْعِتْقِ عَلَى مَالِ وَالصُّلْحِ عَنْ دَمِ الْعَمَدِ فَإِنْ الْمَالَ مَقْصُودٌ فِي كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْأُمُورِ لأَنَّهُ لا يَجِبُ بِدُونِ الذِّكْرِ وَالتُنمِيَةِ فَإِن هَر لا يا صَلِهِ بِأَن تَوَاضَعَا عَلَى أَنْ يَعْقِدَا هَذِهِ الْعُقُودِ بِحُصَيْرِ النَّاسِ وَيَكُونَ با فِى الْوَاقِع مَوْلاً وَاتَّفَقَا عَلَى البِنَاءِ عَلَى الْمَوَاضِعَة بَعْدَ الْعَقْدِ فَالطلاق واقع وَالْمَالُ لَأَزِمٌ عِنْدَهُمَا.
ترجمر تشریح وإِن الفَقَا عَلَى الْبِنَاءِ فَالمَيْرُ الف بالإنفاق :- اور اگر سابق مذاق پر بنائے عقد میں ارونوں متفق ہو گئے تو سب کے نزدیک مہر ایک ہزار واجب ہوگا کیونکہ دو ہزار کا تذکرہ بطور
منزل (مذاق) سے تھا اور بال مذاق کی صورت میں واجب نہیں ہوتا رہا امام ابو حنیفہ کے اس قول کے درمیان کے اور اس قول کہ بیچ میں امام صاحب دو ہزار واجب کرتے ہیں اور نکاح میں ایک ہزار تو یہ ہے کہ اگر شمن رو بزار نہ مقرر کیا جاتا تو ایک ہزار شروط قرار پاتے جو کہ شرط فاسد ہے شرط فاسد بیچ کے لئے مفسد ہے اور شرط فاسد نکاح کے لئے مفسد نہیں ہے نہ نفس نکاح اور نہ مہر میں۔
وَإِنْ أَتَفَقَا عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَحْضُرُهُمَا شَيْءٌ أَوْ اخْتَلَفَا فَالفُكَاح جائز بالف اور اگر خالی الذین ہونے پر دونوں کا اتفاق ہو یا ( بناء علی الحمل کے بارے میں باہم اختلاف ہو ( تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں ) نکاح درست ہے ایک ہزار مہر پر امام محمد کی روایت میں امام ابو حنیفہ سے وقیل بالفین اور بعض نے کہا کہ دو ہزار مہر پر ۔ امام ابو یوسف کی روایت میں امام صاحب سے دوسری روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ امام صاحب مہر نکاح کو بیچ کی صورت پر قیاس فرماتے ہیں اور پہلی روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دو دلیل استحسان پر مبنی ہے کہ مہر نکاح میں تابع ہوتا ہے اس لئے جانب تسمیہ کو منزل پر ترجیح نہ دی جائے گی کیونکہ ترجیح دینے کی صورت میں مہر مقصود بالذات ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ اصل کے خلاف ہے بخلاف بیچ کے کیونکہ بیچ میں شمن (قیمت) مقصود ہوتی ہے لہذا اس کی صحیح (اس کو صحیح اور رائج قرار دینا اور شرط فاسد کو فاسد کر دینا) بھی مقصود ہے اس لئے جانب تسمیہ کو منزل پر ترجیح دی گئی ہے وان كان في الجنس اور اگر جنس مہر میں مذاقی ہو جائیں صورت کہ دونوں نے دنیا میں تواضع کی ہو اور اصل مبردار ہم ہوں۔ فان اتفقا على الاعراض فالمهر ماسميا وانه اتفقا على البناء واتفقا على أنه لم يحضرهما شئى اختلفا ۔ اور اگر مذاق المثل

اور اگر مذاق المثل اعراض پر دونوں کا اتفاق ہو تو مسمی مہر قرار پائے گا اور اگر بناء علی انمول ہونے میں یا خالی الذہن ہونے پر دونوں متفق ہوں یا مذاق پر بناء ہونے اور نہ ہونے میں باہم اختلاف ہو تو مہر مثل واجب ہو گا۔ یاد کو رومیوں صورتوں میں سے پہلی صورت تو بالا تفاق ہے کیونکہ دونوں نے مسمی میں ہنرل کا ارادہ کیا ہے اور مال منزل میں واجب نہیں ہو تا اور وہ واقع میں مہر تھا بخلاف بیچ کے کیونکہ بیچ بغیر شمن کے صحیح نہیں ہوتی لہذا اسمی ( ذکر کردہ رقم ) واجب ہوگی اور بہر حال دونوں صورتوں میں تو امام صاحب کی جو روایت امام محمد سے ہے تو میریل واجب ہو گا جیسا کہ ہم نے اوپر ذکر کر دیا ہے (پہلی صورت میں جو دلیل ہے وہی اس کی بھی ہے ) اور امام ابو یوسف کی روایت میں جو امام صاحب سے انہوں نے کی ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ سچ مچ جو مہر مقرر کیا ہے اس کو ترجیح دیتے ہوئے مهر کسی واجب ہو گا جیسے بیچ میں گذر چکا ہے
وَإِن كَانَ الْمَالَ مقصوداً كَالحُلْمِ وَالْعِتْقِ عَلى مَالٍ وَالصلح عن دم العمد (۳) . اور اگر اس عقد میں مال بحیثیت مقصور کے ہو جیسے خلع اور عتق بشرط اداء مال اور قتل محمد میں مصالحت بالمال کیونکہ مذکورہ تینوں امور میں سے ہر ایک میں مال بحیثیت مقصور کے ہے کیونکہ ان معاملات میں جب تک مال کا ذکر نہ کیا جائے مال واجب نہیں ہوتا۔
فإن هؤلاً بأصله تو اگر دونوں مذاق کرنے والوں کا مذاق اصل عقد کے بارے میں ہے بایں طور کہ دونوں نے طے کر لیا تھا کہ یہ تصرفات لوگوں کے سامنے کریں گے مگر حقیقت اور واقع میں یہ مذاق ہوگا واتفقا على البناء على المواضعة اور تصرف کی بناء تذاق پر ہونے میں دونوں کا اتفاق ہو، عقد کے بعد فالطلاق واقع والمال لازم عندهما تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور مال لازم ہو گا نصاحبین کے نزدیک۔ ثُم اختلفت نَسبْحُ الْمَتَنِ فِى هَذَا الْمُقَامِ فَذَكِرَ فِي بَعْضَهَا فَهُنَا تَحْتَ مَذْهَبِ صناحِبَيْهِ هَذِهِ الْعِبَارَةُ لأَنَّ الْمَوْلَ لايُوثُرُ فِي الْحُلَعِ عِنْدَهُمَا وَلَا تَخْتَلِفُ الْحَالُ بِالْبَنَاءِ أَوْ بِالإعْرَاضِ أَوْ بِالاِخْتِلَافِ وَذَالِكَ لأَنَّ الْخُلَعَ لَا يُحْتَمَلُ خِيَارَ الشَّرْطِ ولهذا لَوْشتَرَطَ الْخِيَارَ لَهَا فِي الْخَلَعِ وَجَبَ الْمَالُ وَوَقَعَ الطَّلاق وَبَطَلَ الْخِيَارُ وإِذَا لَمْ يَحْتَمِلُ خِيَارَ الشَّرْطِ فَلَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْمَالَ لأَنَّ الْهَزَلَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْجِهَارِ فَسَوَاءٌ اِثْفَقَا عَلَى الْبِنَاءِ أَوْ عَلى الإِعْرَاضِ أَوْ عَدَمِ الْحُصُورِ أَوْ إِخْتَلَفَا فِيْهِ يَبْطُلُ الْمَوْلُ وَيَقَعُ الطَّلاقَ يَلْزَمُ الْمَالُ عَلَى أَصْلِهِمَا وَعِنْدَهُ لايَقَعُ الطَّلاقَ بَلْ يَتَوَقُفُ عَلَى اختيار الْمَالِ سَوَاءٌ هَزلاً بأصلِهِ أَوْ قَدْرِهِ أَوْ لِجنسِهِ لأَن المَزلَ فِي مَعْنى خِيَارِ الشَّرْطِ وَقَدْ نَصَّ فِي خِيَارِ الشَّرْطِ مِنْ جَانِبِهَا أَنَّ الطلاق لا يَقَعُ وَلَا يَجِبُ الْمَالَ إِلا إِنْ شائَتِ الْمَرْأةُ فِحِينَئِذٍ يَجِبُ الْمَالُ عَلَيْهَا لِلزوج وَإِنْ أَعْرَضَا أَي
It is not obligatory by it, and what was a dower in reality but not mentioned in the contract is like contracting without a dower, so dower of the like (mahr al-mithl) is obligatory, unlike sale, for sale is not valid without a price, so the named (al-musamma) is obligatory. As for the two (khutba? unclear), in the narration of Muhammad from Abu Hanifa, dower of the like is obligatory for what we mentioned; and in the narration of Abu Yusuf from him, the named (al-musamma) is obligatory, giving preference to the side of seriousness, as in sale. And if the wealth is intended (maqsud) therein, like khul', emancipation for payment, and compromise for intentional bloodshed, then the wealth is intended in each of these matters, for it is not obligatory without mention and specification. Then if they jokingly agree to contract these contracts before the people, but in reality it is a jest, and they agree to build upon the jest after the contract, then divorce occurs and the wealth becomes binding according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings of hazl (jest) in marriage and other contracts, particularly regarding the obligation of mahr. The author discusses how hazl affects the mahr in nikah: if the mahr was mentioned in jest, the actual mahr in reality (mahr al-mithl) is due, analogously to a contract without a specified mahr. This differs from sale, where the price (thaman) is essential and thus the named price is due even if jokingly mentioned. There is a known ikhtilaf in narrations from Abu Hanifa: according to Muhammad al-Shaybani, Abu Hanifa said mahr al-mithl is due (due to the jest), while according to Abu Yusuf, he said the named mahr is due (giving precedence to seriousness). The passage then moves to contracts where the mal (wealth) is maqsud (intended) such as khul', itq 'ala mal, and sulh 'an dam al-amd. In these, since mal does not become obligatory without express mention, hazl in the origin of the contract leads to the ruling that if both parties agree to base the contract on the jest after the fact, then according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the contract is effective (talaq occurs and mal is due). However, there is a variant in the matn regarding the madhhab of the Sahibayn: the statement that hazl has no effect in khul' because khul' does not tolerate khiyar al-shart (option of condition). Hence, regardless of whether they agree to build on the jest or not, the contract is effective and mal is binding. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that talaq does not occur but is suspended upon the wife's choice to pay the mal; if she chooses, then talaq occurs and mal is due. This is because hazl is analogous to khiyar al-shart, and in khiyar al-shart from her side, talaq does not occur without her choice. The passage concludes with this ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
المال المقصود (al-mal al-maqsud): Wealth that is the primary object or intention of a contract.
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife for a consideration paid to the husband.
العتق على مال (al-itq 'ala mal): Emancipation of a slave in exchange for payment.
الصلح عن دم العمد (al-sulh 'an dam al-amd): Compromise in intentional homicide by accepting blood money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if a husband and wife jokingly perform a khul' and later agree to base it on the jest, what is the ruling?
A) The khul' is invalid because it was based on jest.
B) The talaq occurs immediately and the wife must pay the agreed mal.
C) The talaq is suspended until the wife actually pays the mal.
D) The khul' requires a new contract without jest.

Key Takeaway
In contracts where wealth is the primary object, hazl in the origin does not prevent the contract's effect; an ikhtilaf exists between Abu Hanifa (suspension) and the Sahibayn (immediate binding).

The Legal Effect of Jest (Hazl) in Hanafi Usul
Examining the effect of jest on iqrar and the ruling on jest in apostasy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi rule on the effect of jest in iqrar and ridda, apply it to new scenarios, and derive the ruling from the Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Jest nullifies informative statements but does not excuse apostasy.

In Hanafi legal theory, the intent behind a statement can be decisive for some acts but irrelevant for others. This lesson explores the principle through two contrasting applications: jokingly confessing to an obligation is null and void, while jokingly uttering words of disbelief constitutes apostasy. The ruling on ridda is rooted in a direct Quranic decree that makes mockery of religion an act of disbelief regardless of the speaker's internal state.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish statement types
Identify the two categories of speech: informative (ikhbar) like iqrar, and performative (insha) like divorce or sale. In Hanafi usul, the effect of jest depends on the nature of the act.
Iqrar is a report that can be true or false; its validity rests on correspondence with reality.
2
Analyze the role of intention in iqrar
Understand that in iqrar, the speaker's intent is irrelevant if the underlying fact is false. The jesting confession is invalid because the reported fact is false, making the report itself false.
The text uses the example of colluding to fake a sale or marriage in public.
3
Contrast with ridda (apostasy)
Note that in ridda, the act of uttering words of disbelief itself causes apostasy, irrespective of jest or lack of belief. The ruling is derived from the Quranic verse that condemns mockery.
The objection that the speaker did not believe is answered: the jest itself is the cause.
4
Confirm with the Quranic proof
Read the cited verse (9:65-66) and observe that it explicitly declares that those who mocked became disbelievers. This establishes a general rule that jest in matters of religion is disbelief.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala, leaving no room for excuses based on intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ كَانَ ذَالِكَ أي الْهَزْلُ فِي الإِقْرَارِ بِمَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْفُسْخَ كَالْبَيْعِ بِأَنْ يُوَاضِعَا عَلَى أَنْ يَقْرَا بِالْبَيْعِ بِحُضُورِ النَّاسِ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ فِي الْوَاقِعِ إِقْرَارٌ وَبِمَا لَا يَحْتَمِلُهُ كَالنِّكَاحِ وَالطَّلَاقِ بِأَنْ يُوَاضِعَا عَلَى أَنْ يَقِرَّا بِالنِّكَاحِ وَالطَّلَاقِ بِحُضُورِ الْعَامَّةِ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ بَيْنَهُمَا إِقْرَارًا فَالْهَزْلُ يَبْطِلُهُ لِأَنَّ الإِقْرَارَ مُحْتَمَلٌ لِلصِّدْقِ وَالْكِذْبِ وَالْمُخْبَرُ عَنْهُ إِذَا كَانَ بَاطِلًا فَالْإِخْبَارُ بِهِ كَيْفَ يَصِيرُ حَقًّا وَالْهَزْلُ فِي الرِّدَّةِ كُفْرٌ أَيْ إِذَا بِلَفْظِ أَلْفَاظِ الْكُفْرِ هَزْلًا يَصِيرُ كَافِرًا أَوْ يُرَدُّ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّهُ كَيْفَ يَكُونُ كَافِرًا مَعَ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَعْتَقِدْ بِهِ فَأَجَابَ بِقَوْلِهِ لَا بِمَا هَزَلَ بِهِ أَيْ لَيْسَ كُفْرُهُ بِلَفْظِ هَزَلَ بِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ اعْتِقَادٍ لَكِنْ بِعَيْنِ الْهَزْلِ لِكَوْنِهِ هَزَلَ اسْتِحْقَاقًا بِالدِّينِ وَهُوَ كُفْرُهُ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى أَبِاللَّهِ وَآيَاتِهِ وَرَسُولِهِ كُنْتُمْ تَسْتَهْزِئُونَ لَا تَعْتَذِرُوا قَدْ كَفَرْتُمْ بَعْدَ إِيمَانِكُمْ
And if that [jest] occurs in iqrar (confession) regarding what admits of rescission, like a sale: that they agree to confess to a sale in front of people while in reality there is no sale; and regarding what does not admit of it, like marriage and divorce: that they agree to confess to marriage and divorce in front of the common people while there is no confession between them, then jest nullifies it because iqrar admits of truth and falsehood, and if the thing reported is false, how can reporting it become true? And jest in apostasy is disbelief: i.e., if one utters words of disbelief jokingly, he becomes a disbeliever. It is objected: how can he be a disbeliever when he did not believe it? He answered by saying: not by the word he joked with without belief, but by the very jest, because he joked. Deservedly by the religion, his disbelief is due to the statement of Allah the Exalted: 'Is it Allah and His verses and His Messenger that you were mocking? Make no excuse; you have disbelieved after your belief.'
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage discusses two applications of the principle that jest (hazl) has legal effect. First, in iqrar (confession): if two people agree to make a false confession jokingly, that confession is null and void because iqrar is an informative statement that can be true or false. If the underlying fact is false, the statement cannot create a legal obligation. Second, in apostasy (ridda): if someone jokingly utters words of disbelief, he becomes an apostate. The objection that he did not believe it is answered: the ruling is based on the act of jest itself, not on inner belief. The Quranic verse (9:65-66) is cited as proof that mocking religion constitutes disbelief, even if done in jest.

Key Terms
هَزْل (hazl): Saying something contrary to reality with no serious intent, often in a playful or joking manner.
إِقْرَار (iqrar): A statement admitting a legal obligation or fact, characterized as informative (ikhbar).
رِدَّة (ridda): Apostasy from Islam by word or deed, including jesting with words of disbelief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of jest (hazl) in apostasy (ridda)?
A) It is not considered apostasy because the person did not believe it.
B) It is considered apostasy only if done publicly.
C) It is considered apostasy because the act of jest itself is disbelief, even without belief.
D) It is considered a minor sin.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, jest (hazl) nullifies informative statements like iqrar because they require truth, but it does not excuse apostasy because the Quran explicitly declares mockery of religion to be disbelief.

Safah: Definition and Legal Effect
Defining safah linguistically and terminologically with its legal implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define safah (prodigality) according to the Hanafi school, distinguish its linguistic and terminological meanings, and explain its effect on legal capacity (ahliyyah) and the withholding of wealth, citing the Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Safah does not impair legal capacity; the prodigal remains fully obligated, but his wealth is withheld.

This lesson defines a key Hanafi legal term: safah (prodigality). Understanding safah is essential because it challenges common assumptions that a wasteful person loses full legal personality. Instead, the Hanafi school distinguishes between legal capacity and the right to manage property. We will examine the definition, its Quranic basis, and the precise limits it places on the prodigal.

Guided Path
1
Separate linguistic and terminological meanings
Identify the two layers: linguistic (lightness) and terminological (acting contrary to the Law with extravagance).
The terminological definition includes both forbidden acts and permissible acts done excessively.
2
Identify the core claim about legal capacity
Note that the passage explicitly says safah does not cause a defect in ahliyyah.
This is a critical distinguishing feature of the Hanafi position.
3
Locate the Quranic proof
Find the verse cited: 'Do not give the foolish your wealth' (4:5).
The verse is the primary textual evidence for withholding the prodigal's wealth.
4
Analyze the two interpretations
Understand the literal interpretation (guardians' own wealth) and the interpretation that supports the ruling (prodigal's wealth).
The Hanafi school adopts the second interpretation for the ruling.
5
Synthesize the legal effect
Conclude that the prodigal remains mukallaf (obligated to all rulings) but his wealth is withheld upon puberty.
This distinction is crucial for guardians and judges dealing with prodigal individuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالسَّفَه عَطْفٌ عَلَى مَا قَبْلَهُ وَهُوَ فِي اللُّغَةِ الْخِفَّةُ وَفِي الإصْطِلاحِ مَا عَرَّفَهُ الْمُصَنِّفُ بِقَوْلِهِ وَهُوَ الْعَمَلُ بِخِلافِ مُوجِبِ الشَّرْعِ وَإِنْ كَانَ أَصْلُهُ مَشْرُوعًا وَهُوَ السَّرَفُ وَالتَّبْذِيرُ أَنْ يُتَجَاوَزَ الْحَدُّ وَتَفْرِيقُ الْمَالِ إِسْرَافًا وَذَلِكَ لَا يُوجِبُ خَلَلًا فِي الْأَهْلِيَةِ وَلَا يَمْنَعُ شَيْئًا مِنْ أَحْكَامِ الشَّرْعِ مِنَ الْوُجُوبِ لَهُ وَعَلَيْهِ فَيَكُونُ مُطَالَبًا بِالْأَحْكَامِ كُلِّهَا وَيُمْنَعُ مَالُهُ عَنْهُ أَيْ مَالُ السَّفِيهِ عَنِ السَّفِيهِ فِي أَوَّلِ مَا يَبْلُغُ بِالنَّصِّ وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى وَلَا تُؤْتُوا السُّفَهَاءَ أَمْوَالَكُمُ الَّتِي جَعَلَ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ قِيَامًا وَفِي الْآيَةِ تَوْجِيهَاتِ أَحَدُهُمَا أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمَعْنَى عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِ أَيْ لَا تُؤْتُوا يَا أَيُّهَا الْأَوْلِيَاءُ السُّفَهَاءَ مِنَ الْأَزْوَاجِ وَالْأَوْلَادِ أَمْوَالَكُمُ الَّتِي جَعَلَ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ فِيهَا قِيَامًا لِأَنَّهُمْ يُضَيِّعُونَهَا بِلَا تَدْبِيرٍ ثُمَّ تَحْتَاجُونَ إِلَيْهِ لِأَجْلِ نَفَقَانِهِمْ وَلَا يُؤْتُونَكُمْ وَحِينَئِذٍ لَا يَكُونُ الْآيَةَ مِمَّا نَحْنُ فِيهِ وَالثَّانِي أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعْنَى أَمْوَالِكُمْ أَمْوَالَهُمْ وَإِنَّمَا أُضِيفَتْ إِلَيْهِمْ لِأَجْلِ الْقِيَامِ بِتَدْبِيرِهَا وَحِينَئِذٍ يَكُونُ تَمَسُّكًا لِمَا نَحْنُ فِيهِ أَنْ لَا تُؤْتُوا السُّفَهَاءَ أَمْوَالَهُمْ الَّتِي جَعَلَ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ فِيهَا تَدْبِيرَهَا وَقِيَامَهَا.
And 'safah' is connected to what precedes it. It is linguistically lightness (khiffa), and terminologically what the author defined as: it is acting contrary to what the Law requires, even if its origin is legislated, and it is extravagance and squandering: exceeding the limit and dispersing wealth wastefully. That does not cause a defect in legal capacity, nor does it prevent any of the rulings of the Law from being obligatory for him or against him. So he is held accountable for all rulings, but his wealth is withheld from him i.e., the wealth of the prodigal person is withheld from him at the beginning of his reaching puberty, by the text of His statement: 'And do not give the foolish your wealth which Allah has made for you a means of support.' In the verse there are interpretations: one is that the meaning is literal, i.e., O guardians, do not give to the foolish among your spouses and children your wealth which Allah has made for you a support, because they will waste it without management, then you will need it for their maintenance and they will not give it to you. In that case, the verse is not relevant to our topic. The second is that the meaning of 'your wealth' is 'their wealth', and it is attributed to you because of your management of it. In that case, it is a proof for our topic that you should not give the foolish their wealth which Allah has made you responsible for managing and supporting.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage defines safah (prodigality) and its legal effects. Linguistically, safah means lightness, and terminologically, it is acting contrary to the Law's requirements, specifically overspending and wasting wealth. The definition clarifies that safah does not affect legal capacity (ahliyyah); the prodigal person remains fully obligated to all legal duties. However, his wealth is withheld from him upon reaching puberty based on the Quranic verse. The commentary on the verse provides two interpretations: one that the verse addresses the wealth of the guardians and is not directly about the prodigal's own wealth, and another that the verse addresses the wealth of the prodigal himself, which the guardian should not give to him. The latter interpretation supports the ruling that the prodigal's wealth is withheld.

Key Terms
سَفَه (safah): Linguistically lightness; terminologically, acting contrary to the Law in a way that involves extravagance and squandering.
إِهْلِيَة (ahliyyah): Legal capacity to receive rights and obligations. The passage states safah does not cause a defect in ahliyyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition of safah, what is the effect on the legal capacity (ahliyyah) of the prodigal person?
A) His legal capacity is completely removed.
B) His legal capacity is intact, but his wealth is withheld from him.
C) He is not obligated to perform prayers or fast.
D) He is considered insane.

Key Takeaway
Safah restricts the disposal of wealth but does not affect the prodigal's legal capacity or religious obligations.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Legal Effect of Error (Khata') in Hanafi Fiqh
Defining khata' and its excusal in rights of Allah but not rights of servants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that khata' does not negate worldly rulings in rights of servants, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
Error excuses sin but not worldly liability — the hadith lifts afterlife punishment, not this-world obligations.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text clarifies a critical distinction: the famous hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطاء والنسيان' does not erase all consequences of mistakes. While error removes sin and punishment in the Hereafter, it does not eliminate obligations toward other people — such as compensation for damages or validity of contracts. The author presents proofs from the obligation of diyah and kaffarah, and then addresses a key madhhab dispute on mistaken divorce and sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
The passage states that error is not excused in rights of servants. Recognise that this is a fundamental principle: huquq al-‘ibad require recompense regardless of intent.
The principle is derived from the requirement of daman and diyah for accidental harm.
2
Trace the dalil (hadith and its interpretation)
The text cites the hadith of lifting error and forgetfulness. But it interprets it narrowly: only the afterlife ruling (sin) is lifted, not worldly rulings. Evidence is that diyah and kaffarah are still obligatory.
This is a key usul move: restricting the scope of a general text using other proofs.
3
Examine the madhhab dispute on mistaken talaq
The passage contrasts the Hanafi position (talaq takes effect) with the Shafi'i position (does not take effect). Identify the basis: the Shafi'i analogy to a sleeping person, and the Hanafi response distinguishing the mistaken person as mukhtar (has choice) and muqassir (negligent).
Focus on the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in validity of divorce.
4
Analyse the qiyas used
The Shafi'i use qiyas to the sleeper (no choice, no effect). The Hanafi refute by showing the mistaken person has choice, albeit erring. Understand how qiyas is refuted by a difference in the effective cause (illah).
This illustrates the importance of classifying the mukallaf's state in usul.
5
Evaluate the ruling on mistaken sale
The passage also covers sale by mistake: it is concluded but fasid (defective) because the utterance is voluntary but consent is lacking. Note the parallel with duress (ikrah).
Contrast with talaq: sale is fasid, not batil, because the contract has some basis.

Source Text

وَلَمْ يُجْعَلْ عُذْرًا فِي حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ حَتَّى وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ ضَمَانُ الْعُدْوَانِ إِذَا أَتْلَفَ مَالَ إِنْسَانٍ خَطَاءً وَوَجَبَتْ بِهِ الدِّيَةُ إِذَا قَتَلَ إِنْسَانًا خَطَاءً لِأَنَّ كُلَّهَا مِنْ حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ وَبَدَلُ الْمَحَلِّ لَا يُجْزِئُ عَنِ الْفِعْلِ. وَصَحَّ طَلَاقُهُ أَيْ طَلَاقُ الْخَاطِئِ كَمَا إِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يَقُولَ لِأَمَتِهِ: اِقْعَدِي، فَجَرَى عَلَى لِسَانِهِ: أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ. يَقَعُ بِهِ الطَّلَاقُ عِنْدَنَا وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيِّ لَا يَقَعُ، قِيَاسًا عَلَى النَّائِمِ عَدِيمِ الِاخْتِيَارِ. وَالْخَاطِئُ مُخْتَارٌ مُقَصِّرٌ. وَالْمَرَادُ بِالْحَدِيثِ رَفْعُ حُكْمِ الْآخِرَةِ لَا حُكْمُ الدُّنْيَا بِدَلِيلِ وُجُوبِ الدِّيَةِ وَالْكَفَّارَةِ. وَيَجِبُ أَنْ يَنْعَقِدَ بَيْعُهُ أَيْ بَيْعُ الْخَاطِئِ كَمَا إِذَا أَرَادَ أَحَدٌ أَنْ يَقُولَ الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ فَجَرَى عَلَى لِسَانِهِ بِعْتُ مِنْكَ كَذَا فَقَالَ الْمُخَاطَبُ قَبِلْتُ. وَهَذَا مَعْنَى قَوْلِهِ إِذَا صَدَّقَهُ خَصْمُهُ. وَقِيلَ مَعْنَاهُ أَنْ يُصَدِّقَ الْخَصْمُ بِأَنَّ صُدُورَ الْإِيجَابِ مِنْكَ كَانَ خَطَاءً إِذْ لَوْ لَمْ يُصَدِّقْهُ فِي ذَلِكَ يَكُونُ حُكْمُهُ حُكْمَ الْعَامِدِ. وَيَكُونُ بَيْعُهُ كَبَيْعِ الْمُكْرَهِ يَعْنِي يَنْعَقِدُ فَاسِدًا لِأَنَّ جَرَيَانَ الْكَلَامِ عَلَى لِسَانِهِ اخْتِيَارِيٌّ فَيَنْعَقِدُ وَلَكِنْ يَفْسُدُ لِعَدَمِ وُجُودِ الرِّضَا فِيهِ.

فاسد ہو جائیگی کیونکہ کلام کا صدور اس کی زبان سے اختیاری ہے لہذا منعقد ہو جائے گی لیکن فاسد ہو گی کیونکہ اکراہ کی صورت میں اسکی رضامندی نہیں پائی گئی۔
And error is not made an excuse in the rights of servants, so that the compensation for transgression is obligatory upon him when he destroys the property of a person by mistake, and blood-money becomes obligatory by it when he kills a person by mistake, because all of these are from the rights of servants, and the replacement of the object does not substitute for the action. And his divorce is valid, i.e., the divorce of the mistaken person, as when he intended to say to his slave-girl: 'Sit down,' but his tongue slips and says: 'You are divorced.' Divorce occurs by it according to us, but according to al-Shafi'i it does not occur, by analogy to the sleeping person who has no choice. And the mistaken person has choice but is negligent. And the intended meaning of the hadith is the lifting of the ruling of the Hereafter, not the ruling of this world, as evidenced by the obligation of blood-money and expiation. And his sale must be concluded, i.e., the sale of the mistaken person, as when someone intended to say 'Alhamdulillah' but his tongue slips and says 'I sold to you such and such,' and the addressee says 'I accept.' And this is the meaning of his saying 'when his opponent confirms him.' And it is said that its meaning is that the opponent confirms that the utterance of the offer from you was by mistake, because if he does not confirm him in that, his ruling becomes the ruling of the intentional. And his sale becomes like the sale of the coerced person, meaning it is concluded as defective, because the flow of speech on his tongue is voluntary, so it is concluded, but it becomes defective due to the absence of consent in it. (Followed by Urdu translation/commentary explaining the same concepts in detail.)
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from a Hanafi usul text discussing the legal effect of error (khata'). It establishes a fundamental principle: error is excused in matters pertaining to the rights of Allah (e.g., sin and punishment in the Hereafter), but it is not excused in matters pertaining to the rights of servants (huquq al-‘ibad), such as property damage, bodily harm, or contractual obligations. The text begins by stating that error is not considered an excuse for rights of servants. For example, if someone accidentally destroys another's property, he must pay compensation (daman). If he accidentally kills someone, he must pay blood-money (diyah). This is because these are rights of servants that require recompense; merely replacing the object is not sufficient to absolve the act. The passage then addresses the validity of divorce (talaq) uttered by mistake. According to the Hanafi school, if a person intends to say something else but mistakenly pronounces 'You are divorced,' the divorce takes effect. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, analogizing the mistaken person to a sleeping person who has no choice. The Hanafi response is that the mistaken person is a person of choice (mukhtar) who is negligent (muqassir), unlike the sleeper. The hadith 'Rifa al-khata' wa al-nisyan' is interpreted by the Hanafis as removing only the sin in the Hereafter, not the worldly legal consequences. Evidence is that diyah and kaffarah are still obligatory. Next, the text discusses the sale of a mistaken person. If someone intends to say something else but inadvertently makes an offer of sale, and the other party accepts, the sale is concluded but deemed defective (fasid), similar to the sale of a coerced person. This is because the utterance was voluntary, but genuine consent (rida) was absent. The text also clarifies that if the opponent confirms the mistake, the ruling follows accordingly; otherwise, it is treated as intentional.

Key Terms
الخطاء (al-khata'): An act occurring contrary to one's intention and will, due to mistake or slip.
حقوق العباد (huquq al-‘ibad): Rights of human beings (servants of Allah) that involve claims for compensation or enforcement in this world.
رفع حكم الآخرة (raf‘ hukm al-ākhira): The removal of the ruling of the Hereafter, i.e., sin and punishment, which is the scope of the hadith 'raf‘ al-khata' wa al-nisyan'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of a mistaken sale (where the seller intends to say something else)?
A) The sale is void (batil) because there is no consent.
B) The sale is valid because the utterance is voluntary.
C) The sale is concluded but defective (fasid) due to lack of genuine consent.
D) The sale is suspended until the seller confirms the mistake.

Key Takeaway
Error in Hanafi fiqh removes sin but does not eliminate worldly obligations in rights of servants; contracts and liabilities still apply unless proven otherwise.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Definition and Categories of Compulsion (Ikrah)
Defines ikrah and divides it into types and rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify compulsion (ikrah) into three types based on its effect on consent (rida) and choice (ikhtiyar), and state the Hanafi ruling for each type of action under compulsion.

Core Idea
Ikrah does not remove legal capacity; its effect on consent and choice determines the ruling.

This lesson examines the Hanafi legal concept of compulsion (ikrah). You will learn how ikrah is defined, categorized, and how it interacts with the legal obligation of a mukallaf. Understanding ikrah is crucial for correctly applying rulings in cases of coercion, where the balance between necessity and prohibition must be weighed.

Guided Path
1
Define ikrah and its legal significance
Identify the definition of ikrah as forcing a person to do something disliked that he would not do voluntarily. Note that it is an acquired impediment that does not negate legal capacity.
The text states ikrah does not contradict khitab or ahliyyah because intellect and majority remain.
2
Distinguish the three types by their effect on rida and ikhtiyar
For each type, determine whether consent (rida) and choice (ikhtiyar) are present or absent. The three types are: (1) ikrah mulji' (threat to life/limb) – removes both; (2) non-mulji' (imprisonment/beating) – removes rida but not ikhtiyar; (3) threat against family – removes neither.
The distinction is foundational for applying rulings.
3
Identify the four possible rulings for acting under ikrah
List the four categories: fard (obligatory, e.g., eating carrion to save life), haram (prohibited, e.g., murder), mubah (permissible, e.g., breaking fast), and rukhsah (concession, e.g., uttering kufr with heart firm in faith).
Note that haram acts remain haram even under mulji' compulsion.
4
Differentiate between mubah and rukhsah
Understand that in rukhsah, the prohibition is not lifted; the act is treated as mubah only in terms of removing sin, whereas in mubah the prohibition is fully removed.
This nuance affects the legal status of the act itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإكراه وهو عطف على ما قبله وبه تمام الأمور المعترضة المكتسبة وهو حمل الإنسان على ما يكره ولا يزيد ذلك الإنسان مباشرته لولا الأكربة وهو أي الإكراه على ثلاثة أقسام لأنه إما أن يعدم الرضاء ويفسد الاختيار وهو الملجئ الإكراه الملجئ بما يخاف على نفسه أو عضو من أعضائه بأن يقول إن لم تفعل كذا لأقتلنك أو لأقطعن يدك فحينئذ ينعدم رضاؤه ويفسد اختياره البتة أو يعدم الرضاء ولا يفسد الاختيار وهو الإكراه بالقيد أو الحبس مدة مديدة أو بالضرب الذي لا يخاف على نفسه التلف فإنه يبقى اختياره حينئذ ولا يرضى به أو لا يعدم الرضاء ولا يفسد الاختيار وهو أن يهدد بحبس أبيه أو ابنه أو زوجته أو نحو ذلك فإن الرضاء والاختيار كلاهما باق والإكراه بجملته أي بجميع هذه الأقسام لا ينافي الخطاب والأهلية لبقاء العقل والبلوغ الذي العقل عليه مدار الخطاب والأهلية وإنه متردد بين فرض وحظر وإباحة ورخصة يعني أن الإكراه أي العمل به منقسم إلى هذه الأقسام الأربعة ففي بعض المقام العمل به فرض كأكل الميتة إذا أكره عليه بما يوجب الإنجاء فإنه يقتضي عليه ذلك ولو صبر حتى مات موقف عليه لأنه ألقى نفسه إلى التهلكة وفي بعضه العمل به حرام كالزنا وقتل النفس المعصومة فإنه يحرم فعلهما بالإكراه الملجئ وفي بعضه العمل به مباح كالأفطار في الصوم فإنه إذا أكره عليه يباح له الفطر وفي بعضه العمل به رخصة كإجراء كلمة الكفر على لسانه إذا أكره عليه يرخص له ذلك بشرط أن يكون القلب مطمئنا بالإيمان والإكراه ملجئ والفرق بين الإباحة والرخصة أن في الرخصة لا يباح ذلك الفعل بأن ترتفع الحرمة بل يعامل معاملة المباح في رفع الإثم وفي الإباحة ترتفع الحرمة. ترجمہ تشریح ذا الخزان اور اگر وہ اسکا حلف بھی " جمل " پر ہے اس پر اہمیت کے عوراض کسبیہ کا بیان ختم ہو جائے گا اگر اہ انسان کو ایسے کام کے کرنے پر مجبور کرنا جیسے وہ پسند نہیں کرتا کہ اگر مجبور نہ کیا جاتا وہ اس کام کو انجام نہ دیتا و ھو اور یہ یعنی اکراہ کی تین قسمیں ہیں کیونکہ اما ان يقدم الرضاء ويفسد الاختيار وهو الملجئي (1) یا تو رضاء فعل اور اختیار عمل کو ضائع کر دے اسے اکراہ سیجی کہتے ہیں یعنی وہ اگر وہ جس پر اس کو مجبور کیا گیا ہے جس میں انسان اپنی جان کی ہلاکت یا کسی بعضو بدن کے کائے جانے کا خوف کرتا ہے مثلا اس سے کہتا ہے کہ اگر تو نے یہ کام نہ کیا تو تجھ کو قتل کر دوں گا یا پھر تیرا ہاتھ کاٹ دوں گا اس صورت میں اسکی رضا مندی ختم ہو جاتی ہے اور اس کا اختیار یقینی طور پر فاسد ہو جاتا ہے۔ وَيَعْدِمُ الرَّضَاء وَلايُفْسِدُ الاختيار با رضا تو ختم کر دیے لیکن اختیار باقی رہے اس اکراہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ انسان کو قید کر دینے جیل میں ڈالدینے کی دھمکی دی جائے یا ضرب شدید سے ڈرایا جائے لیکن جان سے ہلاک کر دینے کا خوفسنہ دلایا جائے ( اس کو اگر او غیر مسبجی کہتے ہیں ) اس میں انسان کا اختیار تو ہائی رہتا ہے مگر رضامندی شامل نہیں رہتی ہے یعنی وہ ا سکے کرنے پر راضی نہیں ہوتا۔ أوْ لا يَعْدِمُ الرضاءُ وَلايُفسد الاختيار یا رضامند کی ختم نہ کرے اور نہ اختیار میں نقص پیدا کرے مثلا اس کے باپ بیٹے، بیوی کو قید کر دینے کی دھمکی دے اس کی دھمکی میں جس کو دھمکی دی گئی ہے اس کا
And compulsion (ikrah) is a conjunction to what precedes, completing the discussion of acquired impediments. It is forcing a person to something disliked such that he would not do it without compulsion. It is of three types: (1) that which removes consent and spoils choice – this is overwhelming compulsion, when one fears for his life or limb, e.g., 'if you do not do this, I will kill you or cut your hand'; then consent is absent and choice is completely spoiled. (2) that which removes consent but does not spoil choice – compulsion by shackles or long imprisonment or beating that does not threaten life; then choice remains but he is not pleased. (3) that which does not remove consent nor spoil choice – threatening to imprison his father, son, wife, etc.; then both consent and choice remain. All these types do not contradict legal address (khitab) and capacity, because the intellect and majority remain. Acting on compulsion is divided into four categories: obligatory – eating carrion when compelled to save life, as he must do so and if he refrains until death he is sinful for self-destruction; prohibited – adultery and murder of protected life, even under overwhelming compulsion; permissible – breaking the fast in Ramadan when compelled; and concessionary – uttering words of disbelief if compelled, provided the heart is at rest with faith, and the compulsion is overwhelming. The difference between permissible and concessionary is that in concession the act is not made permissible by removal of prohibition, but is treated like permissible in terms of removing sin, while in the permissible the prohibition is removed.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage defines ikrah (compulsion) and categorizes its types and rulings. Ikrah is a person being coerced into doing something they dislike, which they would not do voluntarily. It is divided into three kinds based on whether it destroys consent (rida) and/or choice (ikhtiyar). 1. Mukrih mulji' (overwhelming compulsion): threat of death or loss of limb—both consent and choice are nullified. 2. Non-mulji' compulsion: threat of imprisonment or beating without fear of death—consent is absent but choice remains. 3. Threat against family: threatening to imprison a close relative—neither consent nor choice is affected. Crucially, all forms of compulsion do not negate legal capacity (ahliyyah) because the person retains intellect and is of age. The text then outlines four possible rulings for acting under compulsion: (a) fard (obligatory) when necessary for survival, e.g., eating carrion; (b) haram, e.g., killing a protected person even under threat; (c) mubah, e.g., breaking a fast; (d) rukhsah (concession), e.g., uttering kufr words with a heart firm in faith—this is allowed only as a concession, not as a full permission. The distinction between mubah and rukhsah is explained: in rukhsah, the prohibition is not lifted, but the act is treated like mubah in removing sin.

Key Terms
إكراه ملجئ (ikrah mulji'): Compulsion that destroys consent and choice, typically threat of death or loss of limb.
رضاء (rida'): Contentment or approval of an action, which may be absent under compulsion.
رخصة (rukhsah): A concession allowing an otherwise prohibited act under necessity, without fully lifting the prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification, what is the ruling on eating carrion for a person compelled by threat of death?
A) Haram, because carrion is inherently forbidden.
B) Mubah, because it is permissible under compulsion.
C) Fard (obligatory), to save one's life.
D) Rukhsah, as a concession.

Key Takeaway
Ikrah does not remove legal capacity; the ruling depends on the severity of compulsion and the nature of the coerced act.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Classification of Acts Under Coercion (Ikrah)
Classification of coerced acts into four hukm categories and distinction between ibahah and rukhsah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four hukm categories of acting under coercion (fard, haram, ibahah, rukhsah) and distinguish ibahah from rukhsah using the Hanafi definition.

Core Idea
Coercion does not remove legal address; acts under coercion are fard, haram, mubah, or rukhsah – and prohibition may remain.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar explains that coercion (ikrah) does not negate the legal address because the coerced person retains intellect and legal capacity. The author divides acting under coercion into four legal categories: fard, haram, ibahah, and rukhsah. We will explore each category with examples and examine the critical distinction between ibahah (permissibility with lifted prohibition) and rukhsah (concession with prohibition remaining). We also address a scholarly dispute on whether ibahah is a separate category.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key premise
Recognize that coercion does not invalidate the legal address (khitab) or legal capacity (ahliyyah) because the coerced person retains intellect and puberty.
This premise is crucial for understanding why acts under coercion are still subject to legal categorization.
2
List the four categories
From the passage, extract the four categories: fard (obligatory), haram (prohibited), ibahah (permissible), and rukhsah (concession). Note the examples given for each.
The categories are not mutually exclusive; some acts under coercion may fall into one category depending on context.
3
Apply categories to examples
Match the examples: eating carrion under life threat → fard; adultery and murder even under mulji' coercion → haram; breaking fast for a coerced resident → mubah; uttering disbelief under mulji' coercion with heart firm → rukhsah.
Notice that some acts like murder remain haram regardless of coercion.
4
Distinguish ibahah and rukhsah
Analyze the textual distinction: in ibahah, the prohibition is lifted completely; in rukhsah, the prohibition remains but sin is removed. Understand that rukhsah does not make the act permissible in essence.
This distinction has practical implications for determining the legal status of an act.
5
Analyze the dispute on ibahah
Examine the argument (qil) that ibahah is unnecessary because it falls under fard or rukhsah, and the response that cases like a coerced resident breaking fast do not fit either category, thus ibahah is distinct.
This dispute illustrates the importance of precise categorization in Hanafi usul.

أَوْ ابْنِهِ أَوْ زَوْجَتِهِ أو نَحْوِهِ فَإِنَّ الرَّضَاءَ والاختيار كِلاهُمَا بَاتِ والإكْرَاهُ بِجُمْلَتِهِ أَى بِجَمِيعِ هَذهِ الأَقْسام لايُنَافِى الْخِطَابَ وَالأهْلِيَة لِبَقَاءِ العقل والبلوغ الذي الْعَقْلُ عَلَيْهِ مَدَارُ الْخِطَابِ وَالأهْلَيَةِ وَإِنَّهُ مُتَرَدَّدُ بَيْنَ فَرْض وَحَظِيرٍ وَإِبَاحَةٍ وَرُخصةٍ يَعْنِي أَنَّ الإِكْرَاهَ أي العَمَلَ بِهِ مُنقَسم إلى هذه الأَقْسَامِ الْأَرْبَعَةِ فَفِي بَعْضِ الْمُقَامِ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ فَرْضِ كَاكُلِ المَيْتَةِ إِذَا أُكْرِهَ عَلَيْهِ بِمَا يُوجِبُ الإِنْجَاءَ فَإِنَّهُ يَقْتَرِضُ عَلَيْهِ ذَلِكَ وَلَوْ صَبَرَ حَتَّى يَمُوتَ مُوجِبَ عَلَيْهِ لإِنَّهُ الْقَى نَفْسَهُ إلى التهْلُكَةِ وَفِي بَعْضِهِ العَمَلُ به حرام كَالرِّنَا وَقَتْلِ النَّفْسِ الْمَعْصُوْمَةِ فَإِنَّهُ يَحْرَمُ فِعْلُهُمَا بالإِكْرَاهِ الْمُلْجِي وَفِي بَعْضِهِ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ مُبَاحُ كَالْإِفْطَارِ فِي الصَّوْمِ فَإِنَّةَ إذَا أُكْرِهَ عَلَيْهِ يُبَاحُ لَهُ الْفِطْرُ وَفِي بَعْضِهِ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ رُخْصَةُ كَاجْرَاءِ كَلِمَةِ الْكُفْرِ عَلَى لِسَانِهِ إِذَا أُكْرِهَ عَلَيْهِ يُرَخَّصُ لَهُ ذَلِكَ بِشَرْطِ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْقَلْبُ مُطْمَئِنًّا بِالتَّصْدِيقِ وَالإِكْرَاهُ مَلْجَا وَالْفَرْقَ بَيْنَ الإِبَاحَةِ وَالرُّخْصَةِ أَنْ فِي الرُّخْصَةِ لايُبَاحُ ذَلِكَ الْفِعْلُ بإنْ تَرْتَفِعَ الْحُرْمَةُ بَلْ يُعَامِلُ مُعَامَلَةَ المُباح فى رفع الأثم وفي الإِبَاحَةِ تَرْتَفِعُ الْحُرْمَةُ.
ترجمہ تشریح ذا الخزان (۷) اور اگر وہ اسکا حلف بھی " جمل " پر ہے اس پر اہمیت کے عوراض کسبیہ کا بیان ختم ہو جائے گا اگر اہ انسان کو ایسے کام کے کرنے پر مجبور کرنا جیسے وہ پسند نہیں کرتا کہ اگر مجبور نہ کیا جاتا وہ اس کام کو انجام نہ دیتا و ھو اور یہ یعنی اکراہ کی تین قسمیں ہیں کیونکہ اما ان يقدم الرضاء ويفسد الاختيار وهو الملجئي (1) یا تو رضاء فعل اور اختیار عمل کو ضائع کر دے اسے اکراہ سیجی کہتے ہیں یعنی وہ اگر وہ جس پر اس کو مجبور کیا گیا ہے جس میں انسان اپنی جان کی ہلاکت یا کسی بعضو بدن کے کائے جانے کا خوف کرتا ہے مثلا اس سے کہتا ہے کہ اگر تو نے یہ کام نہ کیا تو تجھ کو قتل کر دوں گا یا پھر تیرا ہاتھ کاٹ دوں گا اس صورت میں اسکی رضا مندی ختم ہو جاتی ہے اور اس کا اختیار یقینی طور پر فاسد ہو جاتا ہے۔ وَيَعْدِمُ الرَّضَاء وَلايُفْسِدُ الاختيار (۳) با رضا تو ختم کر دیے لیکن اختیار باقی رہے اس اکراہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ انسان کو قید کر دینے جیل میں ڈالدینے کی دھمکی دی جائے یا ضرب شدید سے ڈرایا جائے لیکن جان سے ہلاک کر دینے کا خوفسنہ دلایا جائے ( اس کو اگر او غیر مسبجی کہتے ہیں ) اس میں انسان کا اختیار تو ہائی رہتا ہے مگر رضامندی شامل نہیں رہتی ہے یعنی وہ ا سکے کرنے پر راضی نہیں ہوتا۔ أوْ لا يَعْدِمُ الرضاءُ وَلايُفسد الاختيار (۳) یا رضامند کی ختم نہ کرے اور نہ اختیار میں نقص پیدا کرے مثلا اس کے باپ بیٹے، بیوی کو قید کر دینے کی دھمکی دے اس کی دھمکی میں جس کو دھمکی دی گئی ہے اس کا اختیار در ضاء دونوں پاتی ہیں۔ وَالإكْرَاهُ بِجُمْلَتِه اور جمله اکراه به تمام اقسام اکراه لا ينافي لخطاب الاهلية خطاب شرع اور اہلبیت کے منائی نہیں ہیں وانه متردد بين فروض حظر واباحة ورخصة اور یہ وائر ہے فرض حرام اور مباح اور رخصت میں یعنی اکراہ کے مطابق عمل کرنا چار قسموں میں منقسم ہے بعض مقام میں تو اکراہ کے مطابق عمل کرنا فرض ہے خلا میت کا کھانا جب انسان کو میتہ کھانے پر مجبور کر دیا جائے جو الجاء کی نوعیت پیدا کر دے یعنی ایسی چیز سے ڈرایا جائے کہ جس سے انسان مجبور ہو جائے (1) مثلا قتل کرنے کی دھمکی یا عضو کاٹ دینے کی دھمکی تو اس صورت مینی آدمی کو مردار کھا لینا فرض قرار دیا گیا ہے اور اگر مکر و نے اپنے اوپر صبر کیا اور وہ مر گیا تو مکرہ کو سزادی جائے گی (عذاب ہو گا) کیونکہ اس نے اپنی جان کو ہلاکت میں ڈالا ہے۔ فَفِي بَعْضِهِ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ حَرَام اور اکراہ کی بعض صورتوں میں اکراہ کو بموجب عمل کرنا حرام ہے جیسے کسی کو زنا کرنے یا کسی کو مار ڈالنے پر مجبور کرتا تو ان کا انجام و نیا کراہ کی صورت میں بھی حرام ہے خواہ اکراہ مسیحی کیوں نہ ہو اور اکراہ کی بعض صورتوں میں اکراہ کے بموجب عمل کرنا مباح ہے جیسے روزہ کی حالت میں اس کو افطار کرنے پر مجبور کیا جانا کیونکہ اگر مجبور کئے جانے پر اس نے روزہ توڑ دیا تو مباح ہے اور اکراہ کی بعض صورتوں میں اکراہ کے مطابق عمل کرنے کی رخصت ہے جیسے زبان پر کور کفر جاری کر پلجب بندہ کو اس پر مجبور کیا جائے تو اس کو اجراء کی رخصت ہے مگر شرط یہ ہے کہ دل اسلام سے مطئمن ہو اور اگر اہ بھی بطریق میجی ہو۔ وَالْفَرْقَ بَيْنَ الْإِبَاحَةِ وَالرُّحْصَةِ إِبَاحَت اور رخصت دونوں کے درمیان فرق یہ ہے کہ رخصت میں وہ فعل اس کے لئے مباح نہیں ہوتا کہ حرمت کو ختم کر دی جائے حرمت باقی رہتی ہے صرف فعل میں مباح کا معاملہ کیا جاتا ہے اور اباحت میں فعل کی حرمت ہی اٹھالی جاتی ہے۔ وَقِيلَ لَا حَاجَةَ إِلى ذِكْرِ الإِبَاحَةِ لِدُخُولِهَا فِي الفَرَض أَوِ الرُّخْصَةِ إِذْ لَوْ كَانَ المراد بها إبَاحَةُ الْفعْلِ مَعَ الإِثْمِ فِى الصَّبْرُ فَ الْقَرْضَ وَإِنْ كَانَ بِدُونِ الإِثْم في الصبر فى الرُّخْصَةُ فَإِفْطَارُ الصَّائِمِ الْمُكْرَهِ إِنْ كَانِ مُسَافِرًا فَفَرْضَ وَإِنْ كَانَ مُقِيْمًا فَرُحْصَةٌ ولَمْ يُوجَدُ مَايُساوِي الأَقْدَامُ وَالاِمْتِنَاعُ فِيهِ فِى الإِثْم وَالثَّوَابِ حَتَّى يَكُونَ مُبَاحًا وَلا يُنَافِي الاخْتِيَارِ أَنْ لَايُنَافِي الْإِكْرَاهَ اِخْتِيَارُ الْمُكرَةِ بِالْفَتْحِ لَكِنْ الاِخْتِيَارَ فَاسِدٌ فَإِذَا عَارَضَهُ اخْتِيَارُ صَحِيحٌ وَهُوَ اخْتِيَارُ الْمُكْرَهِ بِالْكَسْرِ وَجَبَ تَرْجِيْحُ الصَّحِيحِ عَلَى الْفَاسِدِ إِنْ أَمْكَنَ كه فِي الإِكْرَامِ عَلَى الْقَتْلِ وَإِثْلَافِ الْمَالِ حَيْثُ يَصْلَحُ الْمُكْرَهُ بِالْفَتْحِ أَنْ يَكُونَ الهُ لِلْمُكْرِهِ بِالْكَسْرِ فَيُضَافُ الْفِعْلُ إِلَى الْمُكْرَةِ بِالْكِسَرِ وَيَلْزَمُهُ حُكْمُهُ وَإِلَّا أَىٰ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُن
Or his father, or his wife, or the like, then indeed consent and choice both are [present] and coercion in its entirety, i.e., in all these divisions, does not contradict address [of the Law] and legal capacity due to the preservation of intellect and puberty, upon which intellect is the axis of address and legal capacity, and it is divided between fard, haram, ibahah, and rukhsah. That is, acting upon coercion is divided into these four categories. In some positions, acting upon it is fard, like eating carrion when coerced to it by something that necessitates salvation; then it is [enjoined] upon him, and if he remained patient until death, it is a cause of punishment upon him because he cast himself into destruction. In some of it, acting upon it is haram, like adultery and killing a protected soul; doing both is forbidden even with mulji' coercion. In some of it, acting upon it is mubah, like breaking the fast in fasting; if coerced to it, breaking the fast is permitted. In some of it, acting upon it is rukhsah, like uttering words of disbelief on his tongue if coerced to it; he is granted license for that on condition that the heart is at ease with belief, and the coercion is mulji'. And the difference between ibahah and rukhsah is that in rukhsah, that act is not permitted such that the prohibition is removed; rather, it is treated as mubah in removing sin, while in ibahah, the prohibition is removed.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the legal rulings of ikrah (coercion) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author explains that coercion does not invalidate the legal address (khitab) or legal capacity (ahliyyah) because the coerced person retains intellect and puberty. Acting under coercion falls into four categories: fard (obligatory), haram (prohibited), mubah (permissible), and rukhsah (concession). 

Examples: Eating carrion under life-threatening coercion becomes fard because preserving life is obligatory. Adultery and murder remain haram even under coercion. Breaking the fast under coercion is mubah for a resident, but fard for a traveler. Uttering disbelief under coercion is a rukhsah, provided the heart remains firm in faith. 

The key distinction between ibahah and rukhsah: In ibahah, the prohibition is lifted entirely; in rukhsah, the prohibition remains but the act is treated as mubah in terms of removing sin. The passage also discusses a view that ibahah may not need separate mention because it falls under fard or rukhsah. Finally, it addresses choice: the coerced person's choice is defective (fasid), and when it conflicts with the sound choice of the coercer, the sound choice is given priority if possible, attributing the act to the coercer.

Key Terms
الإكراه (al-ikrah): Coercion: compelling a person to do something they dislike, such that if not coerced they would not do it.
الملجئ (al-mulji'): Overwhelming coercion that destroys both consent and sound choice, typically involving threat of death or loss of limb.
الرخصة (al-rukhsah): A legal concession; an act remains prohibited in essence but is excused under necessity, with sin removed.
الإباحة (al-ibahah): Permissibility: the act becomes legally permissible without sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between ibahah (permissibility) and rukhsah (concession) in cases of coercion?
A) In ibahah, the prohibition is removed; in rukhsah, the prohibition remains but sin is erased.
B) In ibahah, sin remains; in rukhsah, both prohibition and sin are removed.
C) Ibahah applies only to travel; rukhsah applies to all other cases.
D) There is no difference; they are synonymous.

Key Takeaway
Coercion divides acts into four hukm categories; ibahah and rukhsah differ fundamentally in whether the prohibition is lifted or merely the sin is removed.

Categorization of Actions Under Duress: Ibahah vs Rukhsah
Classifies actions under duress and distinguishes ibahah from rukhsah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any action under duress into one of four Hanafi categories (fard, haram, mubah, rukhsah) and distinguish between ibahah and rukhsah using the criterion of whether the original prohibition remains.

Core Idea
Duress changes the ruling but not legal capacity: actions become fard, haram, mubah, or rukhsah based on harm and intention.

Duress (ikrah) is a central concept in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It does not negate legal capacity (ahliyyah) but alters the ruling of an act. This passage from Nur al-Anwar classifies actions under duress into four types and clarifies the critical difference between permission (ibahah) and concession (rukhsah). Understanding this classification is essential for analyzing cases where a person is compelled to act against his will.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
List the four rulings for actions under duress: fard (obligatory), haram (prohibited), mubah (permissible), and rukhsah (concession). Note the examples given for each.
The passage gives examples: eating carrion (fard), zina/killing (haram), breaking fast (mubah), uttering kufr with heart at rest (rukhsah).
2
Distinguish ibahah from rukhsah
Understand that in rukhsah the original prohibition remains but the act is temporarily permitted, whereas ibahah removes the prohibition entirely. The author also mentions a view that ibahah can be subsumed under fard or rukhsah depending on whether there is sin in refraining.
Key difference: rukhsah does not lift the sin of the prohibited act; it merely allows it under duress.
3
Apply the distinction to the example of breaking fast
Analyze the ruling for a coerced fasting person: if a traveler, breaking fast is obligatory (fard) because it is a legitimate dispensation; if a resident, it is a concession (rukhsah) because there is sin in eating without valid excuse.
This shows how context (e.g., travel status) determines whether an act falls under fard or rukhsah.
4
Identify the underlying principle
The classification depends on the balance of harm: when the harm of refraining outweighs the harm of acting, the act becomes obligatory; when both action and refraining are equal in harm, it becomes permissible; when the act itself is inherently prohibited (zina/killing), it remains haram even under duress.
This is rooted in the Hanafi principle of choosing the lesser of two harms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالإكْرَاهُ بِجُمْلَتِه لا ينافي خطاب الاهلية وانه متردد بين فروض حظر واباحة ورخصة ففي بعضه العمل به فرض كأكل الميتة عند الالجاء فَفِي بَعْضِهِ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ حَرَام كالزنا والقتل وفِي بَعْضِهِ مُبَاح كالفطر للصائم وفِي بَعْضِهِ رُخْصَة كالكفر عند الاكراه مع اطمئنان القلب بالايمان وَالْفَرْقُ بَيْنَ الْإِبَاحَةِ وَالرُّحْصَةِ أن الرخصة لا ترفع الحرمة بل يباح الفعل مع بقائها والإباحة ترفع الحرمة وَقِيلَ لا حاجة إلى ذِكْرِ الإِبَاحَةِ لِدُخُولِهَا فِي الفَرَض أَوِ الرُّحْمَةِ إِذْ لَوْ كَانَ المراد بها إبَاحَةُ الْفعْلِ مَعَ الإِثْمِ فِى الصَّبْرُ فَ الْقَرْضَ وَإِنْ كَانَ بِدُونِ الإِثْم في الصبر فى الرُّؤْمَةُ فَإِفْطَارُ الصَّائِمِ الْمُكْرَهِ إِنْ كَانِ مُسَافِرًا فَفَرْضَ وَإِنْ كَانَ مُقِيْمًا فَرُحْصَةٌ ولَمْ يُوجَدُ مَايُساوِي الأَقْدَامُ وَالاِمْتِنَاعُ فِيهِ فِى الإِثْم وَالثَّوَابِ حَتَّى يَكُونَ مُبَاحًا وَلَا يُنَافِي الاخْتِيَارِ أَنْ لَايُنَافِي الْإِكْرَاهَ اِخْتِيَارُ الْمُكرَةِ بِالْفَتْحِ لَكِنْ الاِخْتِيَارَ فَاسِدٌ فَإِذَا عَارَضَهُ اخْتِيَارُ صَحِيحٌ وَهُوَ اخْتِيَارُ الْمُكْرَهِ بِالْكَسْرِ وَجَبَ تَرْجِيْحُ الصَّحِيحِ عَلَى الْفَاسِدِ إِنْ أَمْكَنَ كه فِي الإِكْرَامِ عَلَى الْقَتْلِ وَإِثْلَافِ الْمَالِ حَيْثُ يَصْلَحُ الْمُكْرَهُ بِالْفَتْحِ أَنْ يَكُونَ الهُ لِلْمُكْرِهِ بِالْكَسْرِ فَيُضَافُ الْفِعْلُ إِلَى الْمُكْرَةِ بِالْكِسَرِ وَيَلْزَمُهُ حُكْمُهُ وَإِلَّا أَىٰ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ نِسْبَةُ الْفِعْلِ إِلَى الْمُكْرَةِ بِالْكِسَرِ كَمَا فِي الأَقْوَالِ وَفِي بَعْضِ الْأَفْعَالِ بَقِيَ منسوبًا إلى الاختيار الفَاسِرِ وَهُوَ اخْتِيَارُ الْمُكْرَةِ بالفَتح فَجُعِلَ المُكْرَهُ مُؤاخذا بِفِعْلِهِ ثُمَّ فَرْغَ عَلى هَذَا بِقَوْلِهِ فَفِي الأَقْوَالِ لأَيَصْلَحُ الْمُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الَهُ لِغَيْرِهِ لاَنَّ المُكَلَّمُ بِلِسانِ الغَيْرِ لا يَتَصَوْرُ فَاقْتَصَرَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ حُكْمِ الْقَوْلِ عَلَى الْمُكْرَهِ بِالْفَتْحِ بالفتح فَإِنْ كَانَ الْقَوْلُ مِمَّا لا يَنفَسِحُ وَلَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلى الرِّضَاءِ لَمْ يَبْطَلُ بِالْكُرْمِ كَالطَّلاقِ وَنَحْوِهِ مِنَ الْعِتَاقِ وَالنِّكَاحَ وَالرَّجْعَةِ وَالتَّدْبِيرِ وَالْعَفْوِ عَنْ دَمِ الْعَمَدِ وَاليَمِينِ وَالنُّذْرِ وَالظَّهَارِ وَالإِيْلاَءِ وَالْقَى الْقَوْلِى فِيْهِ وَالإِسْلامُ فَإِن هَذِهِ التَّصَرُّفَاتِ كُلُّهَا لاَتَحْتَمِلُ الفَسْخَ وَلَا تَتَوَقَّفُ عَلى الرِّضَاءِ فَلَوْ أُكْرِهَ بِهَا أَحَدٌ وَتَكلم بها لَمْ يَبْطُلُ بِالْكُرْهِ وَتَنْقُدُ عَلَى الْمُكْرَةِ بِالْفَتْحِ فَقَط.
And duress in its entirety does not contradict the address of legal capacity, and it is oscillating between obligation, prohibition, permission, and concession. In some of it, acting according to it is obligatory, like eating carrion under compulsion. In some of it, acting according to it is prohibited, like fornication and killing. In some of it, it is permissible, like breaking fast for the fasting person. In some of it, it is a concession, like disbelief under duress while the heart is at rest with faith. And the difference between permission and concession is that concession does not remove the prohibition, rather the act is permitted while it remains, and permission removes the prohibition. And it was said: There is no need to mention permission because it is included in obligation or concession. For if what is meant by it is permissibility of the act with sin in refraining, then it is obligation; and if it is without sin in refraining, then it is concession. So the breaking of fast by the coerced fasting person: if he is a traveller, it is obligatory; if he is resident, it is a concession. And there is no found what equals the action and refraining in sin and reward such that it would be permissible. And it does not contradict choice that the choice of the coerced (with fatha) does not contradict duress, but the choice is defective. So when it is opposed by a sound choice, which is the choice of the coercer (with kasra), it is necessary to give preference to the sound over the defective if possible, as in duress to kill and destroy property where the coerced can be a tool for the coercer, so the act is attributed to the coercer and his ruling applies. Otherwise, if the attribution of the act to the coercer is not possible, as in utterances and some actions, it remains attributed to the defective choice, which is the choice of the coerced, so the coerced is held accountable for his action. Then he elaborated on this by his saying: In utterances, because the coerced cannot be a tool for another, for speaking with the tongue of another is inconceivable. So he confined the ruling of the utterance to the coerced with fatha. So if the utterance is of a type that is not voidable and does not depend on consent, it is not nullified by duress, like divorce and similar from manumission, marriage, revocation, tadbir, pardon for intentional bloodshed, oath, vow, zihar, ila', and the pronouncement of qadhf therein, and Islam. For all these dispositions do not admit rescission and do not depend on consent. So if one is coerced in them and utters them, they are not nullified by duress and are executed upon the coerced (with fatha) alone.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage from the commentary of Nur al-Anwar discusses the legal effects of duress (ikrah) on human actions, a key topic in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author explains that duress does not negate legal capacity (ahliyyah) for the divine address; rather, it creates a defective choice. Actions under duress fall into four categories: obligatory (e.g., eating carrion when threatened with death), prohibited (e.g., committing zina or murder, even under duress), permissible (e.g., breaking a fast under duress), and a concession (e.g., uttering kufr under duress while the heart remains firm in faith). The distinction between ibahah and rukhsah is clarified: in rukhsah the prohibition remains but the act is permitted temporarily, whereas ibahah removes the prohibition entirely. Some scholars argued that mentioning ibahah is unnecessary because it either falls under obligation (if there is sin in refraining) or under concession (if no sin in refraining). The passage then addresses the attribution of acts: when choice is defective, sound choice of the coercer is preferred. In acts of killing or destroying property, the coercer is considered the principal and the coerced a tool, so the act is attributed to the coercer. In utterances (aqwal) and some actions, since one cannot speak through another's tongue, the act is attributed to the coerced. Specific utterances (talaq, itq, etc.) are not invalidated by duress because they do not require consent to be effective; they take effect on the coerced person.

Key Terms
الإكراه (al-ikrah): Duress that compels a person to act against his will, categorized as mulji' (complete) or ghayr mulji'.
الرخصة (al-rukhsah): A concession that permits an act while the original prohibition remains, as a temporary dispensation under duress.
الإباحة (al-ibahah): Permissibility that removes the original prohibition entirely, making the act neutral.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between ibahah and rukhsah?
A) Ibahah is for obligatory acts, rukhsah for forbidden acts.
B) Ibahah removes the prohibition, rukhsah permits the act while the prohibition remains.
C) Ibahah applies to acts of worship, rukhsah to worldly acts.
D) There is no difference; they are synonyms.

Key Takeaway
Duress categorizes actions into fard, haram, mubah, or rukhsah; rukhsah permits an act without removing its prohibition, while ibahah removes the prohibition.

Attribution of Acts Under Duress: Coercer vs Coerced and Rulings on Utterances
Discusses attribution of coerced acts and rulings on specific utterances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whether an act under duress is attributed to the coercer or the coerced, and apply the rule that certain utterances (like talaq) take effect on the coerced even under duress.

Core Idea
Acts of killing and property damage are attributed to the coercer; utterances (especially those not voidable) are attributed to the coerced.

The second part of the passage addresses a critical issue: to whom is a coerced act attributed? Hanafi usul distinguishes between physical acts where the coerced can be a mere tool (e.g., killing) and utterances where direct accountability lies with the speaker. Furthermore, certain legal utterances like divorce are not invalidated by duress because they do not require consent. This lesson unpacks these rules and their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of defective vs sound choice
The coerced has a defective choice (ikhtiyar fasid), while the coercer has sound choice (ikhtiyar sahih). When both exist, the sound choice is preferred if possible.
This foundational principle explains why the act can be attributed to the coercer.
2
Identify when attribution shifts to coercer
In acts like killing or destroying property, the coerced can be considered a mere tool (ala) of the coercer. The act is attributed to the coercer, and the coercer bears the ruling (sin, diyah, etc.).
The passage says: 'the coerced can be a tool for the coercer, so the act is attributed to the coercer.'
3
Identify when attribution stays with coerced
In utterances (aqwal) and some actions, the coerced cannot be a tool for another because one cannot speak with another's tongue. Thus the act is attributed to the coerced, and he is held accountable.
Exception: some actions may also follow this rule, but the passage primarily discusses utterances.
4
Apply the rule to specific utterances
Certain utterances like talaq (divorce), itq (manumission), nikah, raj'ah, etc., are not voidable and do not depend on consent. Even if coerced, they take effect on the coerced. They cannot be rescinded.
The passage lists: talaq, itq, nikah, raj'ah, tadbir, pardon for intentional bloodshed, oath, vow, zihar, ila', qadhf, and Islam.
5
Distinguish from utterances that depend on consent
Utterances like sale (bay') depend on consent and can be rescinded under duress. The passage implies but does not explicitly state this; it contrasts those that 'do not admit rescission'.
This distinction is crucial in muamalat (transactions).

Source Text

مُبَاح كالفطر للصائم وفِي بَعْضِهِ رُخْصَة كالكفر عند الاكراه مع اطمئنان القلب بالايمان وَالْفَرْقُ بَيْنَ الْإِبَاحَةِ وَالرُّحْصَةِ أن الرخصة لا ترفع الحرمة بل يباح الفعل مع بقائها والإباحة ترفع الحرمة وَقِيلَ لا حاجة إلى ذِكْرِ الإِبَاحَةِ لِدُخُولِهَا فِي الفَرَض أَوِ الرُّحْمَةِ إِذْ لَوْ كَانَ المراد بها إبَاحَةُ الْفعْلِ مَعَ الإِثْمِ فِى الصَّبْرُ فَ الْقَرْضَ وَإِنْ كَانَ بِدُونِ الإِثْم في الصبر فى الرُّؤْمَةُ فَإِفْطَارُ الصَّائِمِ الْمُكْرَهِ إِنْ كَانِ مُسَافِرًا فَفَرْضَ وَإِنْ كَانَ مُقِيْمًا فَرُحْصَةٌ ولَمْ يُوجَدُ مَايُساوِي الأَقْدَامُ وَالاِمْتِنَاعُ فِيهِ فِى الإِثْم وَالثَّوَابِ حَتَّى يَكُونَ مُبَاحًا وَلَا يُنَافِي الاخْتِيَارِ أَنْ لَايُنَافِي الْإِكْرَاهَ اِخْتِيَارُ الْمُكرَةِ بِالْفَتْحِ لَكِنْ الاِخْتِيَارَ فَاسِدٌ فَإِذَا عَارَضَهُ اخْتِيَارُ صَحِيحٌ وَهُوَ اخْتِيَارُ الْمُكْرَهِ بِالْكَسْرِ وَجَبَ تَرْجِيْحُ الصَّحِيحِ عَلَى الْفَاسِدِ إِنْ أَمْكَنَ كه فِي الإِكْرَامِ عَلَى الْقَتْلِ وَإِثْلَافِ الْمَالِ حَيْثُ يَصْلَحُ الْمُكْرَهُ بِالْفَتْحِ أَنْ يَكُونَ الهُ لِلْمُكْرِهِ بِالْكَسْرِ فَيُضَافُ الْفِعْلُ إِلَى الْمُكْرَةِ بِالْكِسَرِ وَيَلْزَمُهُ حُكْمُهُ وَإِلَّا أَىٰ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ نِسْبَةُ الْفِعْلِ إِلَى الْمُكْرَةِ بِالْكِسَرِ كَمَا فِي الأَقْوَالِ وَفِي بَعْضِ الْأَفْعَالِ بَقِيَ منسوبًا إلى الاختيار الفَاسِرِ وَهُوَ اخْتِيَارُ الْمُكْرَةِ بالفَتح فَجُعِلَ المُكْرَهُ مُؤاخذا بِفِعْلِهِ ثُمَّ فَرْغَ عَلى هَذَا بِقَوْلِهِ فَفِي الأَقْوَالِ لأَيَصْلَحُ الْمُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الَهُ لِغَيْرِهِ لاَنَّ المُكَلَّمُ بِلِسانِ الغَيْرِ لا يَتَصَوْرُ فَاقْتَصَرَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ حُكْمِ الْقَوْلِ عَلَى الْمُكْرَهِ بِالْفَتْحِ بالفتح فَإِنْ كَانَ الْقَوْلُ مِمَّا لا يَنفَسِحُ وَلَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلى الرِّضَاءِ لَمْ يَبْطَلُ بِالْكُرْمِ كَالطَّلاقِ وَنَحْوِهِ مِنَ الْعِتَاقِ وَالنِّكَاحَ وَالرَّجْعَةِ وَالتَّدْبِيرِ وَالْعَفْوِ عَنْ دَمِ الْعَمَدِ وَاليَمِينِ وَالنُّذْرِ وَالظَّهَارِ وَالإِيْلاَءِ وَالْقَى الْقَوْلِى فِيْهِ وَالإِسْلامُ فَإِن هَذِهِ التَّصَرُّفَاتِ كُلُّهَا لاَتَحْتَمِلُ الفَسْخَ وَلَا تَتَوَقَّفُ عَلى الرِّضَاءِ فَلَوْ أُكْرِهَ بِهَا أَحَدٌ وَتَكلم بها لَمْ يَبْطُلُ بِالْكُرْهِ وَتَنْقُدُ عَلَى الْمُكْرَةِ بِالْفَتْحِ فَقَط.
And duress in its entirety does not contradict the address of legal capacity, and it is oscillating between obligation, prohibition, permission, and concession. In some of it, acting according to it is obligatory, like eating carrion under compulsion. In some of it, acting according to it is prohibited, like fornication and killing. In some of it, it is permissible, like breaking fast for the fasting person. In some of it, it is a concession, like disbelief under duress while the heart is at rest with faith. And the difference between permission and concession is that concession does not remove the prohibition, rather the act is permitted while it remains, and permission removes the prohibition. And it was said: There is no need to mention permission because it is included in obligation or concession. For if what is meant by it is permissibility of the act with sin in refraining, then it is obligation; and if it is without sin in refraining, then it is concession. So the breaking of fast by the coerced fasting person: if he is a traveller, it is obligatory; if he is resident, it is a concession. And there is no found what equals the action and refraining in sin and reward such that it would be permissible. And it does not contradict choice that the choice of the coerced (with fatha) does not contradict duress, but the choice is defective. So when it is opposed by a sound choice, which is the choice of the coercer (with kasra), it is necessary to give preference to the sound over the defective if possible, as in duress to kill and destroy property where the coerced can be a tool for the coercer, so the act is attributed to the coercer and his ruling applies. Otherwise, if the attribution of the act to the coercer is not possible, as in utterances and some actions, it remains attributed to the defective choice, which is the choice of the coerced, so the coerced is held accountable for his action. Then he elaborated on this by his saying: In utterances, because the coerced cannot be a tool for another, for speaking with the tongue of another is inconceivable. So he confined the ruling of the utterance to the coerced with fatha. So if the utterance is of a type that is not voidable and does not depend on consent, it is not nullified by duress, like divorce and similar from manumission, marriage, revocation, tadbir, pardon for intentional bloodshed, oath, vow, zihar, ila', and the pronouncement of qadhf therein, and Islam. For all these dispositions do not admit rescission and do not depend on consent. So if one is coerced in them and utters them, they are not nullified by duress and are executed upon the coerced (with fatha) alone.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage from the commentary of Nur al-Anwar discusses the legal effects of duress (ikrah) on human actions, a key topic in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author explains that duress does not negate legal capacity (ahliyyah) for the divine address; rather, it creates a defective choice. Actions under duress fall into four categories: obligatory (e.g., eating carrion when threatened with death), prohibited (e.g., committing zina or murder, even under duress), permissible (e.g., breaking a fast under duress), and a concession (e.g., uttering kufr under duress while the heart remains firm in faith). The distinction between ibahah and rukhsah is clarified: in rukhsah the prohibition remains but the act is permitted temporarily, whereas ibahah removes the prohibition entirely. Some scholars argued that mentioning ibahah is unnecessary because it either falls under obligation (if there is sin in refraining) or under concession (if no sin in refraining). The passage then addresses the attribution of acts: when choice is defective, sound choice of the coercer is preferred. In acts of killing or destroying property, the coercer is considered the principal and the coerced a tool, so the act is attributed to the coercer. In utterances (aqwal) and some actions, since one cannot speak through another's tongue, the act is attributed to the coerced. Specific utterances (talaq, itq, etc.) are not invalidated by duress because they do not require consent to be effective; they take effect on the coerced person.

Key Terms
الاختيار الفاسد (al-ikhtiyar al-fasid): Defective choice that arises under duress; it is still a form of choice but lacks full volition.
الإكراه الملجئ (al-ikrah al-mulji'): Compelling duress that leaves no option but compliance, often threatening life or limb.
الانفساخ (al-infisakh): Rescission or voidability; utterances that can be rescinded are those that depend on consent (e.g., sale).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following utterances is NOT nullified by duress and takes effect on the coerced?
A) A contract of sale
B) A pronouncement of divorce (talaq)
C) A rental agreement
D) A gift contract

Key Takeaway
In physical acts like killing, the act is attributed to the coercer; in utterances, the coerced is accountable, and certain utterances like talaq are effective despite duress.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
Attribution of Actions Under Duress (Ikrah) in Hanafi Usul
Explaining attribution of actions and statements under duress

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi rule for attributing actions under duress and distinguish between statements that are non-rescindable (valid) vs. rescindable (fasid).

Core Idea
Under duress, actions are attributed to the coercer if possible; otherwise to the coerced with corrupt choice—statements always bind the speaker.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the effect of duress (ikrah) on legal acts is nuanced. Duress does not eliminate choice but corrupts it. This passage from Nur al-Anwar explains how actions and statements are attributed when performed under duress, and which legal effects remain binding despite coercion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two modes of attribution
Determine whether the act can be attributed to the coercer (jabr) or must be attributed to the coerced with corrupt choice (ikhtiyar fasad). Physical compulsion often attributes the act to the coercer; otherwise it remains with the coerced.
This is the foundational principle: attribution depends on possibility of instrumentality.
2
Classify statements as rescindable or non-rescindable
For statements under duress, if the statement is inherently non-rescindable and does not require consent (e.g., divorce, manumission), it remains valid. If it is rescindable and requires consent (e.g., sale), it becomes fasid but can be ratified later.
Non-rescindable statements are effective even under duress; rescindable ones are defective without consent.
3
Apply the same classification to actions
Some actions are like statements in that they cannot be performed by another (e.g., eating, intercourse) — these are attributed to the coerced. Other actions where the coerced can be an instrument are attributed to the coercer.
The Hanafi rule: if the act can be done via another, the coercer bears responsibility; otherwise the coerced does.
4
Analyze the examples given
Work through the examples: divorce under duress is valid; a coerced sale is fasid; coerced breaking of fast invalidates the faster's fast but not the coercer's; coerced eating of another's property incurs sin on the eater.
Each example illustrates the attribution principle and its legal consequences.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Note the difference: Shafi'i holds that duress negates intent entirely, making all actions invalid; Hanafi argues that corrupt choice remains, so some acts survive duress.
This ikhtilaf arises from different interpretations of the hadith on forgiveness under duress.

فَيَنْعَقِدُ الْبَيْعَ فَاسِدًا وَلَوْ أَجَازَهُ بَعْدَ زَوَالِ الإِكْرَاهِ يَصِيحُ لأَنَّ الْمُفْسِدَ زَالَ بِالإِجَازَةِ وَلَا تَصِحُ الأَقَادِيرُ كُلُّهَا لِأَنَّ صِحَّتَهَا تَعْتَمِدُ عَلَى قِيَامِ الْمُكْبِرِ بِهَا وَقَدْ قَامَتْ دَلَالَتُهَا عَلَىٰ عَدَمِهِ أَنْ عَدَم ثُبُوْتِ الْمُكْبِرِ بِهَا لأَنَّهُ يَتَكَلَّمُ دَفْعًا لِلسَّيْفِ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ لَا لِوُجُوْدِ الْمُكْبِرِ بِهَا وَلا يَجوزُ أَن يُجْعَل مَجَازًا عَنْ شَيْءٍ لَأَنَّهُ لا يُقْصَبُ الْمَجَارُ مَعَ قِيَام دَلِيْلِ الْكِذَبِ وَهُوَ الإِكْرَاهُ وَالأَفْعَالُ قِسْمَانِ أَحَدُهُمَا كَالأَقْوَالٍ فَلا يَصْلَحُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُكْرَهُ فِيهِ آلَةً لِغَيْرِهِ كَالأَكْلِ وَالْوَطِي وَالزَّنَا فَيَقْتَصِرُ عَلَى الْمُكْرَةِ لِأَنَّ الأَكْلَ بِفَمِ الْغَيْرِ لَا يُتَصَوَّرُ وَكَذَا الْوَطْءُ بِآلَةِ الْغَيْرِ لَا يُتَصَوَّرُ فَإِذَا أُكْرِهَ الْإِنْسَانُ أَنْ يَأْكُلَ فِي الصَّوْمِ يَفْسُدُ صَوْمُ الأَكِلِ وَلَا يَفْسِدُ صَوْمُ الآمِرِ إنْ كَانَ صَائِمًا وَكَذَا لَوْ أُكْرِهَ أَنْ يَأْكُلَ مَالَ غَيْرِهِ يَأْثَمُ الأَكِلُ دُونَ الآمِرِ وَلَكِنَّهُمُ اخْتَلَفُوا فِي حَقِّ الضَّمَانِ فَقِيلَ بِوُجُوبِ الضَّمَانِ عَلَى الْمُكْرَهِ دُونَ الآمِرِ وَإِنْ كَانَ الْمُكْرَهُ يَصْلَحُ آلَةً لِلْآمِرِ
The attribution of the act to the one who compels by force is like in utterances; and in some actions, it remains attributed to the corrupt choice, which is the choice of the coerced (with fatha). So the coerced is held accountable for his action. Then he branched from this by his saying: 'As for utterances, the coerced cannot be an instrument for another because speaking with another's tongue is inconceivable. So the ruling of the utterance is confined to the coerced (with fatha). If the utterance is such that it does not accept rescission and is not dependent on consent, it is not invalidated by duress, like divorce and similar examples: manumission, marriage, revocable divorce, tadbir, pardon for intentional homicide, oath, vow, zihar, ila', revocatory speech in that, and Islam. For all these transactions do not accept rescission and are not dependent on consent. So if someone is coerced regarding them and utters them, they are not invalidated by duress and are binding only on the coerced (with fatha). Translation and commentary: It was said there is no need to mention permissibility... and nothing prevents choice...
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Anwar explains the Hanafi ruling on the effect of duress (ikrah) on statements and actions. The author first establishes a general principle: an action performed under duress is attributed to the coercer (mukrih) when possible, like in physical compulsion; otherwise, it remains attributed to the coerced (mukrah) due to his corrupt choice (ikhtiyar fasad). This is because duress does not eliminate choice entirely but corrupts it. In statements, the coerced can never be a mere instrument for the coercer because speech cannot be performed by another's tongue. Therefore, all utterances made under duress are legally attributed to the speaker. However, they are divided into two categories: (1) Statements that are inherently non-rescindable and do not require consent—such as divorce, manumission, marriage, revocable divorce, tadbir, pardon for intentional homicide, oaths, vows, zihar, ila', and declaring Islam—these are effective and binding even if made under duress. (2) Statements that are rescindable and require consent—such as sale and similar contracts—these are concluded but defective (fasid) due to lack of consent, but if ratified after duress ceases, they become valid. Then the passage discusses actions: some actions are like statements (e.g., eating, intercourse) in that they cannot be attributed to the coercer because they are physically performed by the coerced. For example, if a person is coerced to eat during Ramadan, his fast is invalidated, but not the fast of the coercer. Similarly, if coerced to eat another's property, the eater sins, not the coercer, though there is a difference of opinion on liability for damages.

Key Terms
إكراه (ikrah): Compelling someone by threat of harm to do an act they would not otherwise do
اختيار فاسد (ikhtiyar fasad): Corrupt choice: the coerced's preference of the lesser harm, which is still a form of choice

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a sale contract made under duress in the Hanafi school?
A) It is valid and binding.
B) It is fasid and can be ratified later.
C) It is batil and void from the start.
D) It is suspended until duress ends.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, duress does not eliminate choice but corrupts it; non-rescindable statements remain valid, rescindable ones become fasid, and actions that cannot be performed by another bind the coerced alone.
